SCala perfecco^nis

Capla prime partis /
HEre begynnen the chapytours of this present volume of waltere hylton / named
in laten Scala perfecco^nis englisshed the ladder of perfecco^n / which volume
is divided in two parties / The first book of this present volume
conteyneth.lxxxxiii. chapitours / The second book.xlvi. which hole volume
amo^^teth. C.xxxix. chapitours /

aye^nst te^ptaco^ns of the fe^de / Ca. xxxviii How that god hem that he
chesith: he suffrith to be tarried and tempted / and afterward comforts hem

ne lightly leave the grace that is yeuen him of god / Caplm xl That a man should

That the Inner having of man's soul should be like the utter Caplm primu^
GHosti suster in Ihesu christ I pray the that in the calling which our lord
has callid the to his seruyse thou hold the paid. and sto^de steadfastly
therein / traueyling besely with all the myghtes of thy soul by the grace of
Ihu^ christ: for to fulfylle in sothfastnes of good living the state which thou
haste take in liknes and in semyng / And as thou have forsake the world: as it
were a deed man turned to our lord bodily in (...) of men Right so yt in thyn
heart might be as it were (...) all erthly loves and dredes / turned holy to our
lord Ihu^ (...) wit thou well a bodily turnyng to god without the (...)
lowrng. is but a figure and a lyknes of virtues. and no (...) / wherefore a
wretchyd man or woman is he (...) leuyth the Inwardly keeping of himself / and
shapeth (...) out forth oonly a form and liknes of holiness: in (...) thing /
In speech and in bodily works: beholding (...) deeds. and de ming her defawtes
/ wenyng himself (...) when he is right not. and so begyleth himself (...) not
so. but turn thy heart with thy body pryncipall (...) shape the within to his
ly^knes by mekenes and (...) ghostly virtues. and then^e art thou truly turned
to (...) not that thou so lightly on the first day may be to (...) thy soul
by fulhede of virtues: as thou might with (...) be closid in a house. but that
thou should know that the (...) of thy bodily closyng is / that thou might the
beter com^^^ ghostly closing / And as thy body is closyd fro bodily
co^ue^^^co^n of men / right so that thyn heart might be enclosed from flesshly
loves and dredes of al erthly things / And that th^^ ^^^ghte the beter come
therto^ I shall tell the in this lityl writing / as me thynkith.

Of actyf life. and the works thereof / Caplm ii
THou shalt understood that there is in holy church two manner of lives as
saint gregory says. in the which christian men should be sauf / That one is
called actyf. Greg.
and ye other conte^platyff / without one of thise ii. no man may be sauid
Actyff life lies in love and charity showed outward by good bodily works in
fulfillyng of goddis commandments / and of the vii. works of mercy bodily
and ghostly to a man^es even christian This life longs to all worldly men which
have richesse and plenty of worldly goods for to spend / And so to all other
the which have state office or cure of other men. And have goods for to
spend. lerid and lewd: temporell or spirytuell / And generally all worldly
men are bound to fulfylle it after her might and cu^nyng: as reason and
discreco^n asks / If he much good have / much good for to do / If he
lityll have. less may he do / And if he nout have / then^e must he have a
good will Thise ben works of actyf life other bodily or ghostly / Also a great
part of actyf life lies in great bodily deeds. the which a man does to
himself / as great fasting: much wakyng / and other sharp penance dooyng for
to chastise the flesh with descreco^n for trespace before done / And by such
penance for to refrain lusts and likings of it / and to make him buxum and
ready to the will of the spirit / Thise works though they be^ actiff. they
help right much. and ordeneth a man in the begi^nyng to come to co^te^platyf
life / if they be^ used with descrecio^

Of conte^platiff life and the works thereof / Caplm iii.
COnte^platyf life lies in perfyte love and charity felyd inwardly by ghostly
virtues and by sothfast knowing and sight of god and ghostly things / This life
longs to hem specyalli the which for the love of god forsakith all worldly
richesse warshippes: and outward besines / and holy yeue^ hem body and soul
after her might and cu^nyng to the seruise of god by ghostly ocupaco^n / Now
then^e since it is so that thy state askith for to be conte^platiff / for that
is the^tent of thy enclosing. that thou myt more freely and enteerly give y^ to
gostly ocupaco^n / Then^e behouyth the for to be right besie both night and
day with traueyle of body and of spirit: for to come to that life as nygh as
thou may by such means as thou hopest were best to the. Nevertheless before
that I tell the of the means: I shall tell the first a lityll more of this
life conte^platyff: that thou myt somewhat see what it is / and sithen set it as
a mark in the sight of thy soul: whereto thou shall draw in all thyn
occupaco^n /

Of the first part of conte^placo^n / Caplm iiii^
COntemplatyff life has three parts / The first lies in knowing of god and
ghostly things geten by reason: by techyng of man: and by study in holy
writ / without ghostly affecco^n and July savor felyd. by the special yefte
of the holy ghost / This part have specially lettred men and great clerks
which by long study and trauaylle in holy writ comen to this knowing more
or less after the subtilte of kyndly wit and contynuau^ce of study. of the
general wit that god yeueth to every man that has use of reason / This
knowing is good / and it may be called a part of conte^placo^n. in asmoche as
it is a sight of sothfastnes. and a knowing of ghostly things Nevertheless it
is but a figure and a shawwe of very conte^placo^n / for it has not ghostly
savor in god: ne inwardly swetnes / the which no man may feel but if he be
in great charity / For it is the proper well of our lord / to the which
comes none alien. But this manner knowing is common to good and badde / for it
may be had without charity: and therefore it is not very conte^placo^n / As often
sithes ypocrytes and flesshly living men have more such knowing than many
other christian men. and yet have thise men no charity. Of this manner knowing
spekith saint poul thus / Si habuero oe^m sciencia^. and no uerim misteria
oi^a. caritate^ aute^ non habea^. nihil su^. Cor i3.
If I had full knowing of all thynges^ and I knew al preuytees. and I had not
charity. I am rit naught / Nevertheless if they that have this knowing keep hem
in mekenes and in charity: and flee worldly and flesshly sins after her
might; it is to hem a good way and a great disposing to very conte^placio^ / if
they desire and may devoutly after the grace of ye holy ghost / Other me^ that
have this cu^nyng and turns it to pride and vaynglory of he^self / or in to
couetyse and desiryng of worldly states. Greg.
worships and riches / not mekely taking it to the praising of god: ne
charitably spe^deth it in the profit of her eue^cristen. some of hem fallen
other into heresies and errors / or in to other open sins / by the which
they sclau^der he^self and all holy church / Of this cu^nyng says saint poul
thus. Scie^cia inflat. caritas ante^ edificat / knowi^g alone lifts up the
heart into pride / but me^ge it with charity: and then^e turns it into
edifycaco^n / This knowing alone is but water unsavory and cold / And therefore
if they that have it would mekely offer it up to our lord / and pray him of
grace / he should with his blessyng turn the water in to wine / as he did at
ye prayer of his mother at the fest of Architriclyne / that is for to say / He
should turn the unsavory knowing in to wisdom. and the cold naked reason in to
ghostly light and bre^nyng love by the yefte of the holy ghost /

Of the ii. part of contemplaco^n / Caplm v.
THe ii. part of conte^placo^n lies pryncipally in affeccion without light of
vndersto^ding of ghostly things / and this is comynly of simple and unlettered
men / which yeue^ hem holy to deuoco^n / and this is felyd on this manner /
when man or woman in meditaco^n of god by the grace of the holy ghost felyth
fervor of love and ghostly swetnes by the mind of cryst^ passo^n / or any of
his works in his ma^hede / or he felith a great trust in the goodness and in
the mercy of god f^^ the foryeuenes of his sins: and for his great yeft of
grace. (...) else he felith a dread in his affecco^n with great reverence of the
preuy ^omes of god / the which he sees not / and of his rightwylnes. Or in
prayer he felith the thout of his heart draw up fro all all erthly things.
strenyd togider with all the myghtes of his heart: vpstyeng to our lord by
fervent desire and with ghostly delight And nevertheless in that time he has no
open sight in vndsto^dyng of ghostly thynges^ ne of preuytees of holy writ in
special / but only that him thynkith for the time no thing likyth him
somoche as for to pray or think as he does. for savor delight and comfort
that he fyndeth therein / And yet can he not tell what it is. but he felyth it
well: for it is a yeft of god For out of it spryngen many swete^ teres: bre^nyng
desires / and stylle mournynges^ which scoureth and cle^seth the heart fro all
ye fylth of syn^e / and makes it melte in to wonderful swetnes of Ihu^ christ.
buxum. soople: and ready to fulfylle al goddis will / In somoche that him
thynkith he makith no charge what comyth of himself / so that goddis will
were fulfilled with such many stirynges moo than I can or may say / This
felyng may not be had without great grace / and who so has it for the time he
is in charity / which charity may not be lost ne lessed though the fervor of
it pass away: but by a dedely sin^e / and that is comfortable: This may be
called the ii. part of co^templaco^n / Nevertheless this part has ii. degrees /

Of the lower degree of the ii^ part of conte^placo^n / ca vi:
THe lower degree of this feeling. men which are actyff may have by grace wha^
they be^ visyted of our lord as myghtly and as ferue^tly as they that give hem
holy to conte^platyf life and has this yeft. but this felyng in his fervor
comith not always wha^ a man would. ne it lastith not full long. It comyth and
gooth as he will that yeuyth it / and therefore who so has it. meke himself.
and thank god: and keep it preuy / but if it be to his confessor / and hold
he it aslong as he may with descreco^n / And wha^ it is wythdrawen dread not
tomoche. but stand sadly in faith and in a meke hope / with pacye^ce abidyng
till it come again / This is a lityl tastyng of the swetnes of ye love of god /
of the which david says thus in the sawter / P^ xxxiii
Gustate and videte qm^ suauis est dn^s / Taast ye and see ye the swetnes of
our lord /

Of the hyer degree of the ii. part of co^templaco^n / Caplm vii.
THe hyer degree of this part may not be had and holden but of hem the which
be^ in great rest of body and soul / the which by grace of Ihu^ and long
traueile bodily and ghostly felith a rest of heart and clen^es in conscience.
so y^ hem liken no thing somoche for to do / as to sit stylle in rest of
body / and for to always pray to god. and think on our lord. and to think
sometime on the blessid name of Ihesu which is comfortable and delectable to
hem / that by the mind of it they felen hem fed in her affecco^n / And not
only of y^ name. but al other manner prayers: as the Pater nost and the Auee /
or ympnes or psalms and other devout saye^ges of holy church are turned as it
were in to a ghostly mirth and sweet so^ge ^ by y^ which they are comforted
and stre^gthed against al sins. and much releuyd of bodily disese. Of this
degree spekith saint poul thus ^olite inebriari vino: Eph^e. v.
sed i^pleamin^ sp^u sco^. loquentes vobis metip^is in ympnis and canticis and
psalmis spu^alibus. canta^tes and psalle^tes in cordibus vr^is dn^o / Be ye not
dro^ken with wine / but be ye fulfilled of ye holy ghost saie^g to yourself in
ympnes and psalms and ghostly so^ges: synging and psalmyng in your hertes to
our lord / who so has this grace keep he himself in lowenes / and that he be
ever desiryng for to come to more knowing and felyng of god in the third part
of co^templaco^n /

Of the third part of contemplacion / Caplm viii.
THe third part of conte^placion the which is perfect as it may here lies
both in cognico^n and in affecco^n. That is to say / in knowing and in perfect
loving of god. And that is wha^ a ma^nys soul first is reformed by fulhede of
virtues to the image of Ihu^ / And afterward wha^ he is visited he is taken in
fro all erthly and flesshly affecco^ns: fro vayn thought and ymaginynges of all
bodily creatures / and as it were much rauysshed out of the bodily wits /
And then^e by ye grace of the holy ghost is illumyned for to see by vndsto^dyng
soth fastnes which is god and ghostly things with a soft sweet bre^nyng love
in him so perfitly that he be rauysshed of his love. so the soul is onyd for
the time and co^formyd to the image of ye trinite / The begyn^yng of this
conte^placo^n may be felid in this life / but the fulhede of it is kept into the
bliss of heaven Of this onyng and conformyng to our lord spekith saint poul
thus / Qui adheet deo. vnus sp^s ^ cu^ illo / That is to say / who so by
rauysshi^g of love is fastened to god: then^e god and his soul are not two.
but both one / And sothly in this onyng is ye marriage made betwix god and the
soul: the which shall never be broken /

Of the twyn^ing of the iii. part of conte^placo^n. fro the ii. part of the
praising thereof / Caplm ix
THe other part may be callid bren^yng love in deuoco^n / and this bre^nyng
love in conte^placion. yt is lower. this is ye hier. that is swetter to the
bodily feling / this inwardly felyng better to the ghostly felyng. For it is
more inward. more wothy: more ghostly: more wondful / For this is verily a
tasting so lityl as is and a ernest of the sight of heavenly joy: not clerli.
but half in derkenes. the which shall be fulfilled and openly clered in the
bliss of heaven: as saint poul says / Videmus nu^c per spclm i^ enigmate. i^
cor^ i3.
tu^c aute^ videbimus facie ad facie^ / we see now god by a myrrour as it were
in a derknes / but in heaven shall we see openly face to face. This is the
illumynaco^n of vndstondyng in delites of loving as david says in the sawter.
Psalm^^ C. xviii
Et nox illu^i naro^ mea in deliciis meis / (...) night is my light in my
delyt^ The Other part is milk for children / this is hole mete for perfyte men:
the which have wits assayd to know good fro evil: as saint poul says /
Pfectorum e^ solidus ribus. Hebr^ v.
q he^nt se^sus exercitatos ad discre^o^em boni and mali / The werkynge of the
full use of this yefte may no man have but he be first reformed to ye lyknes of
Ihu^ by fulhede of virtues / Ne there may no man living in dedely flesh have
it co^tynuelly in his fulhede and in the ouerpassyng: but by times when he
(...) iiii is visited / And as I co^ceyue by the writing of holy men it is a
full short time. for soon after he falls in a sobirte of bodily feeling / and
all this work makith charity / Thus as I vndstonde says saint poul of himself
Sieve excedimus deo. sieve sobrii sumus vobis. caritas xp^i vrget nos / wherther
we ouerpasse our bodily wits to god in conte^placo^n. or we are more sobir
to you in bodily felyng. ye charity of crist streyneth us. Of this part of
co^te^placo^n and of reforming to god spekith saint poul openly thus / Nos
aute^ reuelata facie gliam dn^i speclam^ tra^sformati in eande^ ymagine^ a
claritate i^ claritate^^ ta^quamm a dn^i sp^u And this is thus much for to say
Saint poul in the person of himself and of perfyte men says thus / we first
reformed by virtues. the face of our soul vnhelid by openyng of the ghostli
eye beholden as in a myrrour heavenly joy. fulshapid and ouyd to thymage of our
lord fro clerete of faith into clerete of vndstondyng / or else fro clerete of
desire in to clerete of blessed love / and all this is wrout of the spirit of
our lord in a mannis soul as saint poul says: This part of co^te^placo^n god
yeuyth where yt he will / to leryd and to lewd: to men and to wym^en ocupied
in prelacye: and to solitary also / But it is special not common / and also
though a man which al his life is actyf have the yeft of it by a special grace
/ nevertheless the fulness of it may no man have but he be solitary and in life
conte^platyf /

How the showing to the bodily wyittes and the feeling of hem may be both good
and evil / Caplm.x.
By this that I have said may you so^what vndsto^de that visyo^s or reuelaco^ns
of any manner of spirit in bodily aperyng. or in ymaginynge slepyng or wakyng /
or else any other felyng in y^ bodily with made as it were ghostly. other in
sownyng of ere: or sauering in the mouth: or smellyng at ye nose: or else any
se^sible hete as it were fire glowyng and warmyng ye breast or any other part
of ye body / or any other thing yt may be felyd by bodily wit though it be
never so comfortable and lykyng / they ben not very conte^placo^n / ne they
^en but simple and secu^dary though they ben good in reward of ghostly virtues
and of this ghostly knowing and loving of god / But al such manner of felyng
may be good / wrought by a good angel / and they may be deceyuable / wrought
by a wicked angel. when he tra^sfygurith him in to an angel of light / wherefore
sith they may be both good and evil it semith well they are not the best. For
wit you well that the devil may wha^ he has leave feyne in bodily felyng the
lykenes of the same things the which a good angel may work / For right as a
good angel comyth with light: so can ye devil / And so of the other wits /
who so had felid both / he should well tell which were good and which were
evil / But he that never felid neither: or else but that one: may lightly be
deceived / They are like in the manner of felyng outward: but they are full
diverse within / And therefore they are not for to desire greatly. ne for to
receive lightly / but if a soul might by the spirit of discreco^n know the
good fro the evil that he were not begyled / as saint Ioh^n says / Nolite
credere om^isp^ui. sed probare si ex deo sit / Saint Ioh^n bids us that we
should not trust to every spirit / but we shall assaye first whether he be of
god or no / wherefore by one assaye I shall tell the as me thynkith how thou
shall know the good fro evil

How you shall know wha^ the showing to the bodily wyyttes and felyng of hem ben
good or evil / Caplm xi.
IF it so be that thou see any manner of light or bryghtnes with thy bodily eye
/ or in ymaginynge other than every man see / or if thou here any merry wondful
so wnyng with thy bodily ere. or in thy mouth any sweet soden savor other than
of kind. or any hete in thy breast. as it were fire. or any manner delight in any
part of thy body / or if a spirit bodily aperith unto y^ as it were an angel
for to comfort the. and teache y^. or any such felyng which you know well yt
it comith not of thyself ne of no bodily creature / beware in yt time or so ne
after. and wisely behold ye stiryng of thy heart: If you be stirred because of
y^ likyng that you felist to draw out thy heart fro ye mi^de and the beholding of
Ihesu christ and fro ghostly ocupaco^n: As fro prayer and thynkyng of thiself
and thy defaw^es / fro thi^warde desire of virtues and of ghostly knowing and
felyng of god / For to set the sight of thy heart and thy affecco^n / thy delight
and thy rest pryncipally therein / wenyng y^ it should be a part of heavenly joy
and of angels bliss / and for thy the thynkith that you sholdest another pray ne
think not else but al holy tente thereto for to keep it and delight the therein /
This felyng is suspect and of the^mye / and therefore though it be never so
liking and wondful. refuse it and asse^t not thereto / for this is the sleyght
of the^mye. wha^ he sees a soul that would inteerly give it to ghostly
ocupaco^n: he is wondly wroth / For he hates no thing more then^e for to see a
soul in a body of syn^e to feel verily the savor of ghostly knowing and the
love of god. ye which he without body of syn^e lost wylfully / And therefore if
he may not let him by open sins. he would hynd him and begile him by such
vanyte of bodily savors: or swetnes in the wits for to bring a soul in to
ghostly pride and in to a falls sikernes of himself / weninge yt he had thereby a
felyng of heavenly Joy: and that he were half in paradyse for delight that he
felyth about him: wha^ he is nere at hell yates / And so by pride and by
presu^pco^n he might fall in errors or heresies or fa^tasies. or in other
bodily or ghostly myscheues / Nevertheless if it be so that this manner of felyng
let not thy heart fro ghostly ocupaco^n / but it makith the more devout and
more fervent for to pray / it makith the more wise for to think ghostly
thoughts / And though it be so that it astonye the in the begyn^yng /
nevertheless afterward it turns and quyckeneth thyn heart to more desire of
virtues / and increases thy love more to god and to thyn euencrysten / Also it
makith the more meke in thyn own sight / By these tokens may thou know that
it is of god made by the presence and the touching of a good angel / and that
is of the goodness of god either in comfort of simple devout souls for to
increase her trust and her desire to god for to seek thereby the knowing ye
love of god more perfytly for such a comfort / or else if they be^ perfyte that
fele^ such delight: it semyth then^e that it is an ernest and as it were a
shadow of ye glorifyeng of the body which it shall have in ye bliss of heaven.
I wot not whether there be any such man living in earth / This preuylege had
mary mawdeleyne as it semith to my sight in y^ time wha^ she was alone in ye
cave xxx. winter / and every day was borne up with angels and was fed both bodi
and soul by ye presence of hem: thus we read in ye story of her / Of this
manner assaye^g of werkyng of spyrites spekith saint Ioh^n in his pistle thus.
and techeth thus / Oi^s sp^s q soluit ih^m. hic no^ e^ ex deo. Every spirit ye
loses or vnknyttith Ihu^. he is not of god / Thise words may be vndsto^de in
many manners / Nevertheless after one manner I may vndsto^de hem to this purpose
yt I have said.

what knytteth Ihu^ to man's soul: and what loses him therfro / Ca xii.
THe knyttyng and ye fastenyng of Ihu^ to a man's soul: is by good will and
great desire to him only for to have him and see him in his bliss ghostly /
The more yt this desire is. the faster is Ihu^ knytte to the soul: The less
that this desire is ye loslyer is he knitte: Then what spirit or what feling
yt it be the which lesseth this desire and would draw it down fro ye steadfast
mind of Ihu^ christ. and fro ye kyndly styeng up to Ihu^ / this spirit will
vnknytte ihu^ fro ye soul: and therefore it is not of god: but it is the
werkyng of the^mye / Nevertheless if a spirit or a felyng or a reuelaco^n make
this desire more. knytte the knottes of love and deuoco^n to ihu^ faster: and
open the eye of ye soul in to ghostly knowing more clerly: and makith it more
meke in it self this spirit is of god / Here may you see so^what that you shall
not suffer thy heart wilfully for to rest ne for to delight holy in no bodily
felyng of such manner co^fortes or swetnes thou they were good. but you shall
hold hem in thy sight naught or lityl in reward of ghostly desire and on
stedfaff thynking on ihu^ / ne fest the thought of thy heart ouermoche on he^

How and in what things should a conte^platyf man be ocupied / Caplm xiii.
But thou shall ever seek by great besynes in prayers that thou might come to
the ghostly felyng of god / And that is that you might know the wisdom of god
/ the endless might of him / the great goodness of him in himself and in his
creatures / For this is conte^placo^n / and that other is none. thus says
saint poul / In caritate radicati and fu^dati. Eph^^ iii.
vt possitis co^prehendere cu^ oi^bus sci^s que sit longitu do and latitudo.
sublimitas and profundu^ / Be ye roted and grounded in charity that ye might
know he says neither sou^de of the ere ne sweet savor in the mouth: ne none
such bodily thing. but that ye might know and feel with all halowes which
is the length of the endless being of god / the bread of the wonderful charity
and the goodness of god / the heyth of the almighty mageste of him. and the
grou^dles depnes of the wisdom of god In knowing and ghostly felyng of thise
should be the ocupaco^n of a conte^platyff man / For in thise may be understood
the full knowing of al ghostly things / This ocupaco^n is that one thing: the
which saint poul coueyted saye^g thus / Vnu^ que retro su^t obliuisce^s. in
anteriora me extenda^. sequor si quo mo do comp^henda^ supernum braniu^ / Thus
much is to say / ^o thing. Phil. iii
as hoo says. is best to me for to coueyte / and that is that I might fogete
all things the which ben behyndwarde or backewarde / and I shall stretche out
mine heart ever forward for to feel and to grype the souereyne mede of the
endeles bliss / Hynwarde are all bodily things / Forward are goostly things
/ And for saint poul would forgete all bodily things: and his own bodi also.
with that y^ he might see ghostly things /

How in reason and will virtue begins. and in love and in likyng it is made
perfyte / Caplm xiiii.
NOw I have told you a lityll of co^templaco^n what it should be: For this
intent that thou might know it and set it as a mark before the syghte of
thy soul / and for to desire all thy life time to come to any part of it by ^
grace of our lord Ihu^ christ / This is the conformyng of a soul to god / the
which may not be had but if it be first reformyd by fulhede of virtues
turned in to affecco^n. and that is wha^ a man loves virtues / for they be^
good in he^self / There is many a man that has virtue of lownes. patience and
charity to his eue^crysten. and such other only in his reason and will / and
has no ghostly delight ne love in hem / For oftymes he felith grutchinge.
heaviness and bitterness for to do hem / and nevertheless yet he does hem only by
stiryng of reason for dread of god / this man has virtues in reason and in will
/ but not love of he^ in his affeccyo^ But wha^ by grace of Ihu^ and by ghostly
and bodily exercise reason is turned in to light: and will in to love. then^e
has he virtues in affecco^n / For he has so well gnawe on the bitter bark of
the notte that he has broken it: and fedeth him with ye kyrnell / yt is to say
/ The virtues which were first heavy for to do: are now turned into a very
delight and savor: as wha^ a man likes in mekenes: in patience: in cle^nes: in
sobyrte: and in charity. as in any delytes / ^othly till thise virtues ben
turned thus in to affeccio^. he may well have the ii. part of conte^placo^n /
but the iii sothfastly shall he not take /

Of the means that brings a soul to conte^placio^. Caplm xv:
NOw sithe^ virtues are disposyng to conte^placo^n. then^e it behouith ye use
certain means for to come to virtues Three means there be^ which men most
comynly vsen y^ yeuen he^ to conte^placo^n / As redyng of holy writ and of
holy teching: ghostly meditacio^: and besie prayer with deuoco^n: By meditaco^n
shall thou see as I said thy wretchidnes / thy sins. and thy wyckidnes / As
pride: couetise: gloteny: sloth: and lecherye wicked stirynges of envy / ire:
hatred. and male^colye: angrines: bitterness: and unskillful heaviness / Thou
shalt also see thy heart full of vain shames and dredes of thy flesh and of
the world / All these stirynges wyllen all way boylle out of thy heart a
water will ren^e out of ye spring of a stinki^g well. and let y^ site of thy
soul that you may never see ne feel clearly ye love of Ihu^ christ. For wite
you well till thy heart be much cle^sid thru stable troth and besie beholdi^g of
christ ma^hede fro such sins. you may not have ghostly knowing of god perfytly
witnessyng himself in the gospel thus. Bti^ mu^do cord qm^ ip^i de u^
videbu^t. Math^ v.
Blessid be clean of heart. for they shall see god. Also in meditacion you shall
see virtues which be nedful to y^ for to have. as mekenes: myldnes: patience.
ritwisnes: gostly strength te^perau^ce: cle^nes: pees: and sobernes: faith:
hope: and charity / These virtues you shall see in meditacio^. how good how fair
how profitable they be^ / and by prayer you shall desire hem and get hem.
without wiche you may not be conte^platif. For Job says thus. Inhabu^da^cia
igredieris sepulcru^. Job. v.
That is to say. you shall in^ple^te of good bodily werkis and gostly virtues
enter thy grave. yt is the rest in conte^placo^n /

What a man should use and refuse by ye virtue of mekenes / Caplm xvi*
NOw if thou sholdest use wisely gostly works and sikerly traueyle in he^. the
behouyth to begyn^e rit low / Three things ye needs to have first. upon yt
which as on a siker ground thou shall set al thy work. thise iii. are
mekenes: siker faith. and hole intent to god / First the behouyth to have
mekenes in this manner / you shall hold thyselfe in thy will and in thy felyng
if thou may unable to dwell among me^. and unworthy to serve god in
co^uersaco^n with his servant unprofitable to thy eue^cristen: wa^tyng both
cu^nyng and myt to fulfill good works of actif life in help of thy
euencristen: as other men and wym^en done. And therefore as a wretch and
outcaste: and refuse of all men and wym^en art sperred in a house alone / yt you
sholdest dear ne grieve no man or woman by evil ensample. sith thou can not
profit he^ by good werkyng / ^uer this y^ behouith to look feder y^ s^^h you
art so unable to serve our lord by bodily works outward. Tren^. iiii.
how much more behouyth y^ to hold y^ unable and unworthy to serve him
ghostly by inward ocupaco^n / For our lord is a spirit as the prophet says.
Sp^s ante facie^ nr^am xp^s dn^s / Before our face a ghost is our lord christ /
and the kyndly seruyse to him is ghostly / as he says himself. Very adorantes
adorabu^t pre^m in sp^u and veritate / Sothfast servants shall worship him in
spirit and sothfastnesse / Then you that art so boystous. so lewd: so
flesshli: John. iiii.
so blind in goostly things / and namly of thyn own soul: which the
behouyth first to know if thou sholdest come to the knowing of god / How
sholdest thou then feel thyself able or worthy for to have state or lyknes of
conte^platyf life / the which life as I have said lies pryncipally in ghostly
knowing: and felinge of god. This I say to the: not that you sholdest forthynke
thy purpose. and be mispaid with thy enclosyng. but yt thou sholdest feel this
lowenes sothfastly in thy heart if thou might / for it is soth and no lees / And
then^e you shall desire night and day after thy might for to come as nere as thou
may to yt state which you have take / trowyng steadfastly that it is best to
the by the mercy of god. for to traueyle in / And though it be so that thou
may not come to the fulhede of it here in this life. that you mit be in the
begyn^yng of it. and trust sikerly for to have the fulhede by the mercy of god
in the bliss of heaven / For sothly that is my life / I feel me so wretchyd and
so freyle and flesshly / and so fer^ fro true felyng fro that ye I speak: that
I can not ellis but cry mercy. and desire after as I may with an hope y^ our
lord will bring me thereto in the bliss of heaven / Do thou so. and beter
after that god yeuyth the grace / The felyng of this lownes shall put out of
thyn heart vnskylful beholding of other men^es deeds / and it shall drive the
holy to behold thyselfe / as there were no man living but god and thou / And
thou shall deem and hold thyself more vile and more wretch tha^ is any
creature yt beryth life. that uneath shall you suffer thiself for the gretnes and
no^bre of syn^e and fylthe that thou shall feel in the / Thus behouyth the for
to feel sometime if thou will be very meke For I tell the sothly. if thou wylt
be truly meke thou shall think a venyal syn^e in thiself more grievous and
painful to y^ and greter be in thy sight sometime. than great dedely sins of
other men / This is soth to the if thou will be contemplatife. for this skyll /
That thing the which puttith thy soul or lettith it most fro the felyng and
knowing of god: owes to be most grievous and paynfull to the / But a venyall
sin of thiself lettith the more fro the felyng and perfyte love of Ihesu
christ than any other man^es syn^e may do: be it never somoche Semyth it then^e
that thou should more arise in thyn own heart against thyself for to hate and
deem in thyself all manner of si^ne which lets the fro the sight of god /
more than against the defawtes of other men / For if thyn heart be clean of thyn
own sins / sothly the sins of all other me^ should not dear y^ and therefore
if thou will find rest here and in the bliss of heaven / after the counsel
of one of the holy faders say every day what am I / and deem thou no man /

who should blame men^es defawtes and deem hem. and who not / Caplm xvii.
But now see thou how may this be. since it is a deed of charity for to blame
men of her defawtes / and for to deem hem far her amendyng it is a deed of
mercy / As to this I answer as me thynkith / yt to the or to any other the
which has stat^ and purpoos of life co^templatyf it fallyth not for to leave
the keeping of hemself / and for to behold and to blame other men of her
defawtes / but if it were full great need / so that a man should peryssh^ but if
thou blamyd him / But the men which are actyf^ and have soueraynte and cure
over other as prelates and curates and such other: they are bound by their
office and by way of charity for to see and seek. and deem rightfully other
men^es defawtes / Not of desire and delight for to chastise he^. but oonly for
need with dread of god and in his name. for love of saluaco^n of her souls /
Other me^ that are actyf and have no cure of other men. they are bound for to
blame other men of her defawtes by the way of charity only that when the syn^e
is dedely / and it may not well be corrected by none other man and when he
trowyth that he the sooner should be amended by his vndtakyng / Else it is beter
that he cesse. That this is soth it semyth by saint Ioh^n which held the
state of conte^platyf life. and saint peter which had the state of acty^ life.
wha^ our lord in his last sowper with his discyples at the preuy stirynge of
saint peter to saint Ioh^n told saint Ioh^n how Judas should bitraye him /
saint Ioh^n told it not to saint peter as he askid / but he turned him and
laid his head upon cristis breast. and was rauysshid by love in to
conte^placo^n of goddis priuitees And so medefully to him / that he forgate
both Judas and saint peter / in tokenyng and techyng to other men which would
be conte^platyf. that they should dispose hem for to do the same.

Why men should worship other and low he^self in her own heart vnd al other /
Caplm xviii.
THen^e see thou here somewhat that thou shall another deem other men / ne
conceive against hem wylfully none evil suspico^n / but thou shall love hem /
ne see thou no defawte in hem / and worship hem in thy heart such as ledeth in
ye world actyf life / and suffren many trybulaco^ns and te^ptacyons which thou
sittyng in thy house felyst naught of / And they have full much traueyle and
disese for her own and other men^es sustynau^ce / and many of hem had well
lever serve god if they might as thou do in bodily rest / And nevertheless
they in her worldly besynes flee many sins / the which if thou were in her
state thou sholdest fall in / and they do many good deeds which thou cowde
not do / It is no doubt that mani done thus. which they ben. thou wost not
/ And therefore thou shall worship al. and set hem in thy heart al above the as
thy souereyns / and cast the down vnd her fete that thou be vylest and lowest
in thin own sight: for it is no dread ne no peril to the how much thou may
low thyself bynethe al other. though it were so that in goddis sight thou
had more grace than any other. But it is peril to the to hye the and lift
thiself in thy thought wylfully above any other man / though he were the most
wretch: or the most synful caytiff that is in earth / For our lord sayth^
Luc^ xiiii
Qui se huliat exaltabit. et qui se exaltat huliabit / who so hieth himself. he
shall be lowed. and who so lowyth hymself^ he shall be hyed / This part of mekenes
y^ behouyth for to have in thy begyn^yng / and by this and by grace shall thou
come to the fulhede of it and so of all other virtues For who so has one
virtue. he has al other virtues. Asmoche as thou have of mekenes. somoche have
thou of charity. of pacyence. and of other virtues though they ben not showed
outward / Be then^e besie to get mekenes: and hold it for it is ye first
and the last of all virtues / It is the first: for it is the ground as saint
austyn says / If thou think for to bilde an hye house of virtues / ordeyne
the first a deep ground of mekenes. Also it is the last / for it is keeping and
saving of all other virtues / saint gregory says / He that gadreth virtues
without mekenes. he is like to him the which makith and beryth powder of
spicery in the wind / Do thou never so many good deeds / fast thou: wake
thou. or any other good work do thou / if you have no mekenes / it is naught
that thou do /

How men should do that wanten the felyng of mekenes in affecco^n not dredyng
tomoche therefore / Caplm xix.
Nevertheless if thou may not feel this mekenes in thyn heart with affection as
thou would do as thou may meke thyself in will by reason / trowyng that it
should be so as I say / though thou feel it not / And in that hold the a more
wretch that thou may not feel sothfastly thyself as thou art / And if you do
so. though thy flesh rise there again. and will not assent to thy good will.
be not tomoche adrad. but you* shall bear and suffer the false felyng of thy
flessh^ as a pain / and then^e thou shall despise and repreue that feeling.
and break down that risyng of thyn heart: as thou would be well paid for to be
trodden and spourned vnd other me^nes fete. And so by the grace of Ihu^ christ
through steadfast thinkyng on the mekenes of his precious ma^hede shall thou
much abate the stirynges of pride / And the virtue of mekenes yt was first in
thy nakid will shall be turned in to felyng of affecco^n / without which virtue
either in true will or in felyng who so dispose him to serve god in
co^te^platyf life as the blind he shall sto^ble: and he shall never come thereto /
The hyer he clim^yth by bodily penance / and other virtues / and has not this
mekenes. the lower he falls / For as saint gregory says / Greg*
He that can not perfytly despise himself / he found never yet y^ meke wysdom
of our lord Ihu^ christ

How ypocrites and heretykes for lackyng of mekenes hyen hemself in her heart
above al other / Caplm xx.
YPocrites ne heretykes feel not this mekenes neither in good will ne in
affecco^n / but full dry and full cold arn her hertes and her reins fro the
soft felyng of this virtue / and in so much the ferder they ben fro it. that
they wene that they have it / They gnawe on ye dry bark without. but the
sweet kernel of it and the inly savor may they not come to / They show
outward mekenes in habit and holy speech: in lowly beryng / and as it semyth
in many bodily and ghostly virtues / But nevertheless in the will and in
thaffecco^n of her heart where mekenes should be: it is faint / For they deem
and despisen and setten at naught other men that will not do as they done and
teache / they holden hem either foles by vncu^nyng: or blinded by flesshly
living And therefore lift they hemself upon hye in her own sight above al
other. wenyng yt they live better than other: and that they have only the
sothfastnes of good living: and in ghostly felyng and synguler grace of god
both in knowing and in ghostly feling passing other men / And in this sight of
he^self ryseth a delight in her hertes in the which they worship and praise
hemself. as there were none but they. They praysen and thanken god with her
lyppes. but in her hertes they stelen as thieves the worship and the tha^kyng
fro god. and settith it in hemself / and so they have another mekenes in felyng
ne in will / A wretchyd caytyff or a syn^er which falls al day. and he is
sorry that he does so though he have not mekenes in affecco^n / he has it in a
good will / But an heretic or an ypocrite has neither / For they have the
co^dico^n of the pharyse / which came as our lord say the in the gospel with
the publican into the temple for to pray And when he came he prayed not ne
asked ought of god. for him thought he had no need. but he began to thank god
and said thus / Lord I thank the that thou yeuest me grace more than to other
that I am not as other men be / robbers lechours / or other such syn^ers / And
he lokid beside him and saw the publycan which he knew for a wretch:
knockyng on his breast only cryenge after mercy / then^e he thanked god that he
was not such one as he was / for lord he said I fast twyes in the weke / and I
pay truly my tithes / And wha^ he had do. our lord said that he yede home
again without grace as he came. and gate right naught / But now say you. wherein
trespassid this pharyse sith he thanked god and was soth that he said / As to
this I answer and say that this pharysee trespassid in asmoche as he demyd and
repreuid in his heart the publica^ which was justified of god / And also he
trespassyd for he thankyd god oonly with his mouth / but he delyted preuely and
wylfully by a preuy pride in himself of the yeftes of god: stelyng the worship
and loving fro god. and set it in himself / This same condycyon of this
pharysee sothely has heretykes and ypocrytes / They will not gladly pray /
and if they pray: they meke not he^self knowlegyng truly her wretchydnes / but
they make hemself by a fenyng for to thank and love god / and spekith of him
with her mouth / but her delight is vain and falls and not in god / And yet they
wene not so / they can not love god / For as the wise man says / No^ est
speciosa laus in ore peccatoris / It is neither fair Ecc xv^
ne semely praising of god in y^ mouth of a syn^er / wherefore it is profitable
to the and to me and to such other wretches forto leave the condition of this
pharisee and feined loving of god. and follow the plublican in lownes / askyng
mercy and foryeuenes of sins. and grace of ghostly virtues. that we might
afterward with a clean heart sothfastly thank him and love him / and give him
holy ye worship without feynyng / For our lord askith this by his prophet /
Super que^ reqescet sp^s meus. Isay^ 66
nisi super hu^ile^ contritu^ sp^u and tremente^ sermones meos? Upon whom shall
my spirit rest / and he answers himself and says. upon none but upon the
meke poor and contrite in heart and dredyng my words? Then^e if thou will have
the spirit of god rulyng in thy heart: have mekenes and dread him /

What things me^ owe to bileue by a siker faith / ca xxi
The ii. thing which the behouith for to have is siker troth in all tharticles
of the faith and in the sacrament of holy church / trowyng hem stedfastli with
al thy will in thy heart / And thou you feel any stiryng in thy heart against any
of hem by suggestion of thyn enmye for to put the in dowte of hem be thou
steadfast and not tomoche adrad of felyng of such stiringes / but forsake thyn
own wit wytout disputyng or ransakyng of hem / and set thy faith generally
in the faith of holy church / and charge not the stiryng of thy heart / which
as the semyth is contrary thereto / For that stiryng is not thy faith / but the
faith of holy church is thy faith / though you never see it ne feel it / And
bear then^e such stirynges pacie^tly as a scourge of our lord / by ye which
he will cle^se thy heart and make thy faith steadfast / Also the behouyth to love
and worship in thy heart al ye laws and ordinance made by prelates and rulers
of holy church other in declaryng of the faith or of the sacraments or in
general of al criste^ men / mekely and truly assent to hem / thou it be so
that you know not ye cause of her ordinance / And thou the think that some
were unskillful: you shall not deem hem ne repreue hem / but worship hem al
though they long but lytyl to y^ / Ne receive you none opinyon ne fa^tasie ne
synguler co^ceyte vnd color or more holiness as some done that are not wise /
another by thyn own ymagynyng. ne by techyng of none other man. which
contraryeth to the the lest ordinance or general techyng of al holy church.
And over this you shall hope ^tedfastly yt thou art ordened of our lord to be
saved. as one of his chose^ by his mercy / and stire not fro this hope what so
thou herist or see / or what te^ptaco^n thou be in / And though thou think
so ye great a wretch that you were worthy to synke in to hell for that thou
do no good / ne seruest god as thou sholdest do / yet hold the in this
troth and in this hope / and ask mercy^ and al shall be right well / ye and
though all the deuylles of hell apered in bodily lyknes slepyng or wakyng
saye^ge to the that thou sholdest not be saved / or al men living in earth / or
all the angels in heaven / if it might be said to the the same / thou sholdest
not leave hem. ne be stired much fro the hope of saluaco^n This I say to the /
for some be^ so weyke and so simple y^ when they have yeue^ hemself al holy to
serve god after her cunning if they feel any stiryng within by thyncastyng of
the^mye / or else fro without of any of the deuylles prophets which me^
callen sothsayers that they should not be saved / or her state of her manner of
living were not plesau^t to god / they be^ astonyed and stired with such
words / and so for vncu^nyng they fall so^ time in to great heaviness / and as
it were in a dispayr of salvation / wherefore as me think it is spedful to
every creature which by the grace of our lord ^hu^ christ is in full will to
forsake syn^e / and as clerly as his conscience tellith him he suffers no
dedely syn^e rest in him that he ne shryueth him soon thereof. and meke him to
the sacraments of holy church / for to have a trust of saluaco^n / And much
more than they that yeue^ hem holy to god. and fleen venyal sins after her
might / And on ye contrary wise as peryllous it is to him which lies
wyttyngly in dedely syn^e for to have trust of salvation / and in hope of ye
trust will not forsake his syn^e ne low him truly to god and holy church /

How a stable intent is needful to thise that should plese god / and descreco^n
in bodily works / Ca xxii.
THe iii. thing which is nedeful to the for to have in thy begyn^yng. is an
hole and a stable ente^co^n. that is for to saey / A hole will and a desire
only for to plese god / for that is charity / without which al is naught that
you do And thou shall set thyn intent always for to search and traueyle how
thou might plese him. no time for to cesse wylfully of good ocupaco^n other
bodily or ghostly / Ne thou shall not set a time in thy heart. as thus long you
would serve god. and sithe^ to suffer thin heart wylfully fall down into vayn
thoutes and idle ocupacio^s / wenyng that it were nedful for saui^g of thy
bodily kind: leuynge the keeping of thy heart and good ocupaco^n. sekyng a rest
and comfort for a time outward by thy bodili wits. or inwardli vanitees. as
it were for recreaco^n of thy spirit / for it should be more sharper afterward
to ghostly traueyle / for I trow it is not soth / I say not that thou may in
deed perform thyn intent. for oftsithes thy bodily need. etyng drynking
slepyng and spekyng / and the freiltee of thy flessh^ shall let the be thou
never so besye / and hinder the / But I would that thy will and thy intent were
always hole to traueyle ghostly or bodily. and no time to be idle / but always
liftyng up thy heart by desire to god and to the bliss of heaven whether you ete
or drink. or oni other bodily trauelle that thou use: asmoche as you may
wylfully leave it not / For if thou have this intent it shall make y^ ever quick
and sharp in thy traueyle / And if you fall by freilte or neclige^ce in any
idle ocupaco^n or vainspeche it shall smite upon thy heart sharply as a prycke
and make y^ for to yrke and be weary of al vanytees / and for to torn again
hastly to inward thynkyng of Ihu^ christ. or to some good ocupaco^n / For anence
thy bodily kind it is good for to use descrecion in etyng drynkyng and
slepyng^ and in all manner bodily penance. and in long prayer by speech / or in
bodily feli^g by great fervor of deuoco^n other in weeping or such other /
and also in ymaginyng of the spirit wha^ a man felyth no grace / ^n al thise
works it is good to keep descreco^n / for the mean is the best / But in
destruyng of syn^e by keeping of thin heart. and in co^tynuel desire of virtues.
and the bliss of heaven / and for to have the ghostly knowing and the loving of
Ihu^ christ hold you no mean / For the more that it is of this the better it
is / For you shall hate syn^e and all flesshly loves and dredes in thyn heart
without seesyng. And thou shall love virtues and clen^es: and desire hem
without styntyng if thou might / I say not that it is nedfull to saluaco^n /
but I hope it is spdeful. and if thou keep it thou shall profit more in one
year in virtues than you shall without this profit in vii. years /

Of a lityl rehersyng of things said before / and of making of offryng that
should be offryd to god / Caplm xxiii.
NOw I have told the first of end which thou shall behold in thy desire /
and draw toward it as nygh as thou may / Also I have said the of the begyn^yng
what y^ needs for to have / as mekenes siker troth / and an hole intent to
god / upon the which ground thou shall set thy ghostly house by prayer and
by meditaco^n and other ghostly virtues / Then^e say I to the thus / pray thou
or think thou. or oni other deed that thou do good by grace / or bad by
thyn own freilte / or what that thou felist see or herest: smellest or save
rest wythoutforth in thy bodily wits / or within in ymaginaco^n knowing or
felyng in thy reso^ / bring it all within y^ troth and the rules of holy
church / and cast al in ye mortar of mekenes / and break it small with the
pestell of dread of god / and through the powder of all this in the fire of
desire / and offer it so to god / and I tell y^ forsooth well shall that offryng
like in the syghte of thy lord Ihu^ / and sweet shall the smoke of that fire
smelle to the face of thy lord Ihesu / This is for to say / Draw all this
that thou felyst within the truth of holy church. and break thyself in
mekenes / And offer the desire of thyn heart oonly to thy lord Ihu^ for to have
him and naught else but him / And if thou do thus / I hope by the grace of
christ thou shall never be overcome by thyn enmye / This taught us saint poul
when he said thus / Sieve manducatis sieve bibitis. sieve quicquid aliud facitis.
1: cor ^0.
oi^a in nomine dn^i facite / whether ye ete or drink / or what manner of deed
that ye do / all do ye in the name of our lord Ihu^ christ / forsakynge
yourself / and offer it up to him / Means which thou shall most use as I
have before said arne prayer and meditacyon / First I shall show the a lityll
of prayer / and after of meditaco^n

Of prayer that is spedeful to get clennes of heart and virtues / Caplm xxiiii.
PRayer is profit and spedfull to use for to get clen^es of heart by
destroyeng of syn^e and receyuyng of virtues / Not that thou sholdest by thy
prayer make our lord know what thou desyrest For he knows well enough what
the needs / but for to make the able and ready by thy prayer that thou might
receive as a clean vessel. the grace yt our lord will freely give to the /
which grace may not be felt till thou be as said and purifyed by the fire of
desire in devout prayer. For though it be so that prayer is not the cause for
which our lord yeueth grace / nevertheless it is a way by the which grace
freely yeuen comyth to a soul /

How men should pray / and whereon the point of her thought shall be set in
prayer / Caplm xxv.
But now desire thou perauenture for to know how thou sholdest pray / And
upon what thing thou should set the point of thy thought in thy prayer / And
also what prayer were best for the for to use / As to the first I answer and
say thus / That when thou art wakenyd of thy sleep / and ready for to pray.
thou shall feel thyself flesshly and heavy ever dou^warde to vayn thoughts.
other of dremes or fa^tasyes or of vnskylful besines of the world or of thy
flessh^ / Then^e behouyth the for to quycken thyn heart by prayer / and styre
it as much as thou may to some deuoco^n / And in thy prayer that thou set not
thyn heart in any bodily thing / but al thy traueyle shall be for to draw in
thought fro beholding of all bodily thing / that thy desire might be as it
were nakyd and bare fro al erthly things / ever upward styeng unto Ihu^ christ.
whom you may never see bodily as he is in his godhede. ne by bodily lyknes in
ymagynacio^ / But you may through devout and co^tinuel beholding of the mekenes
of his precious ma^hede feel the godenes and the grace of his godhede: wha^ thy
desire is eased and helped and as it were made free fro al flesshly thoughts
and afecco^ns. and is much lift up by ghostly might in to ghostly savor and
delight in him of his ghostly prese^ce^ and hold therein much of the time of
thy prayer so that thou have no great mind of erthly thing / or else the
mind greueth y^ but lityl / if you can pray thus / then^e can thou pray well /
For prayer is naught else but a styenge desire of the heart in to god: by
wythdrawyng of the heart fro al erthly thoughts / And so is prayer lykned to a
fire / which of his own kind leueth ye lowenes of the earth / and always
styeth up in to thayer Right so desire in prayer wha^ it is towchid and
lightened of the ghostly fire which is god. it is ever vpstyeng to him that it
came fro /

Of the fire of love / Caplm xxvi.
A^ men yt speke^ of the fire of love known not well what it is / for what it
is I can not tell ye. save this I may tell y^: that it is neither bodily. ne
bodily felyd / A soul may feel it in prayer or in deuoco^n. which soul is
in ye body / but he felith it not with no bodily wit / For though it be so
y^ it work in a soule^ ye body may torn in to an hete / and as it were
chauffyd for likyng traueyle of y^ spirit / Netheles y^ fire of love is not
bodily. for it is only in ye ghostly desire of ye soul This is no dowte to
no man or woman that felith deuoco^n / But some be^ simple and wene by cause
it is called fire yt it should be hot as bodily fire is / and for thy I say yt
I have said

That the certain prayer in speech ordened of god and of holy church is best to
hem that been new turned to god and to deuoco^n / Caplm xxvii.
NOw as to ye other. for to know what prayer were best for to use / I shall say
as me think / Thou shall vndstonde that there be^ iii. manner of prayers The
first is prayer of speech made specially of god. as is the pater nost: and made
also more generally by thordynau^ce of holy church. as matins eue^song and
hours. And also made by devout men of other special saye^ges as to our lord
and to our lady / and to his sai^tes / As to this manner of prayer which is
callid vocal me thinks unto the that art religious and by custom and rule
art bound for to say mateyns and hours I hold it most spedeful for to say
hem as devoutly as you may / For when thou say thy mateyns / you say also
thy pater nost pri^cipally and other more / For to styre the to more deuoco^n
was it ordened for to say also psalms and ympnes and such other which be^
made by the holy ghost as ye pater nost is / And therefore you shall not say hem
hastily and rechelesly as thou were evil apayd that you art bound with hem /
but thou shall gader thyn affecco^n and thy thought for to say hem more sadly
and more devoutly than any other special prayer of deuoco^n. trowyng forsooth
that since it is ye prayer of holy church / there is no prayer so profitable
to ye which is vocal forto use comynly as y^ is. And so shall you put away al
heaviness / and by grace you shall turn thy need in to a good will: and thy bond
in to a great fredom. y^ it shall no lettyng be to the of ghostly ocupaco^n.
And after this you may if thou will use other. as thy pater nost. or any such
other. and of thise in the which you felest most savor and most ghostly
comfort in / y^ hold I best to ye. this manner of prayer is spedful comynly to
every man in ye begyn^ing of his conversion for to use most of any other
ghostly ocupaco^n / For a man in the begyn^yng is rude and boystous and
flesshly but if he have the grace / and can not think no ghostly thoughts in
meditaco^n. for his soul is not yet cle^sed fro old syn^e / and therefore I
hope it is most spedful for to use this manner of prayer / as for to say his
pat noster and his aue: and to read upon his sawter / and such other / For he
y^ can not ren^e lightly by ghostly prayer. for his fete of knowing and of
loving be^ seek for syn^e, him needs to have a siker staff for to hold him by
/ This staff is special prayer of speech ordened by god and holy church in
help of men^is souls / By y^ which prayer the soul of a flesshly man that
is always falling dou^warde into worldly thoughts and flesshly affecco^ns shall
be lift up fro hem and beholde^ by it as by a staff. fed with sweet words of
the prayer as a child wc milk / and ruled by it that he fall not in to
errors ne fa^tasyes by his vayn meditaco^ns / For in this manner of prayer is
no deceyte who so will steadfastly and mekely traueyle therein /

What peril is to men yt in the begyn^yng of her tornyng to god leueth the
common prayer of thordynau^ce of holy church / and yeuen hem to medytaco^n*
Caplm xxviii.
THen^e may you see by this that thise men if any be such yt in the begyn^yng
of her conversion or soon after when they have felt a lityl ghostly comfort
other in deuocio^ or in knowing and are not yet stabled therein: they leave such
prayer vocal tosone and other bodily exercise. and give hem holy to meditacion
they be^ not wise / For often sithes in her rest for her meditacyo^s they ymagyn
and think on ghostly things after her own wytt and follow her bodily felyng /
and have not yet received grace thereto: and therefore they by vndescreco^n often
sithes ouertraueyle her wittes^ and breke^ her bodily might. and so they fall
in to fantasies and syngler co^ceytes or in opyn errors: and lette^ ye grace
that god yeuith he^ by such vanitees. ye cause of all this is a prive pride of
hemself. as wha^ they have felt a lityl grace they wene it so much passing
other yt they fall in vaynglory. and so they lose it / ^f they wist how lityl
it were that they feel in regard of that y^ god yeuith or may give. they should
be ashamyd to speak out thereof. but it were in great need / Of this manner of
prayer by speech. spekith david in ye sawter thus / Voce mea ad dn^m clamaui.
P^ xiiii.
voce mea ad dn^m dep^catus sum / ^oo david the prophet for to styre other men
to pray both with heart and with mouth said / with my voys I cried to god. and
with my speech I besought our lord /

Of the ii. manner of prayer that is in speech not certain. but folowith the
stiryng of deuoco^n / Caplm xxix
THe ii. manner of prayer is by speech / but it is not of any certain special
saye^g / And this is wha^ a man or a woman felith grace of deuoco^n by the yeft
of god. and in his deuoco^n spekith to him. as he were bodily in his presence
with such words as acordeth most to his stiryng for the time. and as comyth
to his mind after diverse rewards which he felith in his heart / either
rehersyng his sins and his wretchydnes. or ye malice and the sleyghtes of the
enmye / or else the mercy and y^ goodness of god / And with that he cries with
desire of hert^ and with speech of mouth to our lord for socour and for help.
as a man that were in peril among his enmyes. or in siknes showing his sores
to god as to a leche / saye^g as david said: P^ c. i^^.
^ripe me de inimicis meis deus meus / A lord deliver me of mine enmyes / Or
else thus / Sana ai^am mea^ qr peccaui tibi / A lord hele my soul. P^ xl.
for I have syn^ed against the / Or such other as comith to mind. And also him
thinkith so much godenes and grace and mercy in god that him likyth with
great affection of ye heart for to love him and thank him by such words and
psalms as acordeth to ye loving and praising of god. as david said Co^fitemini
dn^o qm^ bonus. qm^ in scl mi^a eius. P^
Love ye and praise our lord. for he is good / and by such other as he is
stired to say

That the ii. manner of prayer pleseth much god. and makith a man to have him
in body as he were dronke / and makith him in soul to be won^ded with the
sword of love / Cplm xxx
THis manner of prayer much pleseth god. for it is oonly of ye affeccio^ in the
heart / and therefore it goth never vnsped without some grace / this prayer
lo^geth to the ii. part of conte^placo^n as I have said before / who soo^ has
this yeft of god ferue^tly / him behouyth for the time to flee presence and
company of al men: and to be alone that he be not let / who so have it
hold it while he may / for it may not long last in the fervor For if grace
come ple^teuously. it is traueylous wondfully to the spirit: though it be
likyng / And it is much wasting to ye bodily kind who so much use it / For
it makith the bodi if grace come myghtly for to styre and turn here and there
as a man that were mad or dro^ken and cowde have no rest / this is a point
of the passion of love / the which by great violence and maistry brekith down
al lusts and likings of any erthly thing / and it wou^deth the soul with
the blisful sword of love. that the body falls down and may not bear it This
touching is of so great might that the most vicyous or flesshli man lyuinge in
earth: if he were well towched ones myghtly with this sharpelswerde / he should
be right sad and sobre a great while after: and loathe all the lusts and
likings of his flesh: and al erthly thiges which he had most delight in /

How the fire of love wastes al flesshly lusts / as other fire wastyth bodily
things / Caplm xxxi.
OF this manner of feeling spekith the prophet Ieremye thus. Tren^^
Et factus est in cord meo quasi ignis estua^s claususque in ossibus meis. and
defeci far no^ sustine^s / This is thus much for to vndstonde The love and
the felyng of god was made in my heart not fire / but as fire glowyng / For as
bodily fire brenneth and wastes al bodily thing where it comith / Right so
ghostly fire / as is the love of god brenneth and wastes all flesshly loves
and likings in a man's soul / And this fire is stokyn in my bones / as the
prophet says of himself: That is for to say / This love fulfyllith the might
of my soule^ as mind reason and will of grace and ghostly swetnes / as marow
fyllith full the bone. and that within. and not without in ye wits Nevertheless
it is so mighty within that it smyteth out in to the body and makith all the
body quake and tremyse / It is sofer tro the bodily kind and so uncouth that
he can no skyll on it. and may not bear it / but faylith and fallyth down as
the prophet says / And therefore our lord temperith it. and with drawyth the
fervor: and suffers the heart to fall in to a sobirte of more softnes / who
can pray thus often. he spedyth soon in his traueyle / He shall get more of
virtues in a lityl time tha^ some man without this or a another as good shall
get in long time. for all ye bodily penance that he might do / And who has
this. it needs not for to charge ye bodily kind with more penance than it
berith / if he have it often /

Of the third manner of prayer that is only in the heart without speech
outward / Caplm xxxii
THe iii. manner of prayer is only in the heart without speech by great rest
and softnes of the body and of the soul / A clean heart him behooves to have
that shall pray well thus For it is of such men and wym^en that by long
traueylle bodily and ghostly / or else by such sharp smytinges of love as I
have before said comen in to rest of spirit / so that her affeccion is
turned in to ghostly savor / that they mow nygh contynuelly pray in her
heart / and love and praise god without great lettyng of temptaco^ns or of
vanytees. as I have before said in the second part of contemplacyon / Of this
manner of prayer says saint poul thus / Nam si orem lingua: spiritus meus orat.
men's autem mea sine fructu est^ Quid ergo? Cor^ xiiii.
Orabo and spiritu orabo and mente^ psallam spiritu psallam and mente That is
to say / if I pray with my tongue only by ye will of spirit and by traueyle
/ ye prayer is medeful. but my soul is not fed / For it felyth not the fruit
of ghostly swetnesse by understanding / What shall I then do says saint
poul / And he answerith and says / I shall pray by traueyle and desire of the
spirit / And I shall pray also more Inwardly in my spyrite without traueyle
in ghostly savor and swetnes of ye love and the sight of god / by the which
sight and felyng of love my soul is fed / Thus as I vndstonde saint poul
cowde pray / Of this manner of prayer spekith our lord in holy writ by
figure thus / Ignis in altari meo se^per ardebit. and cotidie sacerdos surgens
mane subiciet ligna vt ignis no^ extinguat / Leuit. 6.
This is for to say / The fire of love shall ever be light in the soul of a
devout and clean man or woman / the which is the awter of our lord / And the
pressed shall every day at morn lay to styckes and norysshe the fire / That is
to say / This man shall by holy psalms: clean thoughts. and fervent desire
norysshe the fire of love in his heart that it goo not out in any time / This
rest our lord ye^yth to some of his servants as it were a reward of her
traueyle. and a shadow of the love which they shall have in the bliss of
heaven /

How men should do that been traueyled with vain thoughts in her prayers /
Caplm xxxiii^
But now see thou that I speak over hye to the in this manner of prayer / for
it is no maystry to me for to say it / but for to do it there is the maystry
/ Thou say that you can not pray thus deuoutli ne so holy in heart as I
speak of For when thou would have the mind of thyn heart upward to god in
thy prayer. thou felyst so many thoughts in vein of thyn own deeds before
done or what thou shall do / and of other men^es deeds / and such many other
/ lettyng and tarye^g the so that thou may another feel savor ne rest ne
deuoco^n in thy saying / and oftsithes the more thou traueilest to keep thyn
heart: the ferder it is fro the: and the hardersomtyme fro the begyn^yng to the
last end: that the think it is but lost all that thou do / And unto this
that thou say that I speak to hie to the of prayer / I grant well that I
speak otherwise than I can or may do / Nevertheless I say it for this intent /
that you sholdest know how we ought to pray if we did well / And sithen we may
not do so / that we know then^e our feebleness mekely^ and cry god mercy / Our
lord bad thus hymsel wha^ he said / Diliges dn^m deu^ tuu^ ex toto cord tuoex
tota aia tua. M^ xxii.
and ex oibus viribus tuis / Thou shall love god of al thyn heart and al thy
soul. and al thy might / It is impossible to any man for to fulfylle this
biddyng so fully as it is said. living in earth / And yet nevertheless our
lord bad us for to love so for this intent as saint bernarde says / that we
should know thereby our feebleness / and then mekely cry after mercy / and we
shall have it / Nevertheless I shall tell ye as me thynkith in this askyng / when
thou shall pray make thin intent and thy will in the begyn^yng as hole and as
clean to god as thou may shortly in thy mind / and then^e begyn^e and do as
thou may. And though you be never somoche let against thy first will. be
not adrad: ne to angry with thyself / ne inpacye^t against god: that he yeueth
the not the savor and ghostly swetnes with deuoco^n as the thinks that he
yeueth to other creatures / But see thereby thyn own feebleness: and bear it
easily / holdi^g in thyn own sight thyn own prayer feeble as it is with
mekenes of heart / trustyng also sikerly in the mercy of our lord that he shall
make it good and profitable to the more than thou know or felest / For wite
thou well that thou art exscused of thy debt: and thou shalt have mede for it
as for an other good deed yt thou do in charity though thyn heart were not
thereupon in the doing / Therefore do that longs to the. and suffer our lord
to give what he will: and teache him not And though thou think thyself recheles
and neclygent / and as thou were in great defawte for such things /
Nevertheless yet shall thou for this defawte and all other venyals which may
not be eschewed in this wretchyd life lift up thyn heart to god / knowlegyng thy
wretchydnes / and cry mercy with a good trust of foryeuenes and strive no
more therewith: ne hang no longer thereupon as thou would by maistry not feel
such wretchidnes / ^eue of and goo to some other good deed bodily or ghostly /
and think for to do better a another time / But though thou fall on a another
time in the same. ye an hundred times / ye a thousand times / yet do as I
have said: and all shall be well / Ferder more a soul that never may find
rest of heart in prayer / but all her life time is striuyng with her thoughts
and taryeth and trowbleth with hem / if she keep her in mekenes and charity in
other sides / she shall have full much mede in heaven for her good traueyle /

Of meditaco^n of synful men after that they ben hooli turned to god / Caplm
xxxiiii.
Now of meditaco^n shall I tell yt a lityll as me thinks Thou shall vndstonde
that in meditaco^ns may no certain rule well be set every man for to keep / for
they are in free yeft of our lord after the diverse disposynges of chosen sowles
/ and after the state that they ben in / And also after yt they profyten in
virtues and in her astate. so he increases her meditaco^ns both in ghostly
knowing and loving of him. For who so is ever ylike wise in knowing of god and
ghostly things it semyth that he wexeth but a lityl in the love of god / and
that may be showed opinly in thapostles. wha^ they in ye day of pe^tecost were
fulfilled with bren^yng love of ye holy ghost. they were made neither foles ne
foltis / but they were made wonder wise both in knowing and spekyng of god and
of ghostly things / asmoche as a man might have in flesh living / Thus
spekyth holy writ of hem / Repleti su^t oe^s sp^u scto^. et ceperu^t loqui
magnalia dei / They were fulfilled of the holy ghoost / and they began to speak
the great merueyles of god / And all that knowing they had by rauisshyng in
love of the holy ghost / Diverse meditacyons there ben / which our lord
puts in a man's heart. Some shall I tell the as me thynkith for this intent
/ If thou feel any of hem that you sholdest ye better traueyle in hem / In the
beginning of conversion of such a man that has be much foiled with worldly
or flesshely sins / comynly his thought is most upon his sins with great
compunccion and sorrow of heart / with great wepynges and many teres of the eye
/ mekely and besely asking merci and for yeuenes of god for hem / And if he be
towchyd sharply for our lord will make him soon clean / him shall think that
his sins are ever in his sight so foul and so horrible that uneath shall he
mow bear himself / And though he shryue him never so clerly / yet shall he find
fightyng and fretyng and bitynge of his conscience that him shall think that
he is not shriuen right / And uneath shall he mow have any rest / in somoche
that he should not endure such traueyle ne were it that our lord of his mercy
comfort him sometime as he will by great deuoco^n of his passion or of some
other as he will give it. Upon this manner werketh our lord in some men^es
hertes more or less as he will / And all this is the great mercy of our lord
that not oonly will foryeue the sin or the trespase / but he will both
forgive the trespase and the pain for it in purgatory for such a lityl pain
here of bityng of conscience / And also if he will dispose a man to receive any
special yefte of the love of god / him behouyth first to be scowred and
cleansed by such a fire of compuncco^n for all the great sins before done / Of
this manner traueylle spekith david in many places of the sawter / and specially
in the psalm Miserere mei deus / P^ l.


That the meditaco^n of the manhede of christ or of his passion is yeuen freely
of the holy ghost / And how it shall be known when it is yeuen / Caplm xxxv.
ANd then sometime after this traueyle. and sometime with all. such a man or
else a another the which by grace of god has be kept in Innoce^ce / our lord
yeuith a meditaco^n of his manhede / as of his birth or of his passo^n. and of
the compassyon of our lady saint mary / when this medytaco^n is made by the
holy ghost / then it is right profitable and gracyous / And that thou shall
wite by this token / When it is so that thou art styred to a meditaco^n in god
/ and thy thought is suddenly drawn out fro all worldly and flesshly things
and the thinks as thou see in thy soul thy lord Ihu^ in a bodily lyknes
as he was in earth / and how he was taken of the Jews and bounden as a theyf /
beten and dispysed. scourged and demid to death / How lowely he bare the cross
upon his back and how cruelly he was neyled thereupon / Also of the crown of
thorns upon his head / and of the sharp spear that stykked him to the heart /
and thou in this ghostly sight felyst thyn heart styred to so great compassion
and pity of thy lord Ihesu ye thou mornest and wepest and criest with all the
myghtes of thy body and of thy soul / wo^deryng the goodness and the love. the
pacyence and the mekenes of thy lord Ihu^ / that he would for so sifull a
caytif as thou art suffer so much pain / And nevertheless thou felist
somoche goodness and mercy in our lord that thyn heart ryseth up in to a love
and a gladness of him with many sweet teres: having great trust of foryeuenes of
thy sins and of salvation of thy soul by the virtue of this precious passion
/ That when the mind of crystis passion or any point of his manhede is thus
made in thyn heart by such a ghostly syghte / with deuowte affecco^n answeryng
thereto / wit you well then that it is not of thyn own werkyng. ne feynynge
of no wyckid spirit / but by the grace of the holy ghost For it is an openyng
of the ghostly eye in to crystis manhede And it may be called the flesshly
love of god / As saint bernarde callith it / Bern^:
In as much as it is set in the flesshly kind of christ / And it is right
good and a great help in destroyeng of great sins / and a good way to come
to wertues / and so after to contemplacyon of the godhede / For a man shall not
come to ghostly light in contemplacyon of crystis godhede / but if he come
first in ymagynaco^n by bitterness and by compassion / and by steadfast thynkyng
of his manhede / Thus saint poul did / First he said thus / Nichil indicaui me
scire inter vos. nisi ih^m xp^m et hunc crucifixum / I showed you right naught
that I couth^ p^^ cor. 6*
but Ihesu christ. and him crucified / As if he had said / My knowing and my
trust is oonly in ye passion of christ / And therefore said he thus also / Michi
aute^ absit gloriari nisi in cruce dn^i nostri ihu^ cristi / Gal. 9*
Forbode^ be fro me all manner of Joy and likyng but in ye cross and in the
passion of our lord Ihesu christ / And nevertheless afterward he said thus /
Predicamus vobis xp^m dei virtutem and dei sapiencia^ / As who says / First I
preached of the manhede and the passion of christ / Now I preche to you of the
godhede. p^^ cor. ^*
As thus / That christ is the might of god / and the endless wysdom of god /

That the meditacyon of the passion of christ is wythdrawen fro hem that it is
yeuen to often sythes for diverse causes / Caplm xxxvi.
THis manner of meditaco^n a man has not always wha^ he would / but when our
lord will give it / Unto some men and wymmen he yeuyth it all their life time
by sythes when he vysyteth hem / As some men arne so tender in her affection
that when they here men speak / or else that they thynken of his precious
passion. her hertes melten in devotion / and arne fed and comforted against
all manner temptacyons of the enmye / And that is a great yeft of god / To some
men he yeueth it first plenteuously / and afterward he with draws it for
diverse causes Other if a man wexe proud of it in his own sight / or for some
other sin / by the which he makith himself unable for to receive the grace
/ Or else our lord wythdrawyth it / and all other deuocyons sometime fro a man
or a woman / for he will suffer him to be assayd by temptacyons of his enmye /
And so will he dyspose a man for to know and feel himself more ghostly / For
he said so himself to his discyples / ^xpedit vobis vt ego vadam / Si enim no^
abiero: Ioh^^ 16.
peraclitus non veniet ad vos / It is spedefull to you that I goo fro you
bodily / For if I goo not the holy ghost may not come to you / For as long as
he was with hem they loved him much / but it was flesshly in his manhede / And
therefore it was spedefull to hem that he should wythdrawe the bodily form fro
her sight / that the holy ghost might come to hem / and teache hem for to love
him and know him more ghostly / as he did on the day of pentecost. Right so
it is spedefull to some that our lord wythdrawe a lityl the bodily and the
flesshly liknes fro theye of the soul that the heart might be set and fyxed
more besily in ghostly desire / and sekyng of his godhede /

Of diverse temptaco^ns of the fend / Caplm xxxvii.
Nevertheless it behouith a man to suffer many temptacions first / And these
temptacyo^s fallen oftsythes to some men and wymmen after when comfort is
wythdrawen / upon diverse manners by malice of the enmye / As thus. when the
devil perceyueth devotion much wythdrawen. that the soul is left as it were
nakyd for a time / then sends he to some men temptaco^ns of lechery of
glotenye. so hot and so brennyng / that hem shall think that they felyd
never none so grievous in all her life time before when they yaaf hem most to
sin. In so much that they shall think it impossyble for to stand long and
suffer that they ne shall needs fall but they have help / And therefore have
they then much sorrow / both for lackyng of comfort and deuoco^n which
they were wont to have / And they have much dread of falling fro god by such
open sins / And all this werkyth the devil at the suffraunce of god for to
done hem forthynke her good pourpoos / and turn again to sin as they were
wont to do / But who so will abide awhyle and suffer a lityll pain / and
not turn again to sin for no thing the hand of our lord is full nere /
and helpyth right soon For he kepyth him full sykerly / and the man wot not
how as the prophet david says in the person of our lord. Cum ip^o sum in
tribulaco^ne. P^ 9^.
eripiam eu^ and glorificabo eum / I am with him in his trybulaco^n / and in
temptacyon I shall deliver him / and I shall make him glorious in my bliss /
Some men he tempts by ghostly sins malicyously. as by mystrowyng of the
faith or of the sacrament of our lordis blessed body / Also of despeyr or of
blasphemy in our lord or oni of his saints / or lothynge of her life / or
bitterness or unskillful heaviness / or of tomoche dread of hemself and of her
bodi if they put hem holy to goddis seruyse / Some men he tempts also. and
namly solitary men and wymmen by dredes and vglynes. and quakynges and
shakynges / either apperynge to hem in bodily lyknes or else in ymagyning
slepynge and wakyng / And taryeth hem so that uneath may they have any rest.
And also on many other wyses he tempts. moo than I can or may say /

Of diverse remedies against temptaco^ns of the fend Caplm xxxviii.
Emedie to such men and wymmen that arn thus traueyled. or any otherwise. may
be this / First that they will put all her trust in our lord Ihu^ christ / and
bring to mind often his passion: and the peynes that he suffered for us / and
that they then trow steadfastly that all sorrows and traueyle that they
suffer in such temptacyons / which to an vncunnyng man semyth a forsakyng of
