god / That it is no repreuyng ne no forsakynge / but assayenge for her better
/ Either for clensyng of her sins before done / or for great encreasynge of
her mede and disposyng to much grace / if they will suffer a while / and
stand fast that they torn not again wylfully to sin / A another remedy is.
that they dread not ne charge not as for a sin. ne set not at heart such
malicyous stirynges of dispeyre or of blasphemye or of the sacrament. or any
such other that were ugly for to here / For the feeling of these temptacio^s
fyleth the soul no more than if they herd an hou^de berke. or a flee byte /
They tarie^ the soul / but they apeyre not the soul if a man will dispyse
hem. and set hem at naught / For it is not good for to strive with hem for to
put he^ out by maystry / For the more that they strive with such thoughts.
the more they cleue to hem / And therefore they shallen as much as they may
draw out the thought fro hem / and set it to some other ocupaco^n / And yet
if they will ever hang upon hem / then it is good to hem that they be not
angri ne heavy to feel hem / but with a good trust in god bear hem as it were a
bodily pain and a scourge of our lord for clensynge of her sins. as long
as he will for his love / as he was scourged and bare the cross for her love /
And over this it is good to hem for to show her hertes to some wise man in the
beginning before they ben roted in the heart / and that they leave her own wit
and follow the counseyle of him / And that they show hem not lightly to none
vncunnyng or worldly man which never felt such temptaco^ns / For they might
lightly bring a simple sole in to dispeyre by vncu^nynge of hemself / Of these
manner of temptaco^ns by the which a man semyth forsaken of god and is not / In
comfort of hem that arne tempted our lord says thus by his prophet / In
modico dereliqui te. Isa. liiii
and in momento indignaco^nis me percussite / et in miseraco^nibus meis multis
congegabo te / In a lityll I for left the / That is to say. I suffered the for
to be tarried a lityl And in a point of my wrath I smote the. that is to say /
All the penance and the pain that thou suffrest here is but a point of mi
wrath in regard of the pain of hell or of purgatori And yet in my manyfolde
mercies I shall gader together the / when the thinks that thou art forsaken.
then^e shall I of mi great mercy gader ye again to me / For when thou wenyst that
thou art as it were lost: then shall our lord help the as Job says / Cu^
te consumptu^ putaueris: Job xi.
orieris vt lucifer et habebis fiducia^ / That is to say. when thou art
brought so low by traueyle in temptaco^n that the thinks none help ne no
comfort. but as thou were a forloor man / yet stand styfly in hope and pray
god. and sothly thou shall suddenly spring up as the day sterre in gladness of
heart: and have a very trust in god as Job says /

How that god hem that he cheseth he suffers to be tarried and tempted. and
afterward comfort hem. and stableth hem in grace / Caplm xxxix.
ANd also in comfort of such men that they should not dyspeyre in temptacyon.
the wise man says thus of our lord / In temptaco^ne ambulat cu^ eo / In
primis elegit eum. (...) iiii*
ti morem and metu^ and approbaco^nem inducit super illu^. et cruciabit illu^
in tribulaco^ne doctrine sue donec temptet illu^ in cogitaco^ nibus suis. et
credet anime illius. ad iter directu^ adducet illum. and firmabit illu^ and
letificabit illu^ / et denudabit abscondita sua illi: et thezaurisabit super
illu^ sciencia^ and intellectu^ iusticie / This is thus much for to say / The
wise man for he would that no man should dispeyre in temptaco^n. in comfort of
hem saiht thus / In temptaco^n our lord forsakes not a man. but he gooth with
him fro the begyn^yng in to the last end / For he says / first he chesyth
him / And that is when he drawyth a man to him by comfort of devotion / And
afterward sorrow and dread and assayenge he brings upon him And that is /
when he wythdraweth devotion and suffers him to be tempted / And he says that
he turmenteth him in tribulaco^n until he have well assayd him in his
thoughts / And until a man will put all his trust in him fully / And then
after this our lord brings him out in to the right way / and testenyth him
to him and gladeth him / and sythen shewyth him his pyuytees / and yeuyth him
his tresour of knowing and understanding of ryghtwysnes / By these words of
holy writ may thou see that thise temptaco^ns or any other be they never so
ugly. to a man that by grace is in full will to forsake sin arne spedefull
and profitable if he will suffer as he may and abide goddis wyll^ and not
turn again to syn^e which he has forsaken for no sorrow ne pain ne dread
of such temptacyons / but ever stand still in traueyle and in prayer with
good hope / Our lord of his endless goodness having pity and mercy of al his
creatures when he sees time he lays to his hand and smyteth down the devil
and al his power / and eases hem of her traueyle / And puts away all
dredes and sorrows and derkenes out of her hertes / and brings in to her
souls light of grace / and openyth the sight of the soul for to see that all
the traueyle that they had it was spedefull to hem / yeuyng to hem also a new
ghostly might to ayenstonde all the fondynges of the fend / and all dedely
sins without great traueyle / and ledeth hem in to a sadness of good virtues
living / In the which if they ben meke he keeps hem unto her last end / and
then he takes hem all holy to him / This thing I say to the if thou be
tarried or traueyled with any such manner of temptacyons / be not tomoche
adradde / but do as I have said and better if thou may / And I hope by the
grace of Ihesu christ thou shalt never be overcome by thine enmye /

That a man should not give him to ydlenes ne lightly leave the grace yt is yeuen
him of god / Caplm xl
After this when you art escaped such temptacio^s or else our lord has so
kept y^ as he does many by his mercy that thou have not be tarried much with
none such / Then^e it is good to the that thou turn not thy rest in to
ydilnesse For there is many a man that takyth rest upon him to sone But thou
shall yt thou will begin a new game and a new traueyle / And that is for to
enter within in to thyn own soul by medytacion for to know what it is / And
by the knowing thereof to come to the ghostly knowing of god For saint austyn
says / Aug^
By the knowing of myself I shall hete the knowing of god / I say not that it
is nedeful to the and debt for to traueyle so ne to none other man / but he
feel him styred by grace as he were called thereto / For our lord gives diverse
gifts where so he will / not to one man all / ne to al men one / saaf charity
which is common to all men / And therefore if a man or a woman have received a
yefte of god. as devotion in prayer / or in the passion of christ / Or any
other be it never so lityll / leave it not to soon for none other / but if he
feel sothfastly a better / But hold that he has and traueyle therein stably /
ever desiryng a better when god will give it / Nevertheless if that be
wythdrawen somewhat and he sees a better / and felith his heart styred thereto /
Then semith it a calling of our lord to the better / And then it is time
that he follow after for to get it / and fulfylle it as swyftly as he may /

That a man should know the mesure of his gift that he may desire and take a
better when god will give it / Caplm xli.
Our holy faders here before taughten us that we should know the mesure of our
gift / And upon that work not taking upon us by feynyng more than we have in
felinge / We mow ever desire the best / but we mow not ever work ye best. for
we yet have not received that grace / An hou^de that ren^eth after the haar
oonly for he sees other hou^des ren^e when he is weary he rests him or
tourneth him home again But if he run for he sees the haar / he will not
spare for werynes till he have gote^ it / Right so it is ghostly / who so has
grace be it never so lityll / and leuyth wylfully the werking thereof / and
makith himself to traueyle in a another which he has not yet / oonly for he
sees or hereth that other me^ did so / sothly he may run awhyle till he
be weary / And then shall he turn home again / And but he bewaar. he may
hurt his fete by some fantasyes or that he come home But he that werkyth in
such grace as he has / and desires by prayer mekely and lastyngly after more
/ And after felyth his heart styred for to follow the grace which he desired /
he may sykerly run if he keep mekenes / And therefore desire of god as much
as thou may / without mesure or discrecy on of all that longs to his love or
to heaven bliss / For who so can most desire of god / most shall feel of him
/ But werkyth as you may: and cry god mercy for that thou may not / Thus it
semyth saint poul said / Vnusquisque habet donum suu^ a deo. p^ cor vii Ephesians.
iiii p^. cor. ir.
Alius aute^ sic: alius vero sic / Itm^ / Vnicuique nostrum data est gracia
scdm mensura^ donacionis cristi. ^tm^ Diuisiones gra^rum sunt. ^lii datur sermo
sapiencie. alii sermo scie^cie. etc / Itm^. Vt sciamus que a deo donata su^t
nobis Saint poul says that every man has his yefte of god / one thus. and a
another thus / For to every man that shall be saved is yeuen a grace after the
mesure of crystis yeft / And therefore it is spedefull that we know the yeftes
which arn yeuen us of god that we might work in hem / for by those we shall
be saved as some by bodily works: and by deeds of merci / some by great bodily
penance / some by sorrow and weeping for her sins all her life time / some by
prechyng and techyng / some by diverse graces and yeftes of deuoco^n shall be
saaf and come to bliss /

That a man should traueyle to know his owoe soul and the myghtes thereof / and
break down the ground of sin therein / Caplm xlii.
Nevertheless there is one work which is needful and spedefull to traueyle in
/ And I hope an high plain way as much as may be in man's work to
contemplaco^n / And that is a man for to enter in to himself for to knoew his
own soul / and ye myghtes thereof / The fayrnes and the towlnes of it / In
this Inward beholdynge thou shalt mow see the worship and the dignyte which
it should have by kind of the first making / And thou shall see the
wretchydnes and the myscheyf which thou art fall in for sin And of this
syghte shall come a desire with great longing in thyn heart for to recover again
that dignite and worshypp^ which thou have lost / Also thou shall feel a
lothyng and a grysyng of thyself with a great will for to distroye and bear
down thyself and all things that letten the fro that dygnyte and that Joy /
This is a ghostly traueylle hard and sharp in the beginning who so will
quyckely traueyle therein / For it is a traueyle in the soul against the ground
of all sins lytill and much. which ground is naught else but a falls
mysruled love of man to himself / Out of this love as saint austyn says
spryngeth all manner of sin dedely and venyall. And sothly until this ground
be well rasaken and deep doluyn / and as it were nere dried up by outcastyng of
al flesshly and worldly dredes and loves / a soul may never feel ghostly the
brennyng love of Ihesu christ / ne have the homlynes of his gracyous presence /
ne have clear sight of ghostly things by light of understanding / This is the
traueyle that a man behooves to draw his heart and his mind fro the flesshly
love and the likyng of all erthly creatures / fro vayn thoutes and fro fleshly
ymagynaco^ns. and out fro the love and the vicyous felyng of himself / that the
soul shall mow no rest find in no flesshly thoughts / ne erthely
affection / Then in as much as the soul may not find his ghostly rest in
the love and in the sight of Ihu^ Christ / it behouyth nedelynges suffer pain /
This traueylle is somdelyche streyte and narrow / And nevertheless I hope it is
the way which christ teched to hem y^ would be his perfyte lovers in the gospel
saying thus / Conte^dite intrare per angusta^ portam / qm^ arta est via que
ducit ad vita^. Luc. xiii^
et pauci inueniu^t ea^ / Strive ye for to enter by a strayte yate / for the
way y^ ledeth to heaven is narow and few men fyndeth it / And how streyte this
way is our lord tells in a another place thus / Si quis vult venire post me
abneget semetip^m and toliat cruce^ sua^ and sequatur me / Itm^: M^ xvi.
Qui odit ai^am sua^ in hoc mu^do / in vitam eternal custodit ea^ / That is to
say / who so will come after me / forsake himself and hate his own soul.
That is to say / Forsake all flesshly love and hate his own flesshely life /
and vain likyng of al his bodily wits for love of me And take ye cross /
That is to say / Suffer the pain of this a while / and then^e follow me /
that is to say. in contemplaco^n of my manhede and of my godhede / This is a
strayte way and a narow that no bodily thing may pass thorugh it / for it
is a sleeng of all syn^e as saint poul says / Col. iii.
Mortificate me^ bra vestra que su^t super terra^ / immu^dicia^ libidine^
concupiscencia^ malam / Slay your members upon earth / not the members of the
body but of the soul / as uncleanness lust and unskillful love to yourself and
to erthely things / Therefore as thy traueyle has been here before for to
ayensto^de bodily sins and open temptaco^ns of the enmye as it were fro
without. right so the behouyth now in this ghostly work within thyselfe for
to destroy and break the ground of syn^e in thiself asmoche as thou may / And
that thou might the more redily bring it about / I shall tell the as me
thynkyth

How a man shall know the worthiness and the worship of his soul that it had
first of / And what wretchydnes and myscheif it is fall in for sin / Caplm
xliii.
THe soul of a man is a life made of three myghtes / mind reason and will. to
the image and the liknes of the blessed trinyte / In as much as the mind was
made mighty and steadfast by the virtue of the fader almyghtihode. for to hold
him without foryetyng. distractyng or lettyng of any creature / And so it has
lyknes of the fad / The reason was made bright and clear without error or
derknes as perfytly as a soul in a body vnglorifyed might have. And so it
has the liknes of the sone / which is endless wysdom / And the love and the
will was made clean brennyng in to god without bestly love of the flesh or
of any creature by the souereyne godenes of god the holy ghost / And so it
has the lyknes of the holy ghost. which is blessid love / so that a man's
soul which may be called a made trinyte was fulfilled in mind: sight and
love of the unmade most blessed trynite which is our lord / This is the
dignyte the state and the worship of a man's soul by kind of the first
making / This state thou had in adam before the first sin of man. But when
adam sin^ed chesyng love and delight in himself and in creatures / he lost all
his worship and his dignyte. and thou also in him. and fell fro that blessed
trinyte in to a foul derke wretchyd trinyte. that is in to foryetyng of god /
and unknowing of him / and in to a bestly likynge of himself / And that
skilfully / For as david says in the sawter / Homo cu^ in honor esset no^
intellerit: co^peratus est iumentis insipientibus and silis factus est illis /
Psalm^
A man when he was in worship he knew it not / And therefore he lost it and was
made like a best / See now then^e the wretchydnes of thy soul / For as the
mind was sometime stablyd in god / right so now it has forgoten him / and
sekyth his rest in creatures: now from one to an another / and never may find
full rest / For he has lost him in whom is full rest / And right so it is
of reason / and the love also / which was clean in ghostly savor and swetnes
/ now it is tornyd in to a foul bestly lust and likyng in it self. and in
creatures / and in flesshly savors both in the wits as in gloteny and
lechery / and in ymagynyng / as in pride vaynglory and couetyse / In somoche
that thou may uneaths do any good deed / but if thou be defoyled with
vaynglory / Ne thou may not well use none of thy v. wits clenly in no
creature delectable / but if thy heart be taken and engleymed with a vein
lust and likyng of it / which puts out the love of god fro the heart as in
felyng / and the ghostly savor that it may not come therein / Every man that
lives in spirit knowith well all this This is the wretchidnes of the soul and
the mischief for ye first syn^e of man / without al other wretchydnes and
sins which thou have wylfully put thereto / And wit thou well thou thou had
never done syn^e with thy body dedely ne venyal but oonly this that is called
origynall for it is the first syn^e / and that is not else but lesyng of thy
rightfulnes which you was made in should thou never have been saved if our lord
Ihu^ christ by his precious passion had not delyuerde the and restored the again
/

How every man may be saved by the passion of christ be he never so wretched /
Caplm xliiii.
ANd therefore if thou think that I have here before spoken to hye to the. for
thou may not take it ne fulfylle it as I have said or shall say / I will now
fall down to the as low as thou will for my profit as well as for thyn
Then^e say I thus / though thou be never somoche a wretch have thou do never
somoche sin / forsake thyself and all thy works good and bad / cry mercy.
and ask only saluaco^n by virtue of this precious passion mekely and trustly
/ and without dowte thou shall have it / And fro this origynal syn^e and al
other thou shall be saaf. ye and thou shall be saaf as an anchor incluse / And not
oonly thou. but all christian souls which trusten upon this passion. and meken
hemself / knowlegynge her wretchidnes: asking mercy and foryeuenes and the
fruit of this precious passo^n oonly. lowenge hemself to the sacraments of
holy church. though it be so that they have been encombred with sin all her
life time / and never had felyng of ghostly savor or swetnes / or ghostly
knowing of god. they shallen in this faith and in her good will by virtue of
this precious passion of our lord Ihu^ christ be saaf and come to the bliss of
heaven / All this know thou well^ but yet it likes me for to say it. See
here the endless mercy of our lord how low he falls to the and to me and to al
sinful caytyfs / Then^e ask mercy and have it / Thus said the prophet in the
person of our lord. Ioh^is. ^
Ois enim quicu^que inuocauerit nomen dn^i. saluus erit Every man what y^ he be
that calls the name of god / that is to say / askith saluaco^n by Ihu^ and
his passion: he shall be saaf / This certefye of our lord some men taken well
and be^ saved thereby / and some men in trust of this mercy and this curtesye
ly^en still in her sin / and wene for to have it when hem lust / and then
mow they not. for they are taken or they were / and so they dampne hemself /
But then say thou / if this be soth then wonder I greatly for that I find
in some holy men's books / Some saye^ as I vndstonde that he that can not love
this blessed name Ihu^ ne find ne feel in it ghostly Joy and delectable with
ghostly swetnes. in the bliss of heaven he shall be alyene and never shall he
come thereto / Sothly these words when I hem red stonyed me and made me greatly
aferde / For I hope as thou say that by the mercy of our lord shall be saaf
by keeping of the commandments / and by very repentance for her evil living
before done / which felt never ghostly swetnes ne inly savor in the name of
Ihesu / And therefore I merueyle me the more that they say contrari herto as it
semyth / And unto this I may say as me thinks that her saying if it be well
vndstonde is soth / and is not contrary to that yt I have said. For this name
Ihu^ is nout else for to say upon englisshe but heler or hele / Now every man
that lives in this wretchyd life is ghostly seek / For there is no man that
lives without sin which is ghostly syknes / as saint Ioh^n says of him
self and of other perfyte men thus / Si dixerimus qr pccm^ non habemus. John.
ip^i nos seducimus et veritas in nobis no^ est / If we say that we have no
syn^e we begyle ourself. and there is no sothfastnes in us. And therefore he
may never come to the Joy of heaven unto he be first made hole of this
ghostly syckenes / But this ghostly hele may no man have that has use of
reason: but if he desire it and love it: and have delight therin^ in asmoche as
he hopith for to get it / Now the name of Ihu^ is no thing else but this
ghostly hele / wherefore it is soth that they say / that there may no man be
saaf but if he love and like in the name of Ihesu / For there may no man be
ghostly hole / but if he love and desire ghostly health / For right as if a man
were bodily seek. there were no erthly thing so dear ne so nedful to him ne
so much should be desired of him as bodily health / for though you would give
him all the richesse and worshyppes of this world and not make him hole if
thou might / thou plesest him not / Right so it is to a man that is seek
ghostly and felyth the pain of ghostly syknes / no thing is so dear ne so
needful ne so much coueyted of him as is ghostly health. and that is Ihu^ /
without which all the Joys of heaven may not like him / And this is the skille
as I hope why our lord wha^ he took mankind for our saluaco^n he would not be
called by no name that betokenid his endless being or his might or his wysdom
or his ryghtwysnes / but oonly by that ye betoke nyd the cause of his coming.
and was the saluaco^n of man's soul. which saluaco^n betokened this name
Ihu^ / Then^e by this it semyth soth that there shall no man be saaf but if he
love saluaco^n only for to have it through the mercy of our lord Ihu^^ and by
the merits of his passo^n / which love he may have that liuyth and deyeth in
the lowest degree of charytee / Also I may say on that other party that he
that can not love this blessid name Ihu^ with ghostly mirth ne increase in it
with heavenly melody here / he shall never have ne feel in heaven yt fulhede of
souereyne Joy. the which he that might in this life by abou^dance of perfect
charity in Ihu^ shall feel and have / and so may her saying be vndstonde /
Nevertheless he shall be saaf and have full mede in the sight of god / if he in
this life be in the lowest degree of charity by keeping of goddis commandments
/ For our lord says himself thus. John.
In domo patris mei mansiones multe su^t / In my faders house are many soundry
dwellynges / Some are perfyte souls the which in this life were fulfilled of
charity. and grace of the holy ghost / and song louynges to god in
conte^placion of him with wonderful swetnes and heavenly savor / Thise souls
for they had most charity and grace of the holy ghost shall have highest mede in
the bliss of heaven / for these arn called goddis derlynges / Other souls that are not disposid to conte^placo^n of god. ne had not the fulhede of charity. as
apostles and marters had in the beginning of holy church. shall have lower mede
in the bliss of heaven / for thise arne called goddis friends / Thus calls
our lord in holy writ chosen souls saying thus / Comedite amici. et
inebriamini ca^issimi / My friends ete ye. Cant
and my derlynges be ye dronken / As if our lord said thus / ye that arne my
trendes. for ye kept my commandments. and set my love before the love of
ye world / and loved me more tha^ any erthly thing ye shall be fed with
ghostly fode of the bread of life / But ye yt arne my friends that ye not oonly
kept my commandments but also of your own free will fulfilled my
cou^ceylles: and over that ye loved oonly and enteerly with all the myghtes of
your soul. and bre^ned in my love with ghostly delight as dyden principally the
apostles and marters. and all other souls that might by grace come to the
yeft of perfecco^n / ye shall be made dro^ken with the highest and fresshest wine
in my celler / that is the souereyne Joy of love in heaven /

That a man should be besye to reken again his worthynes / and refourme again in
him the image of the Trinyte / Caplm xlv.
Nevertheless though this be soth of the endless merci of god unto the and to me
and to al manki^de / we shall not therefore in trust of this be ye more recheles
wylfully in our lyuinge / but the more besye for to pleyse him / namly now
sythen we are restored again in hope by the passion of our lord to the dignyte
and the bliss which we had lost by adams syn^e / And though we might never
get it fully here / yet we should desire that we might recover here living a
figure and a lyknes of ye dignytee that our soul might be reformed as it were
in a shadow by grace to the image of the trynite / which we had by kynde^ and
after shall have fully in bliss / for that is the life which is very
contemplatyf unto begin here in that feeling of love. and ghostly knowing of
god by opening of the ghostly eye which shall never be lost ne be taken away.
but ye same shall be fulfilled otherwise in ye bliss of heaven / This behyght
our lord to mary mawdeleyne which was contemplatif / and said thus of her /
Maria optima^ parte^ elegit que no^ auferetur ab ea^ ^
That mary had chose the better party that is the love of god in contemplaco^n
/ for it shall never be take away fro her / I say not that thou may her
living recover so hole ne so perfyte clen^es and Innocence knowing and
louinge of god as thou hadest first. ne as thou shall have / ne you may not
escape all ye wretchydnes and pains of syn^e / ne thou living in dedely
flesh may destroy and quench all holy the false vain love in thyselfe /
ne flee all venyall sins that they ne will but if they be stopped by great
fervor of charity spring out of thyn heart as water does fro a stynkyng well
/ But I would that if thou might not fully quench it. that you might somewhat
sleke it. and come to the cle^nes of soul as nere as thou may / For our
lord behite the children of Israel wha^ he ladde hem in to the land of byhest
/ And in figure of hem to all christian men thus / Omne quod calcauerit pes tuus.
tuu^ erit / That is to say / Als much land as thou might trede upon with
thy foot of very desire. Deut^ ii
so here much shall thou have in the land of byhest / that is in the bliss
of heaven when thou comyst thider /

How Ihesu shall be sought. desired: and found / ca xlvi
Seek then that thou have lost that thou might find it / well I wot who
so might ones have an inward syghte a lityll of that dignytee and that
ghostly fayrnes which a soul had by kind. and shall have by grace / he
should loathe and despise in his heart all the bliss. the likyng: and the
fayrnes of this world as the stenche of a carrion. and he shall never have will
for to do other deed night and day saving the freelte and the bare need of
the bodily kind but desire. mourn. and pray and seek how he might come again
thereto / Nevertheless in as much as thou have not yet seen what it is fully /
For thy ghostly eye is not yet opened / I shall tell the oo word for all in
the which thou shall seek desire and find it. for in that one word is all
that thou have lost / This word is Ihesu / I mean not this word Ihesu
painted upon ye wall / or written by lettres on the book. or fourmyd by lips
in sou^de of the mowthe / or feyned in thy heart by traueyle of thy mind / For
in this manner wise may a man out of charity find him. But I mean Ihesu
crist that blessid person god and man sone of virgin mary / whom this name
betokenith that is all goodness: endless wysdom / love / and swetnes / thy Joy.
thy worship. and thyn everlasting bliss / thy god: thy lord. and thy
salvation / Then if it be so that thou felyst a great desire in thyn heart
to Ihesu. either by mind of this name Ihesu. or by mind and saying of any
other word / or in prayer. or in any deed yt thou do / which desire is so
much that it puts out as it were by strength al other thoughts and
desires of the world / and of the flesh that they may not rest in thine
heart / Then sechest thou well thy lord Ihesu And when thou felyst this
desire to god / to Ihesu. all is one helped and comforted by a ghostly might /
in somoche that it is turned in to love and affecco^n / ghostly savor and
swetnes / In to light and knowing of sothfastnes / somoche that for the time
the point of thy thought is set upon no thing that is made / Ne it felyth
no stiryng of vaynglory ne of itself another / ne none other evil affecco^n /
for they mow not appear that time / But oonly is enclosed. rested: softed.
enoynted in Ihesu / then have thou found somewhat of Ihesu / Not him as he
is. but a shadow of him. For the better that thou fyndest him / the more shall
thou desire him / Then by what manner prayer or meditaco^n or occupaco^n that
thou may have grettest and clennest desire to him. and have most feeling of
him / by that ocupacyon thou sechest him best and best fyndest him / Therefore
if it come to thy mind / as it were asking what have thou lost / and what
sechest thou Lift up thy mind and the desire of thy heart to Ihesu christ
though thou be blind and naught may see of his godhede And say that him
have thou lost / and him would thou have. and no thing but him / to be with
him where he is / None other joy none other bliss in heaven ne in earth but him
/ And though it be so that thou feel him in deuoco^n or in knowinge / or in
any other yefte what that it be / rest not there as though thou had fully
found Ihesu. But foryete that. that you have found / and always by desiryng
after Ihesu more and more for to find him better / as though thou had
right naught found in him / For wit thou well what that thou felyst of him.
be it never so much. ye though thou were rauisshed in to the third heaven
with poul / yet have thou not found Ihesu as he is in his Joy / Know thou or
feel thou never so much of him / he is yet above it / And therefore if thou
woll fully find him as he is in the bliss / of loving cease you never while
thou lyuest / ne of ghostly desyryng /

What profit it is to have the desire of Ihesu / Caplm xlvii.
SOthly I had lever feel and have a sothfaste desire and a clean in mine heart
to my lord Ihesu christ / though I see right lityll of him with my ghostly eye
than for to have without this desire all bodily penance of all men living /
all vysions or reuelaco^ns of angels apperyng / songs and so wnynges. savors
and smelles. bren^ynges. and any likings or bodily felynges / And shortly for
to say. or all the Joy of heaven and of earth which I might have without
this desire to my lord Ihesu / Dauyd the prophet felt as I say as I
vndstonde when he sayd^ thus / P^ lxxii.
Quid enim michi est in celo et a te quid volui super terram / Lord what
thing is to me in heaven / or what would I without the above earth / As if he
had said thus / Lord Ihesu what heavenly Joy is likynge to me without desire
of the whiles I am in earth / or without love of the when I come to heaven / As
who say: right none. Then if thou will feel any thing of him bodily or
ghostly / coueyte not but for to feel sothfastly a desire of his grace and of
his mercyful presence: that the thinks that thyn heart may find none other
rest in no thing but in him / Thus coueyted dauyd when he said thus / P^
Concupiuit anima mea desiderare iustificaco^nes tuas in om^i tempore / Lord
my soul coueyted the desire of thy rightwysnes in every time / Seek then as
dauyd did desire by desire / And if thou may feel by thy desire in prayers
and in meditaco^ns the homely presence of Ihesu christ in thy soul / bind thyn
heart fast thereto that it fall not therfro. And if thou stomble^ that thou may
soon find him again /

Where and with what thing Ihesu shall be sought and found / Caplm xliii.
Seek then Ihesu whom thou have lost / He will be sought / and he may then
somewhat be founden / for he says himself / Omnis qui querit inueniet / Every
man that sechyth shall find / The sekyng is traueylous. but the finding is
blysfull / Do therefore after the counseylle of the wise man if thou will find
him / Si quesieris quasi pecunia^ sapienciam and sicut thesaurum effoderis
illam: prouer, xx.
tunc intelliges timorem dn^i and sciencia^ inuenies / If thou seek wysdom the
which is Ihesu as silver and gold and delueste deep thereafter thou shall
find it / The behouyth for to delue deep in thyn heart. for therein he is hid
/ and cast out full clenly all loves and likings sorrows and dredes of all
erthly things / and so shall thou find wysdom Ihesu / Be thou then like to
the woman of the gospel of the which our lord says thus / Que mulier
habens dragmas december. (...)
etc^ what woman is that. that has lost a drame that she ne will light a
lantem and cast her house vpsodowne and seche till she find it / As who say
none. And when she has founden it she calls her friends and says to hem
thus / Makyth mirth with me and melody. for I have founden the drame that I
had lost / This drame is Ihesu that thou have lost / And if thou will find
him / light up a latern that is goddis word as david says / ^s. cxviii
Lucerna pedibus meis verbu^ tuu^ / Lord thy word to my fete is a lantern /
Bithys lantern shalt thou see where he is and how thou shalt find him / And
if thou wylt thou may with this light up an other latern: that is the reason
of thy soul / For as our lord says / Lucerna corporis tui est oculus tuus.
The laterne of thy body is thy bodily eye / Right so may be said that the
lantern of thy soul is reason. by the which the soul may see all ghostly
things / By this lantern may thou find Ihu^ and that is soth if thou hold up
the lantern fro vndneth the busshell. Luc. 10.
as our lord says / Nemo accendit lucernam and ponit eam sub modio sed super
candelabru^ / There is no man that lyghteth a lantern for to set it under a
busshell but upon a candelstycke / That is to say / Thy reason shall not be
ouerlayd with erthly besynes ne vain thoughts and erthly affeccyons but aye
upward above all vain thought and erthly things as much as thou may / And
if thou do so thou shall see then all the molle and all the fylthe and
small motes in thy house / for why he is light / That is to say all flesshly
loves and dredes in thy soul / Not all^ P^ xxiiii
for as dauyd said / Delicta quis intelliget / who may know al his trespasses /
As who say no man / And thou shall cast out of thyn heart all such sins and
swepe thy soul clean with the besome of the dread of god / and with the water
of thyn eyes wasshe it. and so shall thou find thy drame Ihesu / He is drame
he is penny. he is thine heritage / This drame will not be founden so lightly
as it is said / for this work is not of one hour ne of one day / but many
days and years / with much sweet and swynke of body and traueylle of the
soul / And if thou cease not but seche besily. sorrow and syghe deep / mourn
stylly. and stowpe low till thyn eyes watren for anguysshe and for pain for
you have lost thy tresour Ihu^. at the last when he will well shall thou find
thy drame Ihesu / And if thou find him as I have said. that is if thou may in
clennes of conscience feel ye homely and the peesfull presence of that blessed
man Ihesu christ as a shadow or a glemeryng of him / Thou may if thou will
call all thy fre^des to the for to make mirth with the and melodye for thou
have founden the* drame Ihesu /

Where Ihesu is lost and founden again thorugh his mercy / Caplm xlix
SEe now then^e the curtesye and the mercy of Ihu^. you have lost him. but
where? Sothly in thy house / that is in thy soul That is to say / if thou
had lost all the reason of thy soul by the first sin thy soul should
never have found him again / but he left to the thy reason. and so he is in
thy soul / and never shall be lost out of it / Nevertheless thou art never
the nerer to him till thou have found him / He is in the though he be lost fro
the / But thou art not in him till thou have found him / Then was this his
mercy that he would suffer him to be lost oonly where he may be found / It
needs not to run to Rome ne to Iherusalem for to seche him there / but
turn thy thought in to thine own soul where he is hid. as the prophet
says / Vere tu es deus absconditus Sothly lord thou art an hid god / and
seche him there. M^ 13.
Thus says himself in the gospel / Simile est regnu^ celorum thesauro
abscondito in agro. quem qui inuenit homo abscondit and pre gaudio illius
vadit^ and vendit vniuersa que habet. et emit agrum illu^ / The kingdom of
heaven is likened to a tresoure hyd in the field. the which when a man fyndeth
for Joy of it he gooth and sells all that he has and byeth the field /
Ihesu is tresour hid in thy soul / Then if thou might find him in thy
soul. and thy soul in him / I am syker for Joy of it thou would give the
likyng of all erthly thing for to have it / Ihesu slepith in thy heart ghostly^
as he did sometime bodily when he was in the ship with his discyples But they
for dread of perysshynge wakened him. and soon after he saved hem fro tempeste
/ Do thou so. styre him by prayer / and wake him with great cryenge of desire
/ and he shall soon rise and help the /

What lets a man to here and see Ihesu within him self / Caplm L.
Nevertheless I hope better that thou slepest ofter to him than he does to the
/ For he callyth the full often with his sweet pryue voys / and styreth thyn
heart full stylly yt thou sholdest leave all other Ianglyng of al other vanitees
in thy soul / and oonly take keep of him for to here him speak Thus says
Dauyd of our lord / Audi filia and vide et inclina aurem tuam and obliuiscere
populum tuum and domum patris tui / My daughter here and see and bow thine ere
to me. and foryete the folk of thy worldly thoughts. and the housse of thy
flesshly and kyndely affeccyons / Loo here may thou see how our lord callyth
the and all other which wyile harken to him / what lettyth the then^e that
thou may another see him ne here him / Sothly there is so much dynne and
cryenge in thine heart of vain thoughts and flesshly desires that you may
another here him ne see him / Therefore put away unrestful dynne. and break the
love of sin and of vanytee / and bring in to thine heart love of virtues and
full charity. and then shall thou here thy lord speak to the /

That mekenes and charity ben the special lyuerey of Ihesu / through the which
man's soul is reformed to the lyknes of him / Caplm li.
AS long as Ihesu fyndeth not his image reformed in the. he is strange and
the ferther fro the / For thy shape the for to be arrayed in his liknes / that
is in mekenes and charity / the which arn his lyuereys / And then will he
homelyche know the / and show to the his pryuetees / Thus said he himself to
his disciples / John xiiii
Qui diligit me diligetur a patre meo et manifestabo ei meip^m / who so loves
me he shall be loved of my fader and I shall show myself unto him There is no
virtue ne no work that thou may do that may make the like to our lord
without mekenes and charity / for these two arn specially to god most leyf /
And that semyth well in the gospel where our lord spekyth of mekenes thus /
Discite a me quia mitis sum and humilis cord / M. ii.
Learn of me he said not for to goo bare foot ne for to goo in to Deserte / and
there for to fast forty days / ne yet also for to chese you dyscyples / But
learn of me mekenes / for I if you drew in to thyself thy heart thou sholdest
not find naught / but thou sholdest find Ihesu / Not oonly the naked mind
of this name. but thou sholdest tynde Ihesu christ in conscience redely techyng
the / Thou sholdest find light of understanding: and no derknes of vncu^nyng
/ Thou sholdest find love and likyng of him. and no pain of bitterness and
heaviness / But for thou art not reformed therefore when thy soul comes in fro
all bodily things. and fyndeth naught but derkenes and heaviness / him thinks
an hundred winter to he be out again by some bodily delight or vayn thought. and
that is no wonder / For who so comyth home until his house and fyndeth no
thing therein but stynke and smoke. and a chidyng wife he would soon run out
of it / Right so thy soul when it tyndeth no comfort in it self but black
smoke of ghostly blyndnes. and great chidyng of flesshly thoughts cryeng up on
the that thou may not be in peace / sothly it is soon weri till it be out again
/ This is the derknes of conscience /

Who so will find Ihesu him behouith abidyngly to traueyle in ghostly
derkenes against the image of sin / Caplm liiii^
Nevertheless in this derke conscience behooves the to swinke and sweet / That
is to say / The behouith to draw in to thyself thy thought fro all bodily
things as much as thou may / And then when thou fyndest right naught but
sorrow and pain. and blyndnes in this derknes / if thou will find Ihesu the
pain of this derke conscience the behouyth suffer. and abide awhyle therein /
And here the behooves to be waar that thou take Ihesu christ in thy thought
against this each derkenes in thy mind / And by besye prayer and fervent desire
to god / Not setting the point of thy thought in that foresaid naught / but
in Ihesu christ which thou desyrest / Think styfly on the passion and on his
mekenes and thorugh might of him thou shall arise / Do as thou would bear
it down and goo through it / Thou shall agryse and loathe this derkenes. and
this naught right as the devil: and thou shall despise it and al to breast it
/ For all within this naught is Ihu^ hid in his Joy whom thou may not find
by thy sechyng / but if thou pass the derknes of this conscience. This is the
ghostly traueyle that I speak of / And this traueile is cause of all this
writing / for to styre the thereto if thou feel grace / This derkenes of
conscience and this naught that I speak of is the image of the first adam /
Saint poul knew it well / for he said thus of it / Sicut portauimus ymagine^
terreni hominis. Cor^ (...)
ita portemus ymagine^ iam and celestis / As we have here before borne the
image of the erthly man that is the first adam / right so that we might now
bear the image of the heavenly man which is Ihesu the second adam / He bare
this image often full heavy / for it was so comberous to him that he cried out on
it layeng thus / O quis liberabit me de corpore mortis huius / O who shall
deliver me fro this body and this image of death / And then he comforted
himself and other also thus / Gracia dei per ih^m xp^m / To. (...)
The grace of god by Ihesu christ /

What is propirly the image of sin / and what comyth out thereof / Caplm lv
NOw have I told the a lityll of this image how it is naught / Nevertheless if
it be fer fro thy knowing how it might be an image / for naught is but naught.
but so might you not litly vndstonde it. I shall tell ye more openly of this
image as me thinks / This image is a falls mysruled love unto thyself / Out
fro this comen all manner of sins by seven Ryuers / which arne these / Pride.
Envy. Ire. Accidie. Couetise. Glotenye. and Lechery / Loo this is somewhat
that thou may feel / By one of these ryuers ren^eth out al manner of syn^e and
puts the out of charity if it be dedely syn^e / or it lets the fervor
of charity if it be venyall / ^ow may you grope that this image is not naught /
but it is much of bad for it is a great spring of love unto thyself with
such vii ryuers as I have said / But now say thou how may this be soth / I
have forsaken the world / and I am stoken in an house / I meddle with no man /
I chyde not / I strive not / I neither bye ne selle / I ne have no worldly
besynes but by the mercy of god / I keep me chaste and wythholde me fro delytes
/ And over this I pray I wake / I traueyle bodily and ghostly as I may / How
should then this image be so much in me as thou spekest of / As to this I
answer and grant to the / that I hope thou do all thise works and moo
thereto* and yet may it be soth as I say / Thou art besye upon thy might for to
stop the ryuers wythoute^ / but the spring within on hap you leuest hole /
Thou art like to a man the which had in his yerde a stinkyng well with many
rennynges fro it. He yede and he stopped the rennynges and left the spring
hole / and we^de all had be syker / but the water sprange up at the ground of
the well / and stood stylle somoche that it corrupted all the fayrnes of his
garden / and yet ren^eth no water out / ^yght so may it be with the / If it
be so that thou have by grace stopped the ryuers of this image without /
somoche it is well / but be ware of the spring within / Sothly but if thou
stop and cleanse that as much as thou may it will corrupt all ye flowers of
the gardyne of thy soul / show they never so fair outward in syghte of men /
But now say you. whereby shall I know that the ground is stopped / if I
traueylle about it / As unto this I shall tell by assaye how thou shalt
know this image if it be in the / and how much it is in ye and thereby shall
thou wit how much it is stopped and how lityl also in the / And asmoche as
pride is the pryncipall River I shall tell the thereof first /

What pride is / And when it is sin Caplm lvi*
Pride is not else as clerks saye^ but love of thyn own excellence. yt is of
thyn own worship / Then^e the more thou love and likest in thyn own
worship. the more is the pride / and so the more is the image in the / If thou
feel in thyn heart a stiryng of pride / thou that art holyer. Wyser better*
and more virtuous than a another is / that god has yeuen the grace for to serve
him better than other done / and thou thynkest al other byneth the and the
abouen hem / or any other thought of thiself / which shows to thy sight of
thy soul an excellence and an ouerpassynge of other men or wym^en / and of
this stiryng thou felyst love and delight and vayn plesyng in thyself that thou
art so / this is a token that thou berest this black image / which if it be
pryue fro men's eyes. nevertheless it shows him openly in goddis syghte / But
now say thou that thou may not flee such styringes of pride / for often thou
felist hem against thy will. and therefore thou hold hem no sin / or if
they ben syn^e they ben naught but venyall / As to this I say thus that the
felyng of these stirynges of pride or of any other the which spryngen out
either of the corrupco^n of this foul image or by incastyng of the enmye. it
is no sin in as much as thou felyst hem / and that is a grace and a
pryuylege by virtue of the passion of Ihesu christ granted to all cryste^ men
baptized in water and in the holy ghost / For sothly to Jews and sarrazyns
which trow not in Ihesu christ. all such stirynges are dedely sins / For
saint poul says. Om^e quod non est ex fide pccm^ est / All that is done
withouten truth in christ is dedely sin / But we christian men have this
pryuilege of his mercy that such felynges are no syn^e. but they are pain of
the oryginall sin / Nevertheless when by neclygence and by blyndenes of
thiself this felyng is received unwarily in thy thought. and turned in to love
and likynge / then is there sin more or less after the mesure of the love
/ sometime venyall. and sometime dedely / when it is venyall and when dedely /
fully can I not tell the / Nevertheless a lityll I shall say as me thinks /

When pride is dedely sin. And how it is in flesshely living men dedely sin
/ Caplm lvii^
THen^e the stirynge of pride is received and turned in to lykyng somoche that
the heart cheseth it for a full rest and a full delight. and secheth none other
end but oonly likyng therein / then^e is this pride dedely syn^e / for he
makith and chesyth this delight as his god without ayenstondyng of reason and of
will and therefore it is dedely sin / But now say thou / what fool is he
that would chese pride as his god / no man that lives would do so / As unto
this I say that I can not tell the in specyal who syn^eth in pride dedely /
but in general I shall say yt There is two manner of pride / The tone is bodily
pride. the other is ghostly pride / Bodily pride is of flesshly living men.
Ghostly pride is of ypocrytes and heretykes / These three syn^e dedely in pride
/ I mean of such a flesshly living man as saint poul spekith of thus / Si
scdm carne^ vixeritis moriemini / If ye live after your flesh ye shall deye /
Then say I thus that a worldely man which loves and sechyth pryncypally
the worship of himself / and chesyth the likynge of it / as rest of his heart
and the end of his bliss he syn^eth dedely / But now say thou / who would
chese love of his worshypp^ instead of his god / As to this I say thus / that
he that loves his worship as for to seem better and gretter of astate tha^ any
other / and traueyleth about it as much as he may if he love it somoche that
for ye getyng of it ye keeping and the saving of it he brekith the commandment
of god: or brekith love and charity to his even christian. or is ready and in full
will for to break it rather than he should forbere his worship. or lose it
either of his name or of his state / or of fulfillyng of his will: sothly he
syn^eth dedely / For he louyth his worshypp^ and chesyth it more than the love
of god and of his even cryste^ / And nevertheless the man that synneth thus
dedely he would say with his mouth that he will not chese pride for his god /
But he begileth himself for he chesyth it by his deed / Nevertheless a another
worldly man that louith worship of himself. and pursues thereafter if he love
it not so much that he would for the getyng or ye saving of it do a dedely
syn^e or break charity to his even christian / he synneth not dedely but venyall
/ more or less after the mesure of his love and his likynge with other
cyrcumstaunces /

How pride in heretykes is dedely syn^e / Caplm lviii
AN heretyke synneth dedely in pride. for he chesyth his rest and his delight
in his own opinyon and in his own saying / for he weneth that it is soth /
which opinyon or saying is against god and holy church / and therefore synneth
he in pride dedely for he louyth himself and his own will and wit so much
that though it be openly against the ordinance of holy church he will not leave
it but rest him therein as in sothfasnes* and so makyth he it his god / but he
begyleth himself / For god and holy church arn so onyd and acorded together
yt who so does against that one he does against both / And therefore he that
says he louyth god and kepith his biddynges / and dispiseth holy church. and
sets at naught the laws and the ordinances of it made by the head and the
sovereign in governance of all christian men / he lies he chesyth not god. but
he chesyth the love of himself contrary to the love of god / and so he
synneth dedely / And in that he weneth most to pleyse god he most dysplesyth
him / for he is blind and will not see / Of this blyndnes and this false
resting of an heretyke in his own felyng spekith the wise man thus / Est via
que videtur homini recta / et nouissima eius ducu^t ad mortem. pro^^. xiiii
There is a way which semyth to a man ryghtfull / and the last end of it
brings him to endless death / This way specially is called heresye / For
other flesshly sinners that syn^en dedely and lain therein comynly they suppose
amys of hemself. and felen bityng in conscience that they goo not in the right
way But an heretyke supposes that he does well and techeth well and yet no
man so well / And so weneth he that his way were the right way / and
therefore felyth he no bityng of conscience ne mekenes in heart / And sothly
but if god send him mekenes of his mercy. at the last end he gooth to hell
/ And nevertheless yet weneth he for to have done well and gete^ him the bliss
of heaven for his techyng /

How pride in ypocrytes is dedely sin / Caplm lix.
THe ypocryte also synneth dedely in pride / He is an ypocrite that cheseth
vain Joy of himself. as the rest and ye full delight of heart upon this manner
of wise / when a man does many manner of good deeds bodily and ghostly and
then^e is put to his mind by suggesto^n of the enmye beholding of himself and
of his good deeds / How good how holy he is how worthy in men's dome / and
how high in goddis syghte aboue^ other men. he perceyueth this stiryng and
receives it wylfully / for he weneth it be good and of god in as much as it
is soth for he does these good deeds better than other me^ And when it is
received thus by assent of his will as good year ryseth of it alone and a
delight in his heart of himself yt he so much grace has that it rauyssheth
his mind out of all other thoughts both ghostly and flesshly for the time
and settyth it in vain Joy of himself as in a rest of his heart / This
rauysshyng in ghostly pride is delectable / and therefore he kepyth it holds
it and noryssheth it as much as he may For this love and vain delight he
prays and waketh. he fasteth and wereth the hair / and does other
afflycco^ns. and all this greueth him but lityll / He loves he thanketh god
sometime with his mouth / and sometime wryngeth a tere out of his eye: and
then he thinks all saaf enough / But sothly all this is for love of
himself which he cheseth and receives as it were love and Joy in god / and
in that is all the sin / He chesyth not sin wylfully as for sin / but he
che^yth this delight and Joy that he felyth for god / as the rest of his soul
the which is sin wythouten displesyng or again stondyng of will / For he
weneth it were a Joy in god / and it is not so. and therefore synneth he
dedely / Job says thus of an ypocrite / Gaudium ypocrite ad instar pu^cti / Si
ascenderit in celum superbia eius and capud eius nubes tetigerit. Job. 20^
velut sterquiliniu^ in fine perdetur / The Joy of an ypocryte is no more
than a point / For if he stye in to heaven with reysynge of heart / and his
heued touch the skies at the last end he shall be casten out as a dounge hepe
/ The Joy of an ypocryte is but a point / For if he worship himself never
so much. and Joy in himself never so much al his life time / and depeynte
himself with all his good deeds in syghte and in loving of the world / at the
last it is right naught / but sorrow and pain / But now say* thou that there
are few such or else none that is so blind that would hold and chese vain
Joy in himself as for Joy in god / As unto this I can not say ne will not
though I cowde / but one thing I tell that there are many ypocrytes / and
nevertheless they wene that they be^ none / and that be many that drede^ hemself
as ypocrites. and sothly they are none / which is one and which is other god
knows / and none but he / who so will mekely dread* he shall not be bigyled
/ And who so weneth to be syker. he may lightly fall / For saint poul says /
Qui se existimat aliquid esse cum nichil sit. Gal. ^.
ipse se seducit / who so weneth himself to be ought when he is right naught
/ he begyleth himself /

How stirynges of pride and vainglory in good men be^ but venial sins /
Caplm lx
Nevertheless a man or woman which disposyth him to live contemplatyf / if it
be so that he forsake him self as in will / and offer him holy to god with a
full general will that he would not sin in pride wyttyngly: ne have Joy in
himself wylfully but oonly in god if he cowde and might / And after this full
will offered to god he felyth many stirynges of vaynglory / and delyteth in hem
for the time for he perceyueth hem not. This likyng is but venyall sin and
namly if it be so that when he comyth to himself he repreuyth himself and
ayenstondeth this stiryng with displesyng of will / and askyth mercy and help
of god / Then the likyng which before was sin / out lord of his mercy
soon forgyueth it / And yet he shall have mede for his good traueyle in the
ayenstondyng / And that is a curtesye of our lord granted to all those
which arn specially his servants and more homely of his court / as are all
those that for his love forsaken in a good true will all worldly and al
flesshly sin / and yeuen hem holy body and soul unto his seruyse in her
might and her cunning / As done pryncypally ancres encluse and true religyous
/ the which for the love of god and salvation of her souls entren in to any
religyon approved by holy church / Or else if it be so that they entren
first for a worldly cause as for her bodily sustenaunce / or for some other
such / if they repent hem and turn it in to a goostly cause as for the
service of god / These as long as they keep this will and pursue it as they
may upon her freelte are true religyous / Also what man or woman that he be in
what degree he be in holy church priest clerk or lewd man / wydowe or maiden
or wife that will for the love of god and salvation of his soul forsake all the
worshyppes and likings of this world in this world in his heart truly and
fully betwix god and him and all wylful besynes and erthly things to the bare
need / And offer his wyll^nteerly for to be his servant upon his might by
devout prayers and holy thoughts. with other good deeds that he may do
bodily and goostly and kepyth his will hoole to god steadfastly / All these arne
specially goddis servants in holy church / And for this good will and good
pourpoos that they have of the yefte of god they shall encrese in grace and in
charity here living / And they shall have for this special will a special
mede in the bliss of heaven before other chosen souls which offered not holy
her will and her bodi to goddis service / neither openly ne pryuely as they
dyden / All these which I call goddis servants and of his court more
special / if they by freelte and by vnkunnyng when they feel such stirynges
of vaynglory for the time delyten therein / and perceyuen it not for her reason
and her wit is let by the likynge that they feel that it may not see this
stirynge / They sin not dedely in this likynge of vain glory / For that will
that they have generally set in her heart before to plese god / and for to
forsake all manner of sin if they knew it kepith hem here in such stirynges
and in all other that comen of freelte that they sin not dedely / And shall
keep as long as the ground of that will is kept hole /

How diverse states in holy church shall have diverse medes in heaven / And of
two special medes in heaven / Caplm lxi.
ANd over this I say more in comfort of the and of all other having the state
of anchor incluse. and also by grace o^ god in comfort of hem all that enter
any religyon approved in holy church / that all those that by the mercy of
our lord shall be saaf they shall have a special mede and a synguler worship
in the bliss of heaven for her state of living before other souls that had
not that state in holy church though they ben never so holy / which worship
is better than all the worship of this world wythouten comparyson / For if
thou might see what it were thou would not for ye worship of this world if
thou myghtest have it withouten syn^e change the state either of anchor or of
religyous. ne lose that synguler mede in the bliss of heaven / which mede is
called Accydentall mede / Nevertheless that other men mystake not this that I
say / Therefore I shall say it more openly / Thou shall understand that there
are two medes in the bliss of heaven / which our lord gives to chosen
souls / The tone is souereyne and pryncypall / As is loving and knowing of
him after the mesure of charytee given of god to a soul living in dedely
flesh / This mede is best and souereyne for it is god himself / And it is
common to all the souls that shollen be saaf in what state or degree that they
ben living in holy church more or less / after the quantyte and the mochenes
of her charity in his life what degree he be in. For he that most loves god
in charity / he shall have most mede in the bliss of heaven / For he shall
most love god and know him and that is the souereyne mede / And as for this
mede it shall fall that some manner of man or woman / as a lord or a lady /
knight / or squire / marchaunte / or plough man^ or what degree he be in man
or woman shall have more mede thann some priest / or friar / monk / or chanon
/ or anchor incluse / And why? Soothly for he loved god more in charity / An
other mede there is / that is secundary which our lord gives for special
good deeds that a man does wylfully over that he is bounden to / Of three deeds
pryncypall doctors of holy church maken mind / Of marterdome. prechynge. and
manhood / These three works as for an excellence in as much as they passen all
other shull have special mede which they callen aureole. And that is naught
else but a synguler worship and special token ordained of god in reward of
that special deed before other men / that did not so over the souereyne mede
of love of god / ^hyche is common to him and to all other / Right so it is of
al other special good deeds / the which if they ben done soothfastly arne
specially acceptable to the syghte of god / and in the dome of holy church
they arne excellent / As arne enclosynge of ankers done by the auctoryte of
holy church / Also entering in to any religyon approved. And the streyghter
that the relygion is the more excellent is the deed in the dome of holy church
/

Also after these and byneth these the taking of the order of priest either
for cure of men's souls / and for to mynister the sacraments of holy church
/ Or else for synguler devotion to pleyse god and profyten her even christian by
the sacryfyse of the precious body of our lord Ihesu christ / Sothly they arne
special deeds / and excellent openly showed in the dome of holy church / and
in the syghte of our lord / wha^ they arne done sothfastly for god they arne
excellent / and they shullen have special mede each man in his degree in the
bliss of heaven / The state of bishop and prelate is abouen all these deeds
as for this accydentall mede / That this is soth it s^ myth by holy writ
where it says thus in the prophet Danyel / Tu autem vade ad tempus prefinitum
et requiesces ^t stabis in sort tua in fine dierum / This is for to say thus
much / The angel when he had showed to Danyel the pryuytees of god he said to
him thus / Goo thou to the rest of thy bodily death / and thou shalt stand
in thy sort as a prophet at the last day / And sothly as Danyell shall
stand as a prophet at the last day of dome and have the worship and the
excellence of a prophet over the souereyn blessed mede of love and sight of
god / Right so shalt thou stand as an anchor in that sort / and a religyous
in the sort of relygyon And so of other excellent deeds / and have a synguler
worship passing other men at the day of dome /

A short stirynge to mekenes and to charytee / Caplm lxii.
NOw by these words thou may if thou wolte trow hem / conceive comfort for
thy degree of living / and also matere of mekenes / For though it be so that
thou shalt have so much mede specially for thy state of living if you be saaf
/ Nevertheless it may be that there is many a wife and many worldlyche woman
shall be nerer god than thou / and more shall love god and better know him
than thou shall: for all thy state / And that ought to be a shame for the but
if thou be bisye for to get love and charity as fully and as perfytly as a
worldely man or woman / For if thou may have as much charytee of the gift of
god as he or she has that dwellyth stylle in worldly besynes / thou shall
have as much of the souereyn mede as he shall. And you shall over that for that
state which thou have taken have a singular mede and a worship which he shall
not have / Then^e if thou will do well meke thyselfe and forgete thy state as
it were right naught For it is soth. by it self it is right naught / And
that thy desire be and thy besynes for to destroy sins / and for to get
charity and mekenes and other ghostly virtues / for therein lies al /

How a man shall know how much pride is in him / Caplm lxiii.
I Have nyghe forgoten this image / But now I turn again thereto / if thou will
wite how much pride is therein / Thou may yet assaye thyself thus / Look now
wisely / and flater not thyself / if loving praysynge or worshypping. or
flesshly favor of worldly men or of other be likynge to thine hert^ and torn
it to vain gladness and well payeng of thiselfe / Think stylly in thine heart
that men sholden praise thy life / reward thy speech more than of other / And
also on contrary wise / if it be so that men repreue the / and setten the at
naught / Hold the but a fool or an ypocryte / or if they sclau^der the. or
speak evil of the falsely / or in any other way that they disease the
vnskylfully / And for thy thou felyst in thine heart a grievous heaviness against
hem / and a great rysyng in thine heart with ayenstondyng for to suffer any
shame or vylanye in the syghte of the world / If it be thus with the it is a
toke^ that there is much pride in this derke image seem thou never so holy in
the syghte of men / For though these stirynges ben not but lityll and venyall /
nevertheless they shown well that there is much pride hid in the ground of
thine heart / as the fore dares in his den / These styrynges with many moo
^^^^ngen out of this image so much that thou may uneaths do any good deed
but it shall be meddled with some pride or vain delight in thyself / And so
with thy pride thou defowlest all thy good deeds / and makyth hem loothsom in
the syghte of thy lord / I say not that they are lost. for they are meddled
with this pride / But I say that they are not so pleysaunt to thy lord as
they should be if they were simple and truly roted in the virtue of mekenes /
And therefore if thou will have clennes of heart. for to come to the love of
god / the behooves not oonly flee the rest of thin heart in vain glory by
wylfull assentyng to pride / and also the recheles ^ykyng therein of thy freelte
if it be against thy will / But also the feeling of thy pride thou shall flee
and eschew as much as thou may / But that thou may not do but if thou be
full quycke and ready abowte the keeping of thine heart / as I shall tell after
/

Of Envy and ire and of her branches / And how instead of sin man^is
person is often hated / Caplm lxiiii
Turn this image up so wwne / And look well therein. and thou shalt find two
members of envy and ire fastenyd thereto / with many diverse branches spryngyng
out of them / The which letten love and charity / the which thou sholdest
have to thyn even christian / The branches of ire and envy are these / Hatrede.
evil suspecion / falls and unskillful demynge / malecolye risyng of heart
against hem / dyspisyng and unkindness. and bachityng: and myssayenge /
unskillful blamyng / myslikyng. anguisshe. and heaviness aye^ste hem that
dispisen the or speak any evil of the^ or against ye A gladness of her disese /
a felnes against synful men and other that will not do as the thinks they
should do with great desire of thine heart under color of charity and
ryghtwysnesse that they were well punysshed and chastysed for her sin / This
stiryng semyth good / Nevertheless if you ransake it well thou shall find it
more sometime flesshly against the person than ghostly against the syn^e / Thou
shall love the man be he never so sinful / and thou shall hate the sin in
each man what he be / Many are begyled in this / for they set the bitter instead of the sweet. and taken derknes in the stead of light against the
prophet saying / Ve vobis que dicitis malu^ bonu^ and bonum malu^ ponentes
lucem tenebras and amaru^ dulce. ^say^ ^.
woo be to hem that sayen good is evil and evil is good and setten light as
derknes. and bitter instead of sweet. Thus done all tho that when they should
hate the sin of her even christian. and love the person / they hate the
person instead of the sin. and wene that they hate the sin / wherefore it
is a craft by it self who so cowde do it well /

That it is maystry to love men's persons and wisely hate her sins / Caplm
lxv
IT is no maystry for to wake and fast till thyn head ache. ne for to run to
Rome and to Iherusalem upon thy thy bare fete / ne for to sterte about and
preche. as if thou would torn all men by thy prechyng / Ne it is no mayst^^
for to make chirches or chapels: for to feed poor men and make hospitals. but
it is a maistry a man to love his eue^cristen in charity and wisely hate ye
syn^e of him and love the man / For though it be so y^ al thise deeds before
said are good in he^self. nevertheless they are common to good men and to bad /
for each man might do hem if that he would and had whereof / And for thy for
to do that each man may do I hold it no maistry / But for to love his even
christian in charity and hate his syn^e. may no man it do but oonli good men
which have it of the yefte of god and not of her traueile. To* ^
as saint poul says / Caritas dei diffusa est in cordibus vestris per sp^m
sccm^ qui datus est vobis / Love and charity is shed and spread in your hertes
by ye holy ghost. which is yeue^ to you / And therefore it is more precious and
the more deynte for to come by / All other good deeds wythouten this make not a
man good ne worthy the bliss of heaven. but this alone: and oonly this makes a
man good and al his good deeds medeful / All other yeftes of god and works of
man are comin to good and to bad / to chosen and to reproved / but this yeft of
charity is only of godd and of chosen souls /

That for the same deeds diverse men shall have diverse medes Caplm lxvi.
A Good man for the love of god fasteth waketh. gooth on pilgrymage / and
forsakyth all the likings of ye world sothfastly in his heart wythouten
feynynge / he shall have his mede in the bliss of heaven / And an ypocrite for
vaynglori of himself does the same deeds / and receives his mede here / Also
a very precher of goddis word fulfilled of charity and of mekenes sent of god
and of holy church received if he preche and teache goddis word / he shall
have a special mede of god / that is the aureole for his prechyng / An
ypocryte or an heretyke that has no mekenes ne charytee. ne arne send of god
nor yet of holy church / if they preche they have her mede here / Also a good
man in wordly state for love of god makyth many chyrches / chapelles. abbeys.
hospytals / and does many other good deeds of mercy / he shall have his mede
in the bliss of heaven / not for the deed in it self / but for ye good will
and the charity yt he has of ye yeft of god for to do tho good deeds / An
other man for vanytee of himself and worship and pleysyng of the world. and
for his own name does the same good deeds and has his mede here / The cause
is in all these that the tone has charity and the the other none which is one
and which is other our lord knowith and none but he /

That all men's good deeds shall be aproued that has liknes of good. saaf
the opyn heretic and the cursyd man. Caplm lxvii.
ANd therefore we should love and worship al men in our hertes. and aproue
examyn and receive all her deeds yt have the lyknesse of goodness though y^
doers in goddis sight ben bad save of the opyn heretyke and of the opyn cursed
man / Of thise two specially we shall flee and eschew the presence and the
co^minyng with hem / And we shall reprove and refuse her deeds seem they never
so good as long as they arne rebel to god and holy church / As if a worldly
cursed man make a church or feed poor men thou may sykerly hold it naught
and deem it as it is / Also if an opyn heretyke which is rebel to holy
church preche and teache / though he convert a hundred thousand souls /
hold the deed as to himself right naught / For these men are opynly out of
charity / without which is all naught that a man does /

That no good deed may make men saaf without charity / And that charity feel
they only yt be^ meke / ca lxviii
ANd therefore it is a great maistry a man to cun love his even christian in
charity / All this saying may be openly proved by saint poulis words thus / Si
linguis hominum loquar and angelorum / caritatem non habuero. nichil sum / Et
si habuero omne^ fidem ita vt montes transfera^. p^. cor^ i3
caritatem aute^ no^ habeam. nichil sum. Et si nouerim misteria oi^a. et si
destribuero om^es facultates meas in cibos pauperu^ / et tradidero corpus meum
igni vt ardeam / caritatem autem non habuero nichil michi prodest / Saint poul
in praysynge of charytee says thus / If I speak the langage of all men and of
angels also / if I have no charity I am right naught And if I have so great
faith that I may turn hills and bear hem away / and I have no charity I
am right naught And also though I had all manner of knowing of all pryu^tees /
without charity I am right naught / And if I give al yt I have to poor men and
my body to the fire to be brent. and I have no charity it profyteth me ryt nout
/ Here it semith by saint poules words that a man may do all good deeds
bodily wythouten charity / And that charity is naught else but for to love
god and his even cryste^ as himself. How should then any wretched caytit
living in earth what that he be have delight or trust or sykernes in himself for
ought that he can or may do with all his bodily myghtes or his kyndely reason
/ sith all this is naught worth wythouten love and charity to his even christian
/ And this charity may not be gotten with werkyng of himself / for it is a free
yefte of god sent in to a meke soul / as saint poul says. who then dare
hardely say that I have charity or I am in charity / Sothly no man may say
it sykerly / but he that is perfytly and sothfastly meke / Other men may trow
of hemself / and hope that they ben in charity by tokens / But he that is
perfytly meke felyth it / and therefore might he sykerly say it / Thus meke
was saint poul / and for thy said he thus of himself / Quis seperabit nos a
caritate dei? Tribulaco^ an angustia. etc / who shall depart me fro the
charity of god? Tribulaco^n or anguysshe. etc / And he answers himself and
says / There shall no creature put me fro the charity of god which I have in
christ Ihesu / Many men done deeds of charity and have no charity as I have
sayd^ For to repreue a syn^er for his syn^e to his ame^ding and in couenable
time it is a deed of charity. but to hate the syn^er instead of ye syn^e: it
is against charity / He that is verily meke can depart that one fro that other.
and no man but he / For though a man had all moral virtues of all
philosophers he cowde not do this / He should cu^ne hate the syn^e in all
other men for he hates it in himself / But he cowde not love the man in
charytee for all his phylosophye / Also if a man had knowing of all clergy
and of diuynite. and be not sothfastly meke he shall lightly err and stomble
and take the one for that other / But mekenes is worthy to receive a yefte of
god the which may not be learned by cunning of man / And therefore he that is
meke can hate the sin and truly love the man / But now perauenture thou
begynnest to dread for that I have said that charytee may not be gotten by no
work that thou may do / How shall thou then dooo / As unto this I say
that there is no thing so hard to get as charity / this is soth as within
our traueyle / And on the contrary wise I say that there is no yefte of god
that may so lightly be had as charity / For our lord yeuyth no yefte so
freely ne so gladly ne so comynly as he does charytee / How shall thou
then^e have it say thou. Be meke and low in spirit and thou shall have it /
And what is lyghter for to do tha^ for to be meke? Sothly no thing / Then
semyth it yt there is no thing that so lightly may be had as charity / and
therefore the needs not to be much adradde / Be meke and have it / Thus says
James thapostle. Deus superbis resistit^ hu^ilibus aute^ dat gracia^ / Our
lord he says ayenstondeth proud men / but to meke men he yeueth grace /
which grace is propirly his charity / for after the mesure of thy mekenes so
shall thou have charity / If thou have mekenes inperfitly oonly in will: not in
affecco^n. then shall thou have inperfyte charity This is good / for it
suffyseth to salvation as dauyd says Inperfectu^ meum videru^t oculi tui /
Lord with thyn eyes of mercy thou see mine inperfeccyon / But if thou have
mekenes perfytly. P.
then^e shall thou have perfyte charity. and that is best / The the other behouyth
us nedely to have it if we will be saaf. and this should we desire / Then if
thou ask me who is perfytely meke / thou shall no more have of me of mekenes
at this time but this / He is meke that sothfastly knowith himself as he is /

How a man shall wit how much wrath and envy is hyd in the ground of his
heart / Caplm lxix.
NOw turn yet again to this image if thou wolt assay how much ire and envy
is hid in thyn heart that thou felyst not / Look well and behold thyself
wisely when such stirynges of ire and envy against thyn even christian spryngen
out of thyn heart / The more styred that thou art by malencoly bitter or
wicked will against him. the more is this image in the / For the more thou
grutchest by inpacyence either aye^ste god for any trybulaco^n or syknes or
other bodily disese sent of god / or against thyn even christian for ought that
he does against the / the less is the image of Ihesu reformed in the. I say
not that such grutchynges or flesshly angrynes am dedely sins / but I say
that they letten the clennes of heart and pees of conscience that thou may not
have full charity by ye which thou sholdest come to life contemplatyf / For
that end is the purpoos of all my saying. that thou sholdest not oonly cleanse
thyn heart fro dedely sins: but also fro venyall as much as thou myghtest.
And that the ground of sin might by grace of Ihesu christ somewhat be slecket
in the /

By what tokens thou shall know if thou love thyn enmye / And what ensample
thou shall take of christ for to love him / Caplm lxx
FOr though it be so that thou felyst none evil against thyn even cryste^ for
a time / yet art thou not syker that the ground of ire is quenched in the /
ne yet art thou not lord of the virtue of charity / For suffer him towche the
a lityll by angry or a shrewde word / and thou shall feel anon if thine heart
be yet made hole by fulness of charity / The more thou art styred and evil
willed against the persone^ the ferder art thou fro charity / And if thou
naught be styred against the person. neither by angry chere outwarde^ ne by no
preuy hate in thy heart for to dispyse and deem him or for to set him at
naught. but the more shame or vylanye he does to the in word or in deed the
more pity and compassion thou have of him. as thou would have of a man that
were out of his mind / And the thinkyth you can not find in thyn heart for
to hate him. for love is so good in himself / but pray for him and help him.
and desiryng his amendyng / not oonly with thy mouth as ypocrytes can do. but
with affecco^n of love in thyn heart / then^e haast you perfect charity to thyn
even christian / This charity had saint stephen perfitly when he prayed for hem
that stoned him to deed / This charity cou^seyled christ to those that would be
his perfect folowers when he said thus / Diligite inimicos vro^s vn^facite hiis
qui oderu^t vos / etc^ M. v^
Loves your enmyes and do good to hem that haten you / prays for hem that
pursuen you And therefore if thou wol follow christ be like to him in this craft
/ Lere for to love thyn enmyes and sinful men / for all thise arn thy even
cryste^ / Look and bethynke the how christ loved Judas which was both his
dedely enmye and a sinful caytyf How goodly christ was to him. how benygne. how
curteyes / and how lowly to him that he knew dampnable / and nevertheless he
chase him to his apostle: and sent him for to preche with other apostles / He
yaaf him power for to werche miracles* he showed the same to him good chere in
word and in deed as he did to other apostles / He wysshe his fete and fed
him with his precious body / and prechid to him as he did to other appostles /
he wryed him not openly for it was preuy / ne myssaied him not. ne dispysed him
not. ne spoke never evil of him / and yet though he had done all thise. he had
said but soth / And ouermore when Judas took him. he kyssed him and called him
his friend / All this charity showed christ unto Judas the which he knew for
dampnable. in no manner feynyng ne flateryng but in the sothfastnes of good
love and clean charity / For though it were soth that Judas was not worthy for
to have had any yefte of god or any sign of love for his wyckidnes nevertheless
it was worthy and skylfull that our lord should sheew as he is / He is love and
