goodness to all his creatures as he did to Judas / I say not that he loved him
for his sin. ne he loved him not for his chosen as he loved saint peter / but
he loved him in asmoche as he was his creature. and showed him tokens of love
if he would have be amended thereby / Follow after so^what if thou may / for
though thou art stoken in an house with thy body^ nevertheless in thyn heart
where the stead of love is thou should mow have part of such love to thyn
even christian as I speak of / Who so weneth himself to be a perfyte lover and
follower of crystis techyng in his living. as some man weneth yt he is in
asmoche as he precheth and techeth. and is poor of worldly good as christ was /
and can not follow criste in this love and charity for to love his even christian
each man good and bad friends and fooes wythouten feynynge flaterynge and
dispisyng in heart against the man. angrynes malicyous repreuyng: sothly he
begyleth himself / The nerer that he weneth he be. the ferder he is / For
christ said to hem that would be his discyples thus / Hoc est preceptu^ meu^ vt
diligatis inuicem sicut dilexi vos / This is my biddyng that ye should love
together as I have loved you. For if ye love as I have loved then^e are ye my
discyples / But now sayste thou. how shalt thou love him that is badde as well
as him that is good / As unto this I say thus. that thou shall love both good
and badde in charity but not for the same cause as I shall tell how / Thou
shalt love thyn even christian as thyself / Now you shall love thyself only in
god or else for god / In god thou love thyself when you art ryghtfull by
grace and virtuous / and love not thyself but oonly for that ryghtwysnesse
and virtues that god yeuyth ye then love thou thyself in god for thou
love not thyselfe but god / Also for god thou love thyself / as if thou
were in dedeli sin and would be made ryghtfull and wertuous. then^e love
thou thyself not as thou art / for thou art vnryghtful but as thou would be
/ Right so shall thou love thyn even christian / If they ben good and rightful
/ thou shall love hem by charity in god oonly for they ben good and ryghtful /
for then love thou god in hem as goodness and ryghtwysnes. more than if they
ben badde in dedely syn^e / as thyn enmyes that haten the or other of the
which thou have full euyde^ce that they are not in grace / yet shall thou love
hem / not as they arne. ne as good men and ryghtfull men / for they arn badde
and unrightful / but thou shall love hem for god that they might be good and
ryghtful / And so shall thou no thing hate in hem but that thing that is
contrary to ryghtwysnesse / and that is sin / This is as I vndstonde the
techyng of saint Austyn for to depart the love of the man fro the hate of the
sin and the love of thyn even christian / He that is meke or would sothfastly
be me can love thus his even crysten^ and none but he /

How a man shall know how much couetyse is hid in his heart / Caplm lxxi^
Lift well up this image and look well abowte. and thou shall mow see
couetyse and love of erthly things occupye a great party of this image.
though it seem lityl Thou have forsaken richesse and much hauour of this
world / and art spered in a dongeon / but have thou forsaken clenly the love
of all this / I hope not yet / It is less maystry for to forsake worldly good
than to forsake the love of it / Peraue^ture thou have not forsaken thy
couetyse / but thou have changed it fro great things in to small / as fro a
pownde unto a penny / and fro a silver piece unto a disshe of an halfpeny This is
a simple change / thou art no good merchant / These ensamples arn
chyldisshe / nevertheless they betoken more / If thou trow not me assaye
thyself / If thou have love and delight in the having and holdyng of any thing
that thou have such as it is / with ye which love thou fedest thyn heart for
a time Or if thou have desire and yernyng for to have some thing that you haste
not / with which desire thyn heart is traueyled and stourbled by unskillful
belynesse that the clean desire of virtue and of god may not rest therein / this
is a token that there is couetise in this image / And if thou wolte assaye
better / look if any thing that thou have be taken away fro the by maystry or
by borowyng. or by any other wise. and thou may not get it again / and for thy
thou art disesed angered and trowbled in thyn heart both for thou want that
thing that thou would have / and may not have it / and also ayenste him that
has it you art styred for to strive and chyde with him for he might restore
the again and will not / this is a token that thou love worldly goods / For
thus done worldly men / when her good and her richesse is taken fro hem they
arn heavy sorry angry and chiding and striuyng against hem that have it openly by
word and by deed / but thou do all this in thyn heart pryuely where god
sees and yet thou art in more defawte than a worldly man. For you have forsaken
in lyckenes the love of worldly things / but a worldly man has not so / and
therefore he is exscused though he strive and pursue for his goods by lawful
ways for to have hem again / But now say thou that the behooves for to have
thy necessaryes of such things as longen to the as well as a worldly man / I
grant well thereto / but thou should not love it for it self / ne likyng have
in the holdyng ne in ye keeping / ne sorrow ne heaviness feel in the lesyng or
in ye withdrawyng of it / For as saint gregory says / Asmoche sorrow as thou
have in lesyng of a thing. Greg*
so much love had thou in the keeping / And therefore if thyn heart were
made hoole / and thou had sothfastly felt desire of ghostly things: and
had there with all a syghte of the leest ghostly thing that is. all ye love
and the likyng of any erthly thing thou sholdest set it at naught / it
should not cleue upon the / For to love and for to have more than the needs
skylfully oonly for lust and likynge it is a great defawte / Also for to
fetchen thy love upon ye thing that the needs for it self / it is defawte
but not so great But for to have and vsen that thing that the needs wythoute^
love of it more than kind or need asks wythoute^ which the thing may not
be used / it is no defawte / ^othli in this point as I trow many that have
the state and the lyknesse of pouertee arn much let and hyndered fro the
love of god / I ne accuse no man ne no state reprove / for in each astate
some arn good and some arn other / But one thing I say to every man or woman
that has taken the state of wylfull pouerte whether he be religyous or seculer
or what degree he be in / as long as his love and his affection is bounden and
fastened as. and it were glewed with ye love of any erthly thing that he has
or would have / he may not have ne feel sothfastly the clean love and the clear
syghte of ghostly things / Augus.
For saint Austyn said to our lord thus / Lord he loves the but lytill / ye
louyth any thing with the / that he loves not for the / For ye more love and
couetyse of any erthly thing is with the / the less is the love of god in
thyn heart / For though it be so that this love of erthly thing puts hem not
out of charity but if it be so much that it strangle the love of god and of
her even christian / sothely it hyndreth hem and lets hem fro the fervor of
charity / and also fro that special mede which they should have in the bliss
of heaven for perfect pouerte / and that is a great loss if they might see it
/ For who so might know ghostly mede how good how precious and how worthy it
is / for it is aye lasting / he would not for the love of all erthly Joy or
hauour of all erthly thing if he might have it wythoute^ syn^e let ne less
the lest mede of the bliss of heaven which he might have if that he would / I
speak ferther than I do. But I pray the do thus as I say by ye grace of god
if thou may or any other man who so will / For that were a comfort to my
heart that if I may not have it in myself as I say. that I might have it in
the / Or in any other creature which has received more plente of his grace
than I / But see now then sith couetyse in the naked ground lets a man or
a woman so much fro the ghostly felyng of the love of god / how much more
then^e it lets and combreth worldly men and wym^en the which by all her
wits and bodily besynes night and day study and traueyle how they might
get riches and plente of worldly good / They can none other delight have but in
worldly things / ne they will not for they seche it not / I say no more of hem
at this time: for in this writing I speak not to hem / But this I say / if
they might see and would see what they do / they should not do so /

How a man shall know when he synneth not in etynge and drynkyng / and when he
synneth venyally / and when dedely / Caplm lxxii.
YEt may thou see more in this image though it be derke. and that is flesshli
love to thiself. in glotenye accidie and lecherye / Thise flesshly likings
maken a man full bestly and far fro the inly savor of the love of god. and
fro ye clear syghte of ghostly things / But now say thou. Sith the behooves
nedelynges ete and drink and sleep. and that may thou not do wythouten likyng
/ therefore the thynkyth this liking is no sin / As unto this I say. that
if thou keep in etynge or drinking and in other needful things of thy body
mesure in thy need / and thou receyuest no more likynge than kind askyth /
And all this thou do for ghostely delight which thou felyst in thy soul /
I grant ye forsothe that thou then synnest right naught therein / for then
can thou well ete and sleep / Sothly and wythouten doubt I am full far fro
that knowing and ferd fro the werchynge / For to ete I have by kind / but to
cu^ne ete I may not but by the grace of god. Saint poul had by grace this
cunnyng as he says himself thus / Vbique and in oi^bus institutus su^. scio
saciari and esurire / habu^ dare and penuria^ pati. Phil iiii
Oi^a possu^ in eo qui me co^fortat: I am informed and kenned in all things.
For I can hunger and I can ete. I can with plente and I can with pouerte / I
may all in him that strenghthith me / Saint austyn said till our lord thus
Lord thou have teched me that I should take mete as a medicine / Augus.
Hunger is a syknes of kind / and mete is a medicyne there to / Therefore the
likyng that comyth with all in asmoche as it is kyndly and nedfull it is no
syn^e / but when it passith into lust and into wylfull likyng then^e it is
sin / And therefore ther^ lies all the maystrye for to cu^ne depart wisely
need fro lust and wylfull likyng they are so knytte together / and that one
comyth with that other. so that it is hard for to receive that one as the need
and repreue that other as wylfull lust the which often comyth vnd color of
need / Nevertheless sith it is so yt need is the ground of this* and that
need is no sin / for be a man never so holy him behouyth to ete and drink
and sleep therefore the lust and the likynge that comyth vnd the color of this
need and passyth this need is the less syn^e / For a man synneth not dedely
comynly in glotenye. but if he be encombred with other dedely sins beforn
done / then^e may he the light liar sin dedely in this / For it is soth he
that chesyth lust and liking of his flesh and delytes in welfare of mete or
drink as full rest of his heart that he would never have other lyffe ne other
bliss but live ever in such lust of his flesh if he might. it is no dowte
but y^ he syn^eth dedely / for he loves his flesh more than god / But he
that lies in dedely sin of pride or envy or such other he is so blinded
by the devil y^ for the time he has no power of his free will / and therefore
he may not well ayensto^de flesshly likings when they come but falls down
wylfully to hem as a best does to karyon / And in asmoche as he has no
general will before to god principally by cause that he is in dedely syn^e.
therefore ye lust of glotenye the which he falls in lightly is to him dedely
sin / for he makith none aye^stondyng general ne special. But a another man
or woman which in grace or charity has always a good general will to god in
his soul wheder he sleep or wake ete or drink or what good deed yt he does.
so that it be not evil in itself by the which will and desire he chesyth
god above all thing. and has lever forbere all thing of the world than wrath
his god for love of him / This will though it be but general it is of so
great virtue by the grace of our lord Ihu^ that if he fall by freelte in lust
and in likyng of mete and of drink or of such other siknes. either by excess
of tomoche etyng or to often or to gredely or to lustly. and delicatly. or
tosone in vntyme. it saves him and kepith him fro dedely syn^e / And this is
soth aslonge as he is in charity by other deeds. and kepyth his general will
to all that he does. and namly if he know among his own wretchidnes and
cry after mercy. and be in purpose specially to aye^stonde such fleshly
lusts for our lord is good and merciful. and thise venyall sins of glotenye
he foryeuyth right sone unto a meke soul / For the stiryng and the likyng of
glotenye in asmoche as they are hardest for to flee by cause of need of ye
bodily kind among all other sins are most exscuable and leest perilous /
And therefore thou shall not rise against the ground of this syn^e as you shall
against all other sins / for ye ground of this sin is oonly need which
may not be escaped but if thou wylt do worse as slay ye need as many foles
done / which sholden slay the theyf and spare the true man / That is to say /
They sholden slay unskillful lust and the wilful likyng. and spare and keep
the bodily kind. and they do not so / But against all other sins thou shall
arise for to destroy not oonly dedely sins and the great venyals / but also
against the ground of hem as much as thou may / See by this skylle / Thou
may not live without mete and drink / but thou may live without lecherye if
thou will and never but the better / And therefore thou shall not flee only the
deed of it which is dedely sin. but also wylfull likyng of it in thine heart
withouten deed which is venyall syn^e / and sometime it is dely. but also thou
shall traueyle against the ground of it for to destroy the felyng and the
risyng of flesshly stiryng /

How the ground of lechery should be destroyed with ghostli traueyle and with
bodily / Caplm lxxiii.
But this traueyle against the ground of lechery shall be goostly / as by
prayers and ghostly virtues. and not by bodily penance. For wit thou well
that if thou fast and wake and scourge thyselfe / and do all that thou can /
thou shall never have ye clennes and the chastity without the yefte of god and
the garce of mekenes / Thou sholdest sooner slay thyselfe than thou sholdeste
slay flesshly stirynges and felynges of lust and lechery either in thyn heart
or in thy flesh by any bodily penance / But by the grace of Ihesu in a meke
soul the ground may be much stopped and destroyed. and the spring may be
much dried / And that is very chastity in body and in soul / On the same
manner may be said of pride and of couetise and of such other. for thou might
live if thou were not proud ne covetous / And therefore thou shall destroy all
the felynges of hem asmoche as you may / But in glotenye thou shall rise and
smite away the unskillful stirynges. and save the ground hole /

That a man should be besye to put away all stirynges of sin / but more
besye of ghostly sins than of bodily Caplm lxxiiii
ANd therefore he that ryseth against the felyng of flesshly likynge in mete and
drink more fully and more sha^ply than of pride or couetyse / which for they
semen fair aren not lyghtely reproved / Or of Envy. or of Lecherye / I say
that he is half blind / for he sees not yet ghostly uncleanness / As of pride
and envy how foul it is in goddis site / I hope if a man might see with his
eye ghostly how foul pride and couetyse arne in the syghte of god / and how
contrary to him / He should more loath a styryng of pride and the vain liking
of it / And also he should the more agryse and rise against that evil will of
envy or ire to his even christian than many a styryng or lykyng either of
glotenye or of lecherye / Nevertheless all men wenen not so / For comynly men
arn more eschew for to feel a styryng of flesshly sin / and have for it more
sorrow and heaviness than for the great likings in vain glory or in other
ghostly sins / But they arn not wise / For if they will understand holy
writ and doctors sawes thereof / they sholden find as I say / which I ne
may ne will rehearse now / I will not exscuse hem that fallen in likings of
glotenye and lecherye that they sin not / For I wot well that all the spyces
of hem arn sin more or less after the mesure of the lust of the sin and
other lykynges with wylfull cyrcumstaunces / But I would that thou knew and
charged all / ylke a sin as it is / more the more / as arn ghostli sins /
less the less arn as flesshly sins. And yet shall thou nevertheless hate and
flee all both bodily and ghostly upon thy might / For wit thou well that
flesshly desires and unskillful likings in mete and drink / Or any likings
that longen to the body passing reasonable need. though they ben not always
great sins to him that is in charity / nevertheless to a soul that desires
clennes and ghostly felyng of god they arn full heavy paynfull and bitter and
much for to eschew. For the spirit may not feel his kyndly savor with in.
till the flesh have lost his bestly savor wythouten /

That hunger and other bodily pains lets much goostly werchynge / Caplm
lxxv^
ANd therefore if thou wolt come to clennes of heart the behouyth ayenstonde
unskillful stiryng of flesshly desires / But against the ground thou shall not
rise. as I have said before / For the ground of it is need. as kyndely hunger
which thou shall nedelynges feel and tent thereto in time / and help thyself
against it by medicyne of mete. as thou would help thiself reasonable against a
bodily syknes / that thou might more freely serve god both bodily and ghostly
/ For wit thou well what man or woman that shall be occupied ghostly in
thoughts: unskillful pain or hunger wylfully taken or bodily syknes in the
stomach or in the head / or in other party of the body for the defawte of good
rulyng of himself. by tomoche fasting. or by any other wise / shall much let
the spirit / and much hinder him fro the knowing and beholdynge of ghostly
things / but if he have the more grace / For though it be so that bodily
pain / either of penance or of syknesse or else bodily occupacyon sometime
lets not the fervor of love to god in devotion / but often encreasyth it /
Nevertheless I hope that it lettith the fervor of love in contemplaco^n the
which may not be had ne felyd sadly but in rest of body and of soul /

What Remedy a man shall use against defawte made in etynge or drynkyng / Caplm
lxxvi.
FOr thy doo^ thou skylfully that longs to the / and keep thy bodily kind
upon reison / and suffer god then send what he will hele or syknesse / take
it gladly / and grutche not against god wylfully / Do thou as I say: take thy
mete as it commyth / And ordeyne for it if need be upon reason / And take it
gladly as for need / But be well waar of lust that commyth with need / ^schewe
to much as well as to lityll And so when thou haste done / and then it
commyth to thy mind the bytynge of conscience that thou haste eten tomoche /
And so then begynnest for to tarry the / and draw to over much byttyrnesse
/ Lift up the desire of thine heart to thy good lord Ihesu / and know thyself
for a wretch and a best / and ask him forgyuenesse. and say that thou will
amend it / and trust of forgyuenesse / Leave of then and tarry no longer
with all / ne strive not much as thou would destroy it utterly / for it is
not worth for to do so / Thou shalt never bring it so abowte / but redily
ordeyne the redi to some other occupacyon bodily or ghostly / after thou felyst
the disposyd that thou myghtest more profit in other virtues / as meekness
and charity. For wit thou well he that has in his desire and in his
traueylle none other reward to none other thing but to mekenes and charytee /
aye cryenge after hem how he might have hem / he shall in that desire /
werchynge folowand after profit and wexe in all other virtues / as in chastyte
abstynence and such other if he have but lityll reward in hem in a year more
than he should wythouten this desire profit in seven / if he strive with
glotenye lechery and such other contynuelly / and beat himself with scourges
each day fro morrow to euensong time /

That thorough by desire and traueyle for meekness and charytee a man comyth
sooner to other virtues than by traueyle in hemself / Caplm lxxvii.
Get to the then mekenes and charytee / And if thou wolte traueyle and
swynke besily for to have hem. you shall have enough for to do in getyng of hem
/ And if you may get hem / they shall rule the and mesure the full pryuely how
thou shall ete and how thou shall drink and socour all thy bodyly need that
there shall no man wit it but if thou wolte / and that shall not be in
perplexite ne in ire ne in anguyssh^nes and heuines ne in lusts ne in
likings. but in pees of glad conscience wc a sad restfulnes. I speak ferder
tha^ I thout to have spoken in this mater^. but netheles do if you may as I the
say. and I hope god shall make al well / by this yt I have said may you somdel
see in this image of sin how much it lets the / The gospel says how
Abraham spoke to the rich man that was beryed in hell on this wise / Chaos
magnum inter nos and vos firmatum est vt hii qui volu^t transire ad vos non
possu^t nec huc transmeare / There is a great chaos. that it to sayen a thycke
derknesse between us and the that we mow not come to the ne thou till us /
This derke image in thy soul and min also may be called a great chaos / that
is a great derknes. for it lets us that we mow not come to abraham which is
Ihesu / and it lettyth him that he woll not come to us*

Of the derknes of the image of sin. And what comyth in by the wyndowes
thereof / Caplm lxxviii.
Lift up thy lantern and see in this image five wyndowes by the which sin
comyth in to thy soul as ye prophet says / ^
Mors ingreditur per fenestras nostras / Death comyth in by our wyndowes / Thise
wyndowes arn the five wits by the which thy soul gooth out fro by himself /
and sechyth his delight and his fedynge in erthely things against his own kind
/ As by the eye for to see curyous and fair things / and so of other wits
/ By the vnskylful vsyng of thise wits in to vanyte wilfully / thy soul is
much let fro ghostly wits within / and therefore the behooves stoppe^
thise wyndowes or spear hem / but oonly when need asks for to open hem /

That the soul for defawte of knowing of it self gooth onte by five wyndowes
to seche outward likynge. Caplm lxxix.
ANd that were lityll maystry to the if thou myghtest ones see thy soul by
clear understanding what it is and how fair it is in his own kind / Ne it
were that it is so ouerlayed with a black mantell of this foul image. but
for you knowist it not. therefore you leuest the inly sight of thiself and
sechest thy mete forth withoute^ as a best unreasonable. thus says lord
manassyng to a chosen soul in holy writ. Si ignoraste o pulcra inter
mulieres. Cant^ 1.
egredere and abi post vestigia gregu^ sodalium tuorum et pasce edos tuos /
Thou fair among wymmen if thou know not thyselfe. goo out and walk after
the steps of the flock of thy fellows and feed thy get / and it is thus
much for to say / Thou soul fair by kind made to the lyknesse of god freel
as a woman in the body for ye first sin by cause that thou know not
thyselfe / that angels food should be thy delyces within / Therefore thou ghost
out by thy bodily wits and sechest thy mete and thy likynge as a best of
the flock / that is as one repreuyd / and therewyth thou fedest thy thoughts
and thyn affeccyons which arn unclean as gotes / It is a shame to the for to
do so /

That a soul should not beg without forth but with in of Ihesu that it needs
/ Caplm lxxx.
ANd therefore turn home again in thyself and hold the within / and beg no
more wythouten namely swynes mete / For if thou woll algates be a beggar ask
and crave within of thy lord Ihesu / for he is rich enough / and gladlyer
woll give the than thou wolt ask / And run no more out as a best of the
flock / that is a worldly man or woman that has no more delight but in his
bodily wits. And if thou do thus thy lord Ihesu woll give the all that the
needs / For he may led the in to his wine seler / and make the for to assaye
of his wynes which the lyketh best for he has many tonnes / Thus a chosen
soul Ioyenge in holy writ says of our lord / Introduxit me rex in cellam
vinariam / Cant* ^.
A king ladde me in to a wine celer / And that is for to say^ / ^ In as much
as I forsake the dronkennes of flesshely lusts and worldely lykynges / which
arne bitter as wormode / f^r thy the king of bliss lord Ihesu led me in /
That is to say / First in to my self for to behold and know myself / And
after he led me in to his celer / that is to say. abouen myself by
ouerpassyng oonly in till him. and gaaf me assaye of his wine / yt is for to
taast a syknes of ghostly swetnes and heavenly Joy / Thise arne not words of
me a wretchyd caytif living in sin / but they arn words of the spowse of our
lord in holy wrytt / and thise words I say to the that you might draw in thy
soul fro wythouten / and follow after as thou may /

That the hole of ymaginaco^n nedyth to be stopped as well as the wyndowes of
the wits / Caplm lxxxi
But now say thou that thou do so / thou see no worldly things ne
herest none. ne have none use of thy bodily wits more than need asks / and
for thy thou art enclosed / As to this I say. If thou do thus as I hope thou
do then have thou stopped a great wyndow of this image. but yet art thou
not syker. for thou have not stopped the prive holes of the ymaginyng in thine
heart / For if thou see me not with thy bodily eye thou may see me in thy
soul by ymagynaco^n / and so may thou do of al bodily things / Then^e if
thy soul be fed wilfully by ymaginacio^s of vanytees of the world. and
desiryng of worldly things for a wylfull comfort and ease / sothly if thy
soul be within as for the bodyly wits. it is nevertheless full far
wythouten by such vain ymaginaco^n / But now ask thou whether it be any
great sin a soul for to occupye him in such vanytees either in wits or in
ymaginyng / As unto this I say that I would yt thou sholdest never ask man
this questyon / For he that wylt sothfastly love god he askith not cominly
whether this is greter syn^e or this / For him shall think what thing lettith
him fro the love of god is great sin / and him shall think no thing sin
but that thing which is not good. and lets him fro the love of god / What
is sin but a wanting or a forberyng of good / I say not that it shall be
paynful to him as a dedely sin or a venyall should ben. ne I say not but
that he knows dedely fro venyall and more flees it /

When the use of the wits ben dedely syn^e. and when venyall / Caplm lxxxii.
Nevertheless some dele shall I say to thy questyon. For thy desire drawyth
more out of mine heart than I thought for to have said in the beginning / Our
lord says in the gospel thus / Homo quida^ fecit cenam magna^ etvocauit
multos and misit seruu^ suu^ dicere inuitatis vt venire^t / Primus dixit.
Villa^ emi. Luc. xiiii
rogo te habe me excusatu^ / Scds dixit / Iuga bou^ emi quinque et eo probare
illa / Et tercius dixit. Vxore^ duxi ideo non possu^ venire / A man made a
great supper and called many thereto. And sent his servant at supper time after
hem that were prayed / The first exscused him and said on thy^ wise that he
might not come for he had boughte a town / The the other also excused him that
he might not come for he had boughte five yockes of oxen and yede for to assaye
hem / The third for he had weddded a wife / I leave for to speak of the first
and of the last / and I tell the of the myddelest of him that boughte the
oxen / for he is to this purpoos / Five yockes of oxen betoke^ the five wits
which arn beestly as an ox. Now this man that was called to the supper was
not repreued for he boughte these oxen / but for he yede for to assaye he^ and
so he would not come / Right so say I to the / For to have thy wits and
use hem in need. it is no sin / But if thou goo wylfully for to assaye hem
by vain delight in creatures then it is sin / For if thou chese that delight
as for a fynall rest of thy soul. and as a full likyng / that thou kepeste
none other bliss to have but such maner^ worldly vanyte then it is dedely /
for thou chesest it as thy god / and so shall thou be put fro ye supper / For
saint poul forbede us that we should not assaye our wytt so when he said thus /
Post co^cupisce^cias tuas no^ eas. Thou shall not goo after thy lust. ne will
fully assaye thy likings / A man or a woman that is encombred with dedely
syn^e shall not well escape dedely syn^e in this though he see it not / but I
hope it touches not the / Nevertheless if thou by freelte delight the in thy
wits and such vanytee / but in that thou kepest the in charity in other
sides / and thou chesest not this delight for a full rest of thy soul but thou
set test aye god before all thing in thy desire. this sin is venial after the
circu^staunce more or less / ne thou shall not for thise venyall sins be put
fro the supper in the bliss of heaven / but thou shall want the taastyng and
the assayeng of that delycate supper living in earth / but if thou be besye
with all thy mytes for to ayenstonde such venyall sins / For though it be so
that venyall sins break not charity / sothly they let the fervor and the
ghostly felyng of charity /

How a ghostly man or woman shall have hem to hem that come to hem / Caplm
lxxxiii.
But now say thou that thou may not keep the fro heryng of vanytees. for
diverse men worldly and other come often for to speak with the. and tell the
some tales of vanyte As unto this I say thus / that comynyng with thyn even
christian is not much against the but helpith the sometime if thou werche wisely /
For thou may assaye thereby ye mesure of thy charity to thyn even christian
whether it be much or lityll / Thou art bounden as each man and woman is to
love thin eue^ christian pryncypally in thine heart and also in deed / for to
show hem tokens of charity as reason asks after thy might and after thy
knowing / Now sythen it is so that thou owe not to goo out of thyn house
for to seek occasion how thou mite profit thyn even christian by deeds of mercy
/ by cause thou art encloos^ Nevertheless thou art bounden for to love hem
all in thyn heart / and to hem that come to the to show hem tokens of love
sothfastly / And therefore who so will speak with the what that he be. or in
what degree that he be and you know not what he is ne why he comyth / be soon
ready wc a good will for to wit what his will is / Be not dangerous ne suffer
him not long abide the / but look how ready and how glad thou would be if
an angel of heaven would come so and speak with the. so ready and so buxome be
thou in will for to speak with thyn even christian when he comyth to the for thou
woost not what he is ne whi he comes ne what need he has of the. or thou of
him till thou have assayed / And though thou be in prayer or in deuoco^n that
the thinks looth for to break of. for the thinks you sholdest not leave god
for no ma^nys speech / me thinks not so in this caas. For if thou be wise
thou shall not leave god. but thou shall find him and have him and see him in
thyn even christian as well as in prayer / But on a other manner thou shall have
him than in prayer / If thou can well love thyn even christian it should not
hinder the for to speak with hem dyscretly / Dyscrecyon shall thou have on this
manner as me thinks / Who so comyth to the ask him mekely what he will / And
if he come for to tell his dysese and for to be comforted of thy speech here
him gladly / and suffer him say what he will for ease of his own heart / And
when he has done comfort him if you can gladly. goodly and charitably. and
soon break of / And then^e after that if he will fall in to idle tales or
vanytees of the world or of other men's deeds / answer him but litylll ne
feed not his speech / and he shall soon be weary. and sone take his leave / If
it be an other man that comith for to teache the as a man of holy church here
him lowely with reverence for his order / And if his speech comfort the ask
of him. and make the not for to teache him / It falls not to the for to teache
a priest but in need / If his speech comfort the not answer little. and he
will soon take his leave / If it be a another man yt comes to give the his
alms. or else for to here ye speak. or for to be taute of ye. speak godely
and mekeli to hem all. repreue no man of his defawtes / it falls not to the
but if he be ye more homely with the that thou woost well that he will take it
of the / And shortly to say as thou conceyuest that should profit thyn even
christian namly ghostly may thou say if you can and he will take it / And of all
other things keep scilence asmoche as thou may / and thou shall in short
time have but lityll prees that shall let the / Thus me thinks / do better
if thou can /

Of the derke image of sin / and of the clothyng ther^of / Caplm lxxxiiii.
BY this that I have said may thou see a lityll the derknes of this image of
syn^e / not for I have discryued it fully to the as it is for I can not /
Nevertheless by this lityll thou may see more if thou look well / But now say
thou whereby wost thou that I bear such an image about with me as thou spekest
of / As on this I can answer / I may take upon me a word said by the
prophet / (...). 12*
and it is this / Inueni idolu^ michi / That is to say / I have found a falls
image that men callen a mawmente in myself well foul disfygured and forshapen
with wretchydnes of all these sins which I have spoken of / by the which I
am casten down in many flesshly lykynges and worldly vanytees fro clen^es of
heart and felyng of goostly virtues more than I can or may say. and that me
repe^teth and I cry god mercy / By this wretchidnesse that I feel in myself
more than I have said may I the better tell the of thyn image / For all come
we of adam and of eve clothed with clothes of a bestes hyde / as holy writ
says of our lord thus. Fecit deus ade and vrori eius tunicas pelliceas /
Gen^. 3.
Our lord made to adam and to his wife clothes of a bestes hyde / In token
that for his syn^e he was forshape^ like to a best / with which bestly
clothes we al ben borne and vmbilapped and disfigured fro our kyndly shappe /

Which be^ the lym^es of the image of syn^e / Caplm lxxxv.
Then is this an ugly image for to look upon / The head is pride / For pride
is the first and the pryncipall sin as the wise man says / Iniciu^ oi^s
pcti^ superbia / Ecc^^.
The beginning of all manner of sin is pride / The back and the hinder party
of it is couetyse. Phil 3.
as saint poul says / Que retro su^t obliuiscens in anteriora me extendo / I
shall foryete all worldly things which arn backewarde / and I shall stretche
me forward to endless things / The breast in the which is the heart is envy /
for it is no flesshly syn^e but it is a deuels sin as the wise man says /
Inuidia diaboli mors intrauit in orbe^ter rarum. Sap^. 2.
Imitant illu^ oe^s qui ex part eius sunt / By envy of the devil death
comyth in to all the world / For thy all thoo that are of his party follow him
therein. The arms of it are wrath in asmoche as a man wreketh him of his
wrath by his arms against crystis biddyng in the gospel. ^
Si quis te percus serit super vna^ maxilla^ prebe sibi altera^ / If a man
smite the upon the tone cheke with his hand. thou shall not smite him again but
offer him that other cheke^ The belly of this image is glotenye as saint poul
says / Esca ventri et venture escis. ^
deus hu^c and has destruet / Mete serves to the belly. and the belly serves to
get mete / but god shall destroy both belly and mete / That shall be at the
last end in the full reformyng of his chosen and in demyng of reproved / The
members of it are lechery of the which saint poul says thus / No^ exhibeatis
membra ^estra arma iniquitatis ad peccatu^ / ye shall not give your me^bres
specially your pryue members for to be arms of syn^e / The fete of this image
are accidye / Therefore the wise man says to the slow for to styre him to good
works / Discurre festina suscita amicu^ tuum / That is to say / Run quyckly
about unto good works and haast the soon / for the time passyth / prou. ^.
and reyse up thy friend which is Ihesu by devout prayer and meditaco^n /
Here have thou herd the members of this image /

Whereof the image of Ihesu is made. and whereof the image of sin / and how we
ben passing forth in the image of sin / Caplm lxxxvi.
THis is not the image of Ihesu but it is liker an image of the devil / For
the image of Ihesu is made of virtues with mekenes and perfyte love and charity
/ but this is of false flesshly love to thyself with al these members festuyd
thereto This image berest thou and every man what that he be until by grace of
Ihesu it be somdele destroyed and broken down / Thus it semyth that dauyd
says in the sawter book / Veru^p tamen in ymagine pertransit homo. P^ 3viii
sed et frustra conturbat This is for to say / Though it be so that a man
were made in the begyn^yng to the image of god stable and steadfast /
nevertheless by cause of syn^e he forthpassith living in this world in this
image of synne^ by the which he is unstable and trowbled in vain / Also saint
poul spekyth of this image thus Sicut portauimus ymagine^ terreni hominis sic
portemus ymagine^ celestis / That is to say / If we wol come to the love of
god / as we have here before borne ye image of the erthly man. first adam that
is the image of syn^e. Right so now let us bear the image of the heavenly man
Ihesu which is the image of virtues /

How we should crucifye this image of sin. and quycken the image of Ihesu /
Caplm lxxxvii.
WHat shall thou then^e do with this image / I answer the by a word you the
Jews said to pylat of christ. John. 1^.
Crucifige eu^ / Take thou this body of sin and do him on ye cross / That
is for to say / Break down this image and slay the false love of sin in
thyself / as cristis body was slain for our sin and our trespaas / Right so
the behouyth if thou wolte be like to christ slay thy bodily likynge and
flesshely lusts in thyselfe / Gal. ^.
Thus said saint poul / Qui autem cristi sunt came^ suam crucifixerunt cum
viciis and concupiscenciis / Thise that arn cristis folowers has crucified and
slain her flesh that is the image of sin with all the lusts and the
unskillful lykynges of it / Slay then and break down pride. and set up
meekness / Also break down ire and envy and reyse up love and charity to
thyn even christian. Also instead of couetyse. pouertee in spirit / Instead of
accidye. fervor in devotion with glad redynes to all good deeds / And in the
stead of glotenye and lecherye. sobirte and chastyte in body and in soul /
This co^sydered saint poul when he said thus / Deponentes veterem homine^ cu^
suis actibus qui corru^pitur scdm desideria erroris. Ep^. iiii
et induite nouu^ homine^ qui scdm deum creatus est in sanctitate and iusticia
/ ye shall put down the old man that is the image of sin of the old adam
with all his members / for he is rotin in desires of error / and ye shall shape
you and clothe you in a new man which is the image of god by holiness and
ryghtwysnes and full head of virtues / who shall help the. break down this
image / Sothly thy lord Ihesu / In the virtue and in the name of him shall
thou break down this mawmente of sin / Pray him besily and desire. and he
shall help the /

What profit comyth of keeping of the heart / And how much the soul is. and
what it louyth / Caplm lxxxviii:
GAder then thyn heart together and do after the cou^seyl of the wise man
when he says thus / Om^i custodia serua cor tuu^. qm^ ex ip^o vita procedit /
with all thy besynes keep thyn herte^ for out of it comyth life / And that is
soth when it is well kept / For then wise thoughts clean affeccyons and
brennyng desires of virtues and of charity and of the bliss of heaven comen
out of it. and makith the soul to live a blessed life / Also on the contrary
wise if it be not kept / then as our lord says in the gospel / De cord
exiu^t cogitaciones male que coinquinant hominem / Evil thoughts and unclean
affeccyons comen out of the heart the which defoulen man as our lord says
/ They either benymme the life of the soul by dedely sin. Or else they
feeble the soul and maken it syke if they ben venyall / For what is a man but
his thoughts and his loves / These maken a man oonly good or badde / As much
as thou love god and thyn even christian and knowyst him. so much is thy
soul / And if thou lityll love him. lityll is thy soul / and if thou nouhgt
love him. nougte is thy soul / It is naught as for good / but it is much as
for syn^e / And if thou wylt wit what thou love look where upon thou
thynkest / For where the love is there is the eye and where the likynge is
there is most the heart thinking / If thou love much god / the likyth for to
think much upon him / And if thou love lityll / then lityll thou thynkest
upon him / Rule well thy thoughts and thyn affecco^ns and then art thou
virtuous /

How the image of sin shall be broken down / Caplm lxxxix.
Begin then on and break this image when thou have Inwardely bethoughte the
of thyselfe and of thy wretchydnesse as I have said / how proud. how vain.
and how enuyous / how malencolyous / how covetous / how flesshly / and how full
of corrupcyon / Also how lityll knowing felyng or savor thou haast of god /
and of ghostly things / How wise. how quick / and how much savor thou have
in erthly things / And shortly that the thinks the also full of sin as the
hyde is full of flesh / Be thou not to much adradde though thou think so
of thyselfe / And when thou have done thus lift up then the desire of thy
heart to thy lord Ihesu / and pray him of help / Erye to him by great
desires and syghinges that he will help the to bear this great bourden of this
image. or else that he will break it / Think also such a shame it is for the
to be fed with swynes mete of flesshly savors that sholdest feel a ghostly
savor of heavenly Joy / If thou do thus / then begynnest thou for to arise
ayenste the hole ground of sin in the as I have said / And it may so be
that thou shall feel pain and sorrow / for thou shall understand that there
may no soul live without great pain but if he have rest and delight either
in his creator or in a creature / Then when thou rysest against thyself by a
feruente desire for to feel of thy lord Ihesu / and for to draew out thy love
fro al bodyly things / and fro rest in thy bodily feeling. in so much that
thou art encombred of thiselfe / And the thinks that all creatures ryse^
against the / and all things which thou had delight in before tourneth the
to pain / And when thou forsakest thus thyself / and thou may not lightly
find comfort in god / nedelynges thy soul shall suffer pain / Nevertheless
I hope who so would suffer this pain awhyle steadfastly cleuynge upon that
desire and naked mind of Ihesu christ / and upon desire that he would not have
but his lord and fall not lightly therfro / ne seche no comfort outward
for a time / for it lastyth not long / Our lord is nyghe and soon shall ease
the heart / For he will help to bear thy body full of corrupcyon / And he woll
with his mercyful might of gracyous presence break down this false image of
love in thyselfe / Not all atones / but lityll and little till thou be somdele
reformed to his lyckenesse /

How a man shall have him to the stiryng of pride and of all other vices /
Caplm lxxxx.
AFter such an hole rysyng against thyself when it is passyd. thou shall more
sobirly and more easily rule thyselfe / And the more sadly for to keep thy
thoughts and thyn affeccyons for to know hem whether they ben good or bad And
then^e if that thou feel a stiryng of pride in any manner of spyce of it / Be
soon well waar if that thou may / and suffer not it escape lightly away / But
take it in mind and rent it break it and dispyse it / and do all ye shame
that thou may thereto / Look thou spare it not. ne trow it not speak he never
so fair / for it is false though it seem soth as the prophet says / Popule
meus qui te beatu^ dicunt ipsi te desipiu^t et in errorem mittunt / That is to
say thus / Thou man of my people they that sayen thou art blessed and holy.
Isay^ 3.
they begyle and bryngen the in to error / And if thou do thus often besily
thou shall by the grace of Ihu^ within short time stop much of the spring
of pride. and much abate the vayn delight thereof that thou shall uneaths feel
it / And when thou felyst it it shall be so weyke and as it were half deed
that it shall not much grieve the. And then shall thou mow have a ghostly
syghte of meekness how good and how fair it is and thou shall desire it and
love it for the goodness of itself / that the shall lyken for to beholden as
thou art. and if need be for to suffer gladly despyte and reprove for love of
rightwysnes Upon the self manner when thou felyst stirynges of ire and of
male^colye risyng of heart or any other evil will against thyn even cryste^ for
any manner of cause though it seem reasonable and for charity bewaar of it / and
be ready with thy thought for to refreyne it that it turn not in to flesshly
appetite. aye^ stand it and follow it another in word ne in deed asmoche as
thou may / but as he ryseth smite him down again / and so shall thou slay it
with the sword of dread of god that it shall not grieve the / For wit thou well
in all these stirynges of pride vainglory. envy or any other that as soon as
thou perceyuest it and with displeysaunce of thy will and of thy reyson thou
ayenstonde it thou sleest it. though it be so that it cleue stylle upon thyn
heart against thy will and will not lightly pass away / dread it not / for it
lets thy soul fro pees* but it ^^foyleth not thy soul / Right so upon the
same wise shall you do against all evil stirynges of couetyse. accidye.
glotenye. or lecherye / that thou be always ready with thy reason and thy will
for to reprove hem and dispyse hem /

What thing helpith most a man^is knowing and getith to him that he lackith
and most destroys sin in him / Caplm lxxxxi.
ANd that may thou do the better and the more redily if y^ be besye for to
set thyn heart most upon one thing and that thing is naught else but a
ghostly desire to god for to please him / for to love him. for to know him.
for to see him / and for to have him by grace here in a lityll feeling. and in
the bliss of heaven in a full being / This desire if thou keep it shall well
tell the which is sin and which is not / and which is good and which is
better good / And if thou wolt festen thy thought thereto it shall teache the
all that the needs / and it shall get the all that the wants / And therefore
when you shalt rise against the ground of sin in general or else in any
special sin. hang fast upon this desire. and set the point of thy
thought more upon god whom thou desyrest than upon the sin which thou
repreuest / For if thou do so then^e fyteth god for the / and he shall
destroy syn^e in the. Thou shall much sooner come to thy pourpoos if thou do
so tha^ if thou leave thy meke desire to god pryncypally. and will set thyn
heart oonly against the stirynge of sin / as though thou would destroy it
by maystry of thyself / thou shall never so bring it abowte /

How a man shall be shapen to the image of Ihesu / and Ihesu shapen in him /
Caplm lxxxxii.
But do as I have said and better if thou may / And I hope by the grace of
Ihesu thou shall make the deuell a shamed / And all such wicked stirynges
thou shall break away / that they shall not much grieve the / And upon this
manner wise may the image of sin be broken down in the and destroyed: by
the which thou art forshapen fro the kyndely shappe of crystis image / And
thou shall be shappen again to the image of Ihesu man by meekness and charity
and then shall thou be full shapen to the self image of god here living by a
shadow in contemplaco^n and in the bliss of heaven in full sothfastnesse. Of
this shapynge to the lyknes of christ spekith saint poul thus / Filioli quos
iterum perturio donec xp^s formetur in vobis / Gal. iiii
My dear chyldern which I bear as a woman bears her child unto christ be
ayenshape^ in you / Thou have conceived christ by troth and he has life in
the in asmoche as thou have a good will and a desire for to serve him and plese
him / but he is not yet full shapen in the ne thou in him by fullness of
charity / And therefore saint poul bare the and me and other also with traueyle
as a woman bears a child unto ye time that christ has his full shape in us
and we in him /

How a man shall be shapen to the image of Ihesu and Ihesu shapen in him / Caplm
lxxxxii.
WHo so weneth for to come to the werching and to the full use of contemplaco^n
and not by this way / that is for to say not by full head of virtues he
comyth not by the door and therefore as a theyf he shall be cast out / I say
not but yt a man may by the yefte of god have by times a taastyng and a
glemeryng of life contemplatyf / Some man in the beginning / But the sad
felyng of it shall he not have / for christ is the door and he is porter / and
wythouten his leave and his lyuereye may there no man come in as he says
himself / John. iiii /
Nemo venit ad patre^ nisi per me / No man comyth to the fader but by me /
That is for to say / No man may come to the contemplacyon of the godhede but
he be first reformed by fullness of meekness and charity to the kycknesse of
Ihesu in his manhede /

The cause why this book was made. And how she should have her in redynge
thereof that it was made to / Caplm lxxxxiii.
LOo I have told the a lityll as me thinks. first of co^templatyf life what
it is / and sithen of the ways which by grace leden thereto / naught for I
have it in felyng and in werchyng as I have it in saying / Nevertheless I
would by these words such as they aren / first styre mine own necligence
for to do better than I have done / And also my purpoos is for to styre the or
any other man or woman that has taken the state of life contemplatyf for to
traueyle more besily and more mekely in that manner of life by such simple
words as god has give me grace for to say / And therefore if any word be
therein that styreth the or comfort the more to the love of god / thank god.
for it is his gift. and not of the word / And if it comfort the not or else
thou take it not redely / study not tolonge theraboute but lay it beside
the till a another time / and give the to thy prayer or to other ocupaco^n /
Take it as it woll come and not all at ones / Also thise words that I write
take hem not to streytly but there that the thynkith by good auysement that I
speak to shortly either for lacking of english or wantyng of reason I pray
the amend it oonly where need is / Also these words that I write to the they
longen not all to a man that has actyf life / but to the or to any other
which has the state of life contemplatyf /

THE grace of our Lord Ihesu Christ be with the / AMEN
Here begynnen the chapytours of the ii. book /
That a man is the image of god after the soul and not after the body / Caplm
primum How it needs to mankind that oonly thorough the passion of christ
should be restored and reformed that was forshape by the first sin. Caplm
scdm That the Jews and paynems and also falls christian men be^ not reformed
effetually thorough the virtue of the passion for her own defawte / Caplm iii.
Of two manner of refourmynges of this image / one in fulness a another in faith /
Caplm iiii. That refourmyng in party is in two manners. one in faith a another
in feeling / Caplm v. That thorugh the sacrament of baptym that is grounded in
the passion of christ this image is reformed fro origynall sin / Caplm vi.
That thorugh the sacrament of penance that stondeth in contrico^n confession
and satisfacco^n this image is reformed fro actual sin / Caplm vii. How in
the sacrament of baptym and of penance thorough a pryue vnperceyuable werchyng
of the holy ghost this image is reformed though it be not seen ne felt /
Caplm viii. That we should believe steadfastly refourmyng of this image if our
conscience witness to us a full forsakyng of sin and a true tournyng of our
will to good living / Caplm ix^ That all the souls that lyuen mekely in ye
faith of holy church and have her faith quyckened in love and charity ben
reformed by this sacrament / though it be so that they may not feel the
special gift of devotion or of ghoostly feeling / Cap^lm x. That souls
reformed neden ever to fight and to strive strongly against the stirynges of
sin while they lyuen here And how a soul may know when it assentyth to
stiryng and when not / Caplm xi. That this image is both fair and foul while
it is in this life here though it be refourmed^ and of dyuersyte of felynges
pryuely had between these souls that been reformed / and other that been not /
Caplm xii. Of three manner of men of the which some ben not reformed / and
some ben reformed only in faith / and some in faith and in feeling / Caplm
xiii. How men that been in sin forshape hemself into diverse bestes lyknes. and
they ben called the lovers of this world / xiiii How lovers of this world
vnablen hem in diverse manners to the refourmyng of her own soul / Caplm xv. A
lityll counceylle how lovers of this world sholden do if they will be
reformed in her own soul before her partyng hens / Caplm xvi. That
refourmyng in faith and in felyng may not suddenly begoten but by grace and
much bodily and ghostly traueyle in length of time / Caplm xvii. The cause
why so few souls in reward of the multitude of other comyth to this
reformyng in faith and in felyng / xviii An other cause also of the same / and
how wilful bodily customs indiscretly rewarded and used sometime hyndreth
souls fro felyng of more grace / Caplm xix. How that without much bodily and
ghostly business and without much grace and meekness souls may not be
reformed in felyng ne be kept therein after they come thereto / xx. An entree
how a soul shall have her in meaning and werchynge that woll come to this
refourmynge by ensample of a pilgrim going to Iherusalem / And of two manner
of meekness / Caplm xxi. Of taryenges and temptacyons that souls felen by her
ghostly enmyes in her ghostly knowing and gooyng to Iherusalem and of remedies
against hem / Caplm xxii. Of a general remedy against wicked stirynges and
paynful taryenges that fallen to her hertes of the flesh and of the world
and of the fend / Cap^lm xxiii. Of an evil day and a good night what it
meanyth / and how the love of the world is lykned to an evil day. and the
love of god to a good night / Caplm xxiiii. How that the desire of Ihesu felt
in this lyghtsome derknes sleeth all stirynges of sin and ableth the soul to
perceive ghostly lyghtnynges fro the heavenly Iherusalem that is Ihesu / Caplm
xxv. How a man shall know falls illumynacyons feyned by the fend fro the true
light of knowing that comyth out of ihesu and by what tokens / Caplm xxvi. How
great profit it is to the soul to be brought thorough grace in to lyghtsome
derkenesse / and how a man shall dispose him if he will come thereto / Caplm
xxvii. That in refourmynge of a soul the werkynge of our lord Ihesu is
departed in to four times / that is calling. ryghtyng magnifyenge. and
glorifyenge / Caplm xxviii. How it fallyth sometime that souls beginning and
perfytyng in grace seem to have more love as by outward tokens than some have
that been perfyte and yet it is not so in soth within / Caplm xxix. On what
manner a man shall have knowing of his own soul / and how a man should set
his love in Ihesu god and man one person / Caplm xxx. How this manner of
spekyng of refourmyng in felyng of a soul shall be take and on what wise it is
reformed / and how it is found in saint poulis words / Caplm xxxi. How god
openyth the Inner eye of the soul to see him / not all at ones but by diverse
times / and of three manner of refourmynge of a soul by ensample / Caplm xxxii.
How Ihu^ is heaven to ye soul / and why he is called fire. xxxiii Of two manners
of love fourmed and vnfourmed what it means / and how we ben behold to love
Ihesu much for our making / but more for our ayenbyeng / but althermoost for
our saving through the yeftes of his love / Caplm xxxiii. How that some soul
loves ihesu by bodily feruours and by her own manly affecco^ns that been
stired by grace and by reison. And how some louen Ihesu more restfully by
ghostly affeccyons oonly styred Inward thorugh special grace of the holy
ghost / Caplm xxxv. That the yette of love among all the yeftes of Ihesu is
worthyest and most profitable / And how Ihesu does all that is well done in
his lovers oonly for love / and how love makith the vsyng of all virtues and
all good deeds light and eesy / xxxvi. How love thorugh gracyous beholding of
Ihesu sleeth al styrynges of pride and makyth the soul for to lose savor and
delight in all erthly worship / Caplm xxxvii. How love sleeth all stirynges of
wrath and envy softly and refourmyth in the soul the virtues of pees and
pacye^ce and of perfyte charity to his even christian / as he did specially in
the appostles / Caplm xxxviii. How love sleeth couetyse lecherye and gloteny /
and sleeth the flesshly savor and delight in all the five bodily wits softly
and easily thorugh a gracyous beholding of Ihu^ / xxxix What virtues and graces
a soul receives thorugh opening of the Inner eye in to the gracyous
beholdynge of Ihesu / And it may not be gotten oonly thorugh mannys traueylle /
but thorugh special grace and traueyle also / Caplm xl How special grace in
beholding of Ihesu wythdrawith sometime fro a soul / and how a soul shall have
her in the absence and presence of Ihesu / And how a soul shall desire that in
it is always the gracyous presence of Ihu^ / Caplm xli. A co^mendacyon of
prayer offryd to Ihesu of a soul contemplatyffe / And how stablenesse in
prayer is a syker work to stand in. And how every feeling of grace in a
chosen soul may be said Ihesu / but the more clener a soul is the worthier
is his grace / Caplm xlii. How a soul through the openyng of the ghostly eye
receives a gracyous love able to understand holy writ / And how Ihesu that
is hid in holy writ shows himself to his lovers / Caplm xliii. Of the
pryue voys of Ihesu sownynge in a soul whereby it shall be known / and how all
the gracyous Illumynacyons made in a soul be^ called the spekynges of Ihu^ /
Caplm xliiii How thorugh gracyous opening of the gholy eye a soul is made
wise mekely and sothfastly to see the dyuersite of degrees in holy church. as
traueyllyng / and for to see angels kind / first of reproved / Caplm xlv. How
by the same light of grace the blessed angels kind may be seen / and how
Ihesu is god and man above all creatures after that the soul may see him here
/ Caplm xlvi.
Here ends the chapytours of the second book /
Here after folowyth the second book of master walter^ Hylton /
That a man is the image of god after the soul and not after the body / Caplm
primum
FOr asmoche as thou couetyst greatly and askyst it for charity for to here more
of an image the which I have before times in party discriued to the /
therefore I will gladly with dread fall to thy desire / and helpyng the grace of
our lord Jesus christ. in whom I fully trust. I shall open to the a lityll more
of this image / At the beginning if thou wylt wit plainly what I mean by this
image. I tell the forsooth that I vndstonde naught else but thyn own soul /
For thy soul and my soul and every reasonable soul is an image. and that a
worthy image / for it is the image of god as the apostle says / Vir est ymago
dei / That is to say / A man is the image of god. ^
and made to the image and to the lyknes of him / not in the bodily shappe
without but in the myghtes of it within as holy writ says. Formauit deus
homine^ ad ymagine^ and similitudine^ sua^ / That is / Our lord god shope man
in his soul to his own image and lyknes. This is the image that I have spoken
of / This image made to the image of god in the first shapyng was wonderly fair
and bryghte full of brennyng love and ghostly light. but thorugh sin of ye
first man adam it was disfygured and forshapen in to a nether lyknes as I have
before said. For it fell fro ye ghostly lyte and that heavenly fode in to
paynfull derknes and lust of this wretchyd life / exyled and flemyd out fro
the heritage of heaven that it should have had if it had stand stylle in to ye
wretchydnes of this earth: and afterward in to the prison of hell there to
have be without end / Fro the which prison to ye heavenly heritage it might
never have come agayen but if it had be reformed to the first shappe and the
first lickenes But that refourmynge might not be made by none erthly man /
for every man was in the same myscheyff / And none might suffyse to help
himself and so much less a another man / Therefore it needs to be done by
him that is more than man that is oonly god / and that was skylfull that he
should refourme and restore man to bliss if he should be saaf / which of his
endless goodness first shope him thereto How then it might be reformed. and
how it is reformed to the first lyckenes by him that fourmed it by the grace
of god I shall tell the / For that is the entente of this writing /

How it neded to mankind that oonly thorugh the passion of christ it should be
restored and reformed that was forshape by the first sin / Caplm ii.
THe ryghtwysnes of god asks that a trespace done be not foryeuen but if
amends be made for it if it may be done / Now it is sooth. mankind that was
hole in adam the first man trespassed ayenste god so wonder grievously when it
forfeyted the special byddyng of him / and assented to the false counseylle of
the fend. that it deserved ryghtfully for to have be departed fro him and
dampened to hell with outen end. so ferforth that stondynge the ryghtwysnesse
of god it might not be foryeuen. but if amends were first made and full
satysfaccyon therefore / But this amends might no man make that was man
oonly. and comen out of adam by kyndely generacyon for this skylle / For the
trespass and vnworshyppe was endless great / and therefore it passyd mannys
might for to make amends for it / And also for this skylle / He that has
trespassed and shall make amends him behouyth for to give to him that he has
trespassed unto all that he owyth though he had not trespassed / And also over
that him behouyth give so^what that he owyth not but oonly for that he
trespassed / But mankind had not wherewyth that he might pay god for his
trespaas over that he ought him / For what good deed that man might do in
body or in soul it was but his debt / For every man ought as the gospel
says for to love god with all his heart and al his soul and all his myghtes /
and better might he not do than this / And nevertheless this deed suffyced not
to the refourmynge of mankind / Ne this might he not do but if he had be
first reformed / Then neded it that if man's soul should be reformed /
and the trespaas made good / that our lord god himself should refourme this
image / and make amends for this trespaas sythen that no man might / But
that might he not do in his godhede / for he might not ne ought not to make
amends by sufferynge of pain in his own kind / therefore it neded that he
should take the same mankind that had trespassed and become man. And that
might he not do by the common law of generation. For it was impossyble goddis
sone to be borne of towchyd woman / Therefore him must become man thorugh a
gracyous generacyon by the werkynge of the holy ghost of a clean gracyous
maiden our lady saint Mary / and so was it done / For our lord Ihesu goddis
sone became man / and thorugh his precious death that he suffered made amends to
the fader of heaven for mannys gylte / And that might he well do for he was
god. and he ought not for himself / but in as much as he was man borne of
the same kind that adam was that first trespaced And so though he ought it
not for his own person / for himself might not sin / Nevertheless he
ought it of his free will for the trespaas of mankind / the which mankind
he took for the salvation of man of his endeles mercy / For soth it is. there
was never man that might yield to god any thing of his own that he ought
not. but oonly this blessed Ihesu. For he might pay god one thing that he
ought not as for himself / and that was naught but one thing. that was to
give his precious life by wylfull taking of death for love of sothfastnes /
This ought he not / As much good as he might do to the worship of god in
this life: all were but debt / But for to take death for love of ryghtwysnesse
he was not bound thereto / He was bound to ryghtwysnesse / but he was not
bound to deye / for death is oonly a pain ordained to man for his own sin
/ But our lord Ihesu sinned never ne he might not sin / and therefore he
ought not for to deye / Then sythen he ought not for to deye. and yet
wilfully he deyed / then paid he to god more than he ought / And sythen that
was the best man's deed and most worthy that ever was done / therefore was it
reasonable that the sin of mankind should be foryeuen / In as much as man
kind had found a man of the same kind without wem^e of sin / that is
Ihesu that might make amends for the trespaas done and might pay our lord
god all that he ought and over more that he ought not / Then sith that our
lord Ihesu god and man deyed thus for salvation of man's soul. it was
ryghtfull that sin should be foryeuen / and man's soul that was his image
should mow be reformed and restored to the first lyckenesse and to the bliss
of heaven / This passion of our lord and this precious death is the ground of
all the refourmynge of of man's soul / without which might never man's
soul have be reformed to the lyckenesse of him. ne come to the bliss of
heaven / But blessed may he be in all his werkynge / Now is it so that thorugh
the virtue of his precious passion the brennyng sword of Cherubyn that drove
adam out of paradyce is now put away. and the endless gates of heaven arn open
to every man that will enter in thereto / For the person of Ihesu is both god
and king of heaven in the bliss to the fader / and as man he is porter at the
yate ready to receive every soul that will be reformed here in this life to his
lyckenesse / For now may every soul if that he will be reformed to the
lyckenesse of god / sith that the trespaas is foryeuen / and the amends
thorugh Ihesu is made for the first gilte / Nevertheless though this be sothe
all souls have not the profit ne the fruit of this precious passion / ne ame
not reformed to the lickenes of him

That Jews and paynems and also false christian men ben not reformed
effectuelly thorugh the virtue of the passion for her owe defawte / Caplm iii.
TWo manner of men arne not reformed by the virtue of this passion / One is of
hem that trow it not / An other is of hem that love it not / Jews and paynems
have not the benefyce of this passion / for they trow it not / Jews trow not
that Ihu^ the sone of the virgyn mary is goddis sone of heaven / Also the
paynems trow not that the souereyne wisdom of god would become the sone of man.
and in man head would suffer the pains of death / And therefore the Jews held
the prechynge of the cross and of the passion of christ naught but sclaunder
and blasphemye / and the paynems held it naught but fantome and folly / But
true christian men held it the souereyne wysdom of god and his great might Thus
said saint poul / Predicamus vobis cristu^ crucifirum iudeis quidem scandalu^.
gentibus autem stulticiam. ip^is aute^ vocatis iudeis and grecis xp^m dei
virtutem et dei sapienciam That is we preche to you that ye trow that Ihesu
christ crucyfyed the sone of mary is goddis sone souereyne virtue and wysdom of
god / the which Ihesu to Jews and paynems that trow not in him is but
sclaunder and folly / And therefore thise men by her untruth putten hemselfe
fro the refourmynge of her own soul / and stondynge her untruth shall they
never be saaf ne come to the bliss of heaven / For sothe it is / fro the
beginning of the world unto the last ending was there never man saaf ne
shall be saaf but if he had troth general or special in Ihesu christ / to
come or I come / For right as all chosen souls that were before the
Incarnaco^n under the old testamente hadden truth in christ that he should
come and refourme man's soul / either openly as patryarkes and prophets and
other holy men had / or else pryuely and generally as chyldern and other
simple and inperfyte souls hadden that knew not specially the pryuyte of the
Incarnacyon / Right so all chosen souls under the new testamente has
truth in christ that he is come / either openly and felyngly and ghostly men
and wise men have / or else generally as chyldern have that deyen crystned /
and other simple and lewd souls have that arne nourysshed in the bosom of
holy church / Sith this is sothe then thinks me that these men greatly and
grievously erren / that sayen that Jews and sarrasyns by keeping of her own
law may be made saaf / though they trowen not in Ihesu christ / as holy
church trowyth / In as much as they wene that her own troth is good and
syker and suffysaunt to her salvation. And in that truth they done as it
semyth many good deeds of ryghtwysnesse / And perauenture if they knew that
christian faith were better than her own is / they would leave her own and take
it / therefore that they should be saaf / Nay it is not enough so / For christ
god and man is both way and end / And he is medyatour betwyx god and man /
And without him may no soul be reconsyled / ne come to the bliss of heaven
/ And therefore they that trowen not in him that is both god and man may never
be saaf ne come to bliss / Other men also that louen not christ nor his
passion arne not reformed in the soul to the lycknesse of him / And thise men
arne falls christian men the which arne out of charytee / and lyuen and deyen in
dedely sin / These men trowen well as it semyth that Ihesu is goddis sone /
And that his passion suffysyth to saluaco^n of man's soul / And they trow
also all the other artycles of the faith / But it is an vnshaply truth and a
deed: for they love him not. ne they chese not the fruit of his passion / but
they lain stylle in her sin and in the false love of this world unto her
last end / And so they ben not reformed to the lyckenesse of god. but goon
to the pains of hell endelesly. as Jews and sarrasyns done / and in to much
more gretter pain than they / In as much as they had the truth and kept it
not / For that was more trespaas than that they had never had it / Then if
thou wolte wit which souls arne reformed here in this lyffe to the image of
god thorugh the virtue of his passion / soothly oonly those that trowen in him
/ and louen him / in which souls the image of god that was thorugh sin
forshapen^ as it were in to a foul bestes lyckenes is restored and reformed
to the first shape / and to the worthynes and worship that it had in the
beginning / without which restorynge and refourmyng shall never soul be saaf
ne come to bliss /

Of two manner of refourmynges of this image / one in fullness. a another in
faith / Caplm iiii.
NOw say thou how may this be soth that the image of god. the which is
man^es soul might be reformed here in this life to his lyckenesse in any
creature / It semyth nay. it might not be so / For if it were reformed
then should it have stable mind / clear syghte and clear brennynge love in
god and ghostly things euerlastyngly as it had in the beginnynge / But that is
no creature as thou trowest living here in this life / For as against thyself
thou can well say the think the full far therfro / Thy mind thy reason
and the love of thy soul arne so much set in beholdynge and in love of
erthly things / that of ghostly things thou felyst right little / Thou
felyste no refourmynge in thyselfe / but thou art so vnbilapped with this
black image of syn^e for ought that you may do. that upon what side you the
turn thou felist thiself defoyled and spotted with flesshly stirynges of this
foul image: other chau^gyng felyst you none fro flesshlynes in to ghostlines
neither in pryue mytes of thy soul wc in ne in bodyly feeling without /
wherefore ye thynken that it might not be that this image might be reformed /
Or else if it might be reformed / Then^e ask thou how it might be
reformed / To this I answer and say thus. There is two manner of refourmyng
of the image of god which is man's soul / One is in fullness / A another is
in party / Refourmynge in fullness may not be had in this life / but it is
delayed after this life to the bliss of heaven / where man's soul shall fully
be reformed. not to that state that it had at the first beginning by kind.
or might have had thorugh grace if it had stand hole / But it shall be
restored to much more bliss and much hyer Joy thorough the great mercy and
the endless goodness of god than it should have had if it had never fallen / For
then shall the soul receive the hole and the full feeling of god in all
myghtes of it. without medelynge of any other affection / And it shall see
mankind in the person of Ihesu above the kind of angels onyd to the godhede
/ For then shall Ihesu both god and man be all in all / and oonly he. and
none other but he as the prophet says Dominus solus exaltabitur in illa die /
That is our lord Ihesu in that day that is everlasting day shall be hyghed
oonly. and none but he / And also the body of man shall then^e be gloryfyed /
For it shall receive fully the rich dowary of vnde delynes with all that
longs thereto / This shall a soul have with the body / and much more than I
can say. But that shall be in the bliss of heaven and not in this life / For
though it be so that the passion of our lord be cause of all this full
refourmynge of man's soul / nevertheless it was not his will for to grant
this full refourmynge right anon after his passion to all chosen sowles that
were living in time of his passion / But he delayed it unto the last day And
that was for this skylle / Sooth it is that our lord Ihesu Christ of his
mercy has ordained a certain number of souls to salvation which nombre was
not fulfilled in the time of his passion / And therefore it neded that by length
of time thorugh kyndly generacyon of men it should be fulfilled. Then if it
had so be that as sone after the death of our lord every soul that would
have trowed in him should by his life have be blessed and full reformed
without any other abidynge / there would no creature that lived then^e have be
that he ne would have received the faith for to have be made blessed / and
then should generacyon have ceased. And so should we that are now chosen
souls living and other souls that come after us not have been borne / and so
should our lord have failed of his number / But that may not be / And
therefore our lord purueyed much better for us in that that he delayed the
full refourmyng of man's soul till the last end. as saint poul says / Deo
pro nobis melius prouidente. ne sine nobis consu^marentur / That is. He^^*
Our lord purueyeth better for us in the delay of our refourmynge than if he
had granted it then / For this skylle that the chosen souls here beforn
should not make a full end without us that come after / A another skylle is
this / For sith that man in his first fourmynge of god was set in his free
will and had free chesyng whether he would have fully god or noo^ It was
therefore reasonable that sith he would not chese god then^e but wretchydly fell
from him / If he should afterward be reformed that he should be set again
in the same free chesinge that he was first in. whether he would have the
profit of his refourmynge or no / And this may be a skylle why man^es soul
was not reformed fully as fast after the passion of Ihesu christ /

That refourmyng in party is in two manners. one in faith a another in feeling /
Caplm v.
A Another reforming of this image is in party: and this refourming may be had
in this life: and but if it be had in this life it may never be had. ne the
soul may never be saaf / But this refourmynge is on two manners / One is in
faith oonly. A another is in faith and in feeling. The first refourmynge in
faith oonly suffiseth to salvation / The second is worthy to have passing
mede in the bliss of heaven / The first may be had lightly and in short time
/ The second may not so but thorugh length of time and much ghostly
traueyle / The first may be had with the feeling of the image of sin / for
though a man feel no thing in himself but all stirynges of sin and
flesshly desires. not ayenstondynge that feeling / if he wylfully assente not
thereto he may be reformed in faith to the lycknesse of god / But the second
reformyng puttyth out the likyng in feeling of flesshly stirynges and worldly
desires / and suffers no such spots abide in this image / The first
refourmynge is oonly of beginning and profitynge souls. and of actyf men / The
second is of perfyte souls and of contemplatyf men^ For by the first
refourmynge the image of sin is not destroyed. but it is left as it were all
hole in feeling / But the second refourmyng destroys the old felynges of
this image of syn^e / and brings in to the soul new gracyous felynges
thorugh the werkynge of the holy ghost / The first is good. the second is
better / but the third that is in the bliss of heaven is moos best / First
let us speak of that one and sith of that other / and so we shall come to the
third.

That thorugh the sacrament of baptym that is grounded in the passion of Christ
this is reformed fro origynall sin / Caplm vi.
TWo manner of sins makith a soul to lose ye shape and the lyknes of god.
That one is called origynall yt is the first syn^e. the other is called actuel
yt is wylfully done sin. these ii. sins put away a soul fro ye bliss of
heaven. and da^pneth it to thendles pain of hell. but if it be thoru the grace
of god reformyd to his lyckenesse or it pass hens out of this life /
Nevertheless two remedies aren there against thise two sins / by the which a
forshapen soul may be restored again / One is the sacrament of baptym
ayenste origynall sin / a another is the sacrament of penance ayenste
actuell sin / A soul of a child that is borne and is vncrystenyd by cause
of origynall sin has no lyckenesse of god / He is naught but an image of
the fend and a bronde of hell. But as soon as it is crystened it is
reformed to the image of god / and through the virtue of faith of holy church
suddenly it is turned fro the lyckenesse of the fend and made like an angel
of heaven. Also the same falls to a Jew or to a farracyne the which or they
ben crystened arne naught but mancyples of hell / But when they forsaken her
error and fallen mekely to the truth in christ. and receive the baptym of
water in the holy ghost. sothly without any more taryeng they arne reformed
to the lickenesse of god so fully as holy church troweth. that if they might
as soon after baptym pass out of this world. they should streyghte flee to
heaven without any more lettyng / had they done never so much sin before in
the time of her untruth / and never should they feel the pay^ne of hell ne
of purgatori / And that pryuelege should they have by the merit of crystis
passion /

That thorugh the sacrament of penance that stond^^h in contricyon confession
and satisfaccion this image is reformed fro actual sin / Caplm vii.
ALso what christian man or woman that has lost the lickenesse of god thorough a
dedely sin brekynge god^dis commandments / if he thorugh towchynge of
grace sothfastly forsake his sin with sorrow and contricion of heart. and be
