in full will for to amend him / and torn him to good living / And in this
foresaid will receyuyth the sacrament of penance if he may / Or if that he
may not he is in will thereto. Sothly I say that this man's soul or woman's
that was forshapen first to the lyknesse of the devil thorugh dedely sin is
now by the sacrament of penance restored and shapen again to the image of our
lord god / This is a great curteysie of our lord and an cudeles mercy that
so lightly foryeuyth all manner of sin / and so suddenly yeuyth plente of
grace to a synful soul that askyth mercy of him / He abides not great
penance dooyng ne paynful flesshly sufferyng or he foryeue it / But he askyth
a lothynge of sin and a full forsakyng in will of the soul for the love of
him. and a tournynge of the heart to him / This askith he / for this yeuyth he
/ And then^e when he sees this without any delayenge. he foryeuyth the sin
and refourmyth the soul to his lyknesse / The sin is foryeuen that the soul
shall not be dampened / Nevertheless the pain detted for the sin is not yet
fully foryeuen / but if contryco^n and love be the more / And therefore shall he
goo and show him and shryue him to his ghostly fader. and receive penance
enjoined for his trespaas. and gladly fulfill it. so that both the syn^e and
the pain may be done away or he pass hens / And that is the skylfull
ordinance of holy church for great profit of man's soul. that though the
sin be foryeuen thorugh the virtue of contricyon / nevertheless in
fulfyllyng of meekness: and for to make hole satysfaccyon he shall if he may
show to his priest plener confession / for that is his token and his warraunte
of foryeuenesse ayenste all his enmyes. and yt is needful for to have / For if
a man had forfeyted his life ayenste a king of this earth it were not enough
to him as for a full sykernesse for to have oonly foryeuenesse of the king /
but if he have a charter the which may be his token and his warraunte
against all other men / Right so may it be said ghostly / If a man have
forfeyted against the king of heaven his lyffe thorough dedely sin / It is
not enough to him to full sykernesse for to have foryeuenes of god oonly by
contricyon between god and him. but if he have a charter made by holy church
if he may come thereto And that is the sacrament of penance the which is his
charter and his token of foryeuesse / For sith that he forfeyted both ayenste
god and holy church it is skillful that he have foryeuenesse for that one and a
warrant for that other / And this ^o skylle why that confession is needful / A
another skyll is this / For sith this reformyng of the soul sto^dyth in faith
oonly and not in feeling / therefore a flesshly man that is rude and boystouse
and can not deem lightly but outward of bodily things should not mow have
trowyd that his sins had been foryeuen him but if he had some bodily token.
and that is confession thorugh the which token he is made all syker of
foryeuenes if that he do that in him is / This is the troth of holy church
as I understand it / Also a another skyll is this / Though the ground of
foryeuenesse stand not pryncipally in confession but in contryco^n of the
heart. and in forthynkyng of sin / nevertheless I hope that there is many a
soul that shold^ never a felyd very contryco^n. nor had full forsakynge (...)
if confession had not be / For it fallyth oftsythes that (...) time of
confession grace of compu^ccyon comyth to a (...) that before never felid
grace. but ever was cold and d^y^ and ferder fro felyng of grace / And
therefore sith confession (...) so profitable to the more party of christian men
holy (...) ordained for the more sykernesse generally to all christian men that
every man and woman should ones in the year at the lest be shryuen of all her
sins that come to her mind to her ghostly fader^ though they had never so
much contryco^n before time / Nevertheless I hope well that if all men had
been as besye abowte the keeping of them self in eschewynge of all manner of
sin / And had comen to as much great knowing and feeling of god as some man
has / That holy church should not have ordened the token of confession* as
for needful bond for it had not neded / But for all men arn not so perfyte.
and perauenture much of the more party of christian men is imperfect. therefore
holy church ordained confession^ by way of general bond to all christian men
that will know holy church as her mother. and woll be buxome to her biddynge /
If this be soth as I hope it is then^e erreth he gretely that generally says
that confession of sins for to show a priest is neither needful to a syn^er
ne behofull / and that no man is bound thereto / For by that that I have said
it is both needful and spedfull to all souls that in this wretchyd life are
defoyled / thorugh syn^e / and namely to those that arn thorugh dedely syn^e
forshapen fro the lyknes of god which may not be reformed to his lyknes but
by the sacrament of penance that pryncypally stondeth in contrico^n and sorrow
of heart / and secundary in shryfte of mouth following after if it may be had /
Upon this manner by this sacrament of penance is a sinful soul reformed to
the image of god and to his lyknesse /

How in the sacrament of baptym and of penance thorugh a pryue vnperceyuable
worchyng of the holy ghost this image is reformed though it be not seen ne
felt / Caplm viii.
But this reformyng sto^deth in faith and not in felyng / For right as the
propirte of the faith is for to trow that you see not. right so it is for to
trow that thou felyst not. But he that is reformed in his soul by the
sacrament of penance to the image of god he felith no chau^gyng in him self
neither in his bodily kind without ne in the pryue substance of the soul
within other than he did. for he is as he was unto his felyng / and he felyth
the same stirynges of syn^ and the same corrupcion of his flesh in passions
and worldly rysyng in his heart as he did before / And nevertheless he shall
trow that he is thorugh grace reformed to the lyknes of god though he another
feel it ne see it / He may well feel sorrow for his syn^e and a tornynge of his
will fro syn^e to clen^esse of living if that he have grace and take good keep
of himself but he may another see ne feel the refourmynge of his soul how it
is wonderly and vnperceyuably changed fro the fylthe of the fe^de unto the
fayrnes of an angel thorugh a pryue gracyous werchyng of the holy ghost / That
may he not see but he shall trow it / And if he trow it. then is his soul
reformed in truth / For right as holy church trowith by ye sacrament of
baptym sothfastly received a Jew or a sarrasyn or a child borne is reformed
in soul to the lyckenesse of god thorugh a pryue vnperceyuable werchyng of the
holy ghost / not ayenstondyng all the flesshly stirynges of his body of sin.
the which he shall feel after his baptym as well as he did before. Right so
by the sacrament of penance mekely and truly received a falls criste^ man that
has be encombred with dedely sin all his life time is reformed in his soul
within vnperceyuably. out taken a tournyng of his will thorugh a pryue might
and a gracyous werchyng of the holy ghost that suddenly werchith / and in time
of a monent or a twynkelyng of an eye ryghttyth a froward soul. and tourneth
it fro ghostly fylthe to fayrnes vnseable / and of a servant of the (...)
makyth a sone of Joy / and of ye prisoner of hell makyth a perceyuer of
heavenly heritage not ayenstondyng all the fle^shly feeling of this sinful
image that is the bodily kind* For thou shall vndstonde that the sacrament of
baptym or of penance is not of that virtue for to let and destroy utterly all the stirynges of flesshly lusts and paynfull passions that a man's soul
never feel no manner risyng ne styrynges of hem no time / For if it were so
then were a soul fully reformed here to the worship of the first making /
But that may not be fully in this lyffe / But it is of that virtue that it
cleanses the soul fro all the sins before done / And if it be departed fro
the body sauyth it fro da^pnacion. And if it dwell in the body it yeuyth the
soul grace to ayenstonde ye stirynges of sin / and it kepyth it in grace
also that no manner of lusty stirynges or of passions that it felyth in the
flesh be it never so grievous shall dear it ne depart it fro god as long as
it wylfully sentyth not thereto / Thus saint poul meaned when he said thus /
Nichil dampnaco^nis in hiis qui no^ scdm carnem ambulant / That is. Ro^ viii.
These souls that arne reformed to the image of god in faith thorugh the
sacrament of baptym or of penance shall not be dampened for felynges of this
image of sin / if it so be that they goo not after ye stirynges of the
flesh by deed doing /

That we should believe steadfastly refourmynge of this image. if our conscience
witness to us a full forsakyng of sin. and a true torning of our will to
good living / Ca^ ix.
OF this refourmynge in faith spekyth saint poul thus Iustus ex fide viuit /
The rightwisman lives in faith That is. (...). x.
He that is made rightful by baptym or by penance he lives in faith / which
suffyseth unto saluaco^n and to heavenly pees as saint poul says / Iustificati
ex fide pacem habemus ad deu^ / That is: Ro^ v.
we that arne ryghted and reformed thorugh faith in christ has pees and
accord made betwyx god and us. naught ayenstondynge the vycious felynges of
our body of sin / For though this reformyng be pryue and may not well be
felt here in this life / nevertheless who so trowyth it steadfastly. and
shapyth his works bisely for to accord to his troth / and that he turn not
again to dedely syn^e Soothly when the hour of death comyth. and the soul is
departed fro this bodily life then shall he find it sooth that I say now /
Thus said saint Ioh^n in comfort of chosen souls that lyuen here in faith
under the feeling of this painful image / Barissimi. and nunc sumus filii dei:
sed non du^ apparuit quid erimus / Scimus aute^ qm^ cum cristus apparuit tunc
apparebimus cum eo similes ei in gloria / That is: My dear friends we arne now
while we live here the sons of god / for we arn reformed by faith in christ
to his lyckenes But it shewyth not yet what we arn / but it is all pryue /
Nevertheless we know well that when our lord shall show him at the last
day / then shall we appear with him like unto him in endless Joy / If thou
wolte wit then if thy soul be reformed to the image of god or no / by
that I have said thou may have entree / Ransake thy conscience. and look what
thy will is / for there in stondeth all / If it be turned fro all manner of
dedely sin. that thou woldeste for noothynge wyttyngly and wylfully break the
commandment of god / And for that thou haste mysdone here before ayenste his
biddynge thou haste shryuen the thereof mekely with full heart to leave it / and
art sorry that thou dydest it / I say then sykerly that thy soul is
reformed in faith to the lyckenesse of god /

That all the souls that lyuen mekely in the faith of holy church / and have
her faith quyckened in love and cha^ryte ben reformed by this sacrament /
though it be so that they may not feel the special yefte of devotion or of
ghostly feeling / Caplm x^
IN this refourmynge that is oonly in faith the (...) part of chosen souls
leden her life that sette^ her will steadfastly for to flee all manner of dedely
sin / and for to k^pe hem in love and charity to her even christian / and for
to kep^ the commandments of god after her cunning / And when it so is that
wicked stirynges and evil wylles risen in her hertes of pride or of envy of
ire or lecherye / or of any other head sin they ayenstonde hem and stryuen
against hem by dysplesynge of will / so that they follow not in deed these
wicked wylles / And nevertheless if they fall lightly as it were ayenste her
will thorugh freelte or vncu^nynge / as soon her conscience greuyth hem and
pynyth hem so grievously that they mow have no rest till they be shryuen and
may have foryeuenes / Sothly all thise souls that thus lyuen in this
refourmynge and ben found therein. in the hour of death they shall be saaf /
and come to the full refourmynge in the bliss of heaven / though it be so that
they might never have ghostly feeling ne Inward savor. ne special grace of
deuoco^n in all her life time / For else if thou say that no soul shall be
saaf but it were reformed in ghostly feeling that it might feel deuoco^n and
ghostly savor in god as some souls done thorugh special grace. then^e should
few souls be saaf in reward of multitude of other / Nay it is not for to
trow that that for the souls that oonly arn devout. and by grace come to
ghostly felyng. and for no moo our lord Ihesu should have take mankind / and
suffered that hard passion of death. It had be a lityll purchaas to him for to
have come fro so far to so nere / and fro so hye to so low for so few
souls Nay his mercy is spradde larger than so / Nevertheless on the contrary
wise if thou trow that the passion of our lord is so precious. and his mercy
somoche that there shall no soul be dampened. and namely of no christian man do
he never so evil as some fools wene / soothly thou erreste gretely /
Therefore goo in the mean and hold the in the mids. and trow as holy church
trowyth / And that is that the most sinful man that lives in earth if he
torn his will thorugh grace fro dedely sin with sothfaste repentance to the
seruyse of god / he is reformed in his soul / And if he deyed in that state
he shall be saaf / Thus behighte our lord by his prophet saying thus / In
quacu^que hora conuersus fuerit peccator and ingemuerit. E^ xxviii
vita viuet et non morietur / That is / In what time that it be that the
synful. man is turned to god fro syn^e and he have sorrow therefore he shall
live. and he shall not deye endelesly / And on the other side who so liuyth in
dedely syn^e and will not leave it ne amend him thereof: ne receive the
sacrament of penance / or else if he receive it he takyth it not soothfastly
for the love of god / that is for the love of virtue and clennesse but oonly
for dread or shame of the world / or for dread oonly of pains of hell / he
is not reformed to the lyknesse of god / And if he deye in that plyghte he
shall not be saaf / His troth shall not save him / for his truth is deed and
lackyth love. and therefore it seruyth him not / But they that have troth
quyckened with love and charity arn reformed to the lyckenesse of god. though
it be but the leest degree of charity. as arn simple souls the which felen
not the yeft of special devotion ne ghostly knowing of god / as some ghostly
men done. but trowen generally as holy church trowith. and knowyth not fully
what that is. for it needs not to hem^ And in that trowyth they keep hem in
love and charytee to her even christian as they may / and fleen all dedely sin
after her cu^nynge / and dooen the deeds of mercy to her even christian All thise
longen to the bliss of heaven / For it is written in the apoc^ thus. Qui
timetis deum pusilli et magni laudate (...) This is / ye that dreden god both
small and great thank him By great arn understand souls that arn profytyng
in (...) or else perfyte in the love of god. the which arn refourm^^ in
ghostly feeling: By small arn understand souls imperfect of worldly men and
wymmen. and other that have but a ch^^dis knowing of god and full lityll
feeling of him. but (...) brought forth in the bosom of holy church and
nourysshed with the sacrament as chylderne arn fed with milk / All thise
should love god and thank him for saluaco^n of her souls by his endeles mercy
and goodness / For holy church that is mother of all these and has tender
love to all her chyldern goostly prays and asks for hem all tenderly of her
spowse that is Ihesu and geteth hem hele of soul thorugh virtue of his passion
/ And namly for hem that can not speak for hem self by ghostly prayer for her
need / Thus I find in the gospel. That the woman of Chanee asked of our lord
hele to her daughter that was traueyled with a fend / and our lord made
first dau^geour by cause she was an alyene / Nevertheless she ceased not for
to cry till our lord had granted her asking. and said to her thus. Aa woman
much is thy troth be it to ye right as you wolt / In the same hour was her
douter hole. This woman betokenith holy church that asks help of our lord
for simple vncu^nynge souls that are traueyled with temptaco^n of the world /
and can not speak perfitly to god by fervor of devotion ne brennyng love in
contemplacyon / And though it seem that our lord make dau^geour first by
cause that they arn as it were alyened fro him / nevertheless for the great
truth and deserte of holy church he grau^teth to her all that she will / And
so arn these simple souls that trowen steadfastly as holy church trowyth /
and putten hem fully in the mercy of god / and meke^ hem under the sacrament
and laws of holy church made saaf thorugh prayer and troth of her mother holy
church /

That souls reformed neden ever to fight and strive ayenste the stirynge of
sin while they lyuen here / And how a soul may wit when it assentyth to
the stiryng. and when not / Caplm xi.
THis refourmyng in faith is lightly gotten / but it may not so lightly behold
/ And therefore what man or woman that is reformed to the sickness of god in
troth much traueylle and business must they have if they will keep this
image hole and clean that it fall not down again thorugh weykenesse of will to
the image of sin / He may not be idle ne reklees for the image of sin is
so nere festnyd to him / and so contynually pressyth upon him by diverse
styrynges of sin / that but if he be right well waare he shall full lightly
thorough assente fall again thereto / And therefore him needs ever be stryuynge
and fighting ayenste wicked stirynges of this image of sin / and that he
make none accord therwyth / ne take no fre^dshyp to it for to be buxum to his
unskillful biddynges / For if he do he begyleth himself But soothly if he
stryueth with hem him needs not much dread of assenting / For strife brekyth
pees and falls accord. It is good that a man have pees with all thing sauf
with the fend and with this image of syn^e / for ayenste hem him needs ever
fight in his thought and in his deed till he have geten on hem the maystry.
and that shall never be fully in this life / as long as he bears and felyth
this image / I say not but that a soul may thorugh grace have the hier hand
over this image so ferforthe that he shall not follow ne sent to the
unskillful stirynges of it / But for to be so clean delyuerde fro this image
that he should feel no suggestyon ne Jangling of flesshly affection ne of
vain thought no time may no man have in this life / I hope that a soul
that is reformed in feeling by rauysshyng of love in contemplacyon of god may
be so far fro the sensualyte and fro vayn ymagynaco^n aad so far drawn
out and departed fro the flesshly feeling for a time that it shall not feel but
god / but that lasts not ever / And therefore say I that every man behooves
stryffe ayenste this image of sin / and namely he that is reformed in faith
oonly that so lightly may be disceyued therwyth / In the person of which
men says saint poul / Caro concupiscit aduersus spiritu^ et spu^s aduersus
came^ That is: ^
A soul reformed to the lickenesse of god fightith ayenste the flesshly
stirynges of this image of sin / and also this image of sin stryueth against
the will of the spirit This manner of fighting of this dowble image saint
poul knew when he said thus / Inueni legem in membris me is repugnante^ legi
mentis me et captiuum me ducentem in legem peccati / That is / I have found
two laws in myself One law in my soul within / and a another in my flesshly
lym^es without fighting with it that often ledeth me as a wretched prisoner to
the law of sin / By thise two laws in a soul I understand this double
image / By the law of the spirit I understand the reason of the soul when
it is reformed to the image of god / By the law of the flesh I understand
the sensualytees which I call the image of sin / To. vii.
In thise two laws a soul reformed ledeth his life as saint poul says /
Me^te enim seruio legi dei. carne enim legi peccati / In my soul that is in my
will and in my reason I serve to the law of god / but in my flesh that is in
my flesshli appetyte I serve to the law of sin / Nevertheless that a soul
reformed shall not dispeyre though he serve to the law of sin by feeling of
the vicyous sensualyte ayenste the will of the spirit by cause of corrupco^n
of the bodily kind. saint poul excusyth it saying thus of his own person /
Non eni^ quod volo bonum hoc ago. ^
sed malum quod odi hoc facio. Si aute^ malum quod odi hoc facio. no^ ego
operor illud sed quod habitat in me peccatu^ / I do not that good that I would
do. That is. I would feel no flesshly stiryng. and that do I not / But I do
that evil that I hate. That is: The synful stirynges of my flesh I hate /
and yet I feel hem / Nevertheless since it is so that I have the wicked
stirynges of my flesh / and yet I feel hem and often delight in hem against my
will they shall not be reherced ayenste me for dampnaco^n as if I had done hem
/ And why? For the corrupcyon of this image of sin does hem^ and not I. ^oo
saint poul in his person comfort al souls that thorugh grace arn reformed
in faith that they sholden not tomoche dread the bourden of this image with
the unskillful stirynges thereof / if it so be they sent not wylfully thereto /
Nevertheless in this point many souls that arne reformed in truth arne
often times much tormented and trowbled in vayn as thus / When they have felt
flesshly stirynges of pride or enuye^ of couetyse or lechery or of any other
head syn^e. they wot not sometime whether they sent thereto or no. and that is
no great wond / For in time of temptaco^n a freel ma^nis thought is so
trowbled and so over laid that he has no clear sight ne fredom of himself /
but is taken often with likyng unwarily. and gooth forth a great while or then^e
he perceive it / And therefore fallen some in dowte and dwere whed they syn^ed
in time of temptacyon or no / As against this point I say as me think / that
a soul may have assayeng in this manner whed that he assente or no / If it
be so that a man is stired to any manner of sin. and the likinge is so great
in his flesshly felyng that it trowblith his reason. and as it were with
maistry ocupyeth the affecco^n of ye soul / nevertheless he kepyth him that he
follows not in deed / (...) he would not if he might but is rather paynfull to
him for (...) feel the likyng of that syn^e. and feign he would put it away
(...) he might / And then^e when ye stiryng is ouerpased he is glad and well
paid that he is delyuerde of it / by this assay may he wit. that were the
likyng never so great in the flesshly felyng that he assented not ne syn^ed
not namly dedely. Nevertheless ^ remedy there is siker to such a simple soul
that is (...) in itself and can not help it ye he be not to bold in himself
(...) wening yt such fleshly stiryng with likyng are no sin^es. (...) he myt so
fall into rechelesnes and into falls sikernes^ Ne (...) yt he be not to dredful
ne to simple in wit for to deem (...) al as dedely sins nor as great
venyals for another is soth. but yt he hold he^ all as sins and wretchidnes
of himself. and that he have sorrow for he^ and be not to besy for to deem he^
another deed li ne venial. But if his conscience be greatly grieved that he
haastly goo and show to his confessor in general or in special such
stirynges. and namly every stiryng that begyn^eth to festen any rote in the
heart and most ocupieth it for to draw it down to sin and worldly vanytee
/ And then when he is thus shryuen generally or specially trow then^e
steadfastly that they ben foryeuen. and dispute no more about hem that arn
passed and foryeuen whether they were dedely or venyall. But that he be more
besye to keep him better against hem that arn coming And if he do thus then^e
may he come to rest in conscience / But then^e some arn so flesshly and so
vncu^nyng that they would feel or see or here her foryeuenes of her sins as
openly as they might feel and see a bodily thing / And for asmoche as they feel
it not so therefore they fall often in such weeres and doubts of hemself and
never may come to rest / and in that arn they unwise. for faith gooth before
felyng / Our lord said to a man that was in the palsy wha^ he helyd him thus /
^
Co^fide fili remittu^t tibi pcca^ tua / That is: Sone trow steadfastly thy
sins arn foryeuen ye / He said not to him see or feel how thy sins arn
foryeue the / for the foryeuenes of sins is done ghostly and vnseable thorugh
the grace of ye holy ghost. but trow it / Right on the same wise. every man
that will come to rest in conscience him behouith first if he do that in him
is trow without ghostly felyng foryeuenes of his sins / And if he first
trow it / he shall afterward thorugh grace feel it. and understand it that
it is so. ^say. vii
Thus said the apostle / Nisi crederitis no^ intelligetis / That is: But if ye
first trow ye may not vndstonde / Troth gooth before and understanding comyth
after / the which understanding that I call the light of god if it be
gracyous a soul may not have but thorough great clen^esse as our lord says
/ Beati mu^do cord qm^ ip^i deu^ vide bu^t / Blessed be clean of heart for
they shall see god. M. v.
not with her flesshly eye but with the Inner eye that is understanding cle^sed
and lyghted thoruh^ grace of the holy ghost for to fee soth fastnes. yt which
clen^es a soul may not feel but if he have stable troth going before as
thapostle says / Fide mu^da^s corda eorum. Act^ xv.
That is our lord cle^seth ye hertes of his chose^ thoruh^ faith / therefore it
is nedfull yt a soul trow first ye reformyng of himself made thorugh the
sacrament of penance thouh^ he see it not / and that he dispose himself fully
for to live rightfully and virtuously as his troth askyth / so that he may
after come to syghte and to the refourmyng in feeling /

That this image is both fair and foul whiles it is in this life here though
it be reformed / And of dyuersyte of felynges pryuely had between thise souls
that been reformed and other that been not / Caplm xii.
Fair is man's soul. and foul is a man's soul / Fair in as much as it is
reformed in faith to the lickenes of god / But it is foul in asmoche as it is
meddled with flesshly felynges and unskillful stirynges of this foul image of
sin / Foul without as it were a be / fair within like to an angel /
Foul in feeling of the sensualyte / fair in troth of the reason / Foul for
the flesshly appetyte. fair for the good will / Thus fair and thus foul is a
chosen soul / saying holy writ thus / Nigra su^ sed formosa filie Ierlm
sicut tabernacula cedar et sicut pellis salomonis / That is. ^
I am black but I am fair and shaply ye daughter of Ierlm as the tabernacles
of cedar as the skyn^e of solomon / That is ye angels of heaven that arn
daughters of the hye Ierlm wonder not on (...) ne dispyce me not for my black
shadow / For though I (...) black without by cause of my flesshly kind as is
a tabernacle of cedar / Nevertheless I am full fair within as the skyn^e of
solomon. for I am reformed to the lyckenes of god / By cedar is understand a
reproved soul the which is a tabernacle of the devil / By solomon is
understand our lord Ihesu For he is pees and peasyble / By the skin of
solomon is understand a blessed angel in whom our lord dwellyth / And is
hid as is the life hid in the skin of a quycke body / And therefore is an
angel lyckened to a skin / Then may a chosen soul with meke trust in
god and gladenes of heart say thus / Though I be black by cause of my body of
syn^e as a reproved soul yt is one of the tabernacles of the fend /
nevertheless I am within full fair thorugh truth and good will like to an
angel of heaven / For so says he in a another place / Nolite considerare me quoth
fusca su^. qm^ decolorauit me sol. Cant. i.
That is: Behold me not that I am swart for the son has defaded me / The
son^e makyth a skin swarte only without and not within / and it betokenith
this flesshly life / Therefore says a chosen soul thus / Repreue me not for I
am swart. for the swartnesse that I have is all without of touching and of
berynge of this image of sin / but it is no thing within / And therefore
soothly though it be so yt a chosen soul reformed in faith dwell in this
body of sin^e and feel the same flesshly stirynges / and use the same bodily
works as does a tabernacle of cedar so ferforth that in man's dome there
should no dyfference be bytwyx that one and that other. Nevertheless within in
her souls there is a full great dyuersite^ and in the syghte of god there is
full much twinnynge / But the knowing of this which is one and which is other
is oonly kept to god* for it passes man's dome and man^es feeling / and
therefore we shall no man deem as evil for that thing that may be used both
evil and well. A soul that is not reformed is take so fully with the love
of the world / and so much ouerlayed with the likynge of his flesh in all
his se^sualyte that he chesyth it as a full rest of his heart. and in his
pryue meaning he would not else have but yt he might ever be syker thereof. He
felith no lycour of grace stiryng him for to loathe his flesshly life ne for to
desire heavenly bliss / And therefore I may say that he bears not this image of
syn^e / but he is borne of it as a man that were seek and so weyke that he
might not bear himself / And therefore he is laid in a bed and borne in a
lytere / Right so such a sinful soul is so weyke and so vnmyghti for
lackyng of grace that he may neither meue hand ne foot for to do any good
deed: ne for to ayenstonde by displesyng of will the leest stirynge of sin
when it comyth / but it falls down thereto as it were a be upon careyne /
But a soul that is reformed though he use his flesshly wits / and feel
flesshly stirynges / nevertheless he lotheth hem in his herte^ for he would
for no thing fully rest in hem / but he flees the rest as the bitynge of
an adder / and had lever have his rest and the love of his heart in god if that
he cowde^ and sometime desires thereto / and often grutcheth of the liking of
this life for love of the life everlasting / This soul is not borne in this
image of sin as a seek man though he feel it. but he beryth it / For thorugh
grace he is made mighty and strong for to suffer and bear his body with all
the evil stirynges of it without hurtynge or defoylynge of himself / and that
is in asmoche as he loves hem not. ne follows hem not^ ne se^teth not to hem
the which arn dedely sins as a another does / This was bodily fulfilled in
the gospel of a man that was in the palsye. and was so feeble that he might
not goo / and therefore was he laid and borne in a lytere and brought to our
lord / And when our lord saw him in myscheyf of his g^^odnesse he said to
him / Surge et toll grabatum tuu^ et (...) in domum tua^ / That is: Rise up
and take thy bed and (...) in to thy house / And so he did. and was hole /
And soothly right as this man bare upon his back when he was made hole the
bed that before bare him / Right so it may be said ghostly that a soul
reformed in faith berith this image of sin the which bare him before / And
therefore be not adradde tomoche of thy blackenesse that thou haste of beryng of
this image of sin. But as ayenste the shame and the dysco^forte that you have
of the beholding of it / and also again vpbraydyng that thou felist in thy heart
of thy ghostly enmyes when they say to the thus / where is thy lord Ihu^s. what
sekest you. where is ye fairnes that you spekest of. what felist you out but
blindness of sin / where is that image of god that thou say is reformed in
the / Comfort thiselfe and be faithful styfly as I have before said / And if
thou do so thou shall by this troth destroy all the temptacyons of thyn
enmyes / Thus said the appostle poul. Accipe scutu^ fidei in quo omnia tela
hostis nequissima poteris extinguere / That is: Eph^. 6.
Take to the a shield of steadfast troth thorugh the which thou may quench
all the brennyng darts of thyn enmye /

Of three manner of men of the which some ben not reformed / and some ben
reformed oonly in faith / and some in faith and in feeling / Caplm xiii.
BY this that I have said may thou see that after diverse parties of the soul
arne diverse states of men / Some men arne not reformed to the lyckenesse of
god / and some arne reformed to the lyckenesse of god / And some arn reformed
only in faith / and some arne reformed in faith and in feeling / For thou
shall understand that a soul has two parties / That one is called sensualyte
and that is flesshly feeling by the five outewarde wits / the which is common
to man and to be / Of the which sensualyte when it is unskillfully and
vnordynatly ruled is made the image of sin / when it is not ruled after
reason / for then is the sensualyte syn^e / That other party is called
reason / and that is departed in two / In the over party and in the nether /
The over party is lickened to a man / for it should be master and souereyne
and that is propirly the image of god / For by that oonly the soul knowyth god
and louyth him / And the neither is lyckened to a woman / for it should be
buxum to the over party of reison / as woman is buxum to man / and that lies
in knowing and rulynge of erthly things: for to use hem discretly after need.
and for to refuse hem wha^ it is no need. for to have ever with it an eye
upward to the ouerpartie of reason with dread and reverence for to follow it.
Now may I say yt a soul that lives after likings and the lusts of his
flesh / as it were an unskillful be. and neither has knowing of god ne
desire to virtues ne to good living. But is all blinded in pride / frette with
envy. ouerlayed with couetyse / defoyled with lecherye / and other great sins
/ Is not reformed to ye lyckenesse of god / for it lies and rests fully in
the image of sin. that is sensualyte / A another soul that dredeth god / and
ayenstondeth dedely stirynges of the sensualyte / and follows hem not / But
lives resonably in ruelynge and governance of worldly things / and sets
his entente and his will for to pleyse god by his outward works is reformed
to the lyknesse of god in faith / And though he feel the same stirynges of
syn^e as that other does / it shall not disease him for he rests not in hem
as that other does / But a another soul that flees thorugh grace all dedely
styrynges of the sensualyte and venyals also ferforth that he felyth hem not is
reformed in feeling / for he folowyth the ouerparty of reason in beholdynge of
god and ghostly thynges^ as I shall tell the afterward /

How men that been in sin forshapen hemselfe in to diverse bestes lyckenesse /
And they be^ called the lovers of the world / Caplm xiiii.
A wretchyd man is he then that knowyth not the worthynesse of his soul ne
will not know it / how it is most worthy creature that ever god made out
take an angel whom it is like to. hye above all other kind bodily. to the
which no thing may suffyse as full rest / but oonly god / And therefore he
should no thing love ne like but him oonly / ne coueyte ne seek but how he
might be refourmyd to his liknes. but for he knowith not this. therefore he
sekyth and coueytith his rest and his likyng outward in bodily creatures werse
than himself is / Unkindly he does and vnresonably he werkith yt leuith the
souereyn good and everlasting life yt is god unsought and vnloued unknown and
vnworshypped. and chesyth his rest and his bliss in a passing delight of an
erthely thing / Nevertheless thus done all the lovers of this world that
have her Joy and her bliss in this wretchyd lyffe / Some have it in pride and
vaynglory of hemself / that when they have lost the dread of god they traueyle
and study night and day how they mow come to worship and praysyng of the
world / and maken no force how it be so that they might come thereto and
ouerpasse all men either in clergy or in craft in name or in fame. In riches
or in reverence. in souereynte and mastershyp. in hye state and lordshyp Some
men have her rest in riches and in outragyous hauour of erthly good. and
sette^ her hertes so fully for to get it. that they seek not else but how
they might come thereto / Some have her likynge in flesshly lusts of glotenye
and lecherye and in other bodily uncleanness / And some in oo thing and some in a
another. And thus wretchydly thise that done thus forshapen hemself fro the
worthynes of man. and torn hem in to diverse bestes lickenes / The proud man
is turned into a lion for pride: for he would be drade and worshypped of all men
/ and that no man ayenstonde ye fulfyllyng of his flesshly will another in
word ne in deed / And if any man would let his mysproude will. he we^ith
fell and wroth. and woll be wroke^ of him as a lion wrekith him on a lityll
be / This man that does thus is no man for he does vnresonably ayenste
the kind of a man / and so he is turned and transfourmed in to a lion /
^nuyous and angry men arn turned in to hounds thorugh wrath / an envy that
berkyth again her even cryste^ and bityth hem by wicked and malicyous words /
and greuytgh hem that have not trespassed with wrongful deeds. harming hem in
body and in soul aye^ste goddis biddyng / Some men arne forshapen in to asses
ye arne slow to the seruyse of god. and evil wylled for to do any good deed
to her even christian / They arn ready enough for to run for worldly profit and
for erthly worship or for pleisau^ce of an erthly man / But for ghostly mede^
for help of her own souls: or for the worship of god they are soon yrke
they woll not thereof / And if they ought done they goon but a pase and with
froward will / Some are turned in to swyne for they are so blind in wit
and so bestly in manners that they have no dread of god: but folowen only the
lusts and lykynges of her flessh^ / and have no reward to the honest of man
/ ne for to rule hem after the biddynge of reason / ne for to restrain the
unskillful stirynges of the flesshly kind. but as soon as a flesshly stirynge
comyth of syn^e they are ready for to fall thereto and follow as swyne done /
Some men are turned in to wulfes that lyuen by raueyn as falls covetous men done
that through maystry and ouerledynge robben her even cri^^^ of her worldly
goods / Some men are turned in to foxes as falls men and deceyuable men that
lyuen in trecherye and gyle / All thise and many other moo that lyue^ not in
dread of god. but breken his commandments forshapen hemself fro the (...) of
god / and maken hem like to bestes^ ye and worse than bestes for they are like
to the fend of hell / And therefore sothly (...) men that lyuen thus if they
ben not reformed when (...) hour of death comes. and the souls of hem are
departed (...) the bodies. then^e shall her eye be opened that is now stopped
with syn^e / and then shall they feel and find the pain of (...)
wretchydnes that they lived in here / And for asmoche as the image of god was
not reformed through the sacrament of penance in hem neither in faith ne in
feeling here in this life they shall be as cursed cast out fro the blessed
face of our creator / and they shall be dampened with the devil in to the
depnesse of hell there for to be without end / Thus says saint Ioh^n in
thapocalipse / Tumidis et incredulis execratis and homicidis fornicatoribus
venificis et ydolatris and om^ibus men dacibus pars illorum erit in stagno
ardenti igne and sulphur. Apoc. ^
That is. To proud men and mystrowyng men to cursed and to me^ sleers. to
lecherous and covetous. to poyseners and worshyppers of mawmetes. and to all
falls liars her dele shall be with the devil in the pytte of hell bre^nynge
with fire and brymston / If ye lovers of this world would often think on this
how all this world shall pass and draw to an end. and how all wicked love
shall be hard punysshed. they should within short time looth all worldly
lusts that they now most like / and they should lift up her heart for to love
god / and they would besyly seek and traueylle how they might be reformed to
his lyckenes or they pass hens /

How lovers of this world unable hem in diverse manners to the refourmyng of her
own soul / Caplm xv
But now says some of hem thus. I would feign love god and be a good man^ and
forsake the love of the world if that I might / but I have no grace thereto.
If I had the same grace that a good man has I should do as he does / But for
I have it not. therefore I may not / and so it is not to me to wit but I am
excused / Unto thise me^ I say thus Soth it is as they say that they have no
grace / and therefore they lain still in her syn^e and may not rise out / But
that avails hem not against god. for it is her own defawte / They unable hem
by diverse ways somoche that the light of grace may not shine to he^ne rest
in her hertes. For some are so froward that they woll no grace hauene they
woll no good men be / For they wot well that if they should be good men they
must needs forbere the great likyng and the lust of this world that they have
in erthly things / and that woll they not. For hem thynken it is so sweet
that they woll not forgoo it /

And also they must needs take works of penance / As in fasting. waking:
prayenge / And many other good deeds dooynge: In chastysynge of their flesh
/ And in wythdrawynge of their flesshly will / and that may they not do / For
it is made so sharp and so dreadful to her thinking that they vggen and
lothen for to think upon it / and so cowardly and wretchydly dwell they
stylle in her syn^e / Some would have grace as it semith and begyn^en to able
hem thereto. but her will is wonder week / For as soon as any stirynge of syn^e
comyth though it be contrary to the biddynge of god. they fall anon thereto /
for they are so bound through custom by often falling and often assenting to
syn^e before: that hem think it impossyble for to ayensto^de it / and so
feyned hardness of perfourmyng weekyth her will. and smytith it down again: So
me also felen stirynge of grace. as when they have bityng of conscience for her
evil living. and that they should leave it But that is so paynfull to hem and
heavy that they woll not suffer it ne abide it: but they flee therfro and
foryete it if they may so ferforth that they seek likynge and comfort
outward in flesshly creatures. so that they should not feel this bityng of
conscience within her soul / And more over some men are so blind and so
bestly that they wene there is none other life but this. ne that there is no
soul other than of a best / and that the soul of a man deyeth with the body
as the soul of a be / and therefore they say: Ete we. drink we: and make
we merry here / for of this life we be^ syker: we see none other heaven / Sothly
such are some wretches that sayen thus in her hertes / though they say it not
with her mouth / Of the which men the prophet says thus / Dixit insipie^s in
cord suo no^ est deus / That is / ^ unwise man said in his heart: there is no
god / This vnw^se man is every wretchyd man that lives and loves syn^e. and
^hesith the love of this world as rest of his soul: he says there is no god
/ not with his mouth. for he woll speak of him some time when he fares well
flesshly as it were in reverence wha^ he says blessed be god / Sometime in
dyspyte when he is angry against god or his eue^ christian. and sweryth by his
blessed body or any of his me^bres / But he says in his thought that there is
no god / and that is either for he weneth that god sees not his syn^e. or
that he will not punysshe it so hard as holy wrytt says / or that he woll
foryeue him that syn^e though he see it not / or else that there shall no
christian man be dampened do he never so evil / Or else if he fast our lady
fast. or say every day a certain oryson / or here every day ii. masses or
iii. or do a certain bodily deed as it were in worship of god. he shall never
goo to hell do he never somoche syn^e though he forsake it not / this man
says in his heart that there is no god / But he is unwise as the prophet
says / For he shall feel and find in pain that he is a god whom he forgate
and set naught by / but set by the well of the world as the prophet says
/ Sola vexacio dabit intellectu^ auditui / That is: ^
Only pain shall give vndstondynge / For he that knowyth not this here ne
woll not know it: shall well know it when he is in pain.

A lityll counseyle how lovers of this world should do if they woll be
reformed in her soul before her partyng hens Caplm xvi.
These men though they wot well that they arne out of grace and in dedely
syn^e they have no care ne sorrow ne thought therefore. But they make flesshly
mirth and worldly solace asmoche as they may / And the ferder they ben fro
grace ye more myrthe they make / and perchance some holde^ hem well paid that
they have no grace that they may as it were the more fully and freely follow
the likyng of flesshly lusts. as though god were a sleep and might not see
hem / And this is one of ye most defawte that may be / And thus by her own
frowardenes they stop the light of grace fro her own soul that it may not
rest therein / the which grace in asmoche as in it is shyneth to all ghostly
creatures ready for to enter in there it is received: as the son^e shyneth over
all creatures bodily ther^ it is not let / thus says saint Ioh^n in the
gospel. Ioh^is: 1.
Lux in true bris lucet et tenebre ea^ non co^prehenderu^t / That is / the
light of grace shyneth in derknesse / that is to men^es hertes that are derke
through sin / But the derknesse takes it not / That is thise blind hertes
receive not ye gracyous light. ne have not the profit of it: But right as a
blind man is vmbilapped with the light of the son^e when he sto^deth therein.
and yet sees it not. ne has no profit thereof for to goo thereby / right so
ghostly a soul blinded with dedely sin is all vmbylapped with this ghostly
light. and yet he is never the better / for he is blinded and woll not see ne
know his blyndenesse / And that is one of the most lettynge of grace. that a
wretchyd man woll not be a know of his own blyndnesse for pride of himself or
else if he know it he charge not. but makyth myrthe and game as he were
over all syker / Therefore unto al thise men that are thus blinded and bound
with the love of this world / and are foul forshape fro the fayrhede of man I
say and counsel that they think on her soule^ and that they able hem unto
grace asmoche as they may. and that may they do upon this wise if that they
woll / When that they feel hemself out of grace and ouerlayed with dedely
syn^e: then that they think what myscheyf and what peril it is to hem for
to be put out of grace and departed fro god as they ben / For there is no thing
that holds hem fro the pytte of hell that they ne should right soon fall
therein but a bare syngyll threde of this bodily life whe^by they hang / what
lyghtlyer may be lost than a sengyl ^h^ede may be broken in two / For were the
breath stopped in her body: and that may lightly fall. her soul shall pass
forth and anon be in hell without end / And if they would think thus they
should quake and shake for dread of the rightful domes of god. and of the
hard punysshyng of syn^e / and they should make sorrow and morn for her syn^e
and for lackyng of grace / and then^e should they cry and pray yt they might
have grace / and if they did thus then^e should grace fall in and put out
derknesse and hardness of heart and weyknes of will / and give hem might and
strength for to forsake the false love of this world as much as is dedely
syn^e / For there is no soul so far fro god thorugh wickidnes of will in
dedely syn^e: I out take none that lives in this body of syn^e that he ne may
through grace be righted and reformed to clennesse of living. if he woll bow
his will to god with meekness for to amend his life. and hertly axe grace and
foryeuenes of him / and excuse our lord* and fully accuse himself / For holy
writ says. Nolo morte^ pcco^ris sed magis vt co^nertat et viuat / That is.
Our lord says: I wol not the death of a syn^er but I woll more that he be
turned to me and live / For our lord woll that the most froward man that
lives forshapen through syn^e if he torn his will and ask grace that he be
reformed to his lyknesse /

That refourmyng in faith and in feeling may not suddenly be gotten by grace and
much bodily and ghostly traueyle in length of time / Caplm xvii.
THis refourmyng is in faith as I have before said that lightly may be had /
But after this comyth refourminge in faith and in feeling that may not lightly
begote but thorugh long traueylle and much business / For refourmynge in
faith is common to all chosen souls though they ben in the lowest degree of
charity / But refourmyng in felyng is specially of thise souls that may come
to the state of perfeccyon and that may not suddenly be had. but after great
plente of grace and much ghostly traueylle a soul may come thereto / and yt
is when he is first helyd of his ghostly syknes /: and when all bitter
passions and flesshly lusts. and other old felynges are burnt out of the
heart with fire of desire and new gracyous felynges arne brought Inn with
brennynge love and ghostly light / Then right nyghe hygheth a soul to
perfeccyon and to refourmynge in feeling /

For soth it is. right as a man yt is brout nigh to death through bodily siknes
though he receive a medicyne by the which he is restored and siker of his life
/ he may not therefore anon rise up and goo to work as an hole may for the
feebleness of his body holds him down that he must abide a good while and
keep him well with medicynes^ and dyete him by mesure after ye ^echynge of a
leche till he may fully recover bodily hele. Right so ghostly^ he that is
brought to ghostly death through dedely syn^e though he through medicyne of the
sacrament of penance be restored to life that he shall not be dampened /
nevertheless he is not anon hole of all his passions and of all his flesshly
desires. ne able to contemplaco^n / but him behooves abide a great while. and
take good keep of himself / and rule him so that he might recover full hele of
soul. for he shall langern a great while or that he be fully hole /
Nevertheless if that he take medicynes of a good leche. and use hem in time with
mesure and discreco^n he shall much the sooner be restored to his ghostly
strength. and come to refourmynge in feeling / For refourmynge in faith is the
lowest state of all chosen souls / for byneth that might they not well be /
But refourmyng in feeling is the hiest state in this life that the soul may
come to But fro the lowest to the highest may not a soul suddenly (...). no more
than a man that woll clymbe upon a ladder (...) sets his foot upon the
lowest stele may at the next flee up to the hyeste / But him behooves goo by
process one after another till he may come to the ouerest / Right so it is
ghostly. no man is made suddenly souereyn in grace: but through long exercise and
slye werkyng of a soul may com thereto / namly when he helpyth and techyth a
wretchyd soul in whom al grace lies / For without special help and Inwardly
techynge of him may no soul come thereto.

The cause why so few souls in rewar^de of the multitude of other comen to
this refourmynge in faith and in feeling / Caplm xviii.
But now say thou. Sith our lord is so curteys of his goodness. and of his
gracyous yeftes so free / wonder it is then^e that so few souls as it
semyth in reward of ye multitude of other may come to this refourmyng in
feeling / It semyth that he were dangerous and that is not sothe / or that he
took no reward of his creatures. the which by taking of faith are become
his servants / Unto this I may answer and say as me thinks. that one
enchesen is this / Many that are reformed in faith sentten not her hertes for
to profit in grace. ne for to seek none hyer estate of good living thruh^
besye traueylle in prayenge and thynkyng. and other bodily and goostly werkyng
/ but hem think it enough to hem to keep he^selfe out of dedely syn^e. and for
to stand stylle in that plyghte as they are in / For they say that it is
enough to hem for to be saaf and have the leest degree in heaven / They wol
coueyte no more / Thus perchance does some of the chosen souls that leden
in the world actyf life / and that is lityll wonder of hem / For they are so
occupied with worldly business that needs for to be done that they may not
fully set her hertes for to profit in ghostly werkynge / And nevertheless it
is peryllous to hem. for they fall out all day / and are now up and now
down. and may not come to the stablynes of good living Nevertheless they are
somewhat excusable for her astate of living / But other men and wym^en that are
free fro worldly business if they woll and may have her nedfull sustynau^ce
with out great bodily besynes. specially as religyous men and wymmen may that
bynden hemself to the state of perfecco^n by taking of relygion. and other men
also in seculer state that have much reason in great kyndly wit. and might
if they would dyspose hem there to come to much grace / Thise me^ are more to
blame. for they stand stylle as they were idle and woll not prouffyte in
grace. ne in no ferder seeking for to come to the love and the knowing of god
^For sothly it is peryllous to a soul that is reformed oonly in faith and
woll no more seek profit. ne give him besily to ghostly traueyle / for he
may so lightly lose that he has. and fall again to dedely syn^e. For a soul
may not stand still always in one state while that it is in the flesh / For
it is either profitynge in grace or peyrynge in syn^e / For it fares by him as
it does by a man that were draw out of a pytte. and when he were up he would
no ferd goo than the pyttes brynke / Sothly he were a much fool. for a
lityll puff of wind or an unwarily stiryng of himself should soon cast him
down again wors tha^ he was before / Nevertheless if he flee fro ye brynke as
far as he may and goo forth on the earth. then^e though there come a great
storm he is the more syker. for he fallyth not in the pytte / Right so
ghostly. he that is drawn out of the pytte of syn^e through refourmyng of faith
/ and when he is out of dedely syn^e he thy^^kyth himself syker enough / And
therefore he woll not profit but hold him still as he is by the pyttis brynke
as nere as he may sothly he is not wise / for at the leest te^ptaco^n of his
enmye or of his flesh he falls in to syn^e again / But never theles if he
flee fro the pytte. that is if he set his heart (...) for to com^ to more
grace. and for to traueyle besily how he (...) come thereto. and give him hertly
to prayeng: thinkyng and other (...) works doing / though great te^ptaco^ns
rise against him (...) fallyth not lightly to dedely syn^e again / And sothly it
is (...) to me ye sythen grace is so good and so profitable why a (...) when
he has but a little thereof / ye so little that he might no less have that
he wolle say hoo / I wolle no more of this / for I have enough / When I see a
worldly man though he have of worldly good much more than him needs / yet he
woll never say hoo / I have enough I woll no more of this / But he woll
coueyte more and more: and traueyle all his wits and his myghtes / And never
woll stynte of his coueytise till he may have no more / Much more then

How that without much bodily and ghostly besines and without much grace and
meekness souls may not be reformed in feeling / ne keep therein after they
come thereto / Caplm xx.
NOw sayste thou. Sith it is so that refourmyng in faith is so low and so
peryllous for to rest in by cawse of dread of falling again / And refourmynge
in feeling is so high and so syker / who so might come thereto. Then
coueyteste thou for to wit what manner traueylle were most spedefull for to
use / by the which a man might prouffyte inn. and come thereto. Or if there
were any certain traueylle or special deed by the which a man might come to
that grace and that refourmynge in feeling / As unto this I say thus / Thou
wotest well that what man or woman woll dispose him for to come to clennesse of
heart and to feeling of grace him behooves have much traueylle and great
fighting in will and in work lastyngly ayenste wicked stirynges of all the
head sins / Not oonly ayenste pride or Envy but against all other with all the
spices that comen out of them / as I have said before in the first writynge.
For why? Passions and flesshly desires let the clennes of the heart and pees
in conscience / And him behooves also for to traueylle for to get all virtues
/ Not oonly chastity and abstynence / but also pacyence and myldenesse /
charytee and meekness and all the other / And this may not be done by one
manner of work / but by diverse works and many after sundry dysposycyons of
men / As now prayenge: now thinking now worchynge some good works / now
assayenge them self in diverse wise / In hunger: in thirst: in cold: in
sufferynge of shame and dyspyte if need be / And in other bodyly disease for
love of virtue and sothfastnesse / This know thou well / for this redest you
in every book y^ techeth of good living / Thus says every man that woll styre
men^es souls to the love of god / And so it semyth that there is no special
traueyle ne certain deed through which only a soul might come to that grace /
but pryncipally through grace of our lord Jesus. and by many deeds and great in
all that he may done. and yet all this is lityll enough / And one skylle may
be this. For sith our lord Ihu^ himself is special master of this craft:
and he is special leche of ghostly syknes: for without him all is nou^te. it
is therefore reasonable that after that he techeth and stireth so a man follow
and work / But he is a simple master that can not teache his discyple while he
is in learning but ever one lesson / and he is an unwise leche that by one
medycyne woll he^e all sores / Therefore our lord Ihu^ that is so wise and so
go^e for to show his wysdom and his goodness he techeth diverse (...) to his
discyples after that they profit in her learning. and yeueth to diverse souls
sere and diverse medycynes after the ^^lynge of her syknes / Also a another
skylle is this: If there (...) any certain deed by the which a soul might
come to the p^^fyte love of god then^e should a man wene that he might come
thereto by his own work and through his own traueyle as a merchant comyth to
his mede by his own traueyle only (...) his own work / Nay it is not so
ghostly in the love of (...) For he that woll serve god wisely and come to
perfyte love (...) god. he shall coueyte to have none other mede but him (...)
But then for to have him may no creature deserve (...) by his own traueyle
/ For though a man might traueyle (...) much bodily and ghostly as all
creatures that ever were might. he mygte not deserve only by his works for
to have god to his mede: for he is souereyn bliss and e^dles godenes. and
passith without comparison al men^es desert^. and therefore he may not begote^
by no man^es special works as bodily mede may / For he is free and yeuyth
himself where he woll. and wha^ he woll. neither for this ne for ye / ne in
this time ne after that time / For though a soul worche all yt he can and may
all his life time / perfyte love of Ihesu shall he never have till our lord
Ihesu woll freely give it / Nevertheless on that other side I say also I hope he
yeuyth it not but if a man worche and traueyle all that he can and may. ye
till him think he may no more / or else be in full will thereto if he might /
And so it semyth yt neither grace only without full worchyng of a soul that
in it is / ne worchynge alone without grace brings a soul to the refourmyng
in feeling / the which refourmyng stondeth in perfect love and charity / But
that one Joined to ye other / that is grace Joined to worchyng brings in to a
soul the blessed feeling of perfyte love / the which grace may not rest fully
but on meke souls that been full of the dread of god / Therefore may I say: he
that has no mekenes ne does his besynes. may not come to this reformyng in
felyng / He has not full mekenes that can not feel of himself sothfastly as he
is / As thus / He that does all the good deeds that he can / as in fasting:
wakyng: weryng of the heir. and all other suffryng of bodyly penance / or
does all the outward works of mercy to his eue^crysten: or else Inward /
as prayenge: weeping: sighyng / and thynkyng if he rest ever in hem and lene
somoche to hem: and rewards hem so greatly in his own syghte yt he presumyth
of his own deserts. and thinks himself ever rich and good holy and
virtuous / sothly aslong as he felyth thus he is not meke enough / Ne though he
say or think that all that he does is of goddis yeft and not of himself. he
is not yet meke enough for he may not make himself yet naked of all his good
deeds / ne make him poor sothfastly in spirit / ne feel himself naught as he
is / And sothly until a soul can feel ably thorugh grace naught himself. and
baren him from all the good deeds that he does thorugh beholdynge of
sothefastnes of Ihesu he is not perfytly meke / For what is meekness but so
the fastness? Soothly naught else / And therefore he that thorugh grace may
see Ihesu how that he does all / And himself does right naught but suffers
Ih^u worche in him what him likyth. he is meke / But this is full hard. and as
it were Impossyble. and unreasonable to a man that worcheth all by man^es
reason / and sees no ferder for to do many good deeds / and then for to
arrette all to Ihu^. and set himself at naught / Nevertheless who so might
have a ghostly syghte of sothfastnes him should think it full true and full
reasonable for to do so / And sothly he that has this syghte shall never do
the less / but he shall be styred for to traueyle bodily and ghostly much the
more and with the better will / And this may be one cause why some men
peraue^ture swynke and sweet and pyne her wretched body with outragyous
penance all her life time / and are ever saye^g orysons and sawters and many
other deeds / and yet may they not come to the ghostly feeling of the love of
god as it semyth that some done in short time with less pain. for they have
not that mekenes that I spoke of Also on that other side I say he that does
not his business that thinks thus. whereto should I traueyle / whereto should
I pray or think wake or fast / or any other bodily penance do for to come
to such grace sythen it may not be gotten (...) had but only of the free yefte
of Ih^u / Therefore I woll aby^^ in flesshlines as I am. and right naught do of
such works* bodily ne ghostly until he give it / For if he woll give it he
askyth no worchyng of me what so that I do. and how lityll that I do I shall
have it / And if he woll not give it. traueyl^ I never so fast therefore I get
it never the sooner / He that says thus may not come to this refourmyng. for
he drawyth hi^ self wylfully to ydlenes of flessheed: and vnableth him to the
yefte of grace in asmoche as he puts fro him both Inward werkyng yt
sto^dith in lasting desire and in lo^gyng to Ihu^ and outward werkyng by
traueyle of his body in outward deeds. so may he not have it / therefore I say
he yt has no true mekenes ne full hertly besynes other inward only by great
fervor and lastyng desire. and besy prayer and thought in god. or else both
Inward and outward. may he not come to this ghostly refourmynge of his image
/

An entree how a soul shall have her in menynge and worchinge that woll come
to this refourmyng by ensample of a pilgryme going to Iherlm. And of two manner
of mekenes Caplm xxi.
Nevertheless for thou coueytest for to have some manner worchyng by the which
thou might the rather nyghe^ to that refourmyng / I shall say as me thinks
by the grace of our lord Ihesu the shortest and the redyest help that I know
in this werchyng / And how that shall be I shall tell yt by an ensample of a
good pilgrim upon this wise / There was a man that would goo to Ihrlm. And for
he knew not the way he came to a another man that he hoped knew the way
better thither. and asked wheder he might come to that cite / that other man
said to him that he might not come thyd without great disease and much
traueylle / For the way is long and peryllous and full of great thieves and
robbers / and many other lettynges there ben that fallen to a man in the going
/ And also there are many sere ways as it semyth ledyng thydwarde / But men
aldaye are slain and dispoylled and may not come to that place that they
coueyten / Nevertheless there is one way the which who so takes it and
holds it he wolle undertake that he should come to that cytee of Jerusalem.
and he should never lose his lyffe. ne be slain ne deye for defawte He should
often be robbed and evil beat and suffer much disese in the gooynge. but his
life should be saaf / Then^e said the pilgrim / So that I may have my life
saaf and come to that place that I coueyte to. I charge not what myscheyff I
suffer in going / And therefore say me what thou wolt and sothly I behote the
for to do after the. That other man answers and says thus / Lo I set the
in the right way / This is ye way And that thou keep the learning that I teache
the / what so you herest see or felyst that should let the in the way
abide not with it wyllfully / tare not for it restfully. behold it not: like
it not: dread it not / but ever goo forth in thy way. and think yt thou
would be at Ihrlm / for that thou coueytest. and that thou desyrest. and
naught else but that. And if men rob the and dispoyll the: beat the: scorn
the: despise the / strive not again if thou wolte have thy life / but hold the
with the harm that you have* and goo forth as naught were. that thou take no
more harm And also if men woll tarry the with tales. and feed the with
lesynges for to draw yt to myrthes: and for to leave thy pilgrimage: make a
deef ere and answer not again / and say naught else but that thou would be
at Ihrlm / And if men profer the yeftes and wol make the rich with wordly good
tente not to he^ think ever on Ihrlm / And if thou woll hold this way and do
that I have said. I undertake thy life yt thou shall not be slain. but thou
shall come to that place that thou coueytest to / Ghostly to our purpoos: Ihrlm
is asmoche for to say. as a sight of peace / and betokens conte^placo^n in
perfyte love of god / For conte^placo^n is nout else but a syghte of god
which is very pees / Then if thou coueyte for to come to this blyssed sight
of very pees. and be a true pilgryme to Ihrlm (...)^ though it be so that I
were never there: nevertheless as (...) forth as I can I shall set the in the
way thydwarde / The begyn^yng of the high way in the which thou shall goo /
is ^^fourmyng in faith grounded mekely in the faith and in the (...) of holy
church as I have said before / For trust sykerly though you have syn^ed here
before^ if thou be now reformed by the sacrament of penance after the law of
holy church that you art in the right way / Now then^e sithe^ you art in the
syker way if thou woll speed in thy going and make good Iournayes* yt behooves
to hold thise ii. things often in thy mind. meekness and love: and yt is: I
am naught I have nout. I coueyte naught but one / Thou shalt have the meaning
of thise words in thyn intent and in habytt of thy soul lastyngly though thou
hauue hem not ever specially in thy thought. for ye needs not / Mekenes
sayth^ I am naught / I have naught / Love says I coueyte noute but one: and
that is Ihu^ / Thise two stre^ges well festned with the mind of Ihu^ makyth
good a cord in ye harp of the soul when they ben craftly towched with the
finger of reason / For the lower thou smytes upon that one the hyer sowneth
that other / The less thou felyst that thou art or that thou haste of thyself
through mekenes / the more thou coueytest for to have of Ihu^ in desire of love
/ I mean not only of that mekenes that a soul felith in the syghte of his
own syn^e for freelnes and wretchidnes of this life or of the wretchidnes of
his euencrysten / For though this mekenes be soth fast and medicynable.
nevertheless it is boystous and flesshly as in regard not clean ne soft ne
lovely / But I mean also this mekenes that the soul felyth through grace in
syghte and beholdynge of the endless being and the wonderful goodness of Ihu^
And if thou may not see it yet with thy ghostly eye. that thou trow it / For
through syghte of his being either in full faith or in felyng thou shall hold
thyself not only the most wretch that is. but also as naught in substance
of thy soul though thou had never done sin^e. And that is lovely mekenes
For in reward of Ihesu that is sothfastly all: thou art right naught / And
also that thou think that thou have right naught: but art as a vessel that
stondeth ever to me as naught were therein as of thyself / For do thou never so
many good deeds outward or inward till you have and feel that you have ye love
of Jesus: you have rit naught / for with ye precious licour only may thy soul
be fulfilled and with none other / and for asmoche as ye thing alone is so
precious and worthy therefore what you have or what you do hold it as nout for
to rest in without ye site of ye love of Ihu^. Cast it all behind the and
forgete it that thou myt have that. that is the best of all / Right as a true
pilgryme going to Ihrlm leueth behind him house and land. wife and child /
and makyth himself poor and bare fro all thing that he has that he might
goo lightly without lettyng / right so if thou wolt be a ghostly pilgryme thou
shall make thyselfe naked fro all that thou have. that are both good deeds and
badde and cast hem all behind the that thou be so poor in thine own felyng
/ that there be no thing of thyn own worchynge that thou wolt lene upon
restyngly / but ever desiryng more grace and love / and ever seeking the
ghostly presence of Ihu^ / And if thou do thus then shall thou set in thin
heart fully that thou would be at Ihrlm and at none other place but there /
And that is. thou shall set in thyn heart holy and fully that thou would
no thing have but the love of Ihu^ and the ghostly syghte of him as he woll
show him / for to that only (...) thou made and bought / and that is thy
begyn^yng and thyn endyng thy Joy and thy bliss / And therefore what so ever
that thou have. be thou never so rich in other deeds bodily or ghostly but if
you have that and know and feel that thou have it. hold that thou have right
naught / Prynte well this reason in thy meaning of thy heart. and cleue sadly
thereto. and it shall save the fro all ^^rylles in thy gooynge. that thou shall
never perysshe. and it (...) save the fro the thieves and robbers ye which I
call unclean ^^^rytes. that though they spoil the and beat the through diverse
(...) thy life shall ever be saaf / And shortly if thou keep (...) as I shall
say the you shall escape al perils and myscheues. and (...) to the cite of
Irhlm within short time / Now thou art in ye way and know what the place
hyghte and whyd thou shall draw to / Begyn^e then^e for to goo in thy Journey
/ Thy forth going is naught else but ghostly worchynge and bodily also when
need is. which thou shall use by discreco^n upon this wise / what work yt it
be that you shall do after the degree and the state yt thou stondist in bodily
or ghostly if it help this gracyous desire that thou have for to love Ihesu:
and make it more hole: more easy and more mighty to all virtues. and to all
goodness. that work hold I best: be it prechynge. be it thinking / be it
redynge: be it worchyng / And aslonge as that work stre^gthyth most thy heart
and thy will to ye love of Ihu^. and ferdest drawyth thyn affecco^n and thy
thought fro worldly vanytee it is good for to use it / And if it be so that
through use savor of that lesseth^ and the thinks an other work sauoureth ye
more. and thou felyst more grace in a another / take a another and leave that /
For though thy desire and the yernyng of thyn heart to Ihesu should be ever
vnchau^gable: nevertheless thy ghostly works that thou shall use in prayenge or
thinking for to feed and nouryssh^ thy desire may be dyuers^ and may well be
changed after that thou felyste the dysposed through grace in applyeng of thyn
own heart / ^or it fares by works and by desire as it does by styckes and by
a fire / For the more styckes are laid to ye fire: the gretter is the fire /
Right so the more diverse ghostly workynge that a man has in his thought for
to keep hole his desire: ye mytyer and more bren^yng shall his desire be to god
And therefore look wisely what work thou canste best do. and that most
helpyth for to save hole this desire to Ihu^ if thou be free and art not bound
but vnd the common law. and that do / Bind the not to wylfull customs
vnchaungably that should let the fredom of thine heart for to love Ihu^ if
grace would visyte the specially / For I shall tell the which customs are
ever good and nedeful to be kept / Loo such custom is ever good to hold yt
sto^deth in getyng of virtue and lettyng of syn^e. and that custom should
never be left / for you shall ever be meke: pacye^t^ sobre and chaste if thou well
do. and so of al other vtues But the custom of a another thing that lettyth a
better is good for to leave when time is there a man may / As thus If a man
have in custom for to say thus many beedes / or for to think this manner of
thoute thus long time / or for to wake or knele thus long or any other such
bodily deed. this custom is for to leave sometime wha^ reasonable cause lettith.
or else if more grace comyth otherwise /

Of tarienges and temptaco^ns that souls feel by her ghostly enmyes in her
ghostly knowinge and gooyng to Ihrlm. and of remedies ayenste hem / Caplm xxii.
NOw art thou in the way and woost how thou shall go Now bewaar of enmyes
that woll be besy for to let the if they may / for her intent is for to putt
out of thyn heart that desire and that longyng that thou have to the love of
Ihu^ and for to drive the home again to the love of worldly vany / te / for
there is no thing that greueth hem somoche / These enmyes are pryncipally
flesshly desires and vain dredes that risen out of thyn heart through
corrupco^n of thy flesshly kyn^e / and would let thy desire of the love of
god that they might fully and restfully ocupye thyn heart / Thise are thyn next
en^^^es / Also other enmyes there are. as unclean spirytes that a^^besy with
sleyghtes and wyles for to disceyue the / But one r^^medie shall thou have that
I said before / What so it be th^^ they say trow hem not but hold forth thy
way and only (...) the love of Ihu^ / Answer^ ever thus: I am naught I have
^^^ughte I coueyte naught but only the love of our lord Ih^^ If thyn enmyes
say to the first thus by stirynges in heart th^^ thou art not shryuen aright.
or there is some old syn^e (...) thyn heart that thou know not ne never
were shriuen (...) And therefore thou must torn home aye^ and leave thy desire
(...) shryue the better / Trow not this saying for it is false / for y^ art
shryue trust sikerly. and that thou art in ye way and the needs no more
ransakyng of shryfte for that y^ is passed / Hold forth thy way and think
on Ihrlm / Also if they say that thou art not worthy to have the love of god.
whereto shall thou coueyte that thou may not hauene art not worthy thereto.
Trow hem not but goo forth and say thus / Not for I am worthy but for I am
vnworthy^ therefore would I love god / For if I had it. that should make me
worthy / And sythen I was made thereto though I should never have it yet woll I
coueyte it / and therefore woll I pray and think that I might get it / And
then if thine enmyes see that thou begynnest to wax bold and well wylled to
thy work. they begin to wexe aferde of the / Nevertheless they woll not cease
of taryenge the when they may as long as thou art gooynge in the way /
what with dread and manassynge on that one side. what with flaterynge and falls
pleysynge on that other side for to make the break thy purpose and turn home
again they woll say thus. If thou hold forth thy desire to Ihesu so fully
trauelynge as thou begynnest. thou shall fall in to syckenes or in to
fantasyes or in to frenesyes as thou see that some done Or thou shall fall
in to pouertee and bodily myscheyf. and no man shall well help the / Or thou
might fall in to prive temptaco^ns of the fend that thou shall not help
thyselfe For it is wonder peryllous to any man for to give him fully to the
love of god and leave all the world. and no thing coueyte but oonly the love
of hym^ for so many perils may fall that a man knows not of / And therefore
torn home again and leave this desire / for thou shall never bring it to the
end / and do as other worldly men done.

Thus sayen thyn enmyes. but trow hem not / but hold for the thy desire / and
say not else but thou would have Ihesu and be at Ihrlm / And if they
perceive then thy will so strong that thou wolt not spare for syn^e ne for
syknesse. for fantasyes ne for frenesyes / for dowtes ne for dredes of ghostly
te^ptaco^ns / for myscheyf ne for pouerte / for life ne for death. but ever
forth thou wolt with one thing? and no thing but one. and make deef ere to
hem as though you herd hem not. and holdeste ye forth styfly in thy prayer and
in thine other ghostly works without stintyng with discreco^n after counsel
of thy souereyn or of thy ghostly fader / then begin they for to be wroth
and to goo a little nerer the. Then^e they begin for to rob the and beat the
and do the all the shame that they can / And that is when they make that all
the deeds that thou do ben they never so well done are denied of other men
as evil: and turned in to the wors party / And what so ever it be that thou
would have done in help of thy body or of thy soul it shall be let or
hyndred by other men. so that thou shall be put fro thy will in all thing that
thou skilfully coueytes. And all this they done that you sholdest be styred to
ire or male^coly or evil will against thy eue^cristen / But against all thise
diseases and al other that thou may feel use this remedy / Take Ihu^ in thy
mind and anger y^ not with hem / Tarry not with hem. but think on thy lesson
y^ thou art naught that thou have naught thou may noughtelese of erthly good
thou coueytest naught but the love of Ihu^ and hold forth thy way to Ihrlm
with thy occupaco^n / (...) nevertheless if thou be tarried sometime through
freelte of thy^^^ with such vneases that fallen to thy bodily life through
(...) will of man or malice of the fend. as soon as thou may (...) again to
thyself leave of the thynkyng of thy disease and (...) forth to thy work /
Abide not long with hem for (...) thyn enmyes.

Of a general remedy against wicked stirynges and (...) taryenges that fallen
to her hertes of the flesh and of the (...) and of the fend / Caplm xxii^.
ANd after this when thin enmyes see that thou a^te (...) well wylled that thou
art not angry nor heavy ne w^^the ne much stired ayenste no creature for
ought that they may do or speak against the. but set thy heart fully for
to suffer all that may fall. ease or unease: praysyng or lackyng. and that thou
wolt charge no thing with that yt thou might keep thy thought and thy desire
hoole to the love of god. then^e are they much abashed / But then woll they
assaye the with flaterynge and vain plesynge / And that is when they bring to
the syghte of thy soul all thy good deeds and virtues / and bear upon the that
all men praysen the and speken good of thy holiness / and how al men love the
and worship the for thy holy living / Thus done thin enmyes that thou should
think her saying soth and have delight in this vain Joy and rest the there
in / But if thou do well thou shall hold all such Iangelynge falsed and
flateringe of thyn enmye that profereth the to drink venym tempered with honye
/ And therefore refuse it and say thou woll not thereof. but thou would be at
Ihrlm / Such lettynges thou shall feel or else other like. what of thy
