flesh what of the world. what of the fend moo than^e I may reherce now /
For a man aslonge as he suffers his thought wylfully run about the world
in beholdynge of so^dry things he perceyueth few lettynges: But as soon as he
drawyth all his thought and his yernynge to one thing oonly for to have that.
for to know that: for to love that / and that is only Ihu^ / then^e shall he
well feel many paynfull lettynges For every thing that he feleth and is not
that yt he coueyteth is lettynge to him / Therefore I have told the of some
specially as for example / And ouermore I say generally that what styrynge that
thou felyste of thy flesh or of the fend pleysau^te or paynfull / bitter or
sweet: likynge or dredefull. gladsom or sorrowful that would draw down thy
thought and thy desire fro ye love of Ihu^ to worldly vanyte. and let
utterly thy gostly couetyse that thou haste to the love of him. and that thy
heart should be occupied with that stirynge restyngly. set it at naught /
receive it not wylfully. tarry not therwyth tolo^ge. But if it be of worldly
thing yt behooves needs to be done to thyselfe or to thyn euencrysten. speed
the soon of it. and bring it to an end that it ha^ge not on thyn heart / If it
be a another thing yt needs not or else it towcheth not the. charge it not.
Ian gill not therewith. ne anger the not. dread it not: like it not. but smite
out of thyn heart redely. and say thus / I am naught: I have naught. Naught
I seek ne coueyte but the love of Jesus / ^rnyghte thy thought to this desire
and strength it. and mayntene it with prayer and with other ghostly works
that thou forgete it not: and it shall led the in thy right way and save the
fro all perils. that though thou feel hem thou shalt not peryssh^ / And I
hope that it shall bring the to perfect love of our lord Ihu^ / Nevertheless
on that other side I say also / what work or what stirynge it be that may
help thy desire strength it and nouryssh^ it. and make thy thought ferrest
fro lust ^ mind of the world more hole and more bren^ynge to the love of god
whether it be prayenge or thynkyng. stilnes or spekinge: redynge or herynge /
on^lynes or comonynge: going or ^^^tynge keep it for the time and werche
therein aslonge as (...) lastyth / If it be so that thou take therwyth mete and
drink (...) as a pilgryme does / and keep discreco^n in thy worching (...)
counseyle and ordinance of the souereyne: For have he (...) so great haste in
his going / yet he woll ete and drink and (...) Do thou like wise / For
though it let the one time (...) forther the a another time /

Of an evil day and a good night what it means (...) the love of the
world is lykened to an evil day* and (...) of god to a good night / Caplm
xxi^^^*
IF thou wolt wit then^e what this desire is (...) Ihu^ / for he makith this
desire in the and yeueth it (...) he it is that desires in the / and he it is
that is desired / (...) and he does al if thou might see him / Thou do
naught but suffrest him worche in thy soul / and assentyst to him with great
gladness of heart that he wouche sauf for to ^oo so in the / Thou art
naught else but a reasonable Instrument wherein yt he worcheth / And therefore
when you felyst thy thoute by towchi^ge of his grace take up with desire to Ihu^
with a mighty devout will for to plese him and love him. then^ think that thou
have Ihesu. for he it is that thou desire Behold him well for he gooth
before the: not in bodily lyknes but vnsenseably by pryue presence of his
might / Therefore see him ghostly if thou may. and fasten al thy thought and
thine affecco^n to him. and follow him where so he gooth. for he shall led
the the right way to Ihrlm. that is the syghte of pees and conte^placo^n /
Thus prayed the prophet to ye fader of heaven saying thus: Emitte luce^ tua^
and veritate^ tua^. ip^a me dedux eru^t et adduxeru^t in monte^ scm^ tuu^ and
in tab^nacula tua: P. xlii.
That is / Fader of heaven send out thy light and thy sothfastnesse. yt is thy
sone Ihu^ / and he shall led me by desire in me to ye holy hylle and in to thy
tabernacles. that is to the felyng of perfyte love and heyghte in conte^placo^n
/ Of this desire spekyth the prophet thus. Memoriale tuu^ in desiderio ai^e
me. Ai^a mea desiderauit te in nocte: ^
sed and sp^us meus in p^cordiis meis. That is: For de Ihu^ the mind of the is
prynted in desire of my soul / for my soul has desired the in the night.
and my spirit has coueyted the in all thynkynges / And why the prophet says
he has desired god all in the night as a tymefull space bytwix days two /
For wha^ one day is ended a another comith not anon / but first comyth night
and departs the days sometime long and sometime short / and then^e after
comyth a another day / The prophet meaned not only of this manner of night:
but he meaned a ghostly night / Thou shall vndsto^de that there ben two days
or two lyghtes / The first is a falls lygte. the second is a true light / The false light is the love of this world that a man has in himself of corrupco^n
of his flesh / The true light is the perfyte love of Ihesu felyd thorugh
grace in a man^es soul. The love of this world is a false light / For it
passes away and lasts not / and so it perfourmeth not that ye it behoteth
/ This light behighte the fe^de to Adam when he stired him to sin and said
thus / Aperientur oculi vestri et eritis sicut dii / Gen^. 3.
That is / your eyes shall be opened and ye shall be as goddis / And he said
sothe there. For when Adam had sinned anon his Inner eye was sperred and
ghostly light wythdrawe. and his utter eyes were opened / and he felt and saw
a new light of flesshly likyng and worldly love that he saw not before / And
so saw he a new day but this was an evil day / For this was it that Job
waryed when he said thus / Pereat dies in qua natus su^ / That is: Job 3.
Peryssh^ the day in the which I was borne / He waryed not the day rennynge
in the year that god made / but he waryed this day that man made. that is the
co^cupiscens and the love of this world in the which he was borne though he
felyd it not^ Then^e this day and this light he asked of god that it should
perissh^ and no longer last / But the everlasting love of Ihu^ is a true
day and a blessed light / For god is both love and light. and he is
everlasting as saint Ioh^n says / Qui diligit deu^ manet in lumine / That is:
He that loves god dwellyth in the light Than what man perceyueth and sees the
love of this world falls and faylinge. and for that he woll forsake it and seek
the love of Ihu^ / He may not as soon feel the love of him. but he must abide
awhyle in the night / for he may not suddenly come fro that one light to that
other / that is fro the love of the worl^^ to perfyte love of god / This night
is naught else but a forberynge and a wythdrawyng of the thought and of the
soul fro erthly things by great desire and yernyng for to love and see and
feel Ihu^ and ghostly things / This is the night / For right as the night
is derke and ever hydynge from all bodily creature: and a restynges of all
bodily deeds /

Right so a man that settyth him fully for to think on Jesus / and for to
desire only the love of him is besye for to hide his thought fro vain
beholdynge and perceiving. and his affection fro flesshly liking and loving
of all bodily creatures / So that his thought may be made free and not
subgett. ne his affection bound ne pyned ne troubled in no thing lower or
woors than himself / And if he may do so then^e it is night with him: for
then^e he is in derknesse / But this is a good night and a light derknesse /
for it is a stoppynge out of the false love of this world. and it is a nyghing
of the true day / And soothly the derker that this night is the nerer is the
true day of the love of Ihu^ / For the more that ye soul may through longyng
to god be hid fro noise and dyn^e of flesshli affecco^ns and unclean
thoughts the nerer is it for to feel the light of the love of him for it is
even at it / Thus semyth it the prophet meaned when he said thus / Cum in te
nebris sedeo dn^s lux mea est. That is: when I sit in derknes our lord is my
light / That is: when my soul is hid fro all stirynges of sin as it were
in sleep: then^e is our lord my light. for then nygheth he of his grace for
to show me of his light / Nevertheless this night is sometime paynfull /
first when a man is much foul and is not through grace used to be often in
this derknes but would feign have it. and therefore he settyth his thought and
his desire to godwarde asmoche as he may / he would not feel ne think but
only of him. and by cause that he may not lightly have it therefore it is
paynfull / For the custom and the homelynes that he has had with sins
before of the world and of flesshly affecco^ns and erthly things. and his
flesshly deeds prees so upon him and ever smite in by maystry and draw down
all ye soul so hem that he may not well be hid fro hem as soon as he would /
Therefore this derkenes is paynfull to him / and namly wha^ grace towchith not
habu^dantly / Nevertheless if it be so with the. be not to heavy ne strive not
much as though thou would through maystry put hem out of thy thought / for
thou may. not do so but abide grace: suffer easily. and break not thyself
tomoche And slyely if thou may draw thy desire and thy ghostly beholding to
Ihu^: as if thou would not charge hem. For wete thou well when thou would
desire Ihesu and oonly think on him. and thou may not freely for precyng in of
such worldly thoughts: sothly thou art outward of the false day. and thou art
entryng in to this derkenes / But thy derkenes is not restfull by cause of
disease and vncu^nynge and vnclen^es of thy self / And therefore use it often and
it shall by process through feeling of grace be more easy and more restful to
the / And that is when thy soul through grace is made so free and so mighty
and so good and so gadred in to itself that it list not to think on right
naught / Then^e is it in a good derknesse / This naught I mean thus. that a
soul may through grace be gadred into itself freely and holy: and not be
driven against the will ne drawn down by maystry for to think or like or love
with cleuynge of affecco^n to any syn^e or vaynly any erthly thing then
thinks the soul naught / For then^e thynkith it of none erthly thing
cleuyngly / This is a rich naught / And this naught and this night is a great
ease for the soul that desires the love of Ihesu / It is in ease as for
thought of any e^^dely thing / nevertheless it is full besy for to think on
him / What thing then^e makyth this derkenes? Sothly naught else but a
gracyous desire for to have the love of Ihu^ / For yt desire and that longyng
that it has that time to ye love of god ^or to see him and have him dryueth
out of the heart all worldly vanytees and flesshly affecco^ns. and gadreth the
soul in to itself. and occupyeth it oonly for to think how it might come to
the love of him / And that time may it freely and deuo^tly behold Ihu^ whed
it woll pray or think. and so it bryngith it to this rygh^t naught. and
sothly it is not al derke ne nout wha^ it thinkyth thus For though it be derke
fro falls light it is not al derke fro ye true light. for ihu^ yt is both love
and lyte is in this derknes whed it be paynful or restfull / If it be paynful
then^e he is in ye soul as traueylyng in desire and lo^gynge to light. but he
is not yet as resting in love ne as showing his light / And therefore it is
called night and derknesse in asmoche as the soul is hid fro the false
light of the world. and has not yet fully feeling of true light: but is in
abidyng of that blessed love of god which it desires / Then^e if thou wolte
wit when thou art in this syker derkenesse and when not / you may assay thus
and seek no ferder but thus / When thou felyst thyn entente and thy will fully
set for to desire god. and think only ^n him / thou may as it were first
ask thyselfe in thyn own thought whether thou coueyte for to have any thing
of this life for love of itself / or for to have the use of any of thy bodily
wits in any creature / And then if thyn eye answer the thus / I would see
right naught / and thy mouth. I would savor right naught / and after thyn
eere. I would here right naught / and thy body. I would feel right nout / And
after if thine heart say. I would think right naught of erthly thing ne of
bodily deed / ne I would have affecco^n fastened flesshly to no creature but
oonly in god / and to godwarde if that I cowde / And when they answer all thus
to the and that is done full redily if grace towche the. then^e art thou entered
somewhat into this derkues / For though thou feel and perceive gle^tynges and
proferynges of vain thoughts and precynge in of flesshly affeccions.
nevertheless thou art in this profitable derknes if it be so that thyn
thought be not fyxed in hem / For such vayn ymagynaco^ns that fall in the
heart vnauisedly trowble^ this derknes / and pyneth the soul somewhat by cause
that it would be hid fro hem and may not / but they do not away y^ profit
of this derknes / for the soul shall by that way come to restfull myrknes /
And then^e is this derknes restful when the soul is hid for a time fro the
paynfull felyng of all such vayn thoughts. and only is rested in desire and
lo^gynge to Ihu^ with a ghostly beholdynge of him as it shall be said
afterward / But that lasts but a while hoole / Nevertheless though it be
but a short time it is full profitable /

How that the desire of Ihesu felt in this lyghtsom derknes sleeth al stirynges
of syn^e. and ableth the soul to perceive ghostly lyghtnynges fro the heavenly
Iherusalem that is Ihesu / Caplm xxv.
THen^e sithen this derknesse and this night is so good and so restfull
though it be short that stondeth only in desire and longyng to the love of
Ihu^ with a blind thynkyng on him how good then^e and how blessid is it for to
feel his love. and for to be illumyned with his blessid vnseable present light
for to see sothfastnes / the which light a soul receives wha^ the night
passith and the day spryngeth / This I hope was the nyighte that the prophet
meaned when he said: My soul has desired the in y^ night / As I have before
said. it is much better to be hid in this derke night fro beholding of the
world though it were paynful: than for to be out in falls lykyng of this
world yt semyth so shinyng and so comfortable to hem that are blind in
knowing of ghostly light / For when you art in this derknes thou art much
nerer Ihrlm than when thou art in the mids of the false light / Therefore
apply thine heart fully to the stiryng of grace and use for to won in this
derknes. and by often assayeng to be homly therein and it shall be so ^^e made
restfull to the / And the true light of ghostly knowing shall spring to the.
not all at ones: but pryuely by lityll and by lityll / as the prophet says:
Habita^tibus in regione vmbre mortis. lux orta est eis / That is: To dwelling
in the country of shadow of death light was sprongen / That is: Light of
grace sprongen and shall spring to all them that can won in the shadow of
death / that is in this derkenesse that is like to death /

For as death sleeth a living body and all flesshly felinges of it right so
desire to the love of Ihu^ felyd in this derkes sleeth al sins: all flesshly
affecco^ns. and all unclean thoughts for the time / And then nyghest thou
fast to Ihrlm / Thou art not there yet. but by small sodein lyghtynges that
glidyrth out of small caves fro that cytee shall thou mow see it fro far or
that thou come thereto / For wit thou well though yt thy soul be in this
restfull derknesse without troublynge of worldly vanytees / it is not yet
clothed all in light: ne turned all in to fire of love / But it felyth well
that there is so^what above itself that it knowith not ne has not yet. but
would have it and bren^yngly yerneth it / And that is naught else but ye
syighte of Ihrlm without forth. the which is like to a cytee / yt the prophet
Ezechyell saw in his visyons / He says that he saw a cite set upon an
hylle heldinge to the southe that to his syghte when it was moten was no more of
length and of bread than a reed that is vi. cubytes and a palm of length But
as soon as he was brought in to the cite and lokyd about him then^e thought
him that it was wonder much / For he saw many halles and chambres both open
and pryuee. He saw gates and porches outward and Inward / and much more
byldynge tha^ I say now on length and on bread many hundred cubits / Then
was this wonder to him how this cite within was thus long and so large that so
lityll to his sight was when he was without / This cite betokens the perfect
love of god set in the hylle of conte^placo^n. the which unto the syghte of a
soul that without the feeling of it traueyleth in the desire toward semyth
somewhat / but it semyth but a lityll thing no more than a reed that is vi.
cubytes and a palm of length / By vi. cubits are vndstonde the perfecco^n of
man^es work / And by the palm a lityll to wchynge of conte^placo^n / He sees
well that there is such a thing that passes the deserte of all the worchynge
of man a lityll as the palm passes the vi. cubytes / but he sees not within
what it is / nevertheless if he may come within the cite of conte^placo^n /
then sees he much more than he saw first /

How a man shall know falls Illumynaco^ns feyned by ye fend fro the true light
of knowing that comyth out of Ihu^ and by what tokens / Caplm xxvi.
But now bewaar of the mydday fend that feyneth light as it came out of Ihrlm
and is not so. For the tend sees that our lord Ihu^ shewyth light to his
lovers of so the fastnes / therefore in deceyuyng of hem that are unwise he
shewyth a light that is not true under color of a true light and deceyueth
hem. Nevertheless how a soul may know the light of sothfastnes when it
shyneth from god and when it is feyned through the enmye shall I say as me
thinks by an example of the fyrmament / Sometime the fyrmamente shewyth a
light fro the son^e / and semyth the son and is not And sometime shewyth the
true son^e truly. A knowing of that one from that other is this / The feyned
son shewyth him not but bitwix two black reyny clouds / Then^e by cause ye
son is nere there shyneth out fro the clouds a light as it were a son^e and
is none / But the true son^e shewith him when the fyrmament is clear or much
clered fro the black clouds / Now to our purpose / Some men as it semith
forsakes the love of the world and would come to the love of god and (...) the
light of vndstondynge of him. but they woll not com^ through this derknes that
I have spoken of before / They woll know hemselfe truly ne mekely what they
have been (...) ne what they are yet through syn^e / ne how naught they are
(...) her own kind ayenste god / They are not besy for to entree in to
hemself all other things outward left. and flee al wicked stirynges ye risen
in her hertes of pride envy ire or other sins through lasting desire to Ihu^
in prayenge and in thinking: in scylence and in weeping / and in other bodily
and ghostly exercise as devout men and holy men have done / But as soon as they
have forsake the world as it were outward in lyknesse or else soon after
they wene that they are holy and able for to have the ghostly understanding of
the gospel and of holy writ / and namly if they may fulfill letterly the
commandments of god and keep hem fro bodily sins that they wene yt they
love god perfytly / And therefore they woll anon preche and teache all other men
as if they had received grace of vndstondynge in perfecco^n of charity through
special yeft of the holy ghost / And also they are much more styred for as
much as they feel sometime much knowing as it were suddenly yeuen to hem
without great study before had. and also much fervor of love as it semyth
for to preche troth and rightwisnes to her euencrysten / Therefore they hold
it as a grace of god yt vysiteth hem with his blessid light before other
souls / Nevertheless if they woll look well about he^ they shall find that this
light of knowing and that hete that they feel comyth not of the true sone
that is our lord Ihu^. but it comith fro ye myddaye fend that feyneth light
and lykneth him to the son^e And therefore shall he be known by example before
said / Liyghte of cu^nynge that is feyned by the fend to a derke soul is
showed bitwix two black reyny clouds / The over cloud is presu^pcyon and
higheng of hemself / The nether cloud is down puttyng and a lowenge of his
euencristen / Then^e what light of knowing or felyng of fervor that it be yt
shyneth to a soul with presu^pcion and highenge of it self and disdeyne of his
eue^crysteu the same time felyd it is not light of grace yeuen of the holy
ghost though the knowing in itself were so thefast. but it is either of the
fend if it come suddenly or else of man's own wit if it come by studye^
And so it may well be known. yt this feyned light of knowing is not the
light of the true son / Therefore they that have this knowing on this manner
are full of ghostly pride and seen it not. they are so blind with this feyned
lite yt they hold the hines of her own^ heart and thu^buxo^nes to ye laws of
holy church as it were perfect mekenes to ye gospel and to ye laws of god /
and they wene that the following of her own will were freedom of spirit / and
therefore they begin to reyne as black clouds water of errors and heresies:
for the words that they shewe^ by prechynge sownen all to bacbitynge and to
stryuynge and to discord / making repreuynge of states and of persons / and
yet sayen they that all this is charity and zele of ryghtwysnes / But it is not
so the. for saint James thapostle says thus / Vbi enim zelus and co^tencio ibi
inconstancia and om^e opus prauu^ / Non est sapiencia hec desursu^ desce^dens a
patre luminu^. sed est trena ai^alis and diabolica / That is: where so envy
is and flitynge there is vnstablynes and all evil work / And therefore that
cu^nynge that brings forth such sins comyth not from the fader of light
that is god / but it is erthly beestly and fendly / And so by thise tokens that
are pride presu^pcyon vnbuxomnes Indignaco^n (...) bitynge and other such
sins for thise folowen after. may the feyned light be known fro the true /
For the true son shines and shows him not by special vysitaco^n for to
give light of understanding or perfyte charity to a soul but the fyrmament be
first made bryghte and clear fro clouds / that is* but if the conscience be
made clean through fire of brennyng desire to Ihesu in this derkenes the which
wastes and bren^eth all wicked stirynges of pride. vaynglory: ire envy: and
al other (...) in the soul as the prophet says / Ignis ante ip^m (...) et
infla^mabit incircuitu inimicos eius. Fire shall goo (...) him: That is desire
of love shall goo byfor^ Ihesu in (...) soul / and it shall bren^e all his
enmyes / that is: it shall waste all synes / For but if a soul be first smyten
down fro the heighte of itself by dread and mekenes. and be well examyned and
burnt in this fire of desire / and as it were purifyed fro all ghostly fylthe
by long time in devout prayers and other ghostly exercyses it is not able to
suffer the shinynges of ghostly light / ne for to receive the precious lycour
of perfyte love of Jesus / But when it is purifyed and made subtle thorugh this
fire then may it receive the gracyous light of ghostly knowing and the
perfeccyon of love that is true son / Thus says holy writ: Mal^ iiii
Vobis qui timetis deu^ vrietur sol iusticie / The true son of rightwysnes
that is our lord Ihesu shall spring to you that dreden him / that is to meke
souls that meken hemself under her euencrysten by knowing of her own
wretchydnesse / and casten hemself down under god by noughtynge of hemself in
her own substance thorugh reuerente dread and ghostly beholdynge of him
lastyngly / for that is perfyte mekenes / Unto thise souls the true son^e
shall spring. and Illumyn her reason in knowing of sothfastnes / and kyndleth
her affecco^n in brennynge of love and then shall they both brenne and shine
/ They shall thorugh virtue of this heavenly son brenne in perfyte love: and
shine in knowing of god and ghostly things / for then they ben reformed in
felyng / Therefore he that woll not be deceived I hope it is good to him to
draw down himself and hyde him in this derkenes / First from entermetynge
of other men as I have said / and forgete all the world if he may and follow
Ihesu with lasting desire offered in prayers and thinking on him / Then I
trow the light that comith after this derkenes is syker and sothfaste / and
that it shyneth of the cite of Ihrlm from the true son to a soul that
traueleth in derknes / and cries after light for to wyssyn it the waey. and
comfort it in traueyle. For I hope after true derkenes before comyth never
feyned light*

That is if a man truly and fully set him to forsake the love of the world
/ And may thorugh grace come to felyng and knowing of himself / And hold
him mekely in that feeling / he shall not be dysceyued with none errors ne
heresies / ne with fantasyes / For all these comen by the gate of pride /
Then if that pride may be stopped out / then there shall no such sin
rest in a soul / And though that they come and profer hem they shall not enter
/ For grace that the soul felyth in this meke derkenes shall teache the soul
sothe fastnes. and show to it yt al such proferynges are of the^mye /

How great profit is it to the soul to be brought through grace in to
lyhtsome derkenes / And how a man shall dispose him if he woll come thereto /
Caplm xxvii.
THere are many devout souls that through grace come in to this derkenes and
felen the knowing of hemself^ and yet wot they not fully what it is / and that
unknowing in party hyndreth hem / They feel well often her thought and her
affecco^n drawn out and departed fro the mind of erthly things and brought
in to great rest of a delectable softnes with out pinfull trowblynge of vain
thoughts or of her (...) wits / and they feel that time so great freedom of
spirit ^ they may think on Ihesu peasible / and offer her psalms ^ prayers
myghtily sauourly and swetly to him as long as (...) of bodily kind may
suffer it / They wot well that th^^ feeling is good / but they noot what it is
/ Therefore unto (...) such souls I say as me thinks: that this manner of
(...) though it be but short and but seldom it is sothfastly (...) derkenesse
that I speak of / For it is a feeling of hemself (...) and a rysynge above
hemself through bren^ynge desire to the ^^yghte of Ihu^ / Or else if I shall
say more sothly. this gri^^ous feeling is a ghostly syghte of Ihu^ / And if
they may keep hem in that rest or bring it through grace in to a custom so
that they might lightly and freely have it when hem like and hold hem in it /
they should never be overcome by te^ptacion of the fend ne of the flesh / ne
by errors ne heresies: for they are set in the gate of contemplacyon able
and ready for to receive the perfyte love of Ihesu / Therefore he that has it it
is good that he know it mekely / ^repe it tenderly / and poursew it fervently
that no crature let him utterly from it that he ne follow it when he may /
And that he forgete and set at naught all thing that should put him fro
this if he be free of himself / and may do what he woll without sclaunder or
disease of his euencrysten / For me thynkith that he may not come to this rest
lightly but if he have great ple^te of grace / and set himself for to follow
after the stirynge of grace / And that owes he for to do / For grace woll
ever be free / namely fro sin and worldly besynes. and from all other things
that letten the worchyng of it though they are no sin / Nevertheless a another
soul that has not yet received this fullness of grace if he desire for to
come to this gostly knowing of Ihesu / as much as in him is he must able
himself to it / and putt away all lettynges that stoppen grace as much as he
may / He must learn for to deye to ye world and forsake the love of it
truly / First pride bodily and ghostly / that he desire no worship / worldly
cu^nynge. ne worldly craft / benefyces ne richesse / precious clothing: ne
worldly array / ne no thing where through he should be worshypped above other
men / He shall coueyte none of all these / But if they ben putt upon him. take
hem with dread so that he be poor both outward and Inward / or else fully
Inward in heart / And that he coueyte for to be forgeten of the world that
men reward him no more be he never so rich ne so cunning than the poorest
man that lives /

Also that he suffers not his heart rest in beholding of his own deeds or in
his virtues / wenynge that he does better than a another / for he forsakyth the
world and other done not so / and therefore sets well by himself / Also he
must leave all rysyng of heart and evil will of ire and envy against his
euencristen / And that he disease no man ne anger him vnskylfully in word ne
in deed / ne give any man matere where thorugh he might skylfully be angered or
styred / so that he might be free fro every man / And also that he forsake
couetyse that he coueyte right naught of erthly good / but only ask his
bodily sustenaunce that him needs and hold him paid when god styreth other
men for to give him / And that he put no manner of trust in hauour of any
worldly good / ne in help or favor of any worldly friend but pryncypally and
fully in god / For if he do otherwise he byndeth himself to the world / And
he may not therefore be free for to think on Ihesu / And also glotenye and
lecherye and al other flesshly uncleanness utterly he must leave. that the
affecco^n be bound to no woman by flesshly homelynesse / For it is no dowte
that such blind love that is sometime atwyxe a man and a woman / and semyth
good and honest for asmoche as they would not sin in deed / in the syghte of
god is full unclean and well great sin / For it is a great sin that a man
shall suffer his affection that should be festened to Ihesu and to al virtues
and to al ghostly clennes for to be bound wi^h any flesshly love of any
creature wylfully namly if it (...) so much that it bears down the
thought: and makyth (...) vnrestful that he may no savor have in god / Thus
(...) it wylfully that a man does it and says it is sin (...) is so blinded
with it that he woll not see it / And also (...) a man coueyte not delices of
metes and drynkes only (...) of his flesh / but hold him paid with such
(...) may easily have without great besynes namly if (...) what mete it be
that woll do away hu^gre / and keep the (...) in common strength unto the
seruyse of god / And (...) grutche not ne strive not ne anger him not for his
mete th^ugh he be sometime not served as the flesh would / All these sins
and all other must be forsake utterly in his will and in deed when he may. And
other things that lets him so that he may dyspose him for to think freely
on Ihesu / For as long as these lettynges and such other hang upon him he
may not deye to the world: ne come in to this derkenesse of knowing of
himself / And therefore that he might come thereto he must do all these. as
saint poul did saying thus / Michi mu^dus crucifixus est and ego mu^do / This
world is slain and crucyfied to me: Gal. v:
and I to the world / That is: He yt has forsake the love of the world in
worshippes and riches in all other worldly things before said for the love of
god. and loves not it ne pursewyth not it but is well paid that he has right
naught of it ne would have though he might. sothly to him the world is deed /
for he has no savor ne delight therein / Also if the world set him at
naught and has no reward to him. ne favor ne worship: ne set no price by
him but forgeteth him as a deed man / then is he deed to the world / And in
this plyght was saint poul set perfitly. and so must a another man in party
that would follow and come to the perfect love of god / For he may not live to
god fully but if he deye first to the world / This deyenge to the world is
this derkenes / and it is the gate of contemplaco^n and to refourmyng in
felyng. and none other than this There may be many sundry ways and seere
works lettinge and ledyng sundry souls to contemplaco^n / For after diverse
disposynges of men and after sundry states. as are religyous and seculers that
they are in. are diverse exercises in worchyng / Nevertheless there is no gate
but one / For what exercises it be that a soul has. but if he may come by
that exercise to this knowing and to a meke feeling of himself / and that is
that he be mortifyed and deed to the world as in his love / and that he may
fe^le himself sometime in this restful derkenes / by the which he may be hid
fro vanytee of the world as in his love. and yt he may feel himself what he
is sothly he is not yet come to the refourmynge in feeling / ne has not fully
contemplaco^n He is full far therfro / and if he woll come by any gate. he is
but a theyf and a breker of the wall / And therefore as unworthy he shall be
cast out / But he that can bring himself first to naught through grace of
mekenes and deye on this manner he is in the gate / for he is deed to the
world. and he lives to god / Of the which saint poul spekith thus: Col. ^.
Mortui enim estis et vita vestra abscondita est cu^ xp^o in deo / ye are deed
/ That is: ye that for the love of god forsaken all the love of the world are
deed to the world with christ in god / That is: ye live ghostly in the love of
Ihesu / But your life is hid from worldly men as christ lives and is hid in
his godhede fro the love and the sight of flesshly lovers / This gate our
lord himself showed in the gospel when he said thus / Om^is qui reliquerit
patrem aut matrem fratrem aut sororem propter me centuplu^ accipiet et vitam
etnam possidebit Every man that forsakyth for my love fader or mother suster or
brother / ^
or any good erthly he shall have an hundredth fold in this life / and
afterward the bliss of heaven / This hundredth fold that a soul shall have if
he forsake the world is naught but the profit of this lightly derkenes / the
which I call the gate of contemplaco^n / For he that is in this derkenes and
is hid thorugh grace fro worldly vanytee he coueyteth naught of worldly good
/ he sechyth it not / he is not tarried therwyth / he lokyth not after it / he
loves it not / And therefore has he an hundredth fold more than the king or
than he has that coueyteth most of erthly good / For he that naught
coueyteth but Ihesu has an hundredth fold / For he has more rest: more pees
in heart / more very love and delight in soul in one day thanne he that most
coueyteth of the world / And has all the well of it under his welht has in
all his life time /

This is then a good derkenesse and a rich naught that brings a soul to
so much ghostly ease and so stylle softness / I trow da^yd meaned of this
night / or of this naught when he said thus / Ad nichilum redactus sum et
nesciui / That is: I was brought to naught. P*
and I wyste not / That is The grace of our lord Ihesu sent in to mine heart
has slay ne in me / and brought to naught all the love of the world and I
wyste not how / For through no worchynge of myself ne by mine own wit I have
it not but of the grace of our lord Ihesu / And therefore me thynkyth he that
woll have the light of grace and fulsomly feel the love of Ihu^ in his soul
he must forsake all the false light or worldly love and abide in this derkenes /
And nevertheless if he be adradde first for to won^e therein torn not again to
the love of ye world but suffer awhyle: and put all his hope and his trust in
Ihesu / and he shall not long be without some ghostly light / Thus byddeth
the prophet / Qui ambulat in tenebris et non est lumen ei. ^
speret in dn^o and inuitatur super deum suu^ / who so gooth in derkenes and
has no light. that is: who so woll hyde him fro the love of the world and
may not redily feel light of ghostly love dispeyre not / torn not again to the
world but hope in our lord and leen upon him / that is: trust in god / and
clean to him by desire. and abide awhyle and he shall have lyight ^ For it
falls thereby as it does if a man had be a great while in the son / and
after that came suddenly in to a derke house there no son shyneth. he should
be as he were blind. and see right naught / But if he woll abide awhyle he
shall mow see soon about him / First great things and sythen small / And
sythen all that ever is in the house /

Right so it is ghostly: He that forsakyth the love of the world and comyth
to himself in to his own co^scye^ce y^ is first derke somewhat / and blind to
his syghte: But if he stand stylle and hold forth with besye prayenge and
often thynkyng of the same will to the love of Ihu^ / he shall mow see
afterward great things and small that he first knew not / Thus semith it yt
the prophet behight thus saye^g / Oriet in tenebris lux tua. and tenebre tue
eru^t sicnt merid^es: et reqe^ dabit tibi dn^s ds tuus et implebit ai^am tua^
splendoribus / Light shall spring to th in derkenesse / That is: Thou that
forsakest sothfastly the light of all worldly love and hydest thy thought in
this derkenes / light of blessed love and ghostly knowing of god shall spring
to the / and thy derkenes shall be as myddaye / that is thy derkenes of
traueylynge desire and thy blind trust in god y^ thou have first shall torn
in to clear knowing and in to sykernes of love / And thy lord god shall give
rest to the / That is Thy flesshly desires and thy paynfull dredes and
doubts: and wicked spirytes that have contynuelly before hand traueyled the
all thise shall worche and lose much of her might / and thou shall be made so
strong that they shall not dear y^ / For thou shall be hid in rest fro hem
/ And then shall our lord fulfylle thy soul with shynynges / That is: when
thou art brought in to this ghostly rest then^e shall thou more easily tente
to god and naught else do but love him / and then he shall with bemes of
ghostly light fulfill all the myghtes of thy soul. Have thou no wonder
though I call the forsak^^ge of worldly love derkenes / for the prophet
calls it so ^^ynge thus to a soul / Intra in tenebras tuas filia caldeorum
/ Goo in to thy derkenesse thou daughter of caldee / That is ^ Thou soul that
art as a daughter of Caldee for love of the world. forsake it and goo in to
thy derkenes /

That in refourmynge of a soul the worchynge of on^^ lord Ihesu is departed
in to four times / that is. calling rightynge: magnyfyenge and gloryfyenge /
Caplm xxviii.
LOo I have said to the a lytyl if thou coueyte for to be reformed in felyng
how thou shall dyspose the toward in thy forth gooing / Nevertheless I say not
that thou may do thus of thyselfe / For I wot well that our lord Ihesu
bryngith all this to the end where so he woll / For he oonly thorugh his
grace styreth a soul. and bryngyth it in to this derkenesse first: And sythen
in to light as the prophet says / Sicut tenebre eius. ita and lumen eius /
That is: ^
Right as the light of knowing and the feeling of ghostly love is of Ihu^ /
Right so the derkenes. that is the forsakinge of worldly love is of him for he
does all / He fourmyth and refourmith He fourmyth only by hymself^ but he
refourmith us with us For grace yeuen and aplienge of our will to grace
worcheth all this / And on what manner wise he does that. saint poul reherceth
thus / Quos deus p^scinit fieri conformes ymaginis filii eius hos vocauit. Et
quos vocauit hos iustificauit. Et quos instificauit hos magnificauit. Et quos
magnificauit hos et glificauit / These that god knew before should be made
shapely to the image of his sone. thise he called. thise he righted. thise he
magnyfyed: and thise he gloryfyed / Though thise words may be said of all
chosen souls in the lowest degree of charity that are reformed only in faith:
nevertheless they may be vndstonde more specially of thise souls that are
reformed in feeling to the which our lord god shewith much plente of grace
and does much more besynes about hem / For they are his own sons specially
that bear the full shappe and the lickenes of his sone Ihu^ / In the which
words saint poule departs the worchyng of our lord in four times / First
is ye time of caliynge of a soul fro worldly vanyte / and that time is often
easy and comfortable / For in begyn^ynge of tornynge such a man that is
disposed to much grace is so quyckely and so felyngly inspired. and felith
often so great swetnes of deuoco^n. and has so many teres in co^puncco^n yt he
thynkyth him sometime as he were half in heaven / but this softnes passyth after
for a time / And then^e comyth the second time that is ye time of rightynge
that is trauelous / For when he begyn^yth for to goo forth mytly in the way of
rightwisnes. and settith his will full against all syn^e without and within^ and
stretchith out his desire to virtues and to the love of Ihu^ then^e felyth he
much lettynge both with himself of frowardenes and hardness of his own will
/ and fro without forth through temptaco^n of his enmye that he is often in full
great tourment / And that is no wond / For he has so long be crooked to the false love of the world that he may not be made right / as a crokyd staff may
not be made even but if he be cast and weyked in ye fire / Therefore our lord
Ihu^ seenge se^deth what thing is ^^ houefull to a froward soul suffers it
to be traueyled and ta^^ed by sundry te^ptacyons. and for to be well examyned
thorugh ghostly trybulacyons that all the ruste of vnclen^es might ^^ burnt
out of it / And that shall be both within of (...) dowtes and perplexitees
that it shall nerehande fall in disper^^ and it shall seem as it were forsaken
of god and left all in the hondes of the fend out taken a lityll preuy trust
that (...) have in the godenes of god and in his mercy. For that preuy (...)
our lord leueth in such a soul goo he never so fe^re (...) it. by the
which the soul is borne up fro dispeyre and saved (...) ghostly myscheyf. And
also without itself it shall be (...) fyed and pyned in the se^sualyte /
either by diverse syknes or (...) able tourment of the fend. or else through a
preuy might (...) god the sely soul by feeling and berynge of the wrerched
bo^y shall be so pyned. and it shall not wit how that it shall (...) suffer
for to be in the body ne were that our lord Ihu^ kep^ (...) therein / And yet
nevertheless had ye soul lever for to be in (...) this pyne than for to be
blinded with the false love of ye wo^^de. for that were hell to such a soul /
But the sufferynge (...) this manner pyne is naught but purgatory / and
therefore he suffryth it gladly / And he would not put it away though he
might / for it is so prouffytable / All this does our (...) in great
prouffyte of the soul / for to drive it our of the sensualytee / that it
might receive ghostly light / For after this when the soul is thus mortyfyed
and brought fro worldely love in to this derkenesse / that it has no more
savor ne delight of worldly liking thanne of the straw / But he thynkyth it
bitter as wormode / Then commyth the third time of magnyfieng / And that is
when the soul is reformed in feeling in party. and receives the yeft of
perfecco^n and the grace of contemplaco^n / and that is a time of great rest /
for then^e is Ihu^ more homely with a soul / And after this comyth the fourth
time of glorifyenge / That is when the soul shall be fully reformed in the
bliss of heaven / For these souls that are thus called fro syn^e and thus
righted or else on other manner like by diverse assayenge both thorugh fire and
water. and afterward are thus magnyfied they should be gloryfied / For our
lord shall then^e give he^ fully that they here coueyted / and more than they
cowde co^eyte / for he shall areyse hem above al other chosen souls to the
eue^hede of cherubyn and seraphyn / sythen they passed all other in knowing
and loving of god here in this life / Therefore he that woll come to this
magnifye^g dread not this rightyng / for that is ye way For our lord says by
his prophet a word of great comfort to all such souls that are examyned
with fire of trybulacy on thus / Puer meus noli timere. Si transieris per igne^
flamma non nocebit te / That is: My child if thou pass thorugh fire dread not
for the fla^me shall not dear the / It shall cleanse the fro all flesshly
fylthe / and make the able to receive ghostly fire of the love of god / and
that needs for to be done first For as I have before said. it may not else
be reformed in feeling /

How it falls sometime that souls begyn^ynge at profytynge in grace seem to
have more love as by outward tokens than some have that been perfyte / and yet
it is not so in soth within / Caplm xxix:
But now say thou how may this be sothe / For there are many souls new
turned to god that have many ghostly felynges / Some have great co^puncco^n
for her sins. and some have great deuoco^ns and feruours in her prayers. and
often have sundry techinges of ghostly lite in vndstonding: and some me^ have
other manner felynges of comfortable hete and great swetnes / and nevertheless
thise souls come never fully in this restfull derkenes that I speak of with
fervent desire and lastyng love and thought in god / Then^e ask thou whether
thise souls be reformed in feeling or naught / It semyth yes. in asmoche as
they have such great ghostly felynges that other men that stand oonly in
faith feel not of / Unto this I may say as me thynkith. that thise ghostly
felynges whether they stand in compu^ccion or deuoco^n or in ghostly
ymaginacyon are not the felynges which a soul shall have and feel in ye grace
of conte^placo^n / I say not but they are sothfast and gracyously yeue^ of god
/ But these souls that felen such are not yet reformed in feeling. ne they
have not yet the yefte of perfecco^n ne ghostly the bren^inge love of Ihu^ as
they may come to / And nevertheless often it semyth otherwise: that such
souls feel more of the love of god than other that have the yefte of
perfecco^n / in asmoche as the felyng shewyth more outward by great fervor of
bodily tokens. in weeping prayenge kne^^^ge and speaking and other bodily
stirynge. so ferforth yt it semyth to a another man that they were ever
rauysshed in love / And though me thynkith it is not so / well I wot that
thise manner felinges and feruours of deuoco^n and co^puncco^n that thise me^
feel are gracious yeftes of god sent in to chosen souls for to draw hem out
of worldly love and flesshly lust that has been long time roted in her heart.
fro ye which love they should not be drawn out but by such feable stirige of
great feruours: ne^ theles yt the fervor is somoche in outward showing it is
not only for mochenes of love yt they have but it is for litylnes and weyknes
of her soul yt may not ber^ a lityl towching of god for it is yet as it were
fleshly festned to ye flessh^ and neu was yet deperted fro it by gostly
mortifye^g: and therefore ye lest towching of love and ye lest sperkil of
ghostly lyte sent fro heaven in to such a soul is somoche and so comfortable
and so delectable over al ye liki^g that ever it felt before in flesshly love
of erthly thing that it is overtaken with it / And also it is so new and
sodeyn and so uncouth that it may not suffer for to bear it but brestyth and
shewyth out in weeping sobbing and other bodily stirynge Right as the
costrell that is old when it receives new wine that is fresshe and mighty:
the costrell bolneth out and is in point for to cleue and breast until the
wine has boylled and spourged out all vnclen^esse / but also sone as the wine
is fined and cleryd then^e it stondeth still and the costrel hole / Right so a
soul that is old through syn^e when it receives a lityll of the love of god
that is so fresshe and so mighty that the body is in point for to cleue and
to break ne were that god kepith it hole But yet it brestyth out at the eyes
by weeping / and at ye mouth by speaking: and that is more for weyknes and
feebleness of the soul than for mykilnes of love / For afterward when love has
boylled all the vnclen^es out of the soul by such great feruours then^e is
the love clear and stondeth still: And then^e is both the body and the soul
much more in pees / and yet has ye soul much more love than it had before
though it show less outward / For it is now all hole in rest within: and
naught but lityll in outward showing of fervor / And therefore I say that
thise souls that fele^ such great bodily feruours though they ben in much
grace are not yet reformed in feeling / but they are greatly dysposed toward.
For I trow yt such a man namly that has be greatly defoylled in syn^e shall
not be reformed in feeling but if he be first burnt and puryfyed with such
great co^puncco^ns going before /

A another soul that never was much defoylled with love of the world but has
ever be kept fro great sin^es in innoce^ce may lyghtlyer and more pryuely
without great fervor showed outward come to this refourmyng / Then^e is this
soth as I hope that such comfortes and feruours that a soul felyth in the
state of begyn^ynge or of profytynge are as it were his ghostly food sent fro
heaven for to strength him in his traueyle / Right as a pilgryme traueyleth all
day meteles and drynkles^ and is nerehonde overcome with werynes falls at
the last to a good Inn. and there has he mete and drink / and is well
refresshed for the time / Right so ghostly: a devout soul that woll forsake
the love of the worlde^ and would feign love god / and settyth all his besynes
thereto: prays and traueylleth all day bodyly and ghostly / and sometime
feleth no comfort ne savor in deuocon / Then^e our lord having pity over
all his creatures that it should not perisshe for defawte ne torn in to
heaviness or grutchyng sends it among his ghostly fode and comfort it in
deuoco^n as he wouchith saaf / And when the soul feleth any comfort then^e
holds he him well paid for all his traueylle and all the disease that it had
on y^ day when it fares well at even by feeling of any grace / The self wise
falls it of other souls that are profitynge and ferfor the in grace They
felen often times gracyous towchynges of the holy ghost in her soul / both in
understanding and syghte of ghostly things and in affeccion of love / But yet
ben they not reformed in felyng / ne they are not yet perfyte / for why all
such felinges come to hem in that state as it were vnw^arly / for they come or
they wit it / and goth fro hem or they wit it / and they can not come thereto
again. ne wot not where they shall find it for they have not yet homlynes with
he^ of thought and lastyng desire in Ihu^ / ne the eye of her soul is not
opyned to the beholdynge of ghostly thynges^ but they nyghe fast toward. And
therefore they are not yet reformed in feeling / ne they have not yet the full
yefte of conte^placo^n /

On what manner a man shall have knowing of his own soul / and how a man
should set his love in Ihu^ god and man one person / Caplm xxx.
IT needs a soul that would have knowing of ghostly things for to have
first knowing of itself / For it may not have knowing of a kind above
itself but if it have knowing of itself / And that is when the soul is so
gadred in to itself / and departed fro beholding of al erthly things and fro
the use of bodily wits that it felyth itself as it is in y^ own kind
without a body / Then^e if thou coueyte for to know and see thy soul what it
is^ thou shall not torn thy thought with ymagynaco^n in to thy body for to
seek it and feel it as it were hid within thyn heart. as thy heart is hid
and holden within thy body / If thou seek so thou shall never find it in
itself / The more thou secheste for to find and feel it as y^ would feel a
bodily thing. the ferd thou art therfro / For thy soul is no body but a life
vnseable. not hid and holde^ with in thy body as a less thing is hid and
holden within a more but it is holding and quknyng thy body much more than
thy body is in might and in virtue / Then if thou wolt find it wythdraw thy
thought fro all bodily thing outward and fro mind of thyn own body. also
fro all thy five wits asmoche as thou may. and think on the kind of a
reasonable soul ghostly as thou would think for to know any virtue as
sothfastnes or mekenes or any other wertue / Right so think that a soul is a
life vndedely and vnseably / and has might in itself for to see and know
the souereyn sothfastnes^ and for to love the souereyne goodness that is god /
when thou see this then felest thou somewhat of thyself / Seek thyself in
none other place / but the more fully and the more clerly that you may think
of ye kind and the worthynes of a reasonable soul what it is. and what is the
kyndly werking of it the better see you thiselfe / It is full hard for a soul
that is rude and much in the flessh^ for to have sight and knowing of it or of
an angel or of god It falls anon in to ymagynaco^n of bodily shappe^ and it
weneth thereby for to have the sight of it self. and so of god and so of
ghostly things / And that may not be / For all ghostly things are seen and
known by understanding of the soul not by ymagynacyon / Right as a soul
sees by vndstondyng that the virtue of rightwysnes is for to give to every
thing that it owes to have / right so and on such a manner may the soul
see itself by understanding / Nevertheless I say not that thy soul shall rest
stylle in this knowinge / but it shall by this seek hyer knowing above itself
and that is the kind of god / For the soul is but a myrrour in the which you
shall see god ghostly / And therefore thou shall first find thy myrrour and
keep it bryghte and clean fro flesshly fylthe and worldly vanytee / and hold
it well up fro the earth that thou myt see it and our lord therein also / For to
this end traueylen all chosen souls in this life in her meaning and in her
intent. though they have not specially the feeling of this. And therefore it is
said before that many souls begin^yng and profityng have many great feruours
and much sweet deuocio^ and as it semith bre^nynge all in love. and yet have
they not perfytly love ne ghostly knowing of god / For wit thou well feel a
soul never so much fervor / somoche that him thikith that the body may not
bear it. or though he melte all in to weeping. aslonge as his thynkyng and his
beholding of god is most. or all in ymagynaco^n and not in vndstondyng. he
come not yet to perfyte love ne to conte^placion / For thou shall understood
that the lou^ of god is on three manner wise / Al are good. but echone is be^ter
than other / The first comyth only thruh^ faith without gracyous ymagynaco^n
or ghostly knowing of god / Thi^ love is in the leest soul that is reformed
in faith in the lo^^est degree of charity / And it is good: for it suffices to
salvation / The second love is that a soul felyth through faith and
ymagynaco^n of Ihu^ in his manhede. This love is better than the first when
the ymaginacyon is styred by grace? for why the ghostly eye is opened in
beholdinge of our lords manhede / The third love that the soul feleth through
ghostly sight of the godhede in the manhede as it may be seen here / that is
best and most worthy / and that is perfyte loue^ this love a soul felyth
not unto it be reformed in feeling / Souls begyn^ynge and profityng has not
this love. for they can not think on Ihu^ ne love him goodly but as it were al
manly and flesshly after the conditions and lyknes of man / and upon that
reward they shape all her worchynge in her thoughts and in her affecco^ns /
They dread him as a man and worship him and love him pryncypally in manly
ymagynaco^n and goo no ferder / As thus: If they have done amysse and
trespased against god they think then^e that god is wroth with hem as a man
should if they had trespassed against him / and therefore they fall down as it
were to the fete of our lord with sorrow of heart and cryen mercy / And when
they done thus they have a good trust that our lord of his mercy woll foryeue
hem her trespass / This manner of doing is right good / but it is not ghostly
as it might be / Also when they woll worship god they present hem in her
thought as they were before our lords face in a bodily lyckenes. and ymagyn a
wondfull lyh^yte there our lord Ihu^ is / and then they reverence him and
worship him and dread him / and fully put hem in his mercy for to do with hem
what he woll / Also wha^ they woll love god they behold him worship him and
dread him as a man. not yet as god in man either in his passion or in some
other thing of his manhede and in that beholdynge they feel her hertes much
stired to ye love of god / This manner of worchynge is good and gracyous / but
it is much less and lower than is the worching of understanding / That is
when the soul gracyously beholds god in man / For in our lord Ihesu are
two kinds. the manhede. and the godhede / Then right as the godhede is more
souereyne and more worthy thanne is the manhede / Rygh so the ghostly
beholdynge of the godhede in Ihesu man is more worthyer. and more ghostlyer.
and more medefull thanne beholdynge of the manhede alone / whether he behold
the manhede as dedly or as glorified / And right so by the same skyll the love
that a soul felyth in thinkyng and beholdynge of the godhede in man when it is
gracyously showed is worthyer ghostlyer and more medefull than the fervor o^
deuoco^n that the soul feleth by ymagynaco^n only of the ma^hede show it
never somoche outward / For in reward o^ y^ this is but ma^ly / for our lord
shows him not in ymagynaco^n as he is. ne that he is / for the soul might
not that time for freelte of the flesshede suffer it so / Nevertheless unto
such souls that can not think of the godhede ghostly that they should not
err in her deuoco^n^ but that they should be comforted and strengthed through
some manner Inward beholdynge of Ihu^ for to forsake syn^e and the love of the
world. therefore our lord Ihu^ tempreth his vnseable light of his godhede
and cl^theth it under bodile liknes of his manhede. and shewith it unto the
Inner eye of a soul. and fedeth it with the love of his precious flesh
ghostly / The which love is of so great might that it sleeth al wicked love
in the soul and strength it for to suffer bodily penance and other bodily
disease in time of ne^^ for love of Ihesu / And this is the shadowyng of our
lord Jesus over a chosen soul. in the which shadowyng the soul i^ kept fro
bren^ynge of worldly love / For right as a shadow is made of a light and of a
body: right so this ghostly shadow is made of the blessed vnseable light of
the godhede and of the manhede ooned thereto showed to a deuowte soul / of the
which shadow the prophet says thus / Sp^sante facie^ nostra^ xp^s dn^s sub
vmbra eius viuemus int gentes / Our lord christ before our face as a spirit
under his shadow we shall live a mo^ge folk / That is our lord Ihu^ in his
godhede is a spyryte that may not be seen of us living in flesh as he is in
his blessed light / therefore we shall live under the shadow of his manhede as
long as we are here / But though this be sooth that this love in ymaginacyon
be good / Nevertheless a soul should desire for to have ghostly love in
understanding of the godhede. for that is the end and the full bliss of the
soul / and all bodily beholdynges are but means ledynge a soul to it / I say
not that we should refuse the manhede of Ihu^ and depart god fro man. but thou
shall in Ihu^ man behold dread. wonder. and love ghostly the godhede / And so
shall you without de partynge love god in man^ and both god and man ghostly
and not flesshly / Thus taught our lord mary mawdeleyne that should be
contemplatyfe. Joh^. x.
when he said thus / Noli me tangere non du^ enim ascendi ad patrem meu^ /
Towche me not I am not yet styed up to my fader / That is to say: Mary
magdalene loved well our lord Ihu^ before the time of his passion / but her
love was much bodily and lityl ghostly / She trowed well that he was god but
she loved him lityll as god / for she kouth not then^e / and therefore she
suffered al her affecco^n and al her thought fall in him as he was in form of
man / And our lord blamed her not then^e but praised it much / But after when
he was risen fro death and appeared to her she would have worshypped him with
such manner love as she did before / and then^e our lord forbode her and said
thus / Towche me not: That is. Set not thy rest ne the love of thyn heart in
that form of man that thou see with thy flesshly eye only for to rest
therein: For in that form I am not stied up to my fader. That is I am not even
to the fader: for in that form of man I am less than he: Towche me not so.
but set thy thought and thy love in that form in which I am even to the
fader / that is the form of the godhede / and love me: know me. and worship
me as god and man godly / not as a man ma^ly / So shall thou touch me / For
sythen I am both god and man. and all the cause why I shall be loved and
worshipped is for I am god / and for I took the kind of man / And therefore
make me a god in thine heart and in thine love / And worship me in thine
understanding as Ihesu god and man: souereyne sothfastnes and souereyne
godenes and blessed life for that I am / And thus taught our lord her as I
understand and also all other souls that are disposed to conte^placion and
able thereto that they should do so / Nevertheless other souls that are not
subtle in kind. ne are not yet made ghostly through grace it is good to hem
that they keep forth her own worchynge in ymagynaco^n with manly affecco^n
unto more grace come freely to hem / It is not syker to a man to leave one good
thing utterly till he see and feel a better / Upon the self wise it may be
said of other manner felynges that are like to bodily / as herynge of delectable
song / or feeling of comfortable hete in the body: seenge of light. or
swetnes of bodily savor / Thise are not ghostly felynges. for ghostly felynges
are felt in the myghtes of the soul / pryncipally in understanding and love.
and lityll in ymagynaco^n / But thise felynges are felt in the myghtes of the
body in ymaginaco^n / and therefore they are not ghostly felynges / But wha^
they are best and most true. yet are they but outward tokens of the July
grace that is felt in the myghtes of the soul / This may be openly preued by
holy wrytt saying thus / Apparueru^t aplis dispertite (...) taqm^ ignis.
seditque supra singlos eorum sp^s scu^s / The ho^ly ghost appeared to thapostles
in the day of pentecost in y^ li^kenes of bren^ynge tongues and enfla^med her
hertes. and set upon each of hem / Now soth it is ye holy ghost that is god
in himself vnseable was not that fire ne the tongues that were seen. ne that
bren^ing that was felt bodily. but he was vnseable felt in the myghtes of her
souls / for he lyghtned her reason / and kyndeled her affecco^n through his
blessed precense so clere^i and so bren^yngly that they had suddenly the
ghostly knowing of sothfastnes and the perfecco^n of love as our lord behyght
he^ saying thus / Sp^s scu^s docebit vos oe^m veritate^ / That is. Io^.
ye holy ghost shall teache you al sothfastnes / then^e was ye fire and yt
bren^yg naught else but a bodily token outward showed in wytnessynge of that
grace that was Inwardly felt / And as it was in hem / so is it in other
souls that are vysited and lyghtned within of the holy ghost. and has with
that such outward feeling in comfort and wytnessyng of the grace in ward /
But that grace is not as I hope in all souls that are perfyte but there our
lord woll / Other Inperfyte souls that have such felynges outward and have
not yet received Inward grace it is not good to hem to rest in such felinges
outward / but in as much as they help the soul to more loue^ and to more
stablynesse of thought in god / For some may be true and some may be feyned
as I have said before /

How this manner of speaking of refourmynge in feeling of a soul shall be take
And on what wise it is reformed and how it is found in saint poules words /
Caplm xxxi.
NOw I have said to the a lityll of refourmynge in faith. and also I have
towched to the a lityll of the forth-goynge fro that refourmyng to the higher
refourmyng that is in feeling. Not in that intent that I would by thise words
set goddis worchynge vnd a law of my spekinge. As for to say thus worcheth
god in a soul and none other wise / Nay I mean not so. But I say after my
simple felinge that our lord worcheth thus in some creatures as I hope / And
I hope well that he worcheth other wise also that passyth my wit and my
feeling / Nevertheless whether he worche thus or other wise by sundry means in
longer time or shorter time / with much traueyle or lityll traueyle / if all
come to one end. that is to the perfect love of him / then^e it is good enough
/ For if he wolle give one soul on one day the full grace of contemplaco^n
and without any traueyle as he well may / as good is y^ to that soul as if he
had be examyned pynyd mortifyed and purifyed twenty winter / And therefore upon
this manner wise take in my saying as I have said. and namly as I think to
say / For now by the grace of our lord Ihesu shall I speak a lityll as me
thinks more openly of refourmyng in felyng what it is and how it is made. and
which are ghostly felynges that a soul receives / Nevertheless first that I
take not this manner of speaking of refourmyng of a soul in feeling as feynyng
or fantasye / therefore I shall ground it in saint poullis words where he
says thus / Nolite co^formari huic sclosed reformamini in nouitate sensus
vestri / That is: ye that are through grace reformed in faith conform you not
hensforwarde to the manners of the world in pride in couetyse and in other
sins. but be ye reformed in newehede of feeling / Loo here thou may see
that saint poul spekyth of refourmynge in feeling / And what that new feeling
is. he expowneth in a another place thus / Vt impleamini in agnicio^e volu^tatis
eius in om^i intellectu et sapi^a spu^ali / That is: we pray god that ye may
be fulfilled in knowinge of goddis will in all vndstondynge and in all manner
ghostly wysdom / This is refourmynge in feeling / For thou shall understand
that the soul has ii. manner of felinges One without of ye five bodili wits.
a another within of ye ghostly wits the which are properly the myghtes of the
soul / Mind reason and will / when these myghtes are through grace fulfilled
in all understanding of the will of god and ghostly wysdom then^e has the
soul new gracyous felynges / That this is soth he shows in a another place
thus / Renouamini sp^u mentis vestre et induite nouu^ hoi^em q scdm deu^
creatus est in iusticia: sci^tate and vitate Be ye renewed in spirit of your
soul / That is: ye shall be reformed not in bodily feeling ne in ymaginacion
but in the over party of your reason / And clothe you in a new man yt is
shapen after god in rightwysnes holiness and sothfastnesse That is: your
reason yt is properli the image of god through grace of the holy ghost shall be
clothed in a new light of sothfastnesse / holiness. and ryghtwysnes / And
then it is reformed in feeling / For when the soul has perfyte knowing of
god then it is reformed / Thus says saint poul / Expoliantes vetere^
homine^ cu^ actibus suis induite nouu^ qui re nouatur in agnico^ne dei scdm
ymagine^ eius qui creauit eum / Spoil yourself of the old man with all his
deeds That is cast fro you the love of the world with all worldly manners And
clothe you in a new man: Col. 3.
That is: ye shall be renewed in the knowing of god after the lycknes of him
that made you / By these words thou may vndstonde that saint poul would have
men^es souls reformed in perfyte knowing of god. for that is the new feeling
that he spekyth of generally And therefore upon his words I shall say more
openly of this reformyng as god yeueth me grace / For there is two manner
knowing of god / One is had pryncipally in ymagynacyon. and lityll in
vndstondyng / This knowinge is in chosen souls begyn^yng and prouffitynge in
grace that known god. and louen him all manly. not ghostly with manly
affecco^ns and with bodily lyknes as I have before said / This knowing is
good. and it is lykned to milk by the which they are tendly nouryshed as
childn until they ben able for to come to the faders board and take of his
hand hole bread. A another knowing is pryncypally feled in understanding and
lityll in ymagynaco^n / For the understanding is lady and the ymagynaco^n is a
maiden serving to the vndstondyng when need is / ^rnowyng is hole bread mete
for perfyte souls / and it is refourmynge in feeling /

How god opens the In^er eye of the soul to see him not all at ones but by
diverse times / And of three manner of refourmyng of a soul by ensample / Caplm
xxxii.
A Soul that is called fro the love of world and after that is righted and
assayed. mortifyed and purifyed as I have before said: our lord Ihesu of his
merciful goodness refourmyth it in feeling when he wouchyth saaf / He opens
the Inner eye of the soul when he lyghtneth the reason through towchynge and
shinynge of his blessed light for to see him and know him. not all fully
attones / but lityll and lityll by diverse times as the soul may suffer him /
He sees him not what he is. for that may no creature do in heaven ne in
earth / Nor he sees him not as he is / for that sight is only in y^ bliss of
heaven / But he sees him. that he is an vnchanble being: a souereyne might:
souereyne sothfastnes: souereyne goodness: a blessed life: an endless bliss /
This sees the soul and much more that comyth with al not blyndly and nakydly
and vnsauourly as does a clerk that sees him by his clergy only through
might of his naked reason / but he sees him in understanding that is
comforted and lyghted by the yefte of ye holy ghost with a wonderful
reverence and a preuy bren^nyng love. and with ghostly savor and heavenly
delight more clerly and more fully than it may be written or said / This syghte
though it be but shortly and lityll is so worthy and so mighty that it
draws and rauyssheth all the affecco^n of the soul fro beholding and the
mind of all erthly thing thereto for to rest therein evermore if it might /
And of this manner of syghte and knowing the soul groundeth all his worchynge
inward in all the affecco^ns / For then it dredeth god in man as
sothfastnesse wondreth him as might / loves him as goodness / This ^^ighte and
this goodness and this knowing of Ihesu with y^ blessed love that comyth out of
it. may be called refourmyng of a soul in feeling. and in faith that I speak
of.

It is in faith / For it is derke yet as in reward of that full knowing of
Ihesu with the blessed love that comyth out of it that shall be in heaven / For
then shall we see him not oonly that he is. but as he is / As saint Ioh^n
says / p^. ^^.iiii
Tunc videbimus eum sicut est / That is: Then shall we see him as he is /
Nevertheless it is in feeling also as in reward of that blind knowing that a
soul has stondynge oonly in faith / For this soul knowyth somewhat of the
very kind of Ihesu god through his gracyous syghte / but that other knowyth
not. but oonly trowith it is soth / Nevertheless that thou ye better may
conceive what I mean I shall show these three manner refourmynge of a soul by
ensample of three men sto^dyng in the light of the son^e / Of the which three
one is blynde^ a another may see but he has his eyes stopped / the third
lokyth forth full syghte / The blind man has no manner knowing that he is in
the son^e / but he trowyth it if a true man tell him / And he betokens a
soul that is only reformed in faith yt trowyth in god as holy church
techeth and wot not what / This suffyceth as for salvation / That other man
sees a light of the son^e^ but he sees it not clerly what it is for the lydde
of is eye lets him that he may not see / But he sees through the lydde of
his eye a glymerynge of great light And he betokenyth a soul that is
reformed in faith and in felyng: and so is he conte^platyfe / for he sees
somewhat of the godhede of Ihu^ through grace / Not clerly ne fully. for the
lydde that is his bodily kind is yet a wall bytwixe his kind and ye kind of
Ihu^ god and lettyth him fro the clear syghte / But he sees through this wall
after that grace towchyth him more or less that Ihu^ is god. and that Ihu^ is
souereyne goodness and souereyne being. and a blessed life / and all that other
goodness comyth of him / Thus sees the soul by grace notayensto^dyng the
bodily kind. and the more clean and subtle that the soul is made. and the
more it is departed fro flesshlyhede the sharper sight it has and the
myghtyer love of ye godhede of Ihu^ / This syghte is so mighty that though
none other man living would trow in Ihu^ ne love him he would never trow ye
less ne love him the less: for he sees it sothfastly that he may not vntrowe
it / The third man yt has full syghte of the son^e he trowyth it not / for he
sees it fully / And he betokens a full blessid soul that without any wall
of body or of syn^e sees openly the face of Ihu^ in the bliss of heaven /
There is no faith / and therefore he is fully reformed in felyng / There is no
state above the second refourmynge that a soul may come to here in this life.
for this is the state of perfeccyon and the way to heue^warde. Nevertheless all the souls that are in this state are not all like ferforth. For some has it
lityll shortly and seildom. and some le^ger clerer and oftiner: and some has
it best clerest and lengest after the abou^dinge of grace / and yet all these
have the yefte of conte^placo^n / For the soul has not perfyte sight of Ihu^
all at ones / but first a lityll and a little / and after that it profyteth
and comyth to more feeling / And aslonge as it is in this life it may wax
more in knowing and in this love of Jesus / and sothly I wot not what were more
leyf to such a soul that has felt a lytill of it than utterly all other
things left and set at naught. Tent only thereto for to have clerer sight
and clenner love of Ihu^ in whom is all the blessed trynyte. This manner knowing
of Ihu^ as I vndstonde is the openinge of heaven to the eye of a clean soul of
the which holy me^ speak of in her writing / Not as some wene that the
opening of heaven is as if a soul might see by ymagynaco^n thru^ the skies
above the fyrmament how our lord Ihu^ sytteth in his mageste in a bodily
light as much as an hundredth son^es Nay it is not so. ne though he see
never so high on y^ manner sothly he sees not the ghostly heaven / The higher
he styeth above the son^e for to see Ihu^ god so by such ymagynaco^n. the
lower he falls bineth the son^e. Nevertheless this manner syghte is sufferable
to simple souls that can no better seche him that is vnseable /

How Ihu^ is heaven to the soul. and why he is called fire / Caplm xxxiii.
WHat is heaven to a reasonable soul / Sothly noughteelles but Ihesu god / For
if that be heaven oonly that is above al thing / then^e is god only heaven
toman^es soul for he is only above ye kind of a soul / then^e if a soul
may thorugh grace have knowing of that blessed kind of Ihu^* sothly he sees
heaven for he sees god / Therefore there are many men that erren in vndstondynge
of some words that are said of god / for they understand hem not ghostly /
Holy writing says that a soul that wol find god shall lift upward the
Inner eye and seek god above itself / Then some men that would do after
this saying understand this word above hemself as for higher setting instead and worthynes of place as one elemente or planete is above a another in
setting and worthiness of a bodily place / But it is not so ghostly. For a
soul is above all bodily thing: not by setting of stead: but by subtyltee
and worthynes of kind / Right so on the self wise god is above all bodily
and ghostly creatures not by setting of stead but through subtyltee and
worthynes of his unchangeable blessed kind And therefore he yt wol wisely seche
god and find him he shall not ren^e out with his thought as he would clyme
above the son^e and part the fyrmament and ymagin ye mageste as it were of an
hundred sons / he shall rather draw down the son and all the fyrmament
and forgete it. and cast it beneth him there he is. and set all this and all
bodily thing also at naught / and think then^e if he can ghostly both of
himself and of god also / And if he do thus: then^e sees the soul above
itself / then^e sees it in to heaven. Upon this self manner shall this word
within be understand / It is comynly said that a soul shall see our lord
within all thing and within itself / Soth it is that our lord is within al
creatures. but not on that manner that a kernel is hyd within the shell of a
nutte. or as a lityll bodily thing is holden within a another much / but he is
within all creatures as holding and keeping hem in her being through subtylte
and might of his own blessed kind and clennes vnseable / For right as a
thing that is most precious and most clean is laid inerest / right so by
that lyknes it is said that the kind of god that is most precious most clean
and most goodly ferrest fro bodilyhede is hid within all things / And
therefore he that woll seek god within he shall gorgete first all bodily things
for all that is without. and his own body / and he shall forgete thynkyng of
his own soul. and think on the unmade kind. that is Ihu^ that made him:
quiknith him. holdith him. and yeueth him reason and mind and love the which
is within him through his might and souereyne subtylte / Upon this manner shall
the soul do when grace to wchyth it. or else it woll but lityl avail to
seche Ihesu. and to find him within itself and within all creatures as me
thynkyth / Also it is said in holy writ that god is light / So says saint
Ioh^n. Deus lux est / That is. God is light / This light shall not be
understand as for bodily light but it is understood thus / God is light.
That is. God is troth and sothfastnesse / for sothfastnes is ghostly light /
Then^e he that most gracyously knowyth sothfastnes best sees god / And
nevertheless it is lykened to the bodily light for this skylle / Right as the
son shows to the bodily eye itself and all bodily thing by it / right so
sothfastnes that is god shows to the reason of the soul itself first. and
by itself all other ghostly thing that needs to the knowing of a soul /
Thus says the prophet / Dn^e in lumine tuo videbimus lumen / Lord we shall
see thy light by thy light / That is: we shall see the tha^ art sothfastnes by
thyselfe / On the self wise it is said that god is fire / Deus noster ignis
consumens est: That is (...) lord is fire wasting / That is for to say: God
is not fire elementare that heteth a body and bren^eth it / but god is love and
charity / For as fire wastes all bodily thing that may be wasted / Right so
the love of god brenneth and wastes all sin out of the soul. And makyth it
clean as fire makyth clean all manner metalle / These words and all other
that arne spoken of our lord in holy writ by bodyly lyckenesse must needs
be understand ghostly: Else there is no ^a^our in hem / Nevertheless the
cause why such manner words are said of our lord in holy writ is this /
For we are so flesshly that we can not speak of god ne understand of him but
if we by such words first be entered in / Nevertheless when the Inner eye is
opened through grace for to have a lityll sight of Ihu^ / then^e shall the soul
torn lightly enough all such words of bodily things in to ghostly
understanding / This goostly opening of the Inner eye in to knowing of the
godhede I call refourmynge in faith and feeling / for then^e the soul somewhat
feleth in understanding of that thing that it had before in naked trowynge.
and that is the begyn^ynge of contemplaco^n / of the which saint poul says
thus / Non conte^plantibus nobis que vident sed que no^ videntur Quia que
videntur te^poralia su^t. S. cor iiii*
que aute^ non videntur etna sunt / That is: Our contemplaco^n is not in
things that are seen. but it is in things vnseable / For things that are
see^ are passing. but vnseable things are everlasting / to the which syghte
every soul should desire for to come to both here in party and in the bliss
