of heaven fully / For in that sight and in that knowing of Ihu^ is fully the
bliss of a reasonable soul and endless life Thus says our lord / Hec est aute^
vita eterna vt cognosca^tte verum deu^ et quem misisti ih^m xp^m / (...). vii.
That is: Fader this is endless life that thy chosen souls know the and thy
sone whom thou haste sent one sothfaste god /

Of two manner of love reformed and vnfourmed what it meanyth / And how we be
behold to love Ihu^ much for our making / but more for our again byenge /
but all thermooste for our saving through the yeftes of his love / caplm xxxiiii.
But now wondrest thou sythen this knoweng of god is the bliss and the end of
a soul? why then have I said here before that a soul should not else
coueyte but oonly the love of god / I spoke no thing of this sight that a
soul should coueyte this / Unto this may I say thus / that the sight of
Ihesu is full bliss of a soul: and that is oonly for the sight but it is also
for the blessed love that comyth out of that syghte / Nevertheless for love
comyth out of knowing and not knowing out of love / therefore it is said that
in knowing and in syghte pryncypally of god with love is y^ bliss of a soul
and the more he is known the better he is loved / But for asmoche as to this
knowing or to this love that comyth of it. may not the soul come without love
/ therefore said I that you sholdest coueyte love / for love is cause why a soul
comyth to this knowing and to this love that comyth of it / And o^ what manner
that is I shall tell the more openly / Holy writers saye^ and soth it is that
there is two manner of ghostly ^^ue / One is called fourmed. a another is called
vnfourmed / Love unformed is god himself the third person in the ^^^nyte.
that is the holy ghost / He is love vnfourmed and (...) as saint Ioh^n says /
Deus dilecco^ est / God is love: (...) is the holy ghost / Love fourmed is the
affection of the (...) made by the holy ghost of the syghte and of the knowing
(...) sothfastnes that is god. oonly styred and set in him / (...) love is
called fourmed for it is made by the holy ghost / (...) love is not god in
himself for it is made. but it is the love (...) the soul felt of the syghte
of Ihesu and stired to him (...) Now may you see that love formed is not cause
why a (...) comyth to the ghostly syghte of Ihesu / And some men (...) think
that they would love god so brennyngly as it (...) by their own mighte^ that
they were worthy for to have the ghostly knowing of him / Nay it is not so.
But love (...) fourmed that is god himself is cause of all this knowing / For
a blind wretched soul is so far fro the clear knowing and the blessed
feeling of his love thorugh sin and freelte of the bodily kind that it
might never come to it. ne were it the endless mochenes of the love of god /
But then by cause he loves us so much therefore he yeueth us his love that
is the holy ghost / He is the yeuer and the yeft. and makes us then by that
yefte for to know and love him / ^o this is the love that I spoke of that thou
sholdest only coueyte and desire this vnfourmed love that is the holy ghost /
For sothly a less thing or a less yefte than he is may not avail us for to
bring us to the blessed sight of Ihu^ / And therefore should we fully desire
and ask of Ihu^ only this yefte of love that he would for the mochenes of his
love so blessed towche our hertes with his vnseable light to the knowing of
him and depart with us of his love that as he loves us that we might love
him again / Thus says saint Ioh^n / ^os diligamus deu^ qm^ ip^e prior delixit
nos / That is: p^. John.
Love we god now for he first loved us / He loved us much when he made us to
his liknes* but he loved us more when he boute us with his precious blood
through wylful taking of death in his ma^hede fro the power of the fend and
fro the pyne of hell. but he loves us most when he yeueth us the yefte of
the holy ghost that is loue^ by the which we know him and love him. and are
made syker that we are his sons chosen to salvation / For this love are we
more to him bound than for any other love that ever showed he for us. either
in our making or in our aye^byenge / For though he had made us and boughte us:
but if he save us with all? what profyteth it else to us our making or our
byenge / Sothly right naught / Therefore the most token of love showed to us
as me thinks is this / That he yeueth himself in his godhede to our souls /
He gaaf him self first in his manhede to us for our Raunson when he offered
himself to the fader of heaven upon the awter of the cross /

This was a right fair yefte and a right great token of love / But what time
he gives himself in his godhede ghoostly to our souls for our salvation /
And makes us for to know him. and for to love him / Then louyth he us fully
/ for then yeueth he himself to us / and more might he not give us / ne
less might not suffyce to us / And for this skylle it is said that the
ryghtyng of a sinful soul thorugh foryeuenesse of sins is arected and
appropered pryncypally to the worchynge of the holy ghost / For the holy
ghost is love / And in the ryghtynge of a soul our lord Ihesu shows to a
soul most of his love / for he does away all sin and oonyth it to him / And
that is the best thing that he may do to a soul / and therefore it is
appropred to the holy ghost / The making of the soul is appropred to the
fader. as for the souereyne might and power that he shewyth in making of it /
The byenge of it is aretted to the sone as for the souereyne wit and wisdom
that he showed in his manhede / For he overcome the fend pryncypally through
wysdom and not thorugh strength / But the ryghtynge an^ the full saving of a
soul by foryeuenesse of sins is apr^pred to the third person that is the
holy ghost / For therein shows Ihesu most love unto man^es soul / And for
th^^ thing shall he be most loved of us again / His making i^ comen to us
and to all unreasonable creatures / For as he made us of naught. so made he
hem / And therefore is this we^ke greteste of might. but not most of love /
Also the bye^^ge is comen to us and to all reasonable souls / as to Jews ^
^arracyns and to falls christian men / For he deyed for all soule^ ylyke / and
bought hem. if they woll have the perfyte love (...) it / And also it suffyceth
for the bienge of all though it be so^ that all have it not / And this work
was most of wisdom not most of love / But the ryghtynge and the halowyng of
our souls through the yefte of the holy ghost. that is oonly ye worchynge of
love. And that is not comen but it is specyalle gift oonly to chosen souls /
And sothly that is most worchynge of love to us that are his chosen chylderne

This is the love of god that I spoke of which thou should coueyte and desire:
for this love is god himself and the holy ghost / This love unformed when it
is yeuen to us it worcheth in our soul all that good is* and all that longs
to godenes / This love loves us or that we love him. for it cle^seth us first
of our sins: and makyth us for to love him. and makyth our will strong for
to ayenstonde all sins: and styreth us for to assaye ourself through diverse
exercise both bodily and ghostly in all virtues / It stireth us also for to
forsake the syn^e and flesshly affecco^ns and worldly dredes / It keeps us fro
malycyous temptaco^ns of the fende^ and dryueth us out fro besynes and vanyte
of the world: and fro conuersaco^n of worldly lovers / All this does the love
of god vnfourmed when he yeueth himself to us / we do right naught but suffer
him and assente to him: for that is the most that we do that we assente
wylfully to his gracyous worchyng in us / And yet is not that will of us but of
his making: so that me thinkyth that he does in us all that is well done. and
yet see we it not / And not only does he thus: but after this love does
more. for he opens the eye of the soul. and shewith to the soul y^ syghte
of Ihu^ wonderfully: and the knowing of him as the soul may suffer it thus by
little and by little. and by ye syghte he rauyssheth all the affection of the
soul to him. and then^e begyn^eth the soul for to know him ghostly and
bren^yngly for to love him / Then^e sees the soul somewhat of the kind of the
blessed godhede of Ihu^ how that he is all and that he worcheth all. and that
al good deeds yt are done and good thoutes are only of him for he is al
souerein myt and al souerein sothfastnes and al souereyne godenes / And
therefore every good deed is done of him and by him. and he shall only have ye
worship and the thank for all good deeds and no thing but he / For though
wretched me^ stele his worshypp here for a while / Nevertheless at the last
end shall sothfastnesse show well that Ihesu did all* and man did right
naught of him sefe / And then shall thieves of gods good that are not
acorded with him here in this life for her trespaas be demyd to death. and Ihesu
shall be fully worshypped and thanked of all blessed creatures for his
worchynge / This love is not else but Ihu^ himself that for love worcheth all
this in man's soule^ and refourmeth it in feeling to his lyknes as I have
before said and some what as I shall say / This love brings in to the soul
the full head of all virtues and makyth him all clean and true soft and easy.
and torneth him all in to love and in to likynge / And on what manner wise he
does that. I shall tell the a lityll afterward / This love drawyth the soul
fro vain beholdynge of worldly things in to conte^placyon of ghostly
creatures and of goddis pryuitees / fro flesshlihede in to ghostlynes / fro
erthly feeling in to heavenly savor:

How that some soul loves Ihu^ by bodily feruours and by her own manly
affecco^ns that been styred by grace and by (...) And how some louen Ihu^ more
restfully by ghostly affecc^o^s oonly styred Inward through special grace of
the holy ghost* Caplm xxxv.
Then may I say that he that most has of this lo^^ here in this life
most pleseth god. and most clear (...) shall have of him / and most fully
love him in the (...) of heaven / for he has the most yeft of love here in earth
/ The love may not be had by a man^es own traueyle as some (...) / It is
freely had of the gracyous yefte of Ihu^ after moch^ bodily and ghostly
traueyle going before / For there are some ^^uers of god that make^ hemself to
love god as it were by her own might / for they streyne hemself through great
vyolence and panten so strongly that they brast in to bodily feruours as they
would draw donwe god fro heaven to hem / And they sayen in her hertes and with
her mouth / A lord I love the and I would love the: I would for thy love
suffer death / And in this manner of worchynge they feel great fervor and much
grace / And soth it is me thinks this worchynge is good and medfull if it be
well tempred with mekenes and with discrecyon / But nevertheless these men love
not ne have not the yefte of love on that manner as I speak of: ne they ask it
not so / For a soul that has the yeft of love through gracyous beholdynge of
Ihesu as I mean. or else if he have it not yet: but would have it. he is not
besy for to strain himself over his might as it were by bodyly strength for
to have it by bodyly feruours: and so for to feel the love of god. but him
thynkyth that he is right naught* and that he can do right naught of
himself. but as it were a deed thing only hangyng and borne up by the mercy of
god / He sees well that Ihu^ is all and does all. and therefore asks he
naught else but the yefte of love For sythen that the soul sees that his
own love is naught. therefore it would have his love for that is enough /
Therefore prays he and that desires he that the love of god would towche him
with his blessed light that he might see a little of him by his gracyous
presence: for then should he love him / And so by this way comyth the yefte
of love that is god in to a soul / The more that a soul noughtith itself
through grace by sight of this sothfastnes some time without any fervor
outward showed. and the less that it thinkith that it loves or sees god. the
nerer it nygheth for to perceive the yefte of the blessed love / For then is
love master and worcheth in the soul: and makes it forgete itself. and for
to see and behold only how love does / And then^e is the soul more
suffrynge than doing. and that is clean love / Thus saint poul meaned when he
said thus / Quicu^que sp^u dei agunt hii filii dei su^t / All thise that are
wrought with the spirit of god are goddis sons. Ro^ viii
y^ is souls y^ are made so meke and so buxom^ to god yt they work not of
hemself. but suffer ye holy ghost stire hem and worche hem in the felynges of
love with a sweet cord to his styrynges / These arne specially goddis sons
most like unto him / Other souls that can not love thus but traueylen hemself
by her own afflycco^ns and styre hemself through her own thinking of god and
bodily exercise for to draw out of hemself by maystry the feeling of love by
feruours and other bodily signs love not ghostly / They (...) ne well and
medefully if so that they woll know mekely that her werchyng is not the
kyndely gracyous felyng of love. but it is manly doing by a soul at the
biddynge of reason / And nevertheless through the godenes of god by cause that
the soul does that in it is. thise manly affecco^ns of the soul stired (...)
to god by man's werchynge are turned in to ghostly affe^^co^ns. and are
medefull as if they had be done ghostly in ye f^^ste beginning / And this is a
great curtesye of our lord showed to meke souls that torneth all these manly
affeccyons of kindly love in to the affecco^n and in to the mede of his own
love: as if he had wroughte hem all fully by himself / And (...) thise manly
affecco^ns so turned may be called affecco^ns (...) ghostly love through
purchase not through kyndly bryngyng fourth of the holy ghost / I say not that
a soul may worche ^^che manly affecco^ns only of itself without grace / for
(...) well that saint poul says that we may right naught (...) ne think
that good is of ourself without grace / Non (...) sumus sufficie^tes cogitare
aliquid ex nobis quasi ex nobis. (...) sufficie^cia nr^a ex deo e^ / That is.
we that love god wene (...) that we suffyse for to love or for to think good
of ourself^ oonly / but our suffisynge is of god / For god worcheth in (...)
both good work and good will as saint poul says / Deus ^ qui operat in nobis
et velle and perficere pro bona volu^tate / That is: It is god that worcheth in
us good will and fulfyllynge of good will / But I say that such affecco^ns
are good made by the will and mean of a soul after the general grace that he
yeueth to all chosyn souls / not of special grace made goostly by towchynge
of his gracyous presence as he worcheth in his perfyte lovers as I said before
/ for in imperfect lovers love worcheth ferly by the affeccio^s of man. but
inperfyte lovers love werchyth nerely by her own ghostly affeccions: and
sleeth in a soul for the time all other affecco^ns both flesshly kyndly and
manly. and y^ is properly the werchynge of love by him self / Thus love may
be had in a little in party here in a clean soul through the ghostly syghte of
Ihu^. but in the bliss of heaven it is fulfilled by clear syghte in his godhede
/ For there shall none affecco^n be feled in a soul but godly and ghostly /

That the yefte of love among all other yeftes of Ihu^ is worthiest and most
profitable / And how Ihu^ does all that is well done in his lovers only for
love / And how love makyth the using of all virtues and all good deeds light
and easy / Caplm xxxvi.
Ask thou then of god no thing but this yeft of love that is the holy
ghost / For among all the yeftes yt our lord yeueth there is none so good
ne so profitable. so worthy ne so excellent as this is / For there is no yefte
of god that is both the yeuer and the yefte but this yefte of love / And
therefore it is the best and the worthyest / The yefte of prophecy the yeftes
of miracles worchyng. the yefte of the great knowing and cou^seylyng. and the
yefte of great fasting or of great penance doing: or any other such are
great yeftes of the holy ghost. but they are not the holy ghost / For a
reproved soul and a da^pnable might have all thise yeftes as has a chose^
soul / And therefore al these manner yeftes are not greatly for to desire ne
much for to charge / But the yefte of love is the holy ghost god himself. and
him may no soul have and be dampened with all / For that yefte saves it
only fro dampnaco^n: and makyth it goddis sone perceyuer of heavenly heritage /
And y^ love as I have before said is not the affecco^n of love that is formed
in a soul: but it is y^ holy ghost himself that is love vnfourmed that saves
a soul / For he yeueth himself to a soul first or the soul louith him / and
he fourmeth the affection in the soul: and makes the soul for to love him
on^li for himself / And not only that: but also by this yefte the soul loves
itself and all his eue^crysten as itself only for god / And this is the yefte
of love that makyth shedynge atwyx chosen souls and reproved / And this yefte
makyth full pees atwyxe god and a soul. and oonyth all blessed creatures holy
in god for it makith Ihu^ for to love us and us him also: and every each of us
for to love other in him / Coueyte this yefte of love pryncypally as I have
said / For if he woll of his grace give it the on that manner wise it shall open
and lyghte^ the reason of thy soul for to see sothfastnes that is god and
ghostly things / And it shall styre thyn affecco^n holy for to see
sothfastnes that is god and ghostly things / And it shall styre thyn affecion
holy and fully for to love him / And it shall worche in thy soul oonly as he
woll. and thou shall behold Ihu^ reverently with softnes of love and see how
he does / Thus byddeth he by his prophet that we should do saienge thus /
Vacate and vide^e (...) ego su^ deus / Cease ye and sees that I am god / That
is: ye yt are reformed in feeling and have your In^er eye opened in to syghte
of ghostly things cease ye some time of outward worching and see yt I am god
/ That is: See only how I Ihesu god and man do / Behold ye me for I do all /
I am love: and for love I do all that I do: and ye do naught / And that this
is sooth I shall show you / For there is no good deed done by you: ne good
thought felt in you: but if it be done through me / That is. Through might and
wisdom. and love myghtely: wyttely and lovely / Else it is no good deed /
But now is it soth that I Ihu^ am both might and wysdom and blessed love and
ye naught: for I am god / Then mow ye well see that I do all your good
deeds / And all good thoughts: and all your good loves in you: and ye do
right naught / And yet nevertheless ben all these good deeds called yours /
Not for ye worche hem pryncypally. but for I give he^ to you for love that I
have to you / And therefore sythe^ I yt am Ihu^. and for love does all this.
cease then^e ye of the beholdynge of yourself: and set yourself at naught and
look on me. and see that I am god. for I do all this / This is somewhat of the
meaning of the veers of dauyd before said / See then^e and behold what love
worcheth in a chosen soul that he refourmeth in feeling to his lyknes when the
reason is lyghtned a little to the ghostly knowing of Ihu^. and to the feeling
of his love / Then^e brings love in to the soul the full head of virtues.
and torneth hem al in to softnes and in to likynge as it were without worchynge
of the soul: for the soul stryueth not much for the getynge of hem as it
did before. but it has hem easily and felyth hem restfulfully only through
the yefte of love that is the holy ghost / And that is a well great comfort and
gladness unspeakable when it felyth suddenly and wot never how the virtue of
mekenes and patience sobertee and sadness chastyte and clennes louered to his
euencrysten. and all other virtues the which were to him sometime traueylous
paynfull and hard for to keep are now turned in to foftnes and likynge and in
to wondfull lightness: so ferforth that him thynkith no maystry ne no hardness
for to keep every virtue. but it is most liking to him for to keep it: and
all this makyth love / Other men that stonden in the comoetee of charity and
are not yet so ferforth in grace. but worche under the byddyng of reason they
stryuen and fyghten all day against sins for the getynge of virtues: and
sometime they be^ above and sometime byneth as wrastleers are / These men done
full well / They have virtues in reason and will. not in savor ne in love: for
they fyighten with hemself as it were by her own might for he^ / and therefore
may they not have full rest ne fully the hyer ho^de / Nevertheless they shall
have much mede: but they are not yet meke enough / They have not yet putt
he^self all fully in goddis hand: for they see him not yet / But a soul that
has ghostly syghte of Ihu^ takes no great keep of stryuynge for virtues for
that time / He is not besy abowte hem specially but he sets all his besynes
for to keep that syghte and that beholding of Ihu^ that it has for to hold
the mind stably thereto: and bind the love only to it yt it fall not therfro:
and forgete al other things asmoche as it may / And wha^ it does thus then^e
is Ihu^ sothfastly master again all sins: and bishado with it with his
blessed presence and getith it all virtues / And the soul is so comforted and
so borne up with the soft felyng of love that it has of the syghte of Ihu^
that it feleth no great disease outward / And thus sleeth love generally all
sins in a soul: and reformeth it in the new felynges of virtues /

How love through gracyous beholding of Ihu^ sleeth all ^^^rynges of pride: and
makes the soul for to lose savor and delight in all erthly worship / Caplm
xxxvii.
Nevertheless how love sleeth sins and refourmeth virtues in a soul more
specially shall I say. and first of pride and of mekenes that it contrary
virtue thereto / Thou sha^^ understand that there is two manner of mekenes / One
is ha^ by worchynge of reason / A another is felt of the special yefte of love
/ Both are of love: but that one love worcheth by reason of the soul. but
that other he worcheth by himself The first is imperfect: that other is
perfyte / The first mekenes that a man feleth of beholdynge of his ownes
sins and of his own wretchydnes through the which beholding he thinks
himself unworthy for to have any yefte of grace or any mede of god / But him
thinks it enough that he would of his great mercy grant him foryeuenesse of
his sins / And also he thinks him by cause of his own sins that he is
woors than the most sinner that lives / and that every man does better
thanne he / And so by such beholdynge thresteth he him self down in his
thought under all men / And he is besie for to ayenstonde the stirynges of
pride asmoche as he may both bodily pride and ghostly: and dispiseth himself
so that he assenteth not to the felinges of pride / And if his heart be taken
sometime with it that it be defoyled with vayn Joy of worship or of cu^nynge or
of praysynge or of any other thing / as soon as he may perceive it he is
evil paid with himself and has sorrow for it in heart and asks foryeuenes of
it of god. and shewyth him to his confessor* and accuses himself mekely. and
receives his penance / This is good mekenes. but it is not yet perfyte
mekenes. for it is of souls that are begyn^ynge and profitinge in grace caused
of beholdynge of sins / Love worchyth this mekenes by reason of the soul /
Perfyte mekenes a soul feleth of the syghte and the ghostly knowing of Ihu^ /
For when the holy ghost lyghtneth the reason in to the syghte of sothfastnesse
how Ihu^ is all and that he does all / the soul has so great love and so
great Joy in that ghostly syghte / for it is so sothfaste that it foryeteth
itself. and fully leneth to Ihu^ with all the love that it has for to behold
him / It takyth no keep of no unworthiness of itself ne of sins before done /
but settyth at naught itself with all the sins and all the good deeds that
ever it did. as if there were no thing but Ihu^ / Thus meke dauyd was when
he said thus / Et substa^cia mea ta^qm^ nichilu^ an^ te / That is: P^ ^ xxxviii.
Lord Ihu^ the syghte of thy blessed unmade substance and thyn endless being
shows well unto me that my substance and being of my soul is as naught
anence the / Also ane^ce his eue^crysten he has no reward to hem ne demynge
of hem whether they ben better or wors than himself is For he hold himself and
all other men as it were even ylike naught of he^self anence god* and that is
soth / For all the goodness yt is done in he^selfe or in hem is only of god
whom he beholds as al / And therefore sets he al other creatures at naught
as he does himself. Thus meke was the prophet when he said thus / Om^es
gentes quasi non sint sic sunt coram eo et quasi nichilu^ and mane reputate
su^t ei / Al men are before our lord as naught. Isay ^*
and as vnnotefull and naught they are acou^ted to him / That is anentes the
endless being and the vnchau^gable kind of god mankind is as naught / For of
naught it is made and to naught should it torn but if he kept it in the
being that made it of naught / This is sothfastnesse and this should make a
soul meke if it might see thorugh grace this sothfastnes / Therefore when love
opens the Inner eye of the soul for to see this sothfastnes with other
cyrcu^staunces that comen with all. then^e begyn^eth the soul for to be
sothfastly meke / For then^e by the syghte of god it felith and sees itself as
it is / And then forsakith the soul the beholdynge and the lenynge to
itself: and fully fallith to the beholdynge of Ihu^ / And when it does so.
then settith the soul naught by all the Joy and the worship of the world
/ For the Joy of worldly worship is so little and so naught in reward of
that Joy and that love that it felyth in the ghostly syghte of Ihu^ and
knowing of sothfastnes. that though it might have it without any sin he
would naught of it / Ne though men would worship him praise him and favor
him: or (...) him at great state it likyth him naught / Ne though he ha^
cu^nynge of all the vii. arts of clergy and of all crafts vnd the son^e: or
had power for to work al manner miracles. he has no more deinte of all this ne
more savor of he^ than to gnaw^ on a dry stycke / He had well lever foryete all this and for to be alone out of the sight of the world than for to think on
hem and be worshipped of al men / For ye heart of a true lover of Ihu^ is made
somoche and so large through a lytill syghte of him and a little feeling of his
ghostly love that all the likynge and all the Joy of all earth may not suffyce
for to fill a corner of it / And then^e semyth it well that these wretched
worldly lovers that are as it were rauysshed in love of her own worshypp^ /
and poursewe after it for to have it with all the might and all the wit that
they have / they have no savor in this mekenes / they are wonder far
therfro. But the lover of Ihu^ has this mekenes lastyngly. and that not with
heaviness and striuynge for it / but with likynge and gladness. the which
gladness it has not^ for it forsakyth the worship of the world / for that
were a proud mekenes that longs to an ypocryte / but for he has a syghte
and a ghostly knowing of sothfastnes and worthynes of Ihu^ through the yefte of
the holy ghost / That reuerente syghte and that lovely beholding of Ihesu
comfort the love so wonderfully and bears it up so myghtly and so softly
sothly that it may not like ne fully rest in no ne erthly Joy. ne it woll not
/ He makith none force wherther men lack him or praise him / worship him or
dispyse him as for himself / He settyth it not at heart neither for to be well
paid if men despise him as for more mekenes. ne for to be evil paid that men
should worship him or praise him / He had lever for to foryete both that one
and that other: and only think on Ihu^ and get mekenes by that way / And
that is much ye sykerer way who might come thereto / Thus did david wha^ he
said / Ocli mei semper ad dn^m qm^ ip^e euellet de laqueo pedes meos / That is:
P^ xiiii.
Mine eyes are ever open to Ihu^ our lord for why? he shall pluck my fete fro
snares of sin^es / For wha^ he does so then^e forsakyth he utterly himself
and vndcastyth him holy to Ihu^ / and then^e is he in a syker ward for the
sheelde of sothfastnes the which he holds kepyth him so well yt he shall
not be hurt through no stirynge of pride as long as he holds him within the
sheelde as the prophet says / Scuto circu^dabit te veritas eius non timebis a
timore nocturno. P^ x.
Sothfastnes shall vmbiclyppe the with a sheelde. and that is if thou al other
things left only behold him / For then^e shall thou not dread for ye
nyghtes dread / that is: thou shall not dread the spirit of pride whether he
come by night or by day. as the next veers says after thus / A sagitta
volante in die / Pride comyth by night for to assail a soul when it is
despised and repreued of other men that it should by that fall in heaviness and
in to sorrow / It comyth also as an arowe fleinge on ye day when a man is
worshypped and praised of al men. P. x.
whether it be for worldly doing or for ghostly that he should have vain Joy
in himself restyngly. and falls gladness in a passing thing / This is a
sharp arowe and a peryllous / It flees swyftly. and it stryketh softly. but
it wou^deth dedely / But the lover of Ihu^ that stabli beholds by devout
prayers and besy thinking on him is so vmbilapped with the syker sheelde of
sothfastnes that he dredeth not: for this arrowe may not enter in to the soul
/ Ne though it come it hurts not: but gleuteth away and passes forth / And
thus is the soul made meke as I understand by the worchynge of the holy
ghost. that is ye gift of love / For he opens the eye of the soul for to
see and love Ihesu / And he kepyth the soul in that syghte restfully and
sykerly / And he sleeth all the styrynges of pride wonderfully and pryuely and
softly: and the soul wot never how / And also he brings in by that way
sothfastly and lovely the virtue of meekness / All this does love. but not in
all his lovers (...) full / For some has this grace but shortly and lityll as
it (...) in the beginning of it. and a lityll assayenge toward. for the
conscience is not yet cleansed fully through grace / And so^^ have it more fully.
for they have clerer syghte of Ihesu. and they feel more of his love / And some
has it most fully. for they have the full yefte of conte^placo^on /
Nevertheless he that leest has on this manner as I have said. I hope sothly he
has the yeft of perfyte mekenes. for he has ye yeft of perfyte love

How love sleeth all stirynges of wrath and envy softly and refourmeth in the
soul the virtues of pees and patience and of perfyte charity to his
euencrysten as he did specially in the apposles / Caplm xxxviii.
Love worcheth wisely and softly in a soul there he woll for he sleeth
myghtily ire and envy and all passions of angrynes and malencolye in it^ and
brings in to the soul virtues of pacyence and myldenes peasibylite and
louered to his euencrysten / It is full hard and a great maystry to a man that
sto^deth only in worchynge of his own reason for to keep pacyence holy rest
and softnes in heart and charity to his euencrysten if they disease him
vnskylfully and done him wrong that he ne shall somewhat do again to hem through
stirynge of ire or of malencolye either in speaking or in worchynge or both /
And nevertheless though a man be styred and trowbled in himself and made
unrestful. be so that it be not to much passing over the bonds of reason.
and that he keep his hand and his tongue and be ready for to foryeue the
trespase wha^ mercy is asked / yet this man has the virtue of pacyence though
it be but weyke and nakidly. for asmoche as he would have it and traueyleth
besily in refreynynge of his unskillful passions yt he might have it / and
also is sorry yt he has it not as he should / But to a true lover of Ihu^ it is
no great maystry for to suffer all this / For why love fyghteth for him and
sleeth wonder softly such stirynges of wrath and of malencolye. and makyth
his soul so easy and so peasyble so suffryng and so goodly thorugh the
ghostly syghte of Ihesu with the feeling of his blessid love that though he be
despised and repreued of other men: or take wrong or harm shame or vylanye he
charge it not: he is not much styred ayenste him / He woll not be angered ne
styred against him / for if he were much styred he should forbere the comfort
that he felyth within his soul. but yt woll he not / He may lyghtlyer forgete
all the wrong that is done to him than a another man may foryeue it though
mercy were axed / And so he had well lever forgete it. for him thynkyth it
most ease to him / And love does all this. for love openyth the eye of the
soul to the sight of Ihesu. and stablith it with the liking of love that it
feleth by that syghte (...) comfort it so myghtly that it takes no keep
what (...) men Iangle or done against him / It hangs no thing (...) him / The
most harm that he might have were a (...) of ye ghostly syghte of Ihu^ / And
therefore it is lever (...) for to suffer all harms tha^ that alone / All this
may the (...) do well and easily without great trowblynge of the (...) when
disease falls all without forth and towchet^ (...) the body^ as is
bachitynge or scomyng: or spoylynge of (...) as he has / All thise greueth
naught / But it gooth (...) nerer when the flesh is towched and he feleth
smerte (...) is harder / Nevertheless though it be hard and Impossybly (...)
freyle kind of man to suffer bodily penance gladly (...) without bitter
stirynges of ire anger and (...) Impossible to love that is the holy ghost for
to (...) in a soul there he towcheth with the blessed ^^fte (...) But he
yeueth a soul that is in that plyghte (...) of love. and wondfully fastneth it
to Ihu^. and (...) it wond far from the sensualytee through his (...) and
comfort it so swetly by his blessed presence (...) soul felyth lityll
pain or else none of the sensualy^^ (...) is special grace yeuen to the holy
marters / This grace (...) appostles as holy writ says of hem thus / Ibant
(...) a conspectu consilii qm^ digni habiti su^t pro (...) cotumelia^ pati /
That is: The appostles yede Ioyeng (...) counseyle of the Jews when they were
beten with (...) and they were glad that they were worthi for to suffer (...)
bodyly disease for the love of Ihu^ / They were not styred (...) ire ne to
felnes to be avenged on the Jews that beten (...) a worldly man would be when
he suffered a lytyl harm (...) never so lityll of his euencrysten / Ne they
were not styred (...) no pride. ne to hines of he^selfe and to disdeyne: and
to demynge of the Jews as ypocrytes and heretykes are yt woll suffer much
bodily pain. and are sometime ready for to suffer death with great gladness and
with mighty will as it were in the name of Ihu^ for love of him / Sothly that
love and that gladness yt they have in suffryng of bodily myscheyf is not of the
holy ghost It comyth not fro the fire that bren^eth in the hye awter of heaven:
but it is feyned by the fend enfla^med of hell: for it is fully menged with
the heyght of pride and of presu^pcion of he^ self and despyte and demyuge and
disdeyne of hem that thus punissh^ hem / They wene that all this is charity.
and that they suffer al yt for the love of god: but they are begyled of the
myddaye fe^de A true lover of ihu^ wha^ he suffers harm of his eue^cristen is
so stre^ghthed through grace of the holy ghost. and is made so meke so
pacyente so peasyble. and that so sthofastly. yt what wrong or harm it be
that he sufffe of his euencristen he keeps ever mekenes / He dispiseth him
not: he demyth him not but he prays for him in his heart and has of him pity
and compassyon much more tendly than of a another man that never did him harm
/ And sothly better loves him and more fervently desires the saluaco^n of his
soule^ by cause that he sees yt he shall have so much ghostly profit of the
evil deed of that other man though it be against his will / But this love and
this mekenes worcheth oonly the holy ghost above the kind of man in hem that
he makes the true lovers of Ihu^ /

How love sleeth couetyse lecherye and glotenye. and sleeth ye flesshly savor
and delight in all the v. bodily wits softly and easily through a gracyous
beholding of Ihu^ / Caplm xxxix.
COuetyse also is slain in a soul by the worchynge of love: for it makyth the
soul so coueytous of ghostly good and to heavenly riches so ardau^t that it
sets right nough tby all erthly things / It has no more deynte in having
of a precious stone thanne a chalk stone / ne more love has he in a hundredth
pound of gold thanne in a pound of leed / It sets all thing that shall
perysshe at one price / No more he charge that one than that other as in his
love / For it semith well that all thise erthly things that worldly men let
so great price of and love so deyntly should pass away and torn to naught
both the thing in itself and the love of it / And therefore he brings it in
his thought by time in to that plighte that it shall be after: and so
acou^teth it as naught / And when wordly lovers stryuen and fyghten. and plede
for erthly good who may first have it: the lover of Ihu^ stryueth with no
man but kepyth himself in pees. and holds him paid with that yt he has and
wol stryne for no more / For him thynkyth yt he needs no more of all the riches
in earth than a skant bodily sustenau^ce for to save the bodily life with all
aslo^ge as god woll. and that he may lightly have / And therefore wol he no
more than skantly him needs for the time that he may freely be discharged fro
besynes about the keeping and the dispe^dyng of it. and fully give his heart
and his besynes about the seeking of Ihu^ for to find him in clen^es of
spirit: for that to all his couetyse? For why: oonly clean of heart shall see
him Also flesshly love of fader and mother and other worldly friends ha^geth not
upon him / It is even kutte fro his heart with the sword of ghostly love that
he has no more affeccio^ to f^der or mother or to any worldly friend than he
has to a another man. but if he see or feel in hem more grace or more virtue
than in other men / Out take this: that his fader and his mother had the self
grace yt some other me^ have / But nevertheless if they ben not so: then^e
loves he other men better than hem: that is charity / And so sleeth goddis
love couetyse of ye world. and brings in to the soul pouerte in spirit /
And yt does love not only in hem that have right naught of worldly good but
also in some creatures that are in great worldly state and have dispendynge of
erthly riches / Love sleeth in some of hem couetise so ferforth yt they have no
more likinge ne savor in having of hem than of a straw / Ne though they be
lost for defawte of hem that should keep hem they set naught thereby? For why
the heart of goddis lover is through the yefte of ye holy ghost taken so fully
with the syghte of the love of a another thing that is Ihu^. and that is so
precious and so worthy yt it wol receive none other love restyngly that is
contrary thereto / And not only does love this but also it sleeth the lykyng
of lecherye and all other bodily vnclen^es. and brings in to the soul very
chastyte^ and torneth it in to likynge / For the soul felyth so great delight
in the syghte of Ihu^ that it likes for to be chaste and is no great hardness
to it for to keep chastity. for it is so most ease and most rest / And upon
the self wise the yefte of love sleeth lusts of glotenye and makyth the soul
sobre and temperaunte. and bears it up so myghtily that it may not rest in
likynge of mete and drink. but it takes mete and drink what it be that leest
greueth the bodyly complexion if he may lightly come thereto / Not for love of
itself. but for the love of god / On this manner wise the lover of god sees
well yt him needs for to keep his bodily life with mete and drink aslong as
god woll suffer hem to be together / Then^e shall this be ye discreco^n of the
lover of Ihu^ as I vndstonde that has feling and worchynge in the love. that
upon what manner that he may most keep his grace hole and leest be let fro
worchynge in it through taking of bodily sustenau^ce: so shall he do / That
manner of mete that leest lets and leest troubles the heart and may keep
the body in strength be it flesh be it fysshe be it bread and ale: yt I trow
the soul cheseth for to hane if it may come thereby / For all the besynes of ye
soul is for to think on Ihu^ with reverent love ever without lettynge of any
thing if yt it might / And therefore sythen it must nedis so^what be let
and hyndred. the less that it is let and hindered by mete or drink or any
other thing the lever it is / It had lever use the best mete and most of
price vnd the son^e if it less let ye keeping of his heart than for to take
but bread and warter if yt let him more / For he has no reward for to
get him great mede for the pain of fasting. and be put thereby fro softnes in
heart: but all his besynes is for to keep his heart as stably as he may in the
syghte of Ihu^ and in the feeling of his love / And sothly as I trow he might
with less likynge use ye best mete that is good in the own kind than a
another man that worcheth al in reason without the special yefte of love should
mow use the worste. out take mete that through craft of curyosite is only
made for lust / That manner of mete may he not well acorde with all / And also
on that other side if little mete as only bread and ale most helps and
ceseth his heart and kepyth it most in pees it is most leyf than to him for
to use it so: and namly if he feel bodily strength only of the yefte of love
with all / And yet does love more for it sleeth accidye and flesshly ydlenes.
and makes the soul to be occupied in goodness and namly Inward in beholdynge
of him. by the (...) of which the soul has savor and ghostly delight in
prayeng^ in thynkyng and in all other manner of doing that needs (...) be done
after the state that he is in without heaviness or pay^^ful bytternes whether he
be religious or seculer / Also it (...) the vain likynge of the v. bodily
wits / For the sight (...) eye: that the soul has no liking in the syghte
of any (...) thing. but it feleth rather pain and disease in beholding of it
be it never so fair. never so precious never so (...) And therefore as worldly
lovers ren^e out sometime for to (...) new things for to wond on hem: and so
for to feed her heart with the vain sight of hem / Right so a lover of Ihu^ is
besy for to ren^e away and wythdrawe him fro the syghte of such manner things
that the Inner syghte be not let / for he sees ghostly a another manner
thing yt is fayrer and more wondful and that would he not forbere / Right on
the self wise is it of spekyng and heryng / It is a pain to ye soul of a
lover of thu^ for to speak or here any thing that might let the fredom of
his heart for to think on Ihu^. what song or melodye or mynstralsie outward
that it be if it let the thought that it may not freely and restfully pray
or think on him. it likyth him right naught / And the more delectable that it
is to other me^ the more unsavory it is to him / And also for to here any manner
of spekyng of other men but it be so^what towchyng the worchynge of his soul
in the love of Ihu^: it likyth him right naught: he is else right sone weary
thereof / He had well lever be in pees and here right nout. ne speak right
naught tha^ for to here the speaking and the techyng of the grettest clerk of
earth with all the reasons that he can say to him through man's wits. but if
he can speak felyngly and stiryngly of ye love of Ihu^ for that is his craft
pryncipally / And therefore would he not else speak: here ne see but that
might help him and ferder him in to more knowing. and to better feeling of
him / Of worldly speech it is no dowte that he has no savor in spekyng ne
in herynge of it: ne in worldly tales ne in tidinges. ne in none such vain
Iangelynge. that longs not to him / And so it is of smelling and sauerynge
/ The more that the thought should be distracte and broken fro ghostly rest
by ye use either of smelling or sauerynge. or of any of the bodily wits the
more he flees it / The less that he feleth of hem the lever is him / And if
he might live in the body without ye felyng of any of he^ he would never feel
hem / For they trouble the hrete often times / and puttith it fro rest. and they
may not fully be eschewed Nevertheless the love of Ihu^ is sometime so mighty in
a soul that it ouercomith and sleeth all that is contrary thereto for a time /

What virtues and graces a soul receives through opening of ye In^er eye in
to ye gracyous beholding of Ihu^. and how it may not begete only through
man's traueyle. but through special grace and traueyle also / Caplm xl.
THus worcheth love in a soul openyng the ghostly eye in to beholdyyge of Ihu^
by Inspyraco^n of special grace^ and makyth it clean subtle and able to the
work of conte^placyon / what this opening of the ghostly eye is the gretteste
clerk in earth can not ymagyn by his wytt ne show fully by his tongue / For it
may not be get by study ne through man^es traueyle only: but pryncipally by
grace of the holy ghost and with traueyle of man / I dread much to speak out
of it for me thi^keth I can not / I passes mine assaye and my lyppes are
unclean Nevertheless for I hope love axeth and love biddyth: therefore I shall
say a lityl more of it as I hope love techeth / This opening of the ghostly
eye is that lighty derkenes and rich naught that I spoke of before. and it
may be called puryte of spyryte and ghostly rest: Inward stylnes and pees of
conscience: hyghnes of thought and on^lynes of soul: a lyfly feeling of grace
and pryuyte of heart. the waker sleep of the spouse and taastynge of heavenly
savor. bren^yng in love and shynyn^ge in light. enter of co^te^placyon. and
refourmyng in feeling / All thise reasons are said in holy writing by diverse
men. for every of hem spoke of it after his feeling in grace / And though all
thise ben (...) in showing of words: nevertheless they are all in one (...) of
sothfastnes / For a soul that through vysitynge of (...) has one. has all?
For why: a sighyng soul to see the face (...) Ihu^ when it is towched through
special grace of the holy g^^ost it is sodeinly changed and turned fro the
plyte that it was (...) to a another manner of feeling / It is wondfully departed
and (...) first in to itself fro the love and the likyng of al erthly thing
somoche that it has lost the savor of the bodily life and of all thing that
is saaf only Ihu^ / And then^e it is clean fro al ye fylthe of syn^e: so
ferforth that the mind of it and al vnordeynde affection of any creature is
suddenly wasshen and wyped away. that there is no mean lettynge betwyxe Ihu^
and the soul but only the bodily life: and then^e it is in ghostly rest? For
why all paynfull doubts and dredes and all other temptacyous of ghostly enmyes
are driven out of the heart that they trowble not ne synke not therein for the
time / It is in rest fro the noye of wordly business and paynful taryenges of
wicked stirynges. but it is full besye in the fre ghostly worchyng of love /
And the more it traueyleth so. the more rest he feleth This restfull
traueylle is full far fro flesshly ydlenes and fro blind sykernes / It is
full of ghostly work. but it is callid rest. for grace loses the heavy yocke
of flesshly love fro the soul and makyth it mighty and free through the yefte
of ghostly love for to worche gladly softly and delectably in all thing that
grace styreth it for to worche in / And therefore it is called an holy ydlenes
and a rest most besye. and so it is in Inward stylnes fro the great cryenge
of the bestly noise of flesshly desires and unclean thoughts / This stylnes
makyth Inspyraco^n of the holy ghost in beholdynge of Ihu^ /? For why: His
voyse is so sweet and so mighty that it puts scylence in a soul to
Ianglyng of all other spekers^ for it is a voys of virtue softly sowned in a
clean soul. of the which the prophet says thus / Vox dn^i in virtute / That
is: The voys of our lord Ihesu is in virtue / This voys is a lyfely word and a
spedy as the apostle says / Viuus est sermo dei and efficax et penetrabilior
om^i gladio / that is. quycke is the word of Ihu^ and spedy. more perisshynge
than any sword is / Through speaking of this word is flesshly love slain and
the soul kept in scylence fro all wicked stirynges / Of this scilence it is
said in the apocalips thus / Apoc^
Factu^ est scilenciu^ in celo quasi dimidia hora / Scilence was made in heaven
as it were an half hour / Heaven is a clean soul through grace lift up fro
erthly love to heavenly co^uersaco^n and so it is in scylence / But for as
much as that scylence may not last hoole contynually for corrupcyon of the
bodily kind / Therefore it is lyckened to the time of half an hour / A full
short time the soul thinks that it is be it never so long / And therefore
it is but an half hour / And then has it pees in conscience? For why:
Grace puttyth out gnawynge pryckynge and stryuynge and flyghtynge of sins /
And brings in pees and accord. and makyth Jesus and a soul both one in full
acordaunce of will /

There is none vpbradynge of sins: ne sharp repreuynge of defawtes made that
time in a soul For they have kyssed and made friends: and all is forgyuen that
was mysse done Thus felyth the soul then with full meke sikernesse and great
ghostly gladness / And conceyueth a full great boldness of salvation by this
accord making / For it heryth a preuy wytnessynge in conscience of the holy
ghost that he is a chosen sone to heavenly heritage / Thus saint poul says /
Ip^e spiritus testimonium perhibet spiritui nostro quonia^ filii dei sumus /
That is: The holy ghost beryth witness to our spiry^te that we are goddis
sons / This wytnessynge of conscyen^ce sothfastly felt through grace is the
very Joy of the soul as the apostle says / Gloria mea est testimonium
conscienc^^ me / That is: My Joy is the witness of my conscye^ce (...) that
is when it wytnessyth pees and acorde true love and fre^dshyppe betwyxe Ihesu
and a soul / And when it is in th^^ pees: then is it in hyghnes of thought
/

When the soul is bounden with love of the world then^e (...) it byneth all
creatures / For every thing ouergooth it and ^^ryth it down by maystry that
it may not see Ihesu ne (...) him / For right as the love of the world is
vain and flesshly Rygh so the beholdynge and thynkynge^ and the using of all
creatures is flesshly / And that is a thraldom of the soul But then through
opening of the ghostly eye in to Ihesu the love is turned / And the soul is
raised up after his own kind above all bodyly creatures /

And then the beholdynge and thinking and the using of hem is ghostly / For
the love is ghostly / The soul has then full great disdeyne for to be buxom
to love of worldly things. for it is high set above he^ through grace / It
sets naught by all ye world? for why: all shall pass and perissh^ / Unto
this hienes of heart while the soul is kept therein comith none error ne
deceyte of the fe^de: for Ihu^ is sothfastly in syghte of the soul that time
and all thing byneth him / Of this ye prophet spekyth thus / Accedat ho^ ad
cor altu^ et exaltabit deus Come man to high heart and god shall be hyghed /
P. lxiii.
That is: a man yt through grace comyth to the highness of thought shall see
that Ihu^ is only hyghed above all creatures. and he in him / And then^e is
the soul above much strau^ged fro felyship of worldly lovers / Though her
body be in mids among hem. full far ben they departed fro flesshly
affecco^ns of creatures It charge not though it never see man ne speak with
him ne have comfort of him if it might ever be so in that ghostly feeling /
It felyth so great homlynes of the blessed presence of our lord Ihu^ and
somoche savor of him that it may lightly for his love foryete the flesshly
affeccio^ and the flesshly mind of all creatures / I say not that it shall
not love ne think of other creatures. but I say that it shall think on hem in
time and see hem and love hem ghostly and freely. not flesshely and painfully
as it did before / Oseerii
Of this on^lynes speaks the prophet thus / Duca^ ea^ in solitudine. et
loquar ad cor eius / I shall led her in to only stead. and I shall speak to her
heart / That is: Grace of Ihu^ ledeth a soul fro noyous company of flesshly
desires in to on^lynes of thought. and makyth it foryete the liking of the
world and sowneth by swetnes of his Inspyracyon words of love in eeres of the
heart / Oonly is a soul when it loves Ihu^ and tentyth fully to him. and has
lost the savor and the comfort of the world / And that it might better
keep this only nes it flees the company of all men if it may. and sechyth
on^lynes of body: for that much helps to on^lynes of y^ soul and to the
free worchynge of love / The less lettynge that it has without of vain
Jangling or within of vayn thinking the more free it is in ghostly
beholdynge: and so it is in pryuytee of heart / All without is a soul whiles
it is ouerlayed and blinded with worldly love / It is as comen as the hye way.
for every stirynge that comes of the flessh^ or of the fe^de synketh in and
gooth thorugh it / But then through grace it is drawn in to the preuy chamber
in to the syghte of our lord Ihu^. and hereth his preuy counseyle: and is
wonderfully comforted in the herynge / Of this spekith the prophet thus
Secretu^ meum michi^ secretum meu^ michi / My preuytee to me. my preuyte to me
/ That is: The lover of Ihu^ through Inspyraco^n of grace taken up fro outward
feeling of worldly love and rauysshed in to the preuite of ghostly love yeldeth
than king to him saying thus / My pryuete to me: That is* My lord Ihu^ thy
preuyte is showed to me and preuyly hid fr^ all lovers of the world / For it
is called hid manna. yt may lightlyer be asked than told what it is / And
that our lord Jesus behoteth to his lover saying thus / Dabo sibi manna ab^
conditu^ quod nemo nouit nisi qui accipit / That is: I shall give manna hid
that no man knows but he that takith ^ This manna is heavenly mete and angels
fode as holy write says / For angels are fully fed and filled with clear
syghte in brennynge love of our lord Ihesu. and that is manna / For we mow
ask what it is: but not wit what it is But the lover of Ihesu is not filled
yet here: but he is fed (...) by a little taastynge of it whiles he is bounden
in this bodyly life /

This tastynge of this manna is a lyfly feeling of grace had through opening of
the ghostly eye / And this grace is not an other grace that a chosen soul
felith in the beginning of his co^uersyon: but it is the same and the self
grace. but it is otherwise felt and showed to a soul / For why grace wexeth
with ye soul and the soul wexeth with grace / And the more clean ye the soul
is far departed fro the love of the world the more mighty is the grace: more
Inward and more ghostly showing in the presence of our lord Ihu^: so yt the
same grace yt torneth hem first fro syn^e: and makith hem begyn^ynge and
profityng by yeftes of virtue and exercise of good works maken he^ also
perfyte / And that grace is called a lyfly feeling of grace: for he yt has it
feleth it well. and knows well by experye^ce that he is in grace / It is full
lyfly to him for it quyckneth the soul wondfully and makyth it so hole that
it feleth no paynfull disease of the body though it be feeble and sykly? For
why: then^e is ye body mightiest most hole and most restful and the soul
also: with out this grace the soul can not live but in pain: for it thynkyih
yt it might ever keep it and no thing should put it away And nevertheless yet
it is not so. for it passes away full lightly / But nevertheless though the
souereyne felinge passes a way and wythdrawe. the releif leueth still and
keeps the soul in sadness. and makith it for to desire the coming again / And
this is also the waker sleep of the spouse: of y^ which holy writ says thus
/ Ego dormio et cor meu^ vigilat / I sleep and my heart wakith / That is: Cant.
v
I sleep ghostly when through grace the love of the world is slain in me and
wicked stirynges of flesshly desires are deed: somoche that uneaths I feel he^
/ I am not tarried with hem: my heart is made free / And then^e it wakith. for
it is sharp and ready for to love Ihu^ and see him / The more I sleep fro
outward things the more waker I am in knowing of Ihu^ and of Inward things
/ I may not wake to Ihu^ but if I sleep to the world / And therefore the grace
of the holy ghost speryng the flesshly eye does ye soul selpe fro worldly
vanyte: and opening the ghostly eye wakith in to the syghte of god dis mageste
helid vnd the cloud of his precious manhede As the gospel says of the
apostles when they were with our lord Ihu^ in his transfyguraco^n / First
they slepte / Et euigilantes videru^t magestate^ / They waking saw his
mageste By sleep of the apostles is understand deyeng of worldly love through
Inspiraco^n of the holy ghost. by her walking conte^placo^n of Ihu^ / Through
this sleep the soul is brought in to rest fro noise of flesshly lust / And
through walkinge it is raised up in to the syghte of Ihu^ and ghostly things /
The more that the eyes are spered in this manner sleep fro the appetyte of
erthly thing. the sharper is the Inner syghte in lovely beholdynge of heavenly
fayrhede / This slepynge and this wakyng love worcheth through the light of
grace in the soul of the lover of our lord Ihesu /

How special grace in beholdynge of our lord Ihu^ wythdrawyth sometime fro a
soul / And how a soul shall have her in the absence and presence of Ihu^ /
And how a soul shall desire that in it is always the gracyous presence of
Ihesu / Caplm xli.
Show me then^e a soul that through Inspyraco^n of grace has opening of the
gostly syghte in to beholdynge of Ihu^ that is departed and drawn out fro the
love of the world so ferforth that it has puryte and pouerte of spirit:
ghosty ^^ste: Inward scylence. and pees in conscye^ce: highness of thought^
on^lynes and pryuete of heart: waker sleep of the spouse. that hat^ lost
liking and Joys of the world. taken with delyce of heu^^ly sauour^ ever
thristynge: and softly shyghynge yt blessed presen^ce of Ihu^. and I dare
hardly pronounce that this soul bren^eth all in love and shyneth in ghostly
light worthy for to come to the name and to the worship of the spowse. for it
is refourme^ in feeling made able and ready to contemplacion / These are the
tokens of Inspiraco^n in openyng of the ghostly eye? For why when the eye is
opened the soul is in full feeling of all these virtues before said for that
time / Nevertheless it falls often times that grace withdrawyth in party
for corrupcyon of man's freelte and suffers then^e the soul for to fall in
to itself in flesshlyhede as it was beforne / And then is the soul in pain
and in sorrow: for it is blind and unsavory and can no good / It is weyke and
vnmyghty enco^bred with ye body and with all the bodily wits / It secheth and
desires after ye grace of Ihu^ again and it may not find it / For holy writ
says of our lord thus / Postqm^ vultu^ suu^ absco^derit no^ e^ qui
co^te^plet eu^ / That is: After wha^ our lord Ihu^ has hid his face there
is none that may behold him. wha^ he shows him the soul may not vnsee
him. for he is light. and when he hydeth him it may not see him for the soul
is derke / His hidynge is but a subtle assayenge of the soul / His showing
is a wond merciful goodness in comfort of the soul / Have ye no wond though
the feeling of grace be wythdrawe sometime fro a lover of Ihu^ / For holy wrytt
says ye same of the spouse that she fares thus / Quesiui et no^ inueni illu^.
vocaui and no^ respondit michi / I seched and I found him not / I called and
he answered not / That is: Cant. 3
when I fall down to my freelte then^e grace wythdraweth* for my falling is
cause thereof. and not his fleenge / But then^e feel I pain of my wretchidnes
in his absence / And therefore I sought him by great desire of heart: and he
yaue to me no feable answering / And then^e I cried with all my soul / Cant:
6
Reuertere dilecte mi / Torn aye^ thou my loved And yet it semid as he herd
me not / The paynfull felyng of myself and the assaylinge of flesshly loves and
dredes in this time and the wantynge of my ghostly strength is a co^tynuell
cryeng of my soul to Ihu^ / And nevertheless our lord makith strange and
comyth not cry I never so fast / For he is syker ynouh^ of his lover that he
wol not torn again to worldly love fully he may no savor have therein. and
therefore abides he y^ longer But at ye last when he woll he comyth again full
of grace and of sothfastnes. and vysiteth the soul yt languyssheth in desire
by syghe^ges of love to his presence. and towchyth it and anoynteth it full
softly with the oil of gladnes^ and makyth it suddenly hole fro all pyne: and
then^e cries the soul to Ihu^ in ghostly voys with a glad heart thus /
Oleum effusu^ nomen tuum Oil yshedde is thy name / Thy name is Ihesu: Cant. i.
that is hele / Then as long as I feel my soul sore and syke for sin
pyned with the heavy burden of my body sorry and dredynge for perils and
wretchydnes of this life. so long lord Ihesu thy name is oil speryd not
oil yshed to me / But when I feel my soul suddenly towched with the light of
thy grace heled and softed fro all the fylthe of sin. and comforted in love
and in light with ghostly strength and gladness unspeakable. then may I
say with lusty loving and ghostly might to the / Oil yshed is thy name Ihu^
to me / For by the effect of thy gracyous vysitynge I feel well of thy name ye
true expownynge that thou art Ihesu heel / For oonly thy gracyous presence
helith me fro sorrow and fro sin / Blessed is that soul that is ever fed
in feeling of love in his presence. or is borne up by desire to him in his
absence / A wise lover is he and well taught that sadly and reverently has
him in his presence. and lovely beholds him without dyssolute lyghtnes. and
pacyently and easily beryth him in his absence without venemo^^ dispeyre and
over pyneful bytternesse / This chau^gabilyte o^ absence and presence of Ihu^
that a soul felyth is not perfec^^cyon of the soul: ne it is not ayenste the
grace of perfecco^n (...) of contemplacyon: but in so much perfeccyon is the
(...) For the more lettynge that a soul has of itself fro conty^nuell feeling
of grace the less is the grace: and yet neuerthe^les is the grace in itself
grace of conte^placo^n. This chau^g^^^^lyte of absence and presence falls as
well in the state of ^^^feccio^ as in state of begin^yng: but in a another
manner. for ri^^ as there is dyuersyte of feeling in the presence of grace
bytwix thise two states. right so is there in the absence of grace / And
therefore he that knows not the absence of grace is ready to be dysceyued / And
he that kepyth not the presence of grace. is unkind to the vysitynge: whether
he be in state of begyn^ers or perfect Nevertheless the more stablenes that
there is in grace unhurt and unbroken the louelyer is the soul and more like
unto him in whom is no chau^gabilyte as the apostles say the / And it is full
semely that the spouse be like to Ihu^ spouse in manners and in virtues full
acordynge to him in stablynes of perfyte love / But that falls seeldom now
here but in ye special spouse / For he that perceyueth no chau^gabylyte in
feeling of his grace but ylike hole and stable unbroken and unhurt as him
thinks. he is either full perfyte or full blind / He is perfyte that is
sequestyrde fro all flesshly affecco^ns and comonyng of all creatures: and all
means are broken away of corrupco^n and of syn^e betwyx Ihu^ and his soul
fully oonyd to him with softnes of love / But this is only grace above mannis
kind He is full blind that feyneth him in grace without ghostly feeling of
goddis Inspyraco^n: and sets himself in a manner of stablynes as he were
ever in felyng and in worchynge of special grace: demyng that al is grace that
he does and felith with out and within. thynkyng that what so ever he do or
speak is grace: holding himself vnchau^gable in specyalte of grace / If there
be any such as I hope there be none: he is full blind in feeling of grace /
But then^e might thou say thus that we should live only in truth. and not
coueyte ghostly felynges ne reward hem if they come / For the apostle says /
Iustus ex fide viuit / That is: The rightwysman lives in truth / Unto this I
say that bodily felynges ben they never so comfortable we shall not coueyte ne
reward much if they come But ghostly felynges such as I speak of if they
come in ye manner as I have said before we should ever desire: Heb^. x.
that are sleenge of all worldly love opening of the ghostly eye: puryte of
spirit: pees of conscience: and all other before said / We should coueyte to
feel ever the lyfly Inspyracyon of grace made by the ghostly presence of Ihesu
in our soul if that we might. and for to have him in our syghte with
reverence. and ever feel the swetnes of his love by a wondfull homlynes of his
presence / This should be our life and our felyng in grace after the mesure of
his yefte in whom all grace is. to some more and to some less / For his
presence is feled in diverse manner wise as he wouchith saaf / And in this we
should live and worche that longs to us to worche. for without this we should
not cu^ne live / For right as the soul is the life of the body. righ so is
Ihu^ the life of the soul by his gracyous presence And nevertheless this manner
feeling be it never so much it is yet but troth as in reward of that yt
shall be of theself Jesus in the bliss of heaven / Lo this feeling should we
desire. for eueryche a soul reasonable owyth for to coueyte with all the
myghtes of it nyghynge to Ihu^ and oonynge to him through feeling of his
gracyous vnseable presence / How that presence is feled it may better be
known by experyence than by any writing. for it is the life and the love: the
might and the light / the Joy and the rest of a chose^ soul / And therefore
he that has oues sothfastly feled it he may not forbere it without pain he
may not vndesyre it it is so good in itself and so comfortable / what is
more comfortable to a soul here than for to be draw out through grace fro the
vile noye of worldly business and fylth of desires and fro vain affecco^n of
all creatures in to rest and softnes of ghostly love pryuely perceyuyng y^
gracious presence of Ihu^ felably fed with savor of his vnseable blessed
face: Sothly no thing me thinks / No thing may make the soul of a lover
full of myrthe but the gracyous presence of Ihu^ as he can show him to a clean
soul / He is never heavy ne sorry but wha^ he is with himself in flesshlynes /
He is never full glad ne merry but when he is out of himself as he was with
Ihu^ in his ghostlynes / And yet is that no full myrthe. for ever there
hangs an heavy lu^pe of bodily corrupco^n on his soul: and bears it down
and much lets ye ghostly gladness. and yt must ever be whiles it is here in
this life. but nevertheless for I speak of chau^gabilyte of grace how it comyth
and gooth that y^ mystake it not^ therefore I mean not of the common grace that
is had and felt in troth and in good will to god without the which having
and lasting therein no man may be saaf: for it is in the leest chose^ soul
that lives. but I mean of special grace felt by Inspiraco^n of ye holy
ghost in the manner as it is before said / The comen grace that is charity
lasts hole what so ever a man do aslonge as his will and his ente^te is
true to god without the which having and lasting that he would not syn^e
dedely. ne the deed yt he wylfully does is not forbede as for dedely sin /
For this grace is not lost but for dedely sin^e / And then^e it is dedely sin^e
when his conscience witnesses with a vysement that it is dedely syn^e. and yet
nevertheless he does it^ or else his conscience is so blinded that he holds
it no dedely syn^e all though he do the deed wylfully y^ which is forbode of
god and holy church as dedely sin / Special grace felt through the vnseable
presence of Ihu^ that makyth a soul a perfyte lover lastith not ever ylike
hole in the hynes of felyng. but chau^gably comith and gooth as I have said
before / Thus our lord says / Spu^s vbi vult spirat et vocem eius audis and
nescis vnde veniat aut quo vadat / (...). 3
The holy ghost spyreth where he woll and thou herest his voys but thou wost
not when he comyth ne^ whether he gooth / He comyth pryuely some time when thou
art leest waar of him: but thou shall well know him or you goo / For wondfully
he stiryth and myghtily torneth thin heart in to beholding of his godenes. and
does thyn heart melte delectably as wax ayenste the fire in to softnes of his
love. and this is the voys that he sowneth / But then he gooth or thou wot
it for he withdrawith him so^what / naught in all: but fro excess in to
sobirte. The hines passes: but the substance and theffecte of grace dwells
stylle / And that is aslonge as the soul of a lover kepith him clean: and
falls not wylfully to recheleshede or dissolucyon is flesshlynes ne to
outward vanyte. as some time it does though it have no delight therein for
freeltee of it self / Of this chau^gabylite in grace speak I of now /

A co^mendaco^n of prayer offered to Ihu^ of a soul contemplatyfe / And how
stablynes in prayer is a syker work to sto^de in / And how every felinge of
grace in a chosen soul may be said Ihu^: but the more clenner the soul is ye
worthyer is the grace / Caplm xlii.
THe soul of a man while it is not towched with special grace is blunte and
boystous to ghostly work and can naught thereon / It may not thereof for
weyknes of itself / It is both old and dry. undevout and unsavory in
itself / But then^e comyth the light of grace^ and through towchyng makyth it
sharp and subtyl ready and able to ghosty work: and yeueth it a great fredom
and an hole redynes in will for to be buxom to all the stirynge of grace ready
for to worche after that grace styreth ye soul / For by opening of the
ghostly eye it is applied all fully to grace ready to pray / And how the soul
prays then^e shall I tell the / The most special prayer that the soul
uses and has most comfort in I hope is the Pater noster^ or else psalms
of the sawter / The pater noster for lewd men. and psalms and ympnes and
other service of holy church for lettred / The soul prays then^e not in
manner as it did before in common manner of me^ by hyghnes of voys: or by renable
speaking out. but in full great stylnesse of voys and softness of heart For
why. his mind is not trowbled ne tarried with outward things but hole gadred
togider in itself / And the soul is set as it were in a ghostly presence of
Ihu^ and therefore every word and every syllable is sowned sauerly sweet and
delectably with full accord of mouth and of heart? For why the soul is
turned then^e all in to fire of love / And therefore every word that it pryuely
prays is like to a spercle spryngyng out of a fire bronde yt chaffith all ye
myghtes of the soul and torneth he^ in to loue^ and lyghtneth hem so
comfortably that the soul list ever for to pray and do none other thing /
The more it prays the better it may the myghtyer it is. for grace helps the
soul well. and makyth all thing light and easy. that it list right well to
psalm and sing the louynges of god with goostly myrthe in heavenly delight /
This ghostly work is fode of the soul. and this prayer is of much virtue /
For it wastes and brings to naught al temptaco^ns of the fend preuy and
aperte. it sleeth all the mind and the likyng of the world. and of flesshly
sins. It bears up the body and the soul fro paynfull telynge of
wretchydnesse of this life / It kepyth the soul in feeling of grace and
worchynge of love: and nourysshe it ever ylyke hot and fresshe as styckes
norissheth fire / It puttyth away all yrkynge and heaviness of heart* and
holds it in might and in ghostly gladness / Of this prayer spekyth dauyd
thus / Dirigatur oracio mea sicut incensu^ in conspectu tuo / That is: Dressed
be my prayer lord as encense in thy syghte / For right as encense that is cast
in the fire makyth sweet smelle by the reke styghyng up to the air / right so
a psalm sauourly and softly song of said in a bren^ynge heart yeuyth up a
sweet smelle to the face of our lord Ihu^: and to all the court of heaven /
There dare no flesh fly rest upon the pottes brynke boylynge on the fire /
Right so may there no flesshly delight rest upon a clean soul that is happed
and warmed al in the fire of love boylynge and blowynge psalms and louynges to
Ihesu / This prayer is ever herd of Ihesu / It yeldyth grace to Ihesu / And
receives grace again / It makyth a soul homely and felowly with Ihesu^ and
with all the angels of heaven / Use it who so may / The work is good and
gracious in itself / And though it be not al fully contemplaco^n. in itself
ne the werkynge of love by itself. Nevertheless it is a party of
contemplacyon? For why: It may not be done on this manner wise but in plentee

of grace through opening of the ghostly eye / And therefore a soul that has
this fredom and this gracyous feeling in prayenge with ghostly savor and
heavenly delight has the grace of conte^placyon in manner as it is / This prayer
is a rich offrynge filled all in fatnes of devotion: received by angels and
presented to the face of Ihu^ / The prayer of other men that are besy in actyf
works is made of two words. for they often times fourmeth in her hertes one
word through thynkyng of worldly be synes. and sownen in her mouth a another
word of the psalm song or said / And not for that. if her entente be true
yet is her prayer good and medefull though it lack sauoure and swetnes / But
this manner of a man conte^platyfe is made but of one word. for as it is
fourmed in the heart right so holy it sowneth in the mouth. as it were
naught but one thing yt fourmyth and sowneth / And sothly no more it is / For
the soul through grace is made hole in itself so far departed fro the
flesshlyhede that it is master of the body^ and then^e is the body naught
else but as an Instrumente and a trompe of the soul in the which the soul
blowith sweet notes of ghostly loui^ges to Ihu^ / This is the trompe that Dauyd
spoke of thus* Buccinate in neomenia tuba in insigni die sole^pnitatis ^^stre /
Blow ye with a trompe in the new moan / That is ye souls that are reformed
in ghostly life through openyng of the Inner eye. blow ye devoutly sownynge
psalms with ye trompe of your bodily tongue / And therefore for this pray^^ is
plesau^te to Ihu^ and so profitable to the soul: then^e it is good to him
that is new turned to god what that he be yt w^^de pleyse him. and coueyteth
to have some queynt feeling of grace for to coueyte this felynge^ that he might
through grace come to this lyberte of spirit. and offer his prayers and his
psalms to Ihu^ co^tynuelly: and stably and devoutly with hole mind and
brennynge affecco^n in him to have it nere hand in custom when grace woll
styre him thereto / This is a syker feeling and a sothast / If thou may come
thereto and hold it the dare not run abowte here and there: and axe questyons
of every ghostly man what thou should do how thou shall love god: and how you
shalt serve god and speak of ghostly matters that passe^ thy knowing as
perchance some done / That manner of dooyng is not full profitable but if more
need make it / ^repe the to thy prayers stylly first with traueyle yt thou
might come afterward to this restfull feeling of ghostly prayer: and yt shall
teache the wisdom enough sothfastly without feynynge or fantasye. and keep it
fourth if thou have it and leave it not: but if grace come otherwise and woll
remeue it fro the for a time and make the for to worche on a another manner.
then^e may thou leave it for a time and after torn again thereto / And he that
has this grace in prayer asks not whereupon he shall set the point of his
thought in his prayer. whether upon ye words that he says or else on god or
on the name of Ihu^ as some ask. for the feeling of grace techith him well
enough? For why the soul is turned in to the eye and sharply beholds ye face
of Ihu^. and is made syker that it is Ihu^ that it felyth and sees / I mean
not Ihu^ as he is in himself in fulness of his blessed godhede. but I mean Ihu^
as he woll show him to a clean soul holden in body after the clen^esse that
it has / For wit thou well that euryche a feeling of grace is Ihu^ and may
be called Ihu^ / And after that the grace is more or less so felyth the soul
more or less Ihu^ / ye the fyste feeling of special grace in a begyn^er that
is called grace of compu^cco^n and contricio^ for his sins is verily Ihu^?
for why: he makes that contricyon in a soul by his presence / But Ihu^ is
then^e full boystously and rudely felt. full far fro his ghostly subtylte:
for the soul can no better ne may no better for vnclen^esse of itself then^e
Nevertheless afterward if the soul profit and increase in virtues and in
clen^es the same Ihu^ and none other is seen and felt of the same soul wha^ it
is towched with grace. but yt is more ghostly nere to the godly kind of Ihu^ /
And sothly yt is the most thing that Ihu^ loves in a soul that it might be
made godly and ghostly in syghte and in love like to him in grace to that yt he
is by kind. for that shall be the end of all lovers Then may you be syker
that what time yt thou felyste thy soul styred by grace specially in that
manner as it is before said by opening of thy ghostly eye thou see and
feleste Ihu^ / Hold him fast while thou may and keep the in grace: and let
him naught lightly fro the / Look after none other Ihu^ but that same by
feeling of that self grace more godly yt it might wexe in the more and more /
And dread the naught thou Ihu^ yt thou felyst be not Ihu^ as he is in his full
godhede that you sholdest therefore mow be deceived if thou lened to thy
feeling. but trust you well if thou be a lover of Ihu^ y^ thy felyng is true and
that Ihu^ is truly felt and seen of the through his grace as thou may see him
here / And therefore lene fully to thy feeling wh^ it is gracyous and ghostly:
and keep it tendly. and have great (...) not of thyselfe but of it. that thou
might see: and feel Ihu^ (...) better and better / For grace shall even teache
the by itself if tho^ wol fall thereto till you come to the end / But perchance
you beg^^ neste to wonder why I say one time that grace worchyth (...) this:
and on a another time yt love worcheth or god worchy^^ Unto this I say thus:
that when I say that grace worch^^^ I mean love: Ihu^: and god. for all is
one. and naught but (...) Ihu^ is love: Ihu^ is grace: Ihu^ is god / And for
he worcheth (...) in us by his grace for love as god^ therefore may I use wh^^
word of thise iiii. yt me list after my stiryng in this writing

How a soul through the opening of the ghostly eye receives a gracyous love
able to vndstonde holy wrytt / And how Ihesu that is hid in holy writ
shewyth himself to his lovers / Caplm xliii
THen^e ye soul of a lover felith Ihu^ in prayer in ye manner before said. and
thynkith yt it would never feel otherwise / Nevertheless it falls that sometime
grace puts scilence to vocal prayenge: and styreth the soul to see and to
feel Ihu^ in a another manner / And yt manner is first to see Ihu^ in holy writ
For Ihu^ that is al sothfastnes is hid and heled therein wou^den in a soft
sendyle vnd fair words that he may not be known felt but of a clean heart?
For why: sothfastnes woll not show itself to enmyes but to fre^des that love
and desire it with a meke heart. for sothfastnes and mekenes arne full true
systers fastened together in love and charity / and therefore is there no
leynynge of cou^seylle betwyxe hem two / Mekenes presumyth of sothfastnes and
no thing of itself: and sothfastnes tro with well on mekenes: and so they
accorden wond well / Then for asmoche as a soul of a lover is made meke
