through inspiraco^n of grace by opening of the ghostly eye: and sees yt it is
naught of itself: but only hangs in the mercy and the godenes of Ihu^
lastyngly is born^ up by favor and help of him only: and truly desiring the
presence of him therefore sees it Jesus: For it sees sothfastnes of holy writ
wonderly showed and opened above study and traueyle and reason of man's
kyndly wit / And that may well be called the feeling and the perceiving of
Ihu^ / For Ihu^ is well of wisdom. and by a lityll heel dynge of his wysdom in
to a clean soul he makes the soul wise enough for to vndstonde all holy
wrytt. not all at ones in special beholding: but through that grace the soul
receives a new ablynes and a gracyous habyte for to vndstonde it specially
when it comith to mind This openyng and this clernesse of wit is made by the
ghostly presence of Ihu^ / For right as the gospel says of ii. discyples
going to the castle of Emaus bren^ynge in desire and spekyng of our lord
Ihu^: our lord appeared to hem presently as a pilgrim and taught hem yt
prophecyes of himself / And as the gospel says / Apperuit illis sensum vt
intelligerent scripturas / ^uc^ xiiii
He opened to hem clernes of wit that they might understand holy writynge /
Right so the ghostly presence of Ihesu openyth the wit of his lover that it
bren^eth in desire to him: and brings to his mind by mynystraco^n of angels
the words and the sentences of holy writ vnsoughte and unadvised one after a
another. and expowneth hem redily be they never so hard ne so preuy / The
harder that they ben and ferder fro man's reasonable understanding the more
delectable is the true showing of hem / When Ihesu is master it is expowned
and declared literally: morally: mystily: and heavenly. if the matter suffer it
/ By letter that is lyghteste and most plain is bodily kind comforted / By
moralte of holy writ the soul is infourmed of vices and virtues wisely to
cu^ne depart that one fro that other By mystyhed it is illumyned for to see ye
works of Ihesu in holy church. redily for to apply the words of holy writ
to christ our head: and to holy church that is his mysty body / And the fourth
that is heavenly longs only to the worchynge of love / And that is when all
sothfastnes in holy writ is applied to love / And for that is most like to
heavenly feeling therefore I call it heavenly / The lover of Ihu^ is his friend.
not for he has deserved it: but for Ihu^ of his merciful goodness makyth him
his friend by true accord / And therefore as to ^ true friend that pleyseth him
with love. not serves him (...) dread as a thralle: he shewith his preuyte /
Thus he says hym^selfe to his apostles / Iam vos dixi amicos qr quecunque
aud^ui a patre meo nota feci vobis / Now I say that ye are fren^des / For I
make known to you all things that I have herd of my fader / To a clean soul
that has the palett puryfyed from fylthe of flesshly love holy writ is
lyfely food and sustenaunce delectable /

It sauoureth wonder swetely when it is well chewed by goostly understanding?
For why: the spirit of lyffe is hid therein that quyckenyth all the myghtes
of the soul / and fylleth them full of swetnesse of heavenly sauoure and
ghostly delight / But sothly him needs to have white teeth and sharp and well
pycked that should byte of this ghostly bread / For flesshly lovers and
heritykes may not to wche the Inward flower of it / Her teeth are blody and
full of fylthe. therefore they ben fasting fro feeling of this bread / By teeth
are understand the Inly wits of ye soul. the which in flesshly lovers and
in heretykes ben blody full of sin and of worldly vanytees / They would and
they can not come by curyosite of her kyndly wit to y^ soth fastnes in
knowing of holy writ. for her wit is corrupt by origynall sin and
actuell also. And is not yet helyd through grace / And therefore they do but
gnawe upon the bark without speak they never so much thereof / The Inner
savor within they feel not of / They ben not meke they be^ not clean for to
see it / They ben not friends to Ihesu. and therefore he shows hem not his
counsel / The preuyte of holy writ is closed vnd a keye seeled with a
sygnett of Ihu^s finger: that is the holy ghost / And therefore wythouten his
love and his leave may no man come in / He has only the keye of cu^nynge in
his keeping as holy writ says. and he is keye himself / And he lets in
whom he woll by Inspyraco^n of his grace. and breketh not the selle. and yt
does Ihu^ to his lovers / Not to all ylike. but to hem that are specially
Inspyred for to seek sothfastnes in holy writ with great deuoco^n in prayeng:
and with much besynes in studyenge going before / Thise may come to the
fyndyng wha^ our lord Ihu^ wol show it / See now then^e how grace opens the
ghostly eye and clereth ye wit of the soul wondly above the freelte of
corrupt kind / It yeuyth the soul a new ableness whether it woll read holy
writ or here or think it for to vndstonde it truly and sauourly the
sothfastnes of it in the manner before said / And for to torn redily all
reasons and words that are bodily said in to ghostly vndstonding. and that is
no great merueyle / For the same spirit expownyth it and declares it in a
clean soul in comfort of it that first made it. and that is the holy ghost /
And this grace may be and is as well in lewd as in lettred men as anenstes the
substance and the true feeling of sothfastnes and the ghostly sauoure of it in
general though they see not so many reasons in special: for that needs not /
And when the soul is thus abled and lightened through grace. then^e it list for
to be alone some time out of lettynge or comonynge of all creatures that he
might freely assaye his Instrument that I call his reason in beholding of
sothfastnes that is contained in holy writ / And then^e there fall to mind
words and reasons and sentences enough to occupye him in full ordynate and
full sadly / And what comfort and ghostly delight: savor and swetnesse a soul
may feel then^e in his ghostly work thruh^ diverse Illumynaco^ns: Inly
perceyuynges: preuy knowynges and sodeyn towchynges of the holy ghost by assaye
the soul may wit and else not / And I hope that he shall not err be so
that his teeth that been his Inward wits be kept white and clean fro ghostly
pride and fro curyosite of kyndly wit / ^ hope that Dauyd felt full great
delight in this manner werk^ when he said thus / Q^^ dulcia faucibus meis eloquia
tua s^per mel ori meo / How sweet are thy spekynges lord Ihu^ (...) my chekes
over honey to my mouth / That is: Lord Ihu^ thy^ holy words endyted in holy
writ brought to my (...) through grace are swetter to my chekes: that are ye
affeco^ns o^ my soul than honey is to my mouth / Sothly this is a fair work
without paynfull traueylle for to see Ihesus thus / This is one manner of
syghte of Ihesu as I said before / Not as he is: but clothed under lyckenesse
of works and of words / Per speculum in enigmate / By a myrroure and by a
^yckenesse / As the appostle says / Ihesu is endeles might wisdom and
goodness: Ryghtwysnesse: soothfastnesse: holiness. and mercy / And what this
Ihesu is in him self may no soul see ne here. But by effect of his
worchynge he may be seen through the light of grace. as thus / His might is
seen by making of all creatures of naught. his wisdom in ordynate disposynge
of hem: his goodness in saving of hem his mercy in foryeuenesse of sins. his
holiness in yeftes of grace: his rightwysnes in hard punysshynge of syn^e.
his softnes in true rewardyng of good works / And all this is expressed in holy
writ. and this sees a soul in holy writ with all other accidents that
fallen herto / And wite thou well that such gracyous knowynges in holy wrytt or
in other writing that is made thorugh grace are naught else but sweet
letters senden and made betwyxe a loving soul and Ihu^ loved / Or else if I
shall say sothlyer betwyxe Ihu^ the true lover and the souls loved of him /
He has full great tendnes of love to al his chosen childern that are here
closed in claye of this bodily life / And therefore though he be absent fro hem
high hid above in the bosom of the fader fulfilled in delyces of the blessed
godhede. yet notwythstondyng he thinks upon hem and vysyteth hem full often
through his gracyous ghostly presence and comforts hem by his letters of holy
writ. and dryueth out of her hertes heaviness and werynes: dowtes and dredes.
and makes he^ glad and merry in him truly. trowynge to all his byhetynges
and mekely abydinge fulfyllyng of his will / Saint poul says thus / Quecu^que
scripta su^t ad nostra^ doctrina^ scripta sunt vt per consolacione^
scripturarum spe^ habeamus / To. xv.
All that is written to our techynge it is written that by comfort of writing
we might have hope of salvation / And this is a another work of co^templaco^n
for to see Ihu^ in scryptures after opening of the ghostly eye / The clenner
the syghte is in beholdynge. the more comforted is the affeccion in the
tastynge ^ A full little savor felt in a clean soul of holy writ in this
manner before said should make the soul set little price by knowing of all
the vii. arts. or of all the world of all woldly cu^nynges / For the end of
this knowinge is saluaco^n of a man's soul in everlasting life. and the end
of that other as for hemselfe is but vanytee and a passing delight: but if they
be turned through grace to this end.

Of the preuy voys of Ihesu sownyng in a soul whereby it shall be known / And
how all the gracyous Illumynaco^ns made in a soul ben called the spekynges of
Ihu^ / c. xliiii.
^O these are fair new felynges in a clean soul. and if a soul were
fulfilled with such it might be said. and sothly that it were reformed
somewhat in feeling: but not yet fully* for why: yet Ihesu shows more and
ledeth the soul Inner: and begins to speak more homely and more lovely to a
soul. and ready is the soul then to follow the sty^yng of grace / For the
prophet says / Quocu^que ibat spu^s i^ luc gradiebantur et rote sequentes eu^
/ whed so yede the spi^yte thider yede the wheles following him / By wheles
are understand the true lovers of Ihu^ / For they are round in virtue without
angyle of frowardenes. and lightly whyrlynge thorugh redynesse of will to the
styryng of grace / For after tha^ grace styreth and techeth: so they follow
and worche as the prophet says / But they have first a full siker assaye and
^ true knowinge of the voys of grace or they may do so th^^ they be not
deceived by her own feynyng of by the mydda^^ fend / Our lord Ihesu says
thus of his lovers / Oues (...) vocem mea^ audiu^t et cognosco eas and
cognoscu^t me me / ^
(...) sheep heren my voys and I know hem and they know me The preuy voys of
Ihesu is full true. and it makyth a soul true / There is no feynyng in it ne
fantasye ne pride ne ypocrysy / But softness: meekness: pees. love: and
charytee. And it is full of life love and grace / And therefore when it so wnyth
in a soul it is of so great might some time that the soul suddenly lays
of hand all that there is. prayenge: speaking: redynge or thinking in the
manner before said. and all manner bodily work and lystnyth thereto fully heryng
and perceyuinge in rest and in love the sweet steven of this goostly voys. as
it were rauysshed fro ye mind of all erdely things / And then^e some time
shows Ih^u in this pees himself as an hawtful master and sometime as a
reverent fader: and sometime as a lovely sponse / And it kepyth a soul in a
wondfull reverence and in a lovely beholdynge of him that ye soul lyketh well
then. and never so well as then / For it felyth so great sykernesse and
so great rest in Ih^u and so much favor of his goodness yt it would ever be
so and never do other work / It thinkith yt it touchith Ih^u and thruh^
virtue of ye unspeakable touching it is made hole and stable in itself
reverently beholding only Ih^u^ as if there were no thing but Ih^u oo thing
and be a another. borne up only by ye savor and ye wondful goodness of him y^
is that thing yt he felyth and sees / And this feeling is often times without
special beholdynge of holy writ. ne but with few words formyd in ye heart.
naught but thus among fallen in sweet words according to y^ feeling: either
loving or worshyppyng or wondryng: or other wise sownynge as the heart lykyth
/ The soul is full much departed fro love or likynge of the world thorugh
ve^^ue of this gracyous feeling / And also fro mind of the world much in the
mean time / It takyth none head thereof for it has no time thereto / But
then^e sometime anon with this fallyth ^n to a soul diverse Illumynacio^s
thruh^ grace. yt which Illumynaco^ns I call the spekinges of Ihu^ and the
sight of ghostly ^hynges / For wit you well that all the besynes yt Ihu^ makith
a ^^ut a soul. is for to make it a true perfyte spouse to him in ^^e hynes and
the fulness of love. And yt may not be done so sode^ ^^ therefore Ihu^ yt is love
and of all lovers the wysest assayeth by many wyses and by many wondful means
or it may come about And therefore that it might come to theffecte of true
spousage he has such gracyous spekynges this manner of a wower to a chose^
soul / He shows his preuy Jewels. much thing he gives and more he
behiteth. and curteys daliau^ce he shewith / Often he visyteth with much grace
and ghostly comfort as I before said / but he hwo does this in specyal al
fully can I not tell the. for it needs not / Nevertheless somewhat shall I say
after that grace styreth / The drawyng of a soul fully to perfyte love is
first by the showing of ghostly things to a clean soul when the ghostly eye
is openid. not that a soul should rest therein. and make an end there: but by
that seche him and love him only that is highest of al without any beholding
of any other thing than himself / But what are these ghostly things say
you. for I speak often of ghostly things / To this I answer and say. that
ghostly thing may be said all the sothfastnes of holy writ / And therefore a
soul that through ^yghte of grace may see the sothfastnes of it. it sees
ghostly things as I have before said /

How through gracyous opening of the ghostly eye a soul is made wise mekely
and sothfastly to see the dyuersyte of degrees in holy church as traueylynge /
And for to see angels kind and first of reproved / Caplm xlv^
Nevertheless other ghostly things there be^ also the which through light of
grace are showed to the soul. and (...) these / The kind of all reasonable
souls. and the gracyous wo^chynge of our lord Ihu^ in hem / The kind of
angels bless^^ and reproved and her worchyng: and the knowing of the bless^^
trynyte after that grace techith / Holy writ says in the book of songs of
the spouse thus / ^
Surga^ and circuibo ciuitate^ and que ra^ que^ diligit ai^a mea / I shall rise
and I shall goo about the cite and I shall seche him that my soul loves /
That is: I shall rise in to highness of thought and goo about the cite / By
this cite is vndstonde the university of all creatures bodily and ghostly
ordained and ruled under god by laws of kind of reason and of grace / I goo
abowte this cite when I behold the kinds and the causes of bodily creatures^
the yeftes of grace and the blyssis of ghostly creatures^ and in all thise I
seche him that my soul loves / It is fair lokynge with the In^er eye on Ihu^
in bodily creatures for to see his might: his wisdom and his goodness in
ordinance of her kind: but it is much fayrer lokinge on Ihu^ in ghostly
creatures / First in reasonable souls both chosen and reproved to see the
merciful callyuge of him to chosen. how he torneth he^ fro sin^e by light of
his grace. how he helps hem: techeth hem: chastith hem. co^fortith hem. he
ryighteth he cleanses he fedeth: how he makes hem bren^ing in love and in
light by plente of his grace / And thus does he not to one soul only but to
all his chose^ after mesure of his grace / Also of al reproved how ryghtfully
he forsakyth hem and leueth hem in her sins and does hem no wrong. How he
rewards hem in this world suffrynge hem to have the fulfillyng of her will
and after to punyssh^ hem endlesly / Lo this is a lityll beholdynge of holy
church whiles it is in traueylyng in this life to seen how black and how
foul it semyth in souls that are reproved: how fair and how lovely it is in
chosen souls And all this ghostly syte is naught else but the syghte of
Ihu^. not in himself but in his merciful preuy works and in his rightwys
domes every day showed and remembered and renewed to reasonable souls / Also
over this to see with the ghostly eye ye pains of reproved. and the Joy and
the bliss of chosen souls it is full comfortable / For sothfastnes may not be
seen in a clean soul without great delight and wondfull softnes of blessed
bren^ynge love / Also the syghte of angels kind: first of dampened and after
that of the blessed / It is a full fair contemplaco^n of the fend in a clean
soul when grace brings the fend to the syghte of the soul as a clumsid
caytyf bounden with the might of Ihu^ that he may not dear / Then^e the soul
beholds him not bodily but ghostly seenge his kind and his malice. and
torneth him up so down and spoylleth him and renteth him all to naught:
scorneth him and dispyseth him and sets naught by his malice / Thus bids
holy writ when it says thus / Verte impiu^ et no^ erit / Torn the wicked:
that is the fend up soodowne and he shall be as naught / ^
Much wond has the soul that the fend has somoche malice and so lityll
might / There is no creature so vnmyghty as he is: and therefore it is a great
cowardnesse that men dreden him somoche / He may no thing do without leave
of our lord Ihu^. not somoche as enter in to a swyne as the gospel says
Much less may he do then^e to noye any man / And then^e if our lord Ihu^
give hem leave to tarry us it is full worthily and mercyfully done that our
lord Ihu^ does. and therefore welcome be our lord Ihu^ by himself and by all
his messengers / The soul dredeth no more than the blustrynge of the fend than
ye stirynge of a mows / wuder wroth is the fe^de if he durst say nay. but
his mouth his stopped with his own malice. his hondes are bounden as a theyf
worthy to be demid and hanged in hell And then^e the soul accusyth him and
ritfully demith him after that he has deserved / wond not of this saying. for
saint poul meaned the same wha^ he said thus / Fre^s nescitis qm^ anglos
iudicabimus / Brethern wot ye not well that we shall deem angels. that are
wicked spirytes through malice that were made good angels by kind / As who
says yes / This dem^ge is fygured before the dome in contemplatyfe souls /
For they feel a lityl tasting in lyknes of al yt shall be done aftward of our
lord Ihu^ openly in sothfastnes / shamid and shent is ye fe^de greatly in
himself. wha^ he is thus fared with a clean soul. He would fayn flee away and
he may not for ye myte of ye hiest holds him still: and yt greuith him more
tha^ al ye fire of hell. wond mekely fallith ye soul to ihu^ then^e with hertly
louinges yt he so mytly saves a simple soul fro al malice of so fell a enmie
by his great merci.

How by the same light of grace the blessed angels kind may be seen / And
how Ihu^ is god and man above all creatures after that the soul may see him
here / Caplm xlvi.
ANd then^e after this by the self light may the soul see ghostly the
fa^rhede of angels the worthiness of hem in kind. the subtylte of hem in
substance: the co^fermynge of he^ in grace. and the fullness of endless bliss*
y^ sou^dryhede of orders the distyncco^ns of persons how they live all in
light of sothfastnes endless. and how they bren^e all in love of the holy ghost
after the worthynes of orders. how they see and love and praise Ihu^ in blessed
rest without ceesinge / There is no sight of body: ne no figure in
ymaginaco^n in this manner worchinge but all ghostly and. of ghostly creatures /
Then^e begyn^eth the soul to have great aqueyntau^ce of the blessed spirytes
and a great felishyp / They are full tend and full besye about such a soul
to help it / They are masters to teache it. and often through her ghostly
presence and towchynge of her light driven out fantasyes fro the soul: and
they Illumyn the soul graciously. they comfort the soul by sweet words
suddenly sowned in a clean heart / And if any disease fall ghostly they seruen
the soul and mynystre to it all that it needs / Thus saint poul said of he^ /
No^ne oe^s su^t administratorii sp^us missi propter eos qui hereditate^ capiu^t

wot ye not well that holy spirytes are minysters sent of Ihu^ for hem that

no thing else / But then^e with the help of the angel yet the soul sees
more for knowinge ryseth above all this in a clean soul / And yt is to behold
the blessed kind of Ihu^ / First of his glorious manhede how it is hygh^^
worthily above all angels kind. and then after of his bless^^ godhede / For
